Following an Imam Who Wiped Over Khuff
Ruling on following a wiping imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a person who washed his feet following an imam who wiped over khuff or jibira, and explain the talil (effective reasoning) based on the equality of ritual purity.

Core Idea
Washing and wiping are equivalent in effective purity; the imam's khuff does not break that equality.

A common question in congregational prayer is whether differences in the method of achieving purity affect the validity of following an imam. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a specific case: a worshipper who washed his feet in wudu following an imam who wiped over his khuff (leather socks) or jibira (bandage). The ruling provides key insight into the Hanafi understanding of effective purity (hukm al-taharah) and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the permissibility of a person who performed wudu by washing his feet (ghasil) to follow an imam who performed masah over khuff or jibira (masih) in prayer. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih).
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The passage provides a talil (legal reasoning) rather than a textual proof. The reasoning is that both individuals are in a state of ritual purity: the khuff prevents the hadath from reaching the foot, and wiping removes the hadath that occurs on the khuff. Thus their states are equivalent.
This is a qiyas-based argument where the common ground is effective purity.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof applies)
The khuff acts as a barrier (mani') to the transmission of hadath to the foot. When the imam wipes over it, he removes the hadath that has 'attached' to the khuff. Therefore, the imam is in a state of purity comparable to someone who washed his feet directly. The equality of their states allows the follower to be validly led.
This contrasts with the mustahadah (woman with chronic bleeding) whose hadath exists in reality, so she cannot be an imam for someone who is pure from hadath.
4
Note the distinction from the mustahadah
The passage contrasts with a mustahadah. Even though her condition is excused, her hadath remains existent (mawjud haqiqatan). Therefore, she cannot be an imam for someone who is completely pure. This highlights that the permissibility of following a masih depends on the absence of actual hadath, not just on the ruling of pardon.
5
Apply the extension to jibira and the Masjid al-Haram
The commentator expands the ruling to include wiping over jibira (bandage) as even more deserving of permissibility because it is analogous to washing the underlying area. Additionally, the correct view allows following the imam of Masjid al-Haram in all areas connected to the mosque, even if their doors open outside the mosque.
This shows the practical application of the ruling beyond the immediate case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وغاسل بماسح) لاستواء حالهما لأن الخف مانع سراية الحدث إلى القدم وما حل بالخف يزيله المسح بخلاف المستحاضة لأن الحدث موجود حقيقة وإن جعل في حقها معدوماً للضرورة. أطلق الماسح فشمل ماسح الخف وماسح الجبيرة وهو أولى بالجواز لأنه كالغسل لما تحته . الصحيح، وهو اختيار شمس الأئمة الحلواني .اهـ. وعلى الصحيح يصح الاقتداء بإمام المسجد الحرام في المحال المتصلة به وإن كانت أبوابها من خارج المسجد.
His statement: (And one who washed by one who wiped) due to the equality of their states because the khuff prevents the transmission of hadath to the foot, and what is on the khuff is removed by wiping, unlike the mustahadah because the hadath exists in reality even though it is considered non-existent for her due to necessity. He made the one who wipe absolute, so it includes the one who wiped over the khuff and the one who wiped over the jibira, and the latter is more deserving of permissibility because it is like washing for what is under it. The correct view is the choice of Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani. And according to the correct view, it is valid to follow the imam of Masjid al-Haram in the areas connected to it even if their doors are outside the mosque.
Source pages p. 636

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling that a person who performed wudu (washing the feet) can follow an imam who performed masah (wiping over khuff or jibira). The reason is that both states are equivalent: the khuff prevents the hadath from reaching the foot, and wiping removes the hadath that has occurred on the khuff. This is unlike the case of a mustahadah (woman with chronic bleeding) because her hadath exists in reality even though it is excused due to necessity. The commentator notes that the ruling covers both wiping over khuff and wiping over a bandage (jibira), and the latter is even more clearly permissible because it is like washing. The correct view is attributed to Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani. The passage then adds that according to this correct view, it is valid to follow the imam of Masjid al-Haram in areas connected to the mosque even if their entrances are outside the mosque.

Key Terms
غاسل (ghasil): A person who performed wudu by washing the feet (i.e., not wiping).
ماسح (masih): A person who performed masah over khuff or jibira instead of washing.
مستحاضة (mustahadah): A woman with chronic vaginal bleeding outside of menstruation; she must perform wudu for each prayer but her bleeding is excused.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it valid for a person who washed his feet to follow an imam who wiped over his khuff?
A) Because the khuff prevents the hadath from reaching the foot, and wiping removes the hadath from the khuff, making both states equally pure.
B) Because wiping is actually better than washing.
C) Because the mustahadah case proves that even chronic hadath is excused.
D) Because the imam of Masjid al-Haram has special status.

Key Takeaway
A person who washed his feet can validly follow an imam who wiped over khuff or jibira because both are equally pure in effective terms, unlike a mustahadah whose hadath exists in reality.

Ruling on Following an Imam on the Roof of the Mosque
Ruling with proof via analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the mosque roof is part of the mosque to determine the validity of following an imam, and distinguish it from a private roof.

Core Idea
The mosque roof is legally part of the mosque; following an imam on it is valid.

This lesson clarifies a common scenario in congregational prayer: when the imam leads from the roof and the followers are inside (or vice versa). The Hanafi school rules that this is valid because the roof is considered part of the mosque, forming one continuous place of prayer. We will examine the proof and exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
Find the statement that addresses the validity of following an imam on the mosque roof. Note that it is valid (sahih).
2
Examine the objection by Al-Ramli
Al-Ramli mentions an objection from al-Diya' al-Ma'nawi. Understand that the objection is overruled because the roof shares the mosque's ruling.
3
Analyze the proof (qiyas jaliy)
The proof is that the roof is analogous to the interior of the mosque. The common element is that both are part of the same structure, thus a single place for prayer.
This is a clear analogy (qiyas jaliy).
4
Distinguish the private roof
Note the contrast: a private roof (sath dar) is NOT part of the mosque, so following from there would be invalid. This distinction reinforces the rule.
5
Apply the concept of fasad al-wasf
The passage refers to 'invalidity of description' (fasad al-wasf) for similar cases. Understand that the prayer remains valid in essence but may be defective in reward.
This nuance is crucial for differentiating between batil and fasid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وإن كان مسجداً الخ) قال الرملي : يعكر عليه ما في الضياء المعنوي شرح مقدمة الغزنوي : ولو قام الإمام على سطح المسجد والقوم في المسجد ولا يشتبه عليهم حال الإمام صح ا الاقتداء وإن لم يكن له باب لكن لا يشتبه عليهم حال الاقتداء اهـ. وأنت على علم أنه إذا كان على سطح المسجد والقوم في المسجد أو عكسه الإمام صح لم يختلف المكان لأن لسطح المسجد حكم المسجد فكان الكل كبقعة واحدة بخلاف سطح داره تأمل . وينبغي أن يحكم الخ ) قال في النهر : لكن علل الشارح البطلان في الاثني عشرية بأن إمامه قادر على الماء بإخباره واعلم أن المراد بالفساد هنا هو فساد الوصف فقد قال في المحيط : المتوضىء خلف المتيمم إذا رأى الماء أو كان على الإمام فائتة لا يذكرها أو صلى إلى غير القبلة وهو لا يعلم ذلك
His statement: (And if it is a mosque, etc.) Al-Ramli said: It is objected by what is in al-Diya' al-Ma'nawi commentary on Muqaddimat al-Ghaznawi: If the imam stands on the roof of the mosque and the people are in the mosque, and the situation of the imam is not confusing to them, then their following is valid, even if there is no door, as long as the nature of following is not ambiguous. And you know that if he is on the roof and the people are in the mosque, or vice versa, the following is valid because the location does not differ because the roof of the mosque has the ruling of the mosque, so all is like one place, unlike the roof of his house, so reflect. And it is appropriate to judge etc. He said in al-Nahr: But the commentator explained the invalidity in the twelve issues because his imam is able to get water according to his information. And know that by invalidity here is meant the invalidity of the description. It was said in al-Muhit: The mutawaddi' behind the mutayammim, if he sees water or there is on the imam a missed prayer that he does not remember, or he prays facing other than the qibla while he does not know that.
Source pages p. 636

Commentary
This passage addresses the question of whether it is valid to follow an imam when the imam is on the roof of the mosque and the congregation is inside (or vice versa). The matn phrase 'إن كان مسجداً' (if it is a mosque) is being commented on. Al-Ramli raises an objection based on al-Diya' al-Ma'nawi: if the imam is on the roof and the congregation in the mosque, and the imam's actions are clearly visible (no confusion), then following is valid even if there is no direct door. The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq affirms this, reasoning that the roof of the mosque has the same ruling as the mosque itself; they are considered one place. This is unlike the roof of a private house, which is separate. The passage then references al-Nahr and al-Muhit, discussing cases where the mutawaddi' behind a mutayammim imam might see water, or the imam has a missed prayer, or prays facing the wrong direction, and how these affect the validity of the following. The term 'فساد الوصف' (invalidity of description) is used, meaning the prayer is valid in essence but the reward is diminished or it is considered makruh.

Key Terms
سطح المسجد (sath al-masjid): The roof of the mosque; considered part of the mosque for the purpose of following an imam.
فساد الوصف (fasad al-wasf): Invalidity in terms of the description (e.g., diminished reward), not the essence of the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on following an imam who is on the roof of the mosque while the congregation is inside?
A) It is invalid because they are not in the same place.
B) It is valid because the roof of the mosque is considered part of the mosque.
C) It is valid only if there is a direct door connecting the roof.
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
The mosque roof is legally part of the mosque, making it valid to follow an imam on it, unlike a private roof.

Ruling on a Standing Person Following a Sitting Imam
Ruling with proof: following a sitting imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a standing person following a sitting imam, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute, and explain the dalil used to support the relied-upon position.

Core Idea
Following a sitting imam while standing is valid because the Prophet's practice overrides the analogy of building the strong on the weak.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on whether a person standing in prayer can validly follow an imam who is sitting (e.g., due to illness). The matn states that such following does not invalidate the prayer, but there is a well-known intra-madhhab difference. We will explore the evidence of the Sahibayn and the counterargument of Imam Muhammad, and see why the view of the Sahibayn is mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is a qa'im following a qa'id. The matn rules it not invalid. But there is ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
The phrase in the matn: (وقائم بقاعد) is part of a larger list.
2
State the positions of the Sahibayn and Imam Muhammad
Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf): valid. Muhammad: invalid (fasad) due to building strong on weak.
The qiyas analogy is to the case of tayammum where a mutayammim cannot lead a mutawaddi'.
3
Examine the dalil of the Sahibayn
They rely on the hadith of the Prophet's final illness, where he led the prayer sitting and the Companions stood behind him.
This is a sahih hadith in Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Examine the dalil of Imam Muhammad
He uses qiyas: analogy to tayammum, where the person without wudu cannot lead those with wudu. The Hanafi response is that the prophetic practice takes precedence over qiyas.
The Sahibayn argue that the Prophet's action is a specific evidence overriding the general qiyas.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and thamarah
The view of the Sahibayn is mufta bihi. The practical consequence: it is valid to follow a sitting imam while standing.
The later Hanafi masters (e.g., al-Marghinani, al-Haskafi) adopt this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وقائم بقاعد وبأحدب أي لا يفسد اقتداء قائم بقاعد وبأحدب. وأما الأول فهو قولهما، وحكم محمد بالفساد نظراً إلى أنه بناء القوي على الضعيف، ولهما اقتداء الناس بالنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في مرض موته وهو قاعد وهم قيام وهو آخر أحواله، فتعين العمل به بناء على أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان إماماً وأبو بكر مبلغاً للناس تكبيره، وبه استدل على جواز رفع معنی والمقتدي يعلم فقهقه المقتدي كان عليه إعادة الوضوء عندهما خلافاً لمحمد وزفر بناء على ما مر إلا أنه ينبغي على ما اختاره الشارح أن يبطل الأصل أيضاً إذ الفساد لفقد شرط وهو الطهارة فتأمل اهـ. قوله : (وبه استدل الخ) قال في الفتح وليس مقصوده خصوص الرفع الكائن في زماننا بل أصل الرفع لإبلاغ الانتقالات، أما خصوص هذا الذي تعارفوه في هذه البلاد فلا يبعد أنه مفسد فإنه غالباً يشتمل على مد همزة «الله أكبر» أو بائه وذلك مفسد وإن لم يشتمل لأنهم بالغون في الصياح زيادة على حاجة الإبلاغ والاشتغال بتحريرات النغم إظهاراً للصناعة النغمية لا إقامة للعبادة، والصياح ملحق بالكلام الذي بساطه ذلك الصياح وسيأتي في باب ما يفسد الصلاة أنه إذا ارتفع بكاؤه من ذكر الجنة والنار لا تفسد، والمصيبة بلغته ،تفسد لأنه في الأول يعرض بسؤال الجنة والتعوذ من النار، إن كان يقال إن المراد إذا حصل به الحروف ولو صرح به لا تفسد. وفي الثاني لإظهارها ولو صرح بها فقال وامصيبتاه أو أدركوني أفسد فهو بمنزلته، وهنا معلوم أن قصده إعجاب الناس به ولو قال اعجبوا من حسن صوتي وتحريري فيه أفسد. وحصول الحرف لازم من التلحين ولا أرى ذلك يصدر ممن فهم الدعاء والسؤال وما ذلك إلا نوع لعب فإنه لو قدر في الشاهد سائل حاجة من ملك أدى سؤاله وطلبه بتحرير النغم فيه من الرفع والخفض والتغريب والرجوع كالتغني نسب البتة إلى قصد السخرية واللعب إذ مقام طلب الحاجة التضرع لا التغني .اهـ وأقره عليه في النهر. وقال العلامة ابن أمير حاج وقد أجاد رحمه الله تعالى فيما أوضح وأفاد اهـ. أقول: في كون الصياح بما هو ذكر ملحقاً بالكلام فيكون مفسداً وإن لم يشتمل على مد همزة «الله» أو باء أكبر» نظر، فقد صرح في السراج بأن الإمام إذا جهر فوق حاجة الناس فقد أساء .اهـ. والإساءة دون الكراهة لا توجب فساداً على أن كلامه يؤول بالآخرة إلى أن الإفساد إنما حصل بحصول الحرف لا بمجرد رفع الصوت زيادة على حاجة الإبلاغ والقياس على ما ارتفع بكاؤه المصيبة بلغته غير ظاهر لأن ما هنا ذكر بصيغته فلا يتغير بعزيمته، والمفسد للصلاة الملفوظ لا عزيمة القلب على ما تقدم بخلاف ارتفاع الصوت بالبكاء المصيبة بلغته فإنه ليس بذكر فيتغير بعزيمته على أن القياس بعد الأربعمائة منقطع فليس لأحد بعدها أن يقيس مسألة على مسألة كما صرح به العلامة زين ابن نجيم في رسائله كذا ذكر السيد أحمد الحموي في رسالته «القول البليغ في حكم التبليغ والله تعالى أعلم. قلت: وبالله التوفيق: الحق ما قاله الإمام المحقق وأقره عليه كثير، وأما ما ذكره السيد الحموي من النظر فهو ساقط لأنه لم يجعل الفساد مبنياً على مجرد الرفع حتى يرد عليه ما في السراج، بل بناه على زيادة الرفع الملحق بالصياح المشتمل على النغم مع قصد إظهاره لذلك والإعراض عن إقامة العبادة وقوله «على أن كلامه الخ» ممنوع لأنه بنی كلامه على أن مبنی الفساد ما مر وإن لم يحصل به حروف زائدة فمجرد ذلك كافٍ في
His statement: (And a standing person by a sitting person and by a hunched person) meaning that the following of a standing person by a sitting person and by a hunched person is not invalid. As for the first, it is their (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's) view, while Muhammad ruled it invalid due to it being building the strong upon the weak. They support their view with the people's following of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in his illness of death, when he was sitting and they were standing, which was his last state. So acting upon it is determined, based on the fact that he (peace be upon him) was the imam and Abu Bakr was conveying his takbir to the people. By this he inferred the permissibility of raising (voice) for conveying meaning, and if the follower laughed while knowing, he had to repeat wudu according to them, contrary to Muhammad and Zufar, based on what preceded, except that according to the commentator's choice, the original should also be invalid because the invalidity is due to the loss of a condition, i.e., purity, so reflect. His statement: (By it he inferred, etc.) He said in al-Fath: His intention is not specifically the raising that occurs in our time, but the original raising for conveying the transitions. As for this particular custom in these lands, it is not far that it invalidates, for it often includes prolonging the hamzah of 'Allahu Akbar' or its ba', and that is invalid even if it does not include them, because they exaggerate in shouting beyond the need for conveying and occupy themselves with melody adjustments to display musical artistry, not to perform worship. Shouting is annexed to speech whose basis is that shouting. It will come in the chapter on what invalidates prayer that if his weeping increases due to mentioning Paradise and Hell, it does not invalidate, but weeping for a calamity in his language invalidates, because in the first he is seeking Paradise and seeking refuge from Hell, as it is said, if letters are produced, even if he explicitly says it, it does not invalidate. In the second, to express them, even if he explicitly says 'Oh my calamity!' or 'Help me!', it invalidates, so it is like that. And here, it is known that his intention is to impress people with it, and if he said 'Be amazed at my beautiful voice and my modulation', it invalidates. The production of letter is necessary from melody, and I do not think that comes from one who understands supplication and request; it is only a type of play. For if in the witness a needy person requests something from a king and delivers his request with melody in raising, lowering, and returning like singing, he would be attributed to the intention of mockery and play, since the station of request is humility, not singing. It (that statement) ended. And it was endorsed by al-Nahr. And Allamah Ibn Amir Haj said: He excelled, may Allah have mercy on him, in what he clarified and benefitted. I say: Regarding the consideration that shouting which is dhikr is annexed to speech and thus invalidates even if it does not include prolonging the hamzah of 'Allah' or the ba' of 'Akbar', there is consideration. For it is stated in al-Siraj that if the imam raises his voice beyond the need of the people, he has done wrong. And wrong is below disliked, so it does not necessitate invalidity. Moreover, his speech ultimately implies that invalidity is only due to the occurrence of the letter, not merely raising the voice beyond the need of conveying. And analogy to the case of weeping for a calamity in his language is not apparent, because what is here is dhikr in its wording, so it is not changed by his intention. The invalidator of prayer is the utterance, not the intention of the heart, as preceded. Unlike raising the voice with weeping for a calamity in his language, for it is not dhikr, so it changes with his intention. Moreover, analogy after four hundred years is cut off; no one after that can analogize one issue to another, as stated by Allamah Zayn ibn Nujaym in his treatises. Thus mentioned by Sayyid Ahmad al-Hamawi in his treatise 'Al-Qawl al-Baligh fi Hukm al-Tabligh'. And Allah knows best. I say: And by Allah is success: The truth is what the verifying imam said, and many endorsed it. As for what Sayyid al-Hamawi mentioned of consideration, it is invalid because he did not base the invalidity merely on raising the voice, so that the objection from al-Siraj would apply to him; rather, he based it on the increased raising annexed to shouting that includes melodies with the intention of displaying them and turning away from performing worship. And his statement 'Moreover, his speech...' is rejected because he built his speech on that the basis of invalidity is what passed, even if no extra letters occur; merely that is sufficient in
Source pages p. 637

Commentary
This passage covers two related issues: the validity of a standing person following a sitting or hunched imam, and the problem of raising one's voice in prayer in a melodic manner. The first part states the matn that such following is not invalid. It notes an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Sahibayn) rule it valid, while Imam Muhammad rules it invalid because he sees it as building the strong (standing) on the weak (sitting), analogous to the tayammum case earlier. The Sahibayn rely on the established practice of the Companions following the Prophet (peace be upon him) during his final illness when he led the prayer sitting while they stood. This practice is taken as a proof for the permissibility of a standing person following a sitting imam. The commentary then discusses a branch: if the follower laughs (fahqaha) while knowing, he must repeat wudu according to the Sahibayn, but Muhammad and Zufar differ. The second part of the passage deals with the issue of raising the voice (raf') for the purpose of conveying (tabligh) the imam's takbir. The author cites al-Fath, clarifying that the original ruling allowing raf' is for the purpose of conveying the transitions (e.g., takbir, taslim). However, the common practice in some lands of raising the voice with melodic modulation and exaggeration is criticized as potentially invalidating the prayer, because it often involves prolonging the letters of 'Allahu Akbar' (e.g., the hamzah of 'Allah' or the ba' of 'Akbar'), which changes the meaning, or simply because the action amounts to shouting and playing, not worship. The author then engages in a lengthy debate: he quotes a view that such shouting is annexed to speech and thus invalidates, but he raises a counter-argument based on al-Siraj that wrong (isaa'ah) is below dislike and does not cause invalidity. He also argues that analogy to weeping for a calamity is weak because here the words are dhikr and thus not changed by intention. He mentions the principle of 'insidad bab al-qiyas' after four hundred years, citing Zayn ibn Nujaym, to reject any new analogy. Finally, he defends the original position (of the verifying imam) that the basis of invalidity is the added raising with melodies and intention of display, not mere raising. The passage ends abruptly with a refutation of al-Hamawi's objection.

Key Terms
قائم (qa'im): A person praying while standing, which is fard for obligatory prayer in Hanafi.
قاعد (qa'id): A person praying while sitting, either due to illness or as the imam's state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it valid for a standing person to follow a sitting imam according to the majority of Hanafis?
A) Because sitting and standing are equal in rank.
B) Because the Prophet led the prayer while sitting in his final illness and the Companions stood behind him.
C) Because the imam can choose his position freely.
D) Because it is based on qiyas with the tayammum case.

Key Takeaway
The sahih view in the Hanafi school is that a standing person can follow a sitting imam based on the Prophet's practice in his final illness.

The Issue of Raising the Voice in Prayer: When Does It Invalidate?
Ruling with proof: permissibility of raf' and conditions for invalidity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid raising of the voice for tabligh and the invalid melodic shouting, and explain the Hanafi position on what constitutes invalidity.

Core Idea
Raising the voice for conveying takbir is permissible, but melodic shouting with the intention of display invalidates the prayer.

This lesson addresses the second topic from the passage: the permissibility of raising the voice (raf') in prayer, particularly for tabligh (conveying the imam's words). The text first establishes the original ruling using the same hadith from the previous lesson, then engages in a detailed critique of a common practice of melodic chanting, which the author argues invalidates the prayer due to excess and wrong intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original ruling on raf'
The hadith of the Prophet's final illness also supports the permissibility of raising the voice for tabligh.
The Prophet appointed Abu Bakr to convey his takbir to the congregation.
2
Differentiate between original raf' and the common practice
Original raf' is for conveying transitions. The common practice involves melodic modulation and excess beyond the need.
The text criticizes 'this custom in these lands' as often including prolongation of letters and melodies.
3
Analyze the criteria for invalidity
The author lists: prolonging letters (e.g., hamzah of 'Allah', ba' of 'Akbar'), excessive shouting (siyah), and intention to impress people. If these are present, the prayer may be invalid.
Shouting (siyah) is annexed to speech, so it can invalidate.
4
Examine the counterargument from al-Siraj
Al-Siraj states that raising above need is only isaa'ah (dislike), not invalid. The author distinguishes by pointing to the additional factors of melodies and intent.
The author argues that the basis of invalidity is the combination, not mere excess.
5
Resolve the dispute
The author sides with the view that the combined factors (excess, melodies, intention) cause invalidity, rejecting al-Hamawi's objection as 'saaqit' (invalid).
The author emphasizes that the intention to display and turn away from worship is key.

His statement: (And a standing person by a sitting person and by a hunched person) meaning that the following of a standing person by a sitting person and by a hunched person is not invalid. As for the first, it is their (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's) view, while Muhammad ruled it invalid due to it being building the strong upon the weak. They support their view with the people's following of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in his illness of death, when he was sitting and they were standing, which was his last state. So acting upon it is determined, based on the fact that he (peace be upon him) was the imam and Abu Bakr was conveying his takbir to the people. By this he inferred the permissibility of raising (voice) for conveying meaning, and if the follower laughed while knowing, he had to repeat wudu according to them, contrary to Muhammad and Zufar, based on what preceded, except that according to the commentator's choice, the original should also be invalid because the invalidity is due to the loss of a condition, i.e., purity, so reflect. His statement: (By it he inferred, etc.) He said in al-Fath: His intention is not specifically the raising that occurs in our time, but the original raising for conveying the transitions. As for this particular custom in these lands, it is not far that it invalidates, for it often includes prolonging the hamzah of 'Allahu Akbar' or its ba', and that is invalid even if it does not include them, because they exaggerate in shouting beyond the need for conveying and occupy themselves with melody adjustments to display musical artistry, not to perform worship. Shouting is annexed to speech whose basis is that shouting. It will come in the chapter on what invalidates prayer that if his weeping increases due to mentioning Paradise and Hell, it does not invalidate, but weeping for a calamity in his language invalidates, because in the first he is seeking Paradise and seeking refuge from Hell, as it is said, if letters are produced, even if he explicitly says it, it does not invalidate. In the second, to express them, even if he explicitly says 'Oh my calamity!' or 'Help me!', it invalidates, so it is like that. And here, it is known that his intention is to impress people with it, and if he said 'Be amazed at my beautiful voice and my modulation', it invalidates. The production of letter is necessary from melody, and I do not think that comes from one who understands supplication and request; it is only a type of play. For if in the witness a needy person requests something from a king and delivers his request with melody in raising, lowering, and returning like singing, he would be attributed to the intention of mockery and play, since the station of request is humility, not singing. It (that statement) ended. And it was endorsed by al-Nahr. And Allamah Ibn Amir Haj said: He excelled, may Allah have mercy on him, in what he clarified and benefitted. I say: Regarding the consideration that shouting which is dhikr is annexed to speech and thus invalidates even if it does not include prolonging the hamzah of 'Allah' or the ba' of 'Akbar', there is consideration. For it is stated in al-Siraj that if the imam raises his voice beyond the need of the people, he has done wrong. And wrong is below disliked, so it does not necessitate invalidity. Moreover, his speech ultimately implies that invalidity is only due to the occurrence of the letter, not merely raising the voice beyond the need of conveying. And analogy to the case of weeping for a calamity in his language is not apparent, because what is here is dhikr in its wording, so it is not changed by his intention. The invalidator of prayer is the utterance, not the intention of the heart, as preceded. Unlike raising the voice with weeping for a calamity in his language, for it is not dhikr, so it changes with his intention. Moreover, analogy after four hundred years is cut off; no one after that can analogize one issue to another, as stated by Allamah Zayn ibn Nujaym in his treatises. Thus mentioned by Sayyid Ahmad al-Hamawi in his treatise 'Al-Qawl al-Baligh fi Hukm al-Tabligh'. And Allah knows best. I say: And by Allah is success: The truth is what the verifying imam said, and many endorsed it. As for what Sayyid al-Hamawi mentioned of consideration, it is invalid because he did not base the invalidity merely on raising the voice, so that the objection from al-Siraj would apply to him; rather, he based it on the increased raising annexed to shouting that includes melodies with the intention of displaying them and turning away from performing worship. And his statement 'Moreover, his speech...' is rejected because he built his speech on that the basis of invalidity is what passed, even if no extra letters occur; merely that is sufficient in

Commentary
This passage covers two related issues: the validity of a standing person following a sitting or hunched imam, and the problem of raising one's voice in prayer in a melodic manner. The first part states the matn that such following is not invalid. It notes an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Sahibayn) rule it valid, while Imam Muhammad rules it invalid because he sees it as building the strong (standing) on the weak (sitting), analogous to the tayammum case earlier. The Sahibayn rely on the established practice of the Companions following the Prophet (peace be upon him) during his final illness when he led the prayer sitting while they stood. This practice is taken as a proof for the permissibility of a standing person following a sitting imam. The commentary then discusses a branch: if the follower laughs (fahqaha) while knowing, he must repeat wudu according to the Sahibayn, but Muhammad and Zufar differ. The second part of the passage deals with the issue of raising the voice (raf') for the purpose of conveying (tabligh) the imam's takbir. The author cites al-Fath, clarifying that the original ruling allowing raf' is for the purpose of conveying the transitions (e.g., takbir, taslim). However, the common practice in some lands of raising the voice with melodic modulation and exaggeration is criticized as potentially invalidating the prayer, because it often involves prolonging the letters of 'Allahu Akbar' (e.g., the hamzah of 'Allah' or the ba' of 'Akbar'), which changes the meaning, or simply because the action amounts to shouting and playing, not worship. The author then engages in a lengthy debate: he quotes a view that such shouting is annexed to speech and thus invalidates, but he raises a counter-argument based on al-Siraj that wrong (isaa'ah) is below dislike and does not cause invalidity. He also argues that analogy to weeping for a calamity is weak because here the words are dhikr and thus not changed by intention. He mentions the principle of 'insidad bab al-qiyas' after four hundred years, citing Zayn ibn Nujaym, to reject any new analogy. Finally, he defends the original position (of the verifying imam) that the basis of invalidity is the added raising with melodies and intention of display, not mere raising. The passage ends abruptly with a refutation of al-Hamawi's objection.

Key Terms
رفع (raf'): The act of raising the voice in prayer, especially for tabligh (conveying takbir).
صياح (siyah): Shouting or loud vocalization in prayer, which may be annexed to speech.
تبليغ (tabligh): Conveying the imam's words (e.g., takbir) to the congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following would invalidate the prayer when raising the voice?
A) Raising the voice to convey the takbir to the back rows.
B) Raising the voice with a melodic tune to impress the listeners.
C) Raising the voice due to weeping from fear of Hell.
D) Raising the voice slightly above the need of the congregation.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of raising the voice for tabligh is established by the hadith, but the practice of melodic chanting with excessive shouting and display invalidates the prayer.

Following a Seated or Hunchbacked Imam
Commentary on following seated/hunchbacked imam with intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on a standing person following a seated or hunchbacked imam, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute, and explain the relied-upon position.

Core Idea
Following a seated imam is valid based on the Prophet's last practice; Muhammad's objection (building strong on weak) is outweighed.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a key intra-Hanafi disagreement: whether a standing person may validly follow an imam who is seated due to an excuse, or an imam whose hunched back resembles bowing. The ruling of the matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) states it does not invalidate, but Imam Muhammad considers it invalid. The commentary explains the proof and resolution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Recognize that the ruling concerns the validity of a standing person following a seated or hunchbacked imam in obligatory prayer.
The author states 'does not invalidate' (لا يفسد).
2
State the positions and their proofs
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the 'two') rule it valid, citing the hadith of the Prophet ﷺ leading prayer while seated during his fatal illness. Muhammad rules it invalid, arguing it is building the strong (standing) upon the weak (seated).
Sitting is considered a form of standing from one perspective.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The response emphasizes that the Prophet's practice is the last and thus binding; sitting is a kind of standing, so the purpose of worship is achieved. The analogy with a hunchbacked imam is also addressed.
The dispute extends to hunchbacked imams whose hump reaches the bowing limit.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: it is valid. Muhammad's view is considered marjuh.
Tarjih authority: al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and others.
5
Note the practical consequence
In practice, the prayer is valid when following a seated imam with an excuse. The same applies to hunchbacked imams with hump reaching bowing limit.
No need to repeat prayer even if following Muhammad's view mistakenly.

الجلالة أو باء «أكبر». وقوله لأن ما هنا ذكر بصيغته الخ كلام ساقط لأن ذلك قول أبي يوسف بانياً عليه عدم الفساد فيما لو فتح المصلي على غير إمامه أو أجاب المؤذن أو قال لا إله إلا الله جواباً لمن قال أمع الله إله، أو أخبر بما سره فقال الحمد الله، أو بما يعجبه فقال سبحان الله على قصد الجواب ونحو ذلك كما سيأتي، والمذهب الفساد وهو قولهما لأنه تعليم وتعلم في الأولى. وفيما بقي قد أخرج الكلام مخرج الجواب وهو يحتمله فإن مناط كونه من كلام الناس عندهما كونه لفظاً أفيد به معنى ليس من أعمال الصلاة لا كونه وضع لإفادة ذلك، وكونه لم يتغير بعزيمته ممنوع كما ذكره في الفتح. قال في النهر ألا ترى أن الجنب إذا قرأ الفاتحة على قصد الثناء جاز اهـ. وقد ذكروا أشياء تفسد اتفاقاً كما لو كان بين يديه كتاب وعنده رجل اسمه يحيى فقال يا خذ الكتاب بقوة ونحوها مما سيأتي وهذا وارد على أصل أبي يوسف. وقوله «على أن القياس بعد الأربعمائة منقطع الخ نقول بموجبه ولا نسلم أن ما ذكره المحقق من هذا القبيل بل هو : تخريج على ما مر من أصلهما كما هو دأب المشايخ كقاضيخان وأضرابه من تخريجهم ما ليس فيه نص على أصل ظاهر. ومثله ما يذكره المؤلف وغيره من قولهم ينبغي أن يكون كذا ومقتضى القواعد كذا، فلو
المؤذنين أصواتهم في الجمعة والعيدين وغيرهما كما في المجتبى، وليس هو بناء القوي على الضعيف لأن القعود قيام من وجه كالركوع لانتصاب أحد نصفيه وصار كالاقتداء بالمنحني من الهرم، ولا يرد عليه الإيماء فإنه بعض الركوع والسجود ومع . اقتداء ذلك فلم يصح الراكع والساجد بالمومي لوجهين: أحدهما أن القيام ليس بركن مقصود ولهذا جاز تركه في النفل من غير عذر فجاز أن يسد الناقص مسده لعدم فوات المقصود فكان حال الإمام مثل حال المقتدي في المقصود وهو نهاية التعبد بخلاف الركوع والسجود فإنهما ركنان مقصودان وقد فاتا في حق الإمام المومي، ولأن القعود يسمى قياماً. يقال لمن قعد ناهضاً عن نومه قام عن فراشه وقام عن مضجعه ويقال للمضطجع قم واقرأ فإذا نهض وقعد يكون ممتثلاً لأمره بالقيام بخلاف الإيماء فإنه لا يسمى سجوداً. وذكر في المجتبى فرقاً إجمالياً وهو يتخير بين القيام والقعود ولا يتخير بين الإيماء والسجود ولا بين القعود والاستلقاء. وفي الحقائق : الخلاف في قاعد يركع ويسجد لأنه لو كان يومىء والقوم يركعون ويسجدون لا يجوز اتفاقاً. ومحل الاختلاف الاقتداء في الفرض والواجب حيث كان للإمام عذر، أما في النفل فيجوز اتفاقاً واختلف في اقتداء القائم بالقاعد في التراويح والأصح أنه جائز عند الكل كما في فتاوى قاضيخان وأما الثاني وهو اقتداء القائم بالأحدب فأطلقه فشمل ما إذا بلغ حدبه حد الركوع وما إذا لم يبلغ ولا خلاف في الثاني واختلفوا في الأول؛ ففي المجتبى أنه جائز عندهما وبه أخذ عامة العلماء خلافاً لمحمد وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية : لا تصح إمامة أن المتنفل الفساد كما هو صريح أول كلامه وآخره حيث قال فإنه لو قدر في الشاهد الخ» فقوله «وحصول الحرف لازم من التلحين بيان لشيء يستلزمه ذلك المفسد مما قد يكون مفسداً في نفسه، وإن فرض عدم إفساد الملزوم بأن يمد همزة الجلالة أو باء «أكبر». وقوله لأن ما هنا ذكر بصيغته الخ كلام ساقط لأن ذلك قول أبي يوسف بانياً عليه عدم الفساد فيما لو فتح المصلي على غير إمامه أو أجاب المؤذن أو قال لا إله إلا الله جواباً لمن قال أمع الله إله، أو أخبر بما سره فقال الحمد الله، أو بما يعجبه فقال سبحان الله على قصد الجواب ونحو ذلك كما سيأتي، والمذهب الفساد وهو قولهما لأنه تعليم وتعلم في الأولى. وفيما بقي قد أخرج الكلام مخرج الجواب وهو يحتمله فإن مناط كونه من كلام الناس عندهما كونه لفظاً أفيد به معنى ليس من أعمال الصلاة لا كونه وضع لإفادة ذلك، وكونه لم يتغير بعزيمته ممنوع كما ذكره في الفتح. قال في النهر ألا ترى أن الجنب إذا قرأ الفاتحة على قصد الثناء جاز اهـ. وقد ذكروا أشياء تفسد اتفاقاً كما لو كان بين يديه كتاب وعنده رجل اسمه يحيى فقال يا خذ الكتاب بقوة ونحوها مما سيأتي وهذا وارد على أصل أبي يوسف. وقوله «على أن القياس بعد الأربعمائة منقطع الخ نقول بموجبه ولا نسلم أن ما ذكره المحقق من هذا القبيل بل هو : تخريج على ما مر من أصلهما كما هو دأب المشايخ كقاضيخان وأضرابه من تخريجهم ما ليس فيه نص على أصل ظاهر. ومثله ما يذكره المؤلف وغيره من قولهم ينبغي أن يكون كذا ومقتضى القواعد كذا، فلو
The Book of Prayer - Chapter of Imamate. His saying: (And a standing person behind a seated one and behind a hunchbacked one) meaning that the following of a standing person behind a seated one and behind a hunchbacked one does not invalidate [the prayer]. As for the first [case, standing behind seated], it is the view of the two [Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf?], and Muhammad ruled it invalid, considering that it is building the strong upon the weak. And for the two [there is the proof of] the people following the Prophet ﷺ during his fatal illness when he was seated and they were standing, and it was his last state; so acting upon it is determined, based on the fact that he ﷺ was the imam and Abu Bakr was communicating his takbir to the people. And by this they argued for the permissibility of raising the meaning... And if the follower knows [the intention?] and laughs, then according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?] he must repeat wudu, contrary to Muhammad and Zufar, based on what has passed, except that according to the preference of the commentator, the original [prayer] should also be invalidated, because the corruption is due to the loss of a condition, which is purification, so consider. End. His saying: (And by it they argued) etc. He said in al-Fath: His intention is not specifically the raising that occurs in our time, but rather the principle of raising for communicating the transitions. As for this particular practice that has become customary in these lands, it is not unlikely that it is invalidating, because it often includes prolonging the hamza of 'Allahu Akbar' or its ba', and that is invalidating even if it does not include them, because they exceed in shouting beyond the need for communication and occupy themselves with modulating melodies, displaying musical craftsmanship, not performing worship. Shouting is annexed to speech whose essence is that shouting. And it will come in the chapter on what invalidates prayer that if his weeping due to remembrance of Paradise and Hell rises, it does not invalidate, but if it is due to a calamity in his language, it invalidates, because in the first case he is asking for Paradise and seeking refuge from Hell. It is said that the intention is if letters are produced, even if explicitly stated, it does not invalidate. In the second, for showing it, even if he says 'Oh my calamity' or 'Help me', it invalidates, so it is like that. And here it is known that his intention is to impress people; if he said 'Be amazed at the beauty of my voice and my modulation', it invalidates. The occurrence of the letter is necessary from melodious intonation, and I do not see that issuing from one who understands supplication and request; it is nothing but a type of play. For if one imagines a supplicant in the presence of a king, he would perform his request and plea with modulation of tone, raising, lowering, orientalizing, and returning, like singing, he would be absolutely attributed to the intention of mockery and play, because the station of requesting a need is humility, not singing. End. And he [al-Marghinani] endorsed it in al-Nahr. And Allama Ibn Amir Haj said: He has done well, may Allah have mercy on him, in what he clarified and benefited. End. I say: Regarding the view that shouting, being remembrance, is annexed to speech and thus invalidates even if it does not include prolonging the hamza of 'Allah' or the ba of 'Akbar', there is consideration. For it is stated in al-Siraj that if the imam raises his voice beyond the people's need, he has done wrong. End. And wrongdoing is less than dislike, so it does not necessitate invalidation. However, his words ultimately lead to the fact that invalidation only occurs through the occurrence of the letter, not merely by raising the voice beyond the need for communication. And analogy with one whose weeping due to a calamity in his language rises is not apparent, because here it is remembrance in its original wording, so it is not changed by his intention, whereas the invalidator of prayer is the uttered word, not the intention of the heart, as has preceded. In contrast, the raising of voice in weeping for a calamity in his language is not remembrance, so it is changed by his intention. Moreover, analogy after four hundred [years] is discontinued, so no one after that may analogize one case to another, as stated by Allama Zayn ibn Nujaym in his treatises. Thus mentioned sayyid Ahmad al-Hamawi in his treatise 'al-Qawl al-Baligh fi Hukm al-Tabligh'. And Allah Almighty knows best. I say: And by Allah is success: The truth is what the verifying imam said and many agreed with him. As for what sayyid al-Hamawi mentioned of consideration, it is invalid, because he did not base invalidation on mere raising so that what is in al-Siraj would refute it; rather, he based it on the excessive raising annexed to shouting that includes melodies, with the intention of showing off and turning away from performing worship. And his statement 'Nevertheless, his words...' is rejected because he built his words on the basis that the foundation of invalidation is what has passed, even if no extra letters result from it; so that alone is sufficient for invalidation, as is clear from the beginning and end of his words where he said: 'For if one imagines in the witnessed case...' So his statement 'The occurrence of the letter is necessary from melodious intonation' is an explanation of something that necessitates that invalidator, which may itself be invalidating, even if one assumes the non-invalidation of the subject by prolonging the hamza of the Majesty or the ba of 'Akbar'. And his statement 'because here it is remembrance in its original wording' etc. is invalid speech, because that is the view of Abu Yusuf, building on it the non-invalidation in cases where a person praying corrects someone other than his imam, or responds to the mu'adhdhin, or says 'La ilaha illa Allah' in response to someone who said 'Is there a god with Allah?', or tells what pleased him and says 'Alhamdulillah', or what amazed him and says 'Subhanallah' with the intention of response, and similar cases, as will come. And the madhhab [position] is invalidation, which is the view of the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], because in the first case it is teaching and learning. In the remaining cases, he has brought the speech out in the form of a response, and it is possible. For the criterion of it being human speech according to the two is that it is a word by which a meaning is conveyed that is not from the actions of prayer, not that it is put to convey that. And the contention that it is not changed by his intention is rejected, as mentioned in al-Fath. He said in al-Nahr: Do you not see that a junub if he recites al-Fatiha with the intention of praise, it is permissible? End. And they have mentioned things that invalidate by agreement, such as if there is a book in front of him and there is a man named Yahya, and he says 'Take the book with strength', and similar cases that will come. This refutes the principle of Abu Yusuf. And his statement 'Moreover, analogy after four hundred is discontinued' we affirm its implication, but we do not concede that what the verifier mentioned is of this category; rather, it is an extraction based on what has passed from their principle, as is the practice of the shaykhs like Qadikhan and others in extracting rulings for matters for which there is no text from an apparent principle. Similar is what the author and others mention from their saying 'it should be such' and 'the requirements of the rules are such'. So if... the mu'adhdhinin raise their voices on Friday and the two Eids and other occasions, as in al-Mujtaba. And it is not building the strong upon the weak, because sitting is a kind of standing in one respect, like bowing due to the uprightness of one of its halves, and it becomes like following one bent from old age. And the gesturing is not analogous, because it is part of bowing and prostration. And the following of the one who bows and prostrates behind one who gestures is not valid for two reasons: First, standing is not an essential pillar, and for this reason it is permissible to omit it in voluntary prayers without excuse; so it is permissible for the lesser to take the place of the greater because the purpose is not lost. Thus the situation of the imam is like that of the follower regarding the purpose, which is the ultimate worship, unlike bowing and prostration, for they are two essential pillars and they are lost in the case of the imam who gestures. Second, sitting is called standing: it is said to one who sits after rising from sleep 'he stood from his bed' and 'he stood from his sleeping place', and to the one lying down it is said 'stand up and read', so if he rises and sits, he complies with the command to stand, unlike gesturing, for it is not called prostration. And in al-Mujtaba, a general difference is mentioned: he has a choice between standing and sitting, but he does not have a choice between gesturing and prostrating, nor between sitting and lying down. And in al-Haqa'iq: the dispute is about a seated person who bows and prostrates [normally], because if he gestures and the people bow and prostrate, it is not valid by agreement. And the place of disagreement is in obligatory and necessary prayers when the imam has an excuse. As for voluntary prayers, it is valid by agreement. And there is disagreement about a standing person following a seated one in tarawih; the most correct view is that it is permissible according to all, as in Fatawa Qadikhan. As for the second [case, i.e., following a hunchbacked imam], he [the author] has left it open, so it includes both when his hump reaches the limit of bowing and when it does not. There is no disagreement in the second case, and they disagree in the first: in al-Mujtaba it is permissible according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], and this is adopted by most scholars, contrary to Muhammad. And in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya: the imamate of one who prays voluntarily is not valid. The invalidation as is clear from the beginning of his words and the end where he said: 'For if one imagines in the witnessed case...' So his statement 'the occurrence of the letter is necessary from melodious intonation' is an explanation of something that necessitates that invalidator, which may itself be invalidating, even if one assumes the non-invalidation of the subject by prolonging the hamza of the Majesty or the ba of 'Akbar'. And his statement 'because here it is remembrance in its original wording' etc. is invalid speech, because that is the view of Abu Yusuf, building on it the non-invalidation in cases where a person praying corrects someone other than his imam, or responds to the mu'adhdhin, or says 'La ilaha illa Allah' in response to someone who said 'Is there a god with Allah?', or tells what pleased him and says 'Alhamdulillah', or what amazed him and says 'Subhanallah' with the intention of response, and similar cases, as will come. And the madhhab [position] is invalidation, which is the view of the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], because in the first case it is teaching and learning. In the remaining cases, he has brought the speech out in the form of a response, and it is possible. For the criterion of it being human speech according to the two is that it is a word by which a meaning is conveyed that is not from the actions of prayer, not that it is put to convey that. And the contention that it is not changed by his intention is rejected, as mentioned in al-Fath. He said in al-Nahr: Do you not see that if a junub recites al-Fatiha with the intention of praise, it is permissible? End. And they have mentioned things that invalidate by agreement, such as if there is a book in front of him and there is a man named Yahya, and he says 'Take the book with strength', and similar cases that will come. This refutes the principle of Abu Yusuf. And his statement 'Moreover, analogy after four hundred is discontinued' we affirm its implication, but we do not concede that what the verifier mentioned is of this category; rather, it is an extraction based on what has passed from their principle, as is the practice of the shaykhs like Qadikhan and others in extracting rulings for matters for which there is no text from an apparent principle. Similar is what the author and others mention from their saying 'it should be such' and 'the requirements of the rules are such'.
Source pages p. 637

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, specifically on the issue of imamate. The text discusses two main rulings: first, whether a standing person may validly follow a seated or hunchbacked imam; second, whether raising the voice during prayer (especially in transmission of takbir) invalidates the prayer. The commentary begins by affirming the ruling from the matn that it does not invalidate. It then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: the view of the 'two' (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, or Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?) holds it valid, while Muhammad considers it invalid because it involves the strong (standing) building on the weak (seated). The proof for the majority is the hadith of the Prophet ﷺ leading prayer while seated in his final illness, with the people standing behind him. The commentator explains that this hadith is also used to justify raising the voice for transmission (tabligh) during prayer. However, a lengthy discussion ensues regarding the modern practice of melodious raising of the voice (with elongation and modulation), which the commentator from al-Fath considers invalid because it involves exaggeration, showmanship, and turning away from worship. The commentary then delves into a detailed debate about the criteria for invalidation: whether mere shouting beyond necessity invalidates, or only if it produces extra letters. It cites various authorities including al-Siraj, al-Nahr, and al-Hidayah. The passage also addresses the distinction between sitting and gesturing (ima'), explaining why following a seated imam is valid while following a gesturing imam is not, because standing is not an essential pillar in the same way as bowing and prostration. Finally, the text discusses the hunchbacked imam, noting that if his hump reaches the limit of bowing, there is disagreement among the Hanafi imams. Throughout, the commentary maintains the Hanafi madhhab's internal differences and the relied-upon positions.

Key Terms
قاعد (qaʿid): An imam who sits during prayer due to an excuse
أحدب (aḥdab): An imam with a hunched back, where his back is bent so that his posture resembles bowing

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling when a standing person follows a seated imam who has an excuse in an obligatory prayer?
A) The prayer is invalid (batil)
B) The prayer is valid (sahih)
C) The prayer is valid only if the follower also sits
D) The prayer is invalid unless the imam stands for the first rak'ah

Key Takeaway
A standing person may validly follow a seated imam in obligatory prayer based on the Prophet's practice; Muhammad's objection is outweighed by the stronger textual evidence.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Raising the Voice in Prayer: Tabligh and Excessive Shouting
Commentary on raising voice for tabligh and its invalidating excess.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between permissible tabligh (transmission) and invalidating excessive shouting in prayer according to the Hanafi school, and identify the conditions that render it invalid.

Core Idea
Raising voice for necessary transmission (tabligh) is permissible; excessive, melodious shouting with showmanship invalidates the prayer.

This continuation of the commentary discusses the ruling on raising the voice during prayer, initially linked to the hadith of Abu Bakr transmitting the Prophet's takbir. The author (from al-Fath) sharply criticizes the common practice of elaborate, melodic shouting that goes beyond mere transmission, considering it invalidating because it involves extra letters, showmanship, and turning away from worship. A detailed debate follows on the criteria of invalidation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its basic ruling
Tabligh: raising the voice to transmit the imam's takbir to the congregation. The basic ruling is that it is permissible (ja'iz) and not blameworthy.
The hadith of the Prophet using Abu Bakr as a transmitter is the proof.
2
Distinguish between legitimate and excessive raising
Legitimate: raising just enough for communication. Excessive: raising beyond need, especially with melody (ngam), elongation of hamza or ba', and intention to show off.
The passage considers this excessive practice common in some regions.
3
Analyze the invalidation criteria
The author (and the verifier) argue that excessive shouting (ṣiyāḥ) with melody invalidates the prayer. Some say invalidation occurs only if extra letters are produced (e.g., elongating 'Allah'). Others say the mere act of deliberate melodic shouting invalidates regardless of extra letters.
The debate includes reference to weeping for Paradise vs. weeping for calamity.
4
Apply the tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that excessive shouting with melodious modulation and intention to display one's voice invalidates the prayer. This is the view endorsed by the verifier (al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) and many later scholars.
The objection of al-Hamawi is deemed invalid.
5
Note the exceptions
Simple weeping from fear of Allah does not invalidate; weeping for worldly calamity in one's own language does. Also, the junub reciting Fatiha with intention of praise is permissible.
These examples illustrate the principle that intention matters.
