كتاب الصلاة - باب الإمامة
قوله : (وقائم بقاعد وبأحدب أي لا يفسد اقتداء قائم بقاعد وبأحدب. وأما الأول فهو قولهما، وحكم محمد بالفساد نظراً إلى أنه بناء القوي على الضعيف، ولهما اقتداء الناس بالنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في مرض موته وهو قاعد وهم قيام وهو آخر أحواله، فتعين العمل به بناء على أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان إماماً وأبو بكر مبلغاً للناس تكبيره، وبه استدل على جواز رفع المعنى والمقتدي يعلم فقهقه المقتدي كان عليه إعادة الوضوء عندهما خلافاً لمحمد وزفر بناء على ما مر إلا أنه ينبغي على ما اختاره الشارح أن يبطل الأصل أيضاً إذ الفساد لفقد شرط وهو الطهارة فتأمل اهـ. قوله : (وبه استدل الخ) قال في الفتح وليس مقصوده خصوص الرفع الكائن في زماننا بل أصل الرفع لإبلاغ الانتقالات، أما خصوص هذا الذي تعارفوه في هذه البلاد فلا يبعد أنه مفسد فإنه غالباً يشتمل على مد همزة «الله أكبر» أو بائه وذلك مفسد وإن لم يشتمل لأنهم بالغون في الصياح زيادة على حاجة الإبلاغ والاشتغال بتحريرات النغم إظهاراً للصناعة النغمية لا إقامة للعبادة، والصياح ملحق بالكلام الذي بساطه ذلك الصياح وسيأتي في باب ما يفسد الصلاة أنه إذا ارتفع بكاؤه من ذكر الجنة والنار لا تفسد، والمصيبة بلغته تفسد لأنه في الأول يعرض بسؤال الجنة والتعوذ من النار، إن كان يقال إن المراد إذا حصل به الحروف ولو صرح به لا تفسد. وفي الثاني لإظهارها ولو صرح بها فقال وامصيبتاه أو أدركوني أفسد فهو بمنزلته، وهنا معلوم أن قصده إعجاب الناس به ولو قال اعجبوا من حسن صوتي وتحريري فيه أفسد. وحصول الحرف لازم من التلحين ولا أرى ذلك يصدر ممن فهم الدعاء والسؤال وما ذلك إلا نوع لعب فإنه لو قدر في الشاهد سائل حاجة من ملك أدى سؤاله وطلبه بتحرير النغم فيه من الرفع والخفض والتغريب والرجوع كالتغني نسب البتة إلى قصد السخرية واللعب إذ مقام طلب الحاجة التضرع لا التغني .اهـ وأقره عليه في النهر. وقال العلامة ابن أمير حاج وقد أجاد رحمه الله تعالى فيما أوضح وأفاد اهـ. أقول: في كون الصياح بما هو ذكر ملحقاً بالكلام فيكون مفسداً وإن لم يشتمل على مد همزة «الله» أو باء أكبر» نظر، فقد صرح في السراج بأن الإمام إذا جهر فوق حاجة الناس فقد أساء .اهـ. والإساءة دون الكراهة لا توجب فساداً على أن كلامه يؤول بالآخرة إلى أن الإفساد إنما حصل بحصول الحرف لا بمجرد رفع الصوت زيادة على حاجة الإبلاغ والقياس على ما ارتفع بكاؤه المصيبة بلغته غير ظاهر لأن ما هنا ذكر بصيغته فلا يتغير بعزيمته، والمفسد للصلاة الملفوظ لا عزيمة القلب على ما تقدم بخلاف ارتفاع الصوت بالبكاء المصيبة بلغته فإنه ليس بذكر فيتغير بعزيمته على أن القياس بعد الأربعمائة منقطع فليس لأحد بعدها أن يقيس مسألة على مسألة كما صرح به العلامة زين ابن نجيم في رسائله كذا ذكر السيد أحمد الحموي في رسالته «القول البليغ في حكم التبليغ والله تعالى أعلم. قلت: وبالله التوفيق: الحق ما قاله الإمام المحقق وأقره عليه كثير، وأما ما ذكره السيد الحموي من النظر فهو ساقط لأنه لم يجعل الفساد مبنياً على مجرد الرفع حتى يرد عليه ما في السراج، بل بناه على زيادة الرفع الملحق بالصياح المشتمل على النغم مع قصد إظهاره لذلك والإعراض عن إقامة العبادة وقوله «على أن كلامه الخ» ممنوع لأنه بنی كلامه على أن مبنی الفساد ما مر وإن لم يحصل به حروف زائدة فمجرد ذلك كافٍ في الفساد كما هو صريح أول كلامه وآخره حيث قال فإنه لو قدر في الشاهد الخ» فقوله «وحصول الحرف لازم من التلحين بيان لشيء يستلزمه ذلك المفسد مما قد يكون مفسداً في نفسه، وإن فرض عدم إفساد الملزوم بأن يمد همزة الجلالة أو باء «أكبر». وقوله لأن ما هنا ذكر بصيغته الخ كلام ساقط لأن ذلك قول أبي يوسف بانياً عليه عدم الفساد فيما لو فتح المصلي على غير إمامه أو أجاب المؤذن أو قال لا إله إلا الله جواباً لمن قال أمع الله إله، أو أخبر بما سره فقال الحمد الله، أو بما يعجبه فقال سبحان الله على قصد الجواب ونحو ذلك كما سيأتي، والمذهب الفساد وهو قولهما لأنه تعليم وتعلم في الأولى. وفيما بقي قد أخرج الكلام مخرج الجواب وهو يحتمله فإن مناط كونه من كلام الناس عندهما كونه لفظاً أفيد به معنى ليس من أعمال الصلاة لا كونه وضع لإفادة ذلك، وكونه لم يتغير بعزيمته ممنوع كما ذكره في الفتح. قال في النهر ألا ترى أن الجنب إذا قرأ الفاتحة على قصد الثناء جاز اهـ. وقد ذكروا أشياء تفسد اتفاقاً كما لو كان بين يديه كتاب وعنده رجل اسمه يحيى فقال يا خذ الكتاب بقوة ونحوها مما سيأتي وهذا وارد على أصل أبي يوسف. وقوله «على أن القياس بعد الأربعمائة منقطع الخ نقول بموجبه ولا نسلم أن ما ذكره المحقق من هذا القبيل بل هو : تخريج على ما مر من أصلهما كما هو دأب المشايخ كقاضيخان وأضرابه من تخريجهم ما ليس فيه نص على أصل ظاهر. ومثله ما يذكره المؤلف وغيره من قولهم ينبغي أن يكون كذا ومقتضى القواعد كذا، فلو
المؤذنين أصواتهم في الجمعة والعيدين وغيرهما كما في المجتبى، وليس هو بناء القوي على الضعيف لأن القعود قيام من وجه كالركوع لانتصاب أحد نصفيه وصار كالاقتداء بالمنحني من الهرم، ولا يرد عليه الإيماء فإنه بعض الركوع والسجود ومع . اقتداء ذلك فلم يصح الراكع والساجد بالمومي لوجهين: أحدهما أن القيام ليس بركن مقصود ولهذا جاز تركه في النفل من غير عذر فجاز أن يسد الناقص مسده لعدم فوات المقصود فكان حال الإمام مثل حال المقتدي في المقصود وهو نهاية التعبد بخلاف الركوع والسجود فإنهما ركنان مقصودان وقد فاتا في حق الإمام المومي، ولأن القعود يسمى قياماً. يقال لمن قعد ناهضاً عن نومه قام عن فراشه وقام عن مضجعه ويقال للمضطجع قم واقرأ فإذا نهض وقعد يكون ممتثلاً لأمره بالقيام بخلاف الإيماء فإنه لا يسمى سجوداً. وذكر في المجتبى فرقاً إجمالياً وهو يتخير بين القيام والقعود ولا يتخير بين الإيماء والسجود ولا بين القعود والاستلقاء. وفي الحقائق : الخلاف في قاعد يركع ويسجد لأنه لو كان يومىء والقوم يركعون ويسجدون لا يجوز اتفاقاً. ومحل الاختلاف الاقتداء في الفرض والواجب حيث كان للإمام عذر، أما في النفل فيجوز اتفاقاً واختلف في اقتداء القائم بالقاعد في التراويح والأصح أنه جائز عند الكل كما في فتاوى قاضيخان وأما الثاني وهو اقتداء القائم بالأحدب فأطلقه فشمل ما إذا بلغ حدبه حد الركوع وما إذا لم يبلغ ولا خلاف في الثاني واختلفوا في الأول؛ ففي المجتبى أنه جائز عندهما وبه أخذ عامة العلماء خلافاً لمحمد وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية : لا تصح إمامة أن المتنفل الفساد كما هو صريح أول كلامه وآخره حيث قال فإنه لو قدر في الشاهد الخ» فقوله «وحصول الحرف لازم من التلحين بيان لشيء يستلزمه ذلك المفسد مما قد يكون مفسداً في نفسه، وإن فرض عدم إفساد الملزوم بأن يمد همزة الجلالة أو باء «أكبر». وقوله لأن ما هنا ذكر بصيغته الخ كلام ساقط لأن ذلك قول أبي يوسف بانياً عليه عدم الفساد فيما لو فتح المصلي على غير إمامه أو أجاب المؤذن أو قال لا إله إلا الله جواباً لمن قال أمع الله إله، أو أخبر بما سره فقال الحمد الله، أو بما يعجبه فقال سبحان الله على قصد الجواب ونحو ذلك كما سيأتي، والمذهب الفساد وهو قولهما لأنه تعليم وتعلم في الأولى. وفيما بقي قد أخرج الكلام مخرج الجواب وهو يحتمله فإن مناط كونه من كلام الناس عندهما كونه لفظاً أفيد به معنى ليس من أعمال الصلاة لا كونه وضع لإفادة ذلك، وكونه لم يتغير بعزيمته ممنوع كما ذكره في الفتح. قال في النهر ألا ترى أن الجنب إذا قرأ الفاتحة على قصد الثناء جاز اهـ. وقد ذكروا أشياء تفسد اتفاقاً كما لو كان بين يديه كتاب وعنده رجل اسمه يحيى فقال يا خذ الكتاب بقوة ونحوها مما سيأتي وهذا وارد على أصل أبي يوسف. وقوله «على أن القياس بعد الأربعمائة منقطع الخ نقول بموجبه ولا نسلم أن ما ذكره المحقق من هذا القبيل بل هو : تخريج على ما مر من أصلهما كما هو دأب المشايخ كقاضيخان وأضرابه من تخريجهم ما ليس فيه نص على أصل ظاهر. ومثله ما يذكره المؤلف وغيره من قولهم ينبغي أن يكون كذا ومقتضى القواعد كذا، فلو
The Book of Prayer - Chapter of Imamate. His saying: (And a standing person behind a seated one and behind a hunchbacked one) meaning that the following of a standing person behind a seated one and behind a hunchbacked one does not invalidate [the prayer]. As for the first [case, standing behind seated], it is the view of the two [Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf?], and Muhammad ruled it invalid, considering that it is building the strong upon the weak. And for the two [there is the proof of] the people following the Prophet ﷺ during his fatal illness when he was seated and they were standing, and it was his last state; so acting upon it is determined, based on the fact that he ﷺ was the imam and Abu Bakr was communicating his takbir to the people. And by this they argued for the permissibility of raising the meaning... And if the follower knows [the intention?] and laughs, then according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?] he must repeat wudu, contrary to Muhammad and Zufar, based on what has passed, except that according to the preference of the commentator, the original [prayer] should also be invalidated, because the corruption is due to the loss of a condition, which is purification, so consider. End. His saying: (And by it they argued) etc. He said in al-Fath: His intention is not specifically the raising that occurs in our time, but rather the principle of raising for communicating the transitions. As for this particular practice that has become customary in these lands, it is not unlikely that it is invalidating, because it often includes prolonging the hamza of 'Allahu Akbar' or its ba', and that is invalidating even if it does not include them, because they exceed in shouting beyond the need for communication and occupy themselves with modulating melodies, displaying musical craftsmanship, not performing worship. Shouting is annexed to speech whose essence is that shouting. And it will come in the chapter on what invalidates prayer that if his weeping due to remembrance of Paradise and Hell rises, it does not invalidate, but if it is due to a calamity in his language, it invalidates, because in the first case he is asking for Paradise and seeking refuge from Hell. It is said that the intention is if letters are produced, even if explicitly stated, it does not invalidate. In the second, for showing it, even if he says 'Oh my calamity' or 'Help me', it invalidates, so it is like that. And here it is known that his intention is to impress people; if he said 'Be amazed at the beauty of my voice and my modulation', it invalidates. The occurrence of the letter is necessary from melodious intonation, and I do not see that issuing from one who understands supplication and request; it is nothing but a type of play. For if one imagines a supplicant in the presence of a king, he would perform his request and plea with modulation of tone, raising, lowering, orientalizing, and returning, like singing, he would be absolutely attributed to the intention of mockery and play, because the station of requesting a need is humility, not singing. End. And he [al-Marghinani] endorsed it in al-Nahr. And Allama Ibn Amir Haj said: He has done well, may Allah have mercy on him, in what he clarified and benefited. End. I say: Regarding the view that shouting, being remembrance, is annexed to speech and thus invalidates even if it does not include prolonging the hamza of 'Allah' or the ba of 'Akbar', there is consideration. For it is stated in al-Siraj that if the imam raises his voice beyond the people's need, he has done wrong. End. And wrongdoing is less than dislike, so it does not necessitate invalidation. However, his words ultimately lead to the fact that invalidation only occurs through the occurrence of the letter, not merely by raising the voice beyond the need for communication. And analogy with one whose weeping due to a calamity in his language rises is not apparent, because here it is remembrance in its original wording, so it is not changed by his intention, whereas the invalidator of prayer is the uttered word, not the intention of the heart, as has preceded. In contrast, the raising of voice in weeping for a calamity in his language is not remembrance, so it is changed by his intention. Moreover, analogy after four hundred [years] is discontinued, so no one after that may analogize one case to another, as stated by Allama Zayn ibn Nujaym in his treatises. Thus mentioned sayyid Ahmad al-Hamawi in his treatise 'al-Qawl al-Baligh fi Hukm al-Tabligh'. And Allah Almighty knows best. I say: And by Allah is success: The truth is what the verifying imam said and many agreed with him. As for what sayyid al-Hamawi mentioned of consideration, it is invalid, because he did not base invalidation on mere raising so that what is in al-Siraj would refute it; rather, he based it on the excessive raising annexed to shouting that includes melodies, with the intention of showing off and turning away from performing worship. And his statement 'Nevertheless, his words...' is rejected because he built his words on the basis that the foundation of invalidation is what has passed, even if no extra letters result from it; so that alone is sufficient for invalidation, as is clear from the beginning and end of his words where he said: 'For if one imagines in the witnessed case...' So his statement 'The occurrence of the letter is necessary from melodious intonation' is an explanation of something that necessitates that invalidator, which may itself be invalidating, even if one assumes the non-invalidation of the subject by prolonging the hamza of the Majesty or the ba of 'Akbar'. And his statement 'because here it is remembrance in its original wording' etc. is invalid speech, because that is the view of Abu Yusuf, building on it the non-invalidation in cases where a person praying corrects someone other than his imam, or responds to the mu'adhdhin, or says 'La ilaha illa Allah' in response to someone who said 'Is there a god with Allah?', or tells what pleased him and says 'Alhamdulillah', or what amazed him and says 'Subhanallah' with the intention of response, and similar cases, as will come. And the madhhab [position] is invalidation, which is the view of the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], because in the first case it is teaching and learning. In the remaining cases, he has brought the speech out in the form of a response, and it is possible. For the criterion of it being human speech according to the two is that it is a word by which a meaning is conveyed that is not from the actions of prayer, not that it is put to convey that. And the contention that it is not changed by his intention is rejected, as mentioned in al-Fath. He said in al-Nahr: Do you not see that a junub if he recites al-Fatiha with the intention of praise, it is permissible? End. And they have mentioned things that invalidate by agreement, such as if there is a book in front of him and there is a man named Yahya, and he says 'Take the book with strength', and similar cases that will come. This refutes the principle of Abu Yusuf. And his statement 'Moreover, analogy after four hundred is discontinued' we affirm its implication, but we do not concede that what the verifier mentioned is of this category; rather, it is an extraction based on what has passed from their principle, as is the practice of the shaykhs like Qadikhan and others in extracting rulings for matters for which there is no text from an apparent principle. Similar is what the author and others mention from their saying 'it should be such' and 'the requirements of the rules are such'. So if... the mu'adhdhinin raise their voices on Friday and the two Eids and other occasions, as in al-Mujtaba. And it is not building the strong upon the weak, because sitting is a kind of standing in one respect, like bowing due to the uprightness of one of its halves, and it becomes like following one bent from old age. And the gesturing is not analogous, because it is part of bowing and prostration. And the following of the one who bows and prostrates behind one who gestures is not valid for two reasons: First, standing is not an essential pillar, and for this reason it is permissible to omit it in voluntary prayers without excuse; so it is permissible for the lesser to take the place of the greater because the purpose is not lost. Thus the situation of the imam is like that of the follower regarding the purpose, which is the ultimate worship, unlike bowing and prostration, for they are two essential pillars and they are lost in the case of the imam who gestures. Second, sitting is called standing: it is said to one who sits after rising from sleep 'he stood from his bed' and 'he stood from his sleeping place', and to the one lying down it is said 'stand up and read', so if he rises and sits, he complies with the command to stand, unlike gesturing, for it is not called prostration. And in al-Mujtaba, a general difference is mentioned: he has a choice between standing and sitting, but he does not have a choice between gesturing and prostrating, nor between sitting and lying down. And in al-Haqa'iq: the dispute is about a seated person who bows and prostrates [normally], because if he gestures and the people bow and prostrate, it is not valid by agreement. And the place of disagreement is in obligatory and necessary prayers when the imam has an excuse. As for voluntary prayers, it is valid by agreement. And there is disagreement about a standing person following a seated one in tarawih; the most correct view is that it is permissible according to all, as in Fatawa Qadikhan. As for the second [case, i.e., following a hunchbacked imam], he [the author] has left it open, so it includes both when his hump reaches the limit of bowing and when it does not. There is no disagreement in the second case, and they disagree in the first: in al-Mujtaba it is permissible according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], and this is adopted by most scholars, contrary to Muhammad. And in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya: the imamate of one who prays voluntarily is not valid. The invalidation as is clear from the beginning of his words and the end where he said: 'For if one imagines in the witnessed case...' So his statement 'the occurrence of the letter is necessary from melodious intonation' is an explanation of something that necessitates that invalidator, which may itself be invalidating, even if one assumes the non-invalidation of the subject by prolonging the hamza of the Majesty or the ba of 'Akbar'. And his statement 'because here it is remembrance in its original wording' etc. is invalid speech, because that is the view of Abu Yusuf, building on it the non-invalidation in cases where a person praying corrects someone other than his imam, or responds to the mu'adhdhin, or says 'La ilaha illa Allah' in response to someone who said 'Is there a god with Allah?', or tells what pleased him and says 'Alhamdulillah', or what amazed him and says 'Subhanallah' with the intention of response, and similar cases, as will come. And the madhhab [position] is invalidation, which is the view of the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], because in the first case it is teaching and learning. In the remaining cases, he has brought the speech out in the form of a response, and it is possible. For the criterion of it being human speech according to the two is that it is a word by which a meaning is conveyed that is not from the actions of prayer, not that it is put to convey that. And the contention that it is not changed by his intention is rejected, as mentioned in al-Fath. He said in al-Nahr: Do you not see that if a junub recites al-Fatiha with the intention of praise, it is permissible? End. And they have mentioned things that invalidate by agreement, such as if there is a book in front of him and there is a man named Yahya, and he says 'Take the book with strength', and similar cases that will come. This refutes the principle of Abu Yusuf. And his statement 'Moreover, analogy after four hundred is discontinued' we affirm its implication, but we do not concede that what the verifier mentioned is of this category; rather, it is an extraction based on what has passed from their principle, as is the practice of the shaykhs like Qadikhan and others in extracting rulings for matters for which there is no text from an apparent principle. Similar is what the author and others mention from their saying 'it should be such' and 'the requirements of the rules are such'.
Source pages p. 637

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, specifically on the issue of imamate. The text discusses two main rulings: first, whether a standing person may validly follow a seated or hunchbacked imam; second, whether raising the voice during prayer (especially in transmission of takbir) invalidates the prayer. The commentary begins by affirming the ruling from the matn that it does not invalidate. It then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: the view of the 'two' (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, or Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?) holds it valid, while Muhammad considers it invalid because it involves the strong (standing) building on the weak (seated). The proof for the majority is the hadith of the Prophet ﷺ leading prayer while seated in his final illness, with the people standing behind him. The commentator explains that this hadith is also used to justify raising the voice for transmission (tabligh) during prayer. However, a lengthy discussion ensues regarding the modern practice of melodious raising of the voice (with elongation and modulation), which the commentator from al-Fath considers invalid because it involves exaggeration, showmanship, and turning away from worship. The commentary then delves into a detailed debate about the criteria for invalidation: whether mere shouting beyond necessity invalidates, or only if it produces extra letters. It cites various authorities including al-Siraj, al-Nahr, and al-Hidayah. The passage also addresses the distinction between sitting and gesturing (ima'), explaining why following a seated imam is valid while following a gesturing imam is not, because standing is not an essential pillar in the same way as bowing and prostration. Finally, the text discusses the hunchbacked imam, noting that if his hump reaches the limit of bowing, there is disagreement among the Hanafi imams. Throughout, the commentary maintains the Hanafi madhhab's internal differences and the relied-upon positions.

Key Terms
صياح (ṣiyāḥ): Loud shouting or raising the voice beyond need, often with melodic modulation, during prayer
تبليغ (tablīgh): The act of transmitting the imam's takbir to the congregation when the imam's voice is faint
مد (madd): Prolonging a letter, e.g., the hamza of 'Allah' or the ba of 'Akbar', which produces an extra letter (harf) that invalidates prayer if done deliberately
نغم (naḡam): Melodic modulation of the voice, often like singing; during prayer it turns worship into performance

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling if a person in prayer melodiously prolongs the hamza of 'Allahu Akbar' to an excessive degree, intending to display his voice?
A) The prayer is valid but makruh tanzihi
B) The prayer is invalid (mufsid) and must be repeated
C) The prayer is valid and the act is sunnah
D) The prayer is invalid only if the imam does it, not the follower

Key Takeaway
Excessive, melodious shouting in prayer with the intention to show off invalidates the prayer, while necessary tabligh for transmission is permissible.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Ruling of a Standing Person Praying Behind a Sitting Person (Qa'id)
Establishes permissibility of qaim behind qaid with proofs and exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a standing person (qaim) praying behind a sitting imam (qa'id) and distinguish the conditions for obligatory and supererogatory prayers.

Core Idea
A standing person can follow a sitting imam who bows and prostrates, because sitting is linguistically and legally akin to standing.

This lesson explores a nuanced Hanafi ruling: when can a healthy, standing worshipper follow an imam who is sitting? The source text from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides proofs from language and legal reasoning, clarifying that the key is the imam's ability to bow and prostrate normally. Understanding this ruling prevents unnecessary invalidation of congregational prayers when the imam has a valid excuse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is a standing person (qaim) following a sitting imam (qa'id). The ruling is that it is valid (jaiz) under specific conditions.
The imam must be able to bow and prostrate normally; he is qa'id, not muumi.
2
Understand the objection and the Hanafi response
The text first refutes the objection that this would be 'building the strong upon the weak'. The Hanafi response: sitting is a form of standing because the upper body is erect, similar to bowing.
This is based on istihsan and linguistic usage.
3
Analyze the proofs (dalil)
Two proofs are given: (1) Standing is not an essential pillar in itself, so a sitting imam can substitute; (2) Linguistically, 'qama' (stood) applies to one who sits up from sleep, so a sitting person fulfills the command to stand.
Contrast with muumi (gesturing) where bowing and prostration are essential and therefore absent.
4
Identify the scope of the ruling
The ruling applies to obligatory (fard/wajib) prayers only when the imam has an excuse. For supererogatory (nafl) prayers, it is valid without any excuse by consensus.
Taraweeh is specifically mentioned as permissible by all scholars.
5
Apply the ruling to a modern scenario
Consider an imam with a leg injury who leads 'Isha prayer sitting but can bow and prostrate. Is it valid for you to follow him? Yes, if he has an excuse.
If the imam cannot bow/prostrate and only gestures, it is not valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس هو بناء القوي على الضعيف لأن القعود قيام من وجه كالركوع لانتصاب أحد نصفيه وصار كالاقتداء بالمنحني من الهرم، ولا يرد عليه الإيماء فإنه بعض الركوع والسجود ومع . اقتداء ذلك فلم يصح الراكع والساجد بالمومي لوجهين: أحدهما أن القيام ليس بركن مقصود ولهذا جاز تركه في النفل من غير عذر فجاز أن يسد الناقص مسده لعدم فوات المقصود فكان حال الإمام مثل حال المقتدي في المقصود وهو نهاية التعبد بخلاف الركوع والسجود فإنهما ركنان مقصودان وقد فاتا في حق الإمام المومي، ولأن القعود يسمى قياماً. يقال لمن قعد ناهضاً عن نومه قام عن فراشه وقام عن مضجعه ويقال للمضطجع قم واقرأ فإذا نهض وقعد يكون ممتثلاً لأمره بالقيام بخلاف الإيماء فإنه لا يسمى سجوداً. وذكر في المجتبى فرقاً إجمالياً وهو يتخير بين القيام والقعود ولا يتخير بين الإيماء والسجود ولا بين القعود والاستلقاء. وفي الحقائق : الخلاف في قاعد يركع ويسجد لأنه لو كان يومىء والقوم يركعون ويسجدون لا يجوز اتفاقاً. ومحل الاختلاف الاقتداء في الفرض والواجب حيث كان للإمام عذر، أما في النفل فيجوز اتفاقاً واختلف في اقتداء القائم بالقاعد في التراويح والأصح أنه جائز عند الكل كما في فتاوى قاضيخان
And it is not a building of the strong upon the weak because sitting is a kind of standing, like bowing, due to the erection of one of its halves, and it becomes like the following of one who leans due to old age. And gesturing (ima') is not similar because it is part of bowing and prostration. And following that, it is not valid for one who bows and prostrates to follow one who gestures for two reasons: one, that standing is not an intended pillar, thus it is permissible to leave it in supererogatory prayer without excuse, so the deficient can take its place due to lack of loss of the intended; so the case of the imam is like that of the follower in the intended, which is the ultimate worship, unlike bowing and prostration which are two intended pillars and are missed in the right of the imam who gestures. And because sitting is called standing: it is said to one who sits after waking from sleep 'he stood from his bed', and to one who is lying down 'stand and read', so when he rises and sits he is complying with the command to stand, unlike gesturing which is not called prostration. And it is mentioned in al-Mujtaba a general distinction: he may choose between standing and sitting, but cannot choose between gesturing and prostration, nor between sitting and lying down. And in al-Haqa'iq: the disagreement is about one who sits and bows and prostrates, because if he gestures and the people bow and prostrate, it is not valid by agreement. And the locus of disagreement is following in obligatory and necessary prayers when the imam has an excuse; as for supererogatory, it is valid by agreement. And there is disagreement about a standing person following a sitting person in taraweeh; the correct view is that it is permissible according to all, as in Fatawa Qadikhan.
Source pages p. 638

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion probe on the ruling of a standing person (qaim) praying behind a sitting person (qa'id) who can bow and prostrate. The author first refutes the objection that this would be building the strong upon the weak by arguing that sitting is a form of standing, as the upper body is erect. He then contrasts this with the case of an imam who only gestures (muumi), which is invalid because bowing and prostration are essential pillars. Two proofs are given: (1) standing is not an inherently required pillar, so it can be substituted, unlike bowing and prostration; (2) the Arabic language uses 'qama' (stood) for one who sits up, so a sitting person is fulfilling the command to stand. The passage further clarifies that the disagreement only applies to obligatory and necessary prayers when the imam has an excuse; for supererogatory prayers, it is unanimously valid. Regarding taraweeh, the relied-upon position is that it is permissible by all scholars.

Key Terms
قاعد (qa'id): A person who sits during prayer but can still bow and prostrate normally.
مومئ (muumi): A person who gestures with head for bowing and prostration due to inability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, can a standing person (qaim) pray behind a sitting person (qa'id) who bows and prostrates normally?
A) No, it is invalid because the imam is weak.
B) Yes, but only in supererogatory prayers.
C) Yes, for obligatory prayers if the imam has an excuse, and for all supererogatory prayers.
D) Yes, unconditionally for all prayers.

Key Takeaway
A standing person may validly follow a sitting imam who can bow and prostrate, provided for obligatory prayers the imam has an excuse; for supererogatory prayers it is always valid.

The Bent-Over Imam: Standing Behind an Ahdab
Intra-Hanafi dispute on imamate of the bent-over

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a standing person following an imam who is bent over (ahdab), identify the relied-upon view, and apply the analogy (qiyas) used by the majority.

Core Idea
A bent-over imam is not inferior to a sitting imam – the Hanafi majority permits him to lead the standing.

The imamate is a central element of congregational prayer, but what if the imam has a severe curvature of the spine (ahdab) that makes his body nearly horizontal? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on this point grounded in an insightful analogy. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the positions of the three leading Hanafi imams and the operative ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage distinguishes between two cases: the bent-over imam whose bend does NOT reach bowing level (valid by consensus) and the one whose bend DOES reach bowing level (disputed).
2
Note the consensus on the non‑reaching case
When the bend is less than the bowing position, the imamate is valid without disagreement.
3
Locate the intra‑Hanafi ikhtilaf
When the bend reaches bowing level, the majority (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al‑Shaybani, and most scholars) hold it permissible; Muhammad ibn al‑Hasan alone considers it invalid.
The dispute is between the Sahibayn and Imam Muhammad.
4
Analyze the analogy (qiyas) used by the majority
The majority draw an analogy with a sitting imam: a sitting imam has his upper half erect, while a bent‑over imam has his lower half erect. Neither is fully erect, but the sitting imam is considered valid by consensus. Therefore, the bent‑over imam is no worse and also valid.
The analogy is based on erectness of different body parts.
5
Determine the mufta bihi view
The commentary declares the majority view (permissibility) as the correct one, and it is adopted for fatwa.
Later works occasionally report the contrary, but the first is stronger.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الثاني وهو اقتداء القائم بالأحدب فأطلقه فشمل ما إذا بلغ حدبه حد الركوع وما إذا لم يبلغ ولا خلاف في الثاني واختلفوا في الأول؛ ففي المجتبى أنه جائز عندهما وبه أخذ عامة العلماء خلافاً لمحمد وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية : لا تصح إمامة الأحدب للقائم. هكذا ذكر محمد في مجموع النوازل. وقيل يجوز والأول أصح اهـ. ولا يخفى ضعفه فإنه ليس أدنى حالاً القاعد لأن القعود استواء النصف الأعلى وفي الحدب استواء النصف الأسفل، ويمكن أن يحمل على قول محمد وأشار إلى أن اقتداء القاعد خلف مثله جائز اتفاقاً، وكذا الاقتداء بالأعرج أو من بقدمه عوج وإن كان غيره أولى.
As for the second, which is the standing person following the one who is bent over, he (the author) left it unrestricted, so it includes whether his bend reaches the limit of bowing or not. There is no disagreement in the second case (if it does not reach the limit), but they disagreed in the first case. According to al-Mujtaba, it is permissible according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and most scholars adopted that, contrary to Muhammad (alone). In al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya: the imamate of the bent over for the standing is not valid. Thus mentioned Muhammad in Majmu' al-Nawazil. And it was said it is permissible, and the first is more correct. And its weakness is not hidden, because he (the bent over) is not less in condition than the sitting person, since sitting involves erectness of the upper half, while in bending it is the erectness of the lower half. And it can be interpreted as the opinion of Muhammad. And it indicated that a sitting person following another sitting person is permissible by agreement, and likewise the following of a lame person or one with a crooked foot, although another (imam) is better.
Source pages p. 638

Commentary
This passage addresses the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a standing person following an imam who is bent over (ahdab). The ruling depends on the degree of bend: if it does not reach the bowing limit, it is valid by consensus. If it does, there is disagreement: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) deem it permissible, and most scholars follow this, while Muhammad alone holds it impermissible. The author then notes that some later works (al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya) declare it invalid, but the first view (permission) is more correct. The commentary adds that the bent over person is not worse off than a sitting person, since sitting has the upper half erect while bending has the lower half erect, and draws analogy to the permissibility of a sitting person following another sitting person. Additionally, the ruling is extended to a lame person or one with a crooked foot, with the remark that another imam is preferable.

Key Terms
أحدب (ahdab): A person who is bent over, with a hump or curvature, such that his body may reach bowing level.
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following an imam in prayer; the act of the ma'mum (follower) performing prayer behind an imam.
إمامة (imamah): The leadership of prayer; the status and role of the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, can a standing person pray behind an imam who is bent over to the extent of bowing?
A) No, it is invalid.
B) Yes, it is permissible.
C) Only if the imam is also standing.
D) Only in supererogatory prayers.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi majority permits a standing person to follow a bent-over imam (ahdab) even when the bend reaches bowing level, based on analogy with a sitting imam; this is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Ruling of a Pedestrian Praying Behind a Rider
States the ruling that a pedestrian cannot pray behind a rider in normal circumstances.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a pedestrian following a rider in prayer and identify the exception when both are on the same animal.

Core Idea
A pedestrian cannot follow a rider in prayer; both must be on the same mount.

You may have seen people praying in congregation while traveling, some on foot and some on animals. Is it valid for a person on foot to follow a rider? This lesson from the Khulasa states the Hanafi position clearly: it is not permissible unless all followers are on the same animal. Understanding this rule helps maintain the proper performance of congregational prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is being ruled? A pedestrian (nazil) following a rider (rakib) in prayer. The ruling: not permissible (la yajuz).
2
Identify the exception
When is it allowed? When the followers are on the same animal as the imam.
If they pray on an animal collectively, the imam and those on his animal are valid; others (on foot) are not.
3
Note the authority
This is the position in the zahir al-riwayah (apparent narration), i.e., the relied-upon view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخلاصة: ولا يجوز اقتداء النازل بالراكب ولو صلوا على الدابة بجماعة جازت صلاة الإمام كان ومن معه على دابته ولا تجوز صلاة غيره في ظاهر الرواية .
And in al-Khulasa: It is not permissible for a pedestrian to follow a rider. If they pray on an animal collectively, the prayer of the imam is valid, and those with him on his animal, but the prayer of others (on foot) is not valid in the apparent narration.
Source pages p. 639

Commentary
This is a concise ruling from the Khulasa: a person on foot (nazil) cannot follow a rider (rakib) in prayer, due to the disparity in ability to perform movements. However, if all are riding the same animal and form a congregation, the imam's prayer and that of the followers on the same animal are valid, but those on foot may not join. This is the position in the zahir al-riwayah.

Key Terms
نازل (nazil): A person on foot, not riding.
راكب (rakib): A person riding an animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Yes, it is valid.
B) No, it is not permissible.
C) Only in traveling.
D) Only if the rider is on the ground.

Key Takeaway
A pedestrian cannot follow a rider in prayer; the only exception is when the follower is on the same mount.

Ruling of a Voluntary Prayer Behind an Obligatory Prayer
Explains the permissibility of nafl behind fard with reasoning and dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mutanaffil following a muftarid, explain the proof (building weak upon strong), and evaluate the intra-Hanafi disagreement reported by Qadikhan.

Core Idea
A nafl prayer behind a fard imam is valid – the weak is built upon the strong.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a common scenario: a person performing a supererogatory prayer (nafl) wishes to join a congregation led by an imam performing an obligatory prayer (fard). The matn rules that this is valid, based on a key Hanafi principle. However, an intra-school dispute exists, as later noted by Qadikhan. We will unpack the ruling, its proof, and the nuances of the disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Find the direct statement in the matn: 'لا يفسد اقتداء متنفل بمفترض' – it does not invalidate a nafl follower behind a fard imam. This establishes permissibility.
The matn is clear; the ruling is that the act is valid (sahih).
2
Understand the Proof: Building Weak on Strong
The author gives two proofs: (1) 'بناء الضعيف على القوي' – building the weak (nafl) upon the strong (fard) is sound. (2) Recitation obligations change: in nafl, recitation in the last two rak'ahs is normally obligatory (fard), but when following an imam, the follower is prohibited from reciting, so recitation becomes voluntary (nafl) for him as well.
The second proof relies on the Hanafi rule that the follower does not recite behind the imam.
3
Scope of the Ruling
The passage says 'أطلقه فشمل' – the ruling is unrestricted, so it includes any nafl, such as taraweeh prayer following the fard imam.
This reinforces the generality of the principle.
4
Analyse the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
The author notes that Qadikhan reported a difference: some later Hanafis deemed it impermissible. The author finds this problematic because it contradicts the 'building weak on strong' principle. Understand the tension between the clear matn and the later fatwa.
This shows that even within the Hanafi school, later scholars sometimes differ from the early texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ومتنفل بمفترض أي لا يفسد اقتداء متنفل بمفترض لأنه بناء الضعيف على القوي، والقراءة في النفل وإن كانت فرضاً في الأخيرتين نفلاً في الفرض لكن إنما تكون فرضاً إذا كان المصلي منفرداً، أما إذا كان مقتدياً ،فلا لأنها محظورة كذا في الغاية. ولأنه بالاقتداء صار تبعاً للإمام في القراءة فكانت نفلاً فيهما في حقه كإمامه . أطلقه فشمل اقتداء من يصلي التراويح بالمكتوبة، وذكر في فتاوى قاضيخان اختلافاً وأن الصحيح عدم الجواز وهو مشكل فإنه بناء
His saying: 'And a voluntary prayer follower behind an obligatory prayer' means that it does not invalidate the following of a voluntary prayer behind an obligatory prayer because it is building the weak upon the strong. And recitation in supererogatory prayer, even though it is obligatory in the last two rak'ahs in obligatory prayer, it is only obligatory if the worshipper is alone; but if he is following, it is not, because it is prohibited (to recite behind the imam). And because by following, he becomes a follower in recitation, so it becomes voluntary in both rak'ahs in his right like his imam. He left it unrestricted, so it includes one performing taraweeh following an obligatory prayer. And it is mentioned in Fatawa Qadikhan that there is a difference and that the correct view is impermissibility, and it is problematic because it is building...
Source pages p. 639

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling that a person performing a supererogatory prayer (nafl) can validly follow an imam performing an obligatory prayer (fard). The reasoning is that this is building the weak upon the strong. Although recitation in nafl is normally obligatory in the last two rak'ahs for a single worshipper, when following an imam, the follower is prohibited from reciting, and he becomes a follower in recitation, making it nafl for him as well. The ruling is general and includes taraweeh. However, the author notes that Qadikhan mentioned a disagreement and that the correct view is impermissibility, which is problematic because it involves building the weak upon the strong. The text cuts off, but the main point is that the prevalent Hanafi view allows nafl behind fard.

Key Terms
متنفل (mutanaffil): A person performing a supererogatory (nafl) prayer.
مفترض (muftarid): A person performing an obligatory (fard) prayer.
بناء الضعيف على القوي (binā' al-ḍa'īf 'alā al-qawī): A legal principle meaning 'building the weak upon the strong', used to justify the validity of a less emphasized act when attached to a more emphasized one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq), can a person praying nafl follow an imam praying fard?
A) No, it is invalid.
B) Yes, it is valid.
C) Only in taraweeh.
D) Only if the imam is also nafl.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a voluntary prayer behind an obligatory prayer is valid because the weaker act is built upon the stronger one, though an intra-school disagreement exists.

Ruling on a Hunchbacked Person Leading a Standing Person: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains the ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on an akhdab leading a qa'im

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on a hunchbacked person leading a standing person and evaluate the tarjih based on the commentator's reasoning.

Core Idea
A hunchbacked person is not lower than a sitting person; thus the two shaykhs permit his leading a standing person, but Muhammad rejects it.

In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of an imam's posture relative to the followers is carefully regulated. This lesson examines a specific intra-madhhab dispute: can a hunchbacked person (akhdab) lead a standing person in prayer? Imam Muhammad reports it as invalid, but the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) allow it. The commentator Ibn Nujaym weighs the arguments, ultimately weakening the tarjih towards Muhammad's view and leaning to the two shaykhs.

Guided Path
1
State the factual scenario
Identify the two persons: al-akhdab (hunchbacked) as imam and al-qa'im (standing) as follower. The question is whether the imamah is valid.
The akhdab's posture is bent forward, but he is not completely unable to stand.
2
Identify the two positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that it is valid; Imam Muhammad holds it is invalid. The base text (matn) mentions Muhammad's view first.
Muhammad's view is recorded in his Majmu' al-Nawazil.
3
Follow the commentator's critique
Ibn Nujaym critiques the preference for Muhammad's view, arguing that the akhdab is not in a lower state than a sitting person (qa'id). He explains that sitting involves straightening the upper half, while hunchbackedness involves straightening the lower half.
The commentator says 'ولا يخفى ضعفه' (its weakness is not hidden).
4
Apply the analogy
If a sitting person can lead another sitting person by agreement, then by analogy an akhdab should be able to lead a standing person, because his posture is comparable to sitting.
This analogical reasoning (qiyas) supports the two shaykhs' view.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Despite the text initially saying 'الأول أصح' (the first is more correct), the commentator's critique shows its weakness. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the view of the two shaykhs, i.e., validity, though some later Hanafis follow Muhammad.
Authority weight: nawadir (from Muhammad's collection), but tarjih favors the two shaykhs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بقاعد وبأحدب بمثله ومتنفل بمفترض وإن ظهر أن إمامه محدث أعاد وأن اقتدى وموم الأحدب للقائم. هكذا ذكر محمد في مجموع النوازل. وقيل يجوز والأول أصح اهـ. ولا يخفى ضعفه فإنه ليس أدنى حالاً القاعد لأن القعود استواء النصف الأعلى وفي الحدب استواء النصف الأسفل، ويمكن أن يحمل على قول محمد وأشار إلى أن اقتداء القاعد خلف مثله جائز اتفاقاً، وكذا الاقتداء بالأعرج أو من بقدمه عوج وإن كان غيره أولى.
And [the ruling on] a sitting person and a hunchbacked person with his like, and a supererogatory performer with an obligatory performer, and if it becomes apparent that his imam is in a state of hadath, he repeats; and the following of a hunchbacked person for a standing person. Thus Muhammad mentioned in Majmu' al-Nawazil. And it was said that it is permissible, and the first is more correct. And its weakness is not hidden because he is not in a lower state than the sitting person, for sitting is the straightening of the upper half, and in hunchbackedness the straightening of the lower half. And it can be carried upon the saying of Muhammad. And he indicated that the following of a sitting person behind his like is permissible by agreement, and likewise the following of a lame person or one whose foot has a curvature, even if someone else is preferable.
Source pages p. 639

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of a ruling and an intra-Hanafi dispute. It begins with the matn (base text) listing several rulings: the permissibility of a sitting person following another sitting person, a hunchbacked person following his like, a supererogatory prayer following an obligatory prayer, and the case of discovering the imam's hadath. The commentary then specifically addresses the ruling of a hunchbacked person (الأحدب) leading a standing person (القائم). Imam Muhammad reports in his Majmu' al-Nawazil that such leadership is not permissible. Another view says it is permissible, but the first view is considered more correct (الأول أصح). The commentator then critiques this, noting that the hunchbacked person is not in a lower state than a sitting person, because sitting involves straightening the upper half while hunchbackedness involves straightening the lower half. The commentator suggests that the ruling of correctness might be attributed to Muhammad's view alone, and that there is agreement that a sitting person may follow another sitting person. The ruling for a lame person or one with a foot curvature is similar, though another person is preferable.

Key Terms
الأحدب (al-akhdab): A person with a hunchback (curvature of the spine) that makes his upper body bent forward.
القاعد (al-qa'id): A person who sits during prayer due to inability or license.
القائم (al-qa'im): A person who stands during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, it is valid
B) No, it is not valid
C) It is valid only if the follower is also hunchbacked
D) It is valid only if the imam sits

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on whether a hunchbacked person can lead a standing person; the mufta bihi permits it based on analogy with the sitting person.

Ruling on a Mumi Following a Mumi
Explains that a gesturer may follow another gesturer, with exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of a mumi' following a mumi' and identify the condition that invalidates the following.

Core Idea
A gesturer may validly lead another gesturer only if their postures are equally weak.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains an important ruling for those who pray with gestures due to illness. While a gesturer can follow another gesturer, there are limits based on the strength of their states. Let's examine the ruling and its reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a mumi' following another mumi' in prayer. The ruling is sahih (valid) because it is not invalidated.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is qiyas (analogy) based on the equality of states (istiwa' al-halayn).
The text explicitly says 'li-istiwa' halayhima'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Since both imam and follower are mumi', they are in equal conditions, so following is valid by analogy to cases where equal states permit following.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Al-Tamartashi held it valid in all cases including when the imam is lying down; the chosen view restricts it.
The commentary says 'al-mukhtar raddan 'ala ma sahhabahu al-Tamartashi'.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi is that the follower can follow if both are gesturing, but not if the imam is lying down and the follower is sitting or standing, due to the follower's stronger state.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وموم) بمثله أي لا يفسد اقتداء موم بموم لاستواء حالهما. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان الإمام يومىء قائماً أو قاعداً بخلاف ما إذا كان الإمام مضطجعاً والمؤتم قاعداً أو قائماً فإنه لا يجوز لقوة حال المأموم لأن القعود معتبر بدليل وجوبه عليه عند القدرة بخلاف القيام لأنه ليس بمقصود لذاته، ولهذا لا يجب عليه القيام مع القدرة عليه إذا عجز عن السجود. وفي الشراح إنه المختار رداً لما صححه التمرتاشي من الجواز عند الكل.
His statement: 'and a gesturer with his like' i.e., the following of a gesturer by a gesturer is not invalidated because of the equality of their states. He made it absolute, so it includes when the imam is gesturing while standing or sitting, contrary to when the imam is lying down and the follower is sitting or standing, for it is not permissible due to the strength of the follower's state. Because sitting is considered, as evidenced by its obligation upon him when able, unlike standing, because it is not an end in itself. For this reason, standing is not obligatory upon him when he is able to do so if he is unable to prostrate. And in the commentaries, it is the chosen view, rejecting what al-Tamartashi corrected of permissibility according to everyone.
Source pages p. 639

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of a matn phrase. The commentator clarifies that a person who gestures (موم) due to severe illness or disability may follow another person who also gestures, because their states are equal. This ruling applies whether the imam gestures while standing or while sitting, because both are valid postures for gesturing prayer. However, if the imam is lying down (مضطجع) while the follower is sitting or standing, the following is not permissible because the follower is in a stronger state (قوة حال). The commentator explains that sitting is considered a valid posture for prayer and is obligatory when one can sit, whereas standing is not required if one cannot prostrate. This ruling is the chosen view (المختار), rejecting a contrary view from al-Tamartashi who claimed permissibility in all cases.

Key Terms
المومئ (al-mumi'): A person who performs prayer by gestures (إيماء) due to illness or inability to perform full actions like bowing and prostrating.
الاستواء (al-istiwa'): Equality in the ability to perform prayer; both imam and follower are in the same category of gesturing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, it is valid
B) No, it is not permissible because the follower is in a stronger state
C) It depends on whether the follower can stand
D) It is valid only if the imam also sits

Key Takeaway
A gesturer may lead another gesturer only if their states are equal; if the follower is stronger, the following is invalid.

Supererogatory Following Obligatory: The Principle of Building Weak upon Strong
Explains the ruling on a mutanawwil following a muftarid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a mutanawwil may follow a muftarid, explain the underlying qiyas, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding Tarawih.

Core Idea
Building the weak upon the strong: a supererogatory prayer may follow an obligatory one.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling that a person performing a supererogatory (nafl) prayer may validly follow an imam who is performing an obligatory (fard) prayer. The key principle is that the weaker (supererogatory) is built upon the stronger (obligatory). The text also addresses special cases like Tarawih and other sunnah prayers, where there is some scholarly difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The text states that following a muftarid by a mutanawwil is not invalid (لا يفسد). State this as the primary ruling.
The ruling is from the matn being commented on.
2
Extract the Principle
The reason given is 'building the weak upon the strong' (بناء الضعيف على القوي). This is the underlying legal maxim.
This principle is used to justify the ruling.
3
Examine the Proof (Qiyas)
The text uses qiyas: the supererogatory prayer is weak, the obligatory prayer is strong, so the weak may be built on the strong. Identify the asl, far', and illa.
Asl: obligatory prayer; Far': supererogatory prayer; Illa: relative strength.
4
Analyze the Recitation Aspect
The text explains that for a follower, recitation is not obligatory; thus the follower's prayer remains supererogatory. This removes a potential objection.
This is crucial because recitation in nafl is not required when following.
5
Apply to Tarawih and Other Cases
The ruling applies generally, including Tarawih. Note the disagreement reported in Fatawa Qadikhan and the author's critique. Also explore the other examples given in the text.
This step shows the scope and limitations of the principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ومتنفل بمفترض أي لا يفسد اقتداء متنفل بمفترض لأنه بناء الضعيف على القوي، والقراءة في النفل وإن كانت فرضاً في الأخيرتين نفلاً في الفرض لكن إنما تكون فرضاً إذا كان المصلي منفرداً، أما إذا كان مقتدياً فلا لأنها محظورة كذا في الغاية. ولأنه بالاقتداء صار تبعاً للإمام في القراءة فكانت نفلاً فيهما في حقه كإمامه. أطلقه فشمل اقتداء من يصلي التراويح بالمكتوبة، وذكر في فتاوى قاضيخان اختلافاً وأن الصحيح عدم الجواز وهو مشكل فإنه بناء الضعيف على القوي. وأشار إلى أن اقتداء المتنفل بمثله جائز وفي اقتداء الحنفي في الوتر بمن يراه سنة اختلاف المشايخ، ولو تكلم الإمام في شفع الترويحة ثم أمهم في ذلك الشفع جاز، وكذا إذا اقتدى في سنة العشاء بمن يصلي التراويح أو في السنة بعد الظهر بمن يصلي الأربع قبل الظهر صح اهـ.
His statement: 'and a supererogatory performer with an obligatory performer' i.e., the following of a supererogatory performer by an obligatory performer is not invalidated because it is building the weak upon the strong. And the recitation in supererogatory prayer, even if it is obligatory in the last two rak'ahs in obligatory prayer, but it is only obligatory if the person praying is alone; whereas if he is a follower, it is not, because it is prohibited (to recite). This is as in al-Ghayah. And because by following, he becomes subordinate to the imam in recitation, so it is supererogatory in both for him, like his imam. He made it absolute, so it includes the following of a person praying Tarawih with an obligatory prayer. And in Fatawa Qadikhan, there is disagreement, and the correct view is that it is not permissible, and this is problematic because it is building the weak upon the strong. And he indicated that the following of a supererogatory performer by his like is permissible. And regarding the following of a Hanafi in Witr by one who considers it sunnah, there is disagreement among the mashayikh. And if the imam speaks during the shaf' of Tarawih, then leads them in that shaf', it is permissible. Likewise, if one follows in the sunnah of Isha with a person praying Tarawih, or in the sunnah after Dhuhr with a person praying four before Dhuhr, it is valid.
Source pages p. 639

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the ruling that a person performing supererogatory prayer (متنفل) may follow a person performing obligatory prayer (مفترض). The underlying principle is that the weaker (supererogatory) may be built upon the stronger (obligatory). The commentator explains that in supererogatory prayer, the recitation is not obligatory in the way it is in obligatory prayer when alone, but when following, the follower's recitation is considered supererogatory. The text then applies this to Tarawih: the ruling covers a person praying Tarawih following someone praying the obligatory prayer. However, Fatawa Qadikhan reports a difference of opinion, with the correct view being impermissibility, which the author finds problematic since it contradicts the principle. The discussion extends to other related cases: a mutanawwil following another mutanawwil, a Hanafi following someone who considers Witr as sunnah, and cases where the imam speaks or where one follows a different sunnah prayer.

Key Terms
المتنفل (al-mutanawwil): A person performing a supererogatory (nafl) prayer.
المفترض (al-muftarid): A person performing an obligatory (fard) prayer.
بناء الضعيف على القوي (bina' al-da'if 'ala al-qawi): The principle of building the weaker upon the stronger, used to justify the validity of a mutanawwil following a muftarid.
التراويح (al-tarawih): The supererogatory night prayers performed during Ramadan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is it valid for a mutanawwil to follow a muftarid?
A) Because the imam's recitation is stronger
B) Because it is building the weak upon the strong
C) Because the follower's prayer becomes obligatory
D) Because the imam must be in the same state

Key Takeaway
A supererogatory prayer may validly follow an obligatory prayer because the weaker is built upon the stronger.

Ruling When Imam's Hadath Becomes Known
Ruling with proof using qiyas and intra-madhhab nuance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a follower discovers the imam was in hadath, identify the reasoning behind it, and apply the exception when the imam admits his impurity.

Core Idea
If the imam's prayer was invalid due to hadath, the follower's building collapses – repetition is wajib.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a common scenario: after prayer, you discover that your imam was in a state of hadath (ritual impurity) without knowing. What is your obligation? The text clarifies that the follower must repeat the prayer as a fresh obligation, explains the legal reasoning behind this ruling, and discusses a nuanced exception regarding the imam's own confession. Understanding this ruling reinforces the principle that following an imam is like building on a foundation – if the foundation is unsound, the building cannot stand.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the matn rules on: the follower's prayer when it appears that the imam was in hadath. The ruling is that the follower must repeat (أعاد) the prayer.
The commentator emphasizes that this repetition is performing the fard again, not a compensatory repetition for a deficiency.
2
Understand the term 'i'adah'
The text clarifies that 'أعاد' here means doing the fard over. In usul al-fiqh, 'i'adah' often means a repeat that compensates for a deficiency, but here it is a fresh obligation because the original prayer was invalid.
The commentator suggests it would have been clearer to say 'بطلت' (it becomes invalid).
3
Grasp the legal reasoning (qiyas al-bina')
The follower's prayer is invalid because following (iqtida') is like building on a foundation. If the imam's prayer was void (due to missing purity, pillar, or condition), the follower's building is on nothing.
This is a qiyas: the imam's prayer is the foundation; if it is non-existent, the construction is impossible.
4
Apply the exception: imam's confession
The text from al-Mujtaba reports a view that if the imam himself admits that he led without purity, the followers are not obligated to repeat. The reasoning: his admission implies kufr (disbelief), and the statement of a kafir is not accepted in religious matters.
The commentator finds this problematic because praying with impurity does not necessarily cause kufr, especially given differences of opinion (e.g., Malik considers it sunnah in one view).
5
Distinguish knowledge conditions
From al-Mubtagha: only those who actually know of the imam's impurity are required to repeat. The imam is not obligated to inform the congregation, nor does he sin by not informing.
The last part of the passage discusses following someone praying a different prayer; the correct view is that it is not permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وإن ظهر إن إمامه محدث أعاد أي على سبيل الفرض، فالمراد بالإعادة الإتيان بالفرض لا الإعادة في اصطلاح الأصوليين الجابرة للنقص في المؤدي، فلو قال بطلت لكان أولى. وإنما بطلت صلاة المأموم لأن الاقتداء بناء والبناء على المعدوم محال، ولا فرق في ذلك بين أن يظهر أن الإمام عدم ركناً أو شرطاً وفي المجتبى : ولو أخبرهم الإمام أنه أمهم شهراً بغير طهارة أو علمه بالنجاسة المانعة لا يلزم الإعادة لأنه صرح بكفره، وقول الفاسق غير مقبول في الديانات، فكيف قول الكافر؟ اهـ. وهو مشكل فإنه لا يكفر إذا صلى بالنجاسة المانعة عمداً للاختلاف في وجوب إزالتها فإن مالكاً يقول في قول بسنيتها، وفي المبتغى بالمعجمة ومن علم أن إمامه على غير طهارة أعاد وإلا فلا. ولا يلزم على الإمام أن يعلم الجماعة بحاله ولا يأثم بتركه . وفي معراج الدراية : ولا يلزم على الإمام المكتوبة أو بمن يصلي نافلة غير التراويح اختلف المشايخ فيه والصحيح أنه لا يجوز اهـ .
His statement: 'And if it appears that his imam is in a state of hadath, he repeats' i.e., by way of obligation. By 'repetition' is meant performing the obligatory prayer, not repetition in the terminology of the usuliyyun which compensates for deficiency in what is performed. So if he had said 'it becomes invalid', it would have been better. The prayer of the follower is invalid because following is a construction, and constructing upon something non-existent is impossible. There is no difference in this between it appearing that the imam omitted a pillar or a condition. And in al-Mujtaba: If the imam informs them that he led them for a month without purity, or that he knew of the preventing impurity, they are not obligated to repeat, because he has declared his own disbelief, and the statement of a fasiq is not accepted in religious matters, so how about the statement of a disbeliever? This is problematic, because he does not become a disbeliever if he prays with preventing impurity intentionally, due to the difference of opinion regarding its removal. For Malik says in one opinion that it is sunnah. And in al-Mubtagha: Whoever knows that his imam is without purity repeats, otherwise not. And it is not obligatory upon the imam to inform the congregation of his state, nor does he sin by leaving it. And in Miraj al-Diraya: It is not obligatory upon the imam (to inform), and regarding [following] someone praying an obligatory prayer or a supererogatory other than Tarawih, the mashayikh differed, and the correct view is that it is not permissible.
Source pages p. 640

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling when a follower discovers after prayer that his imam was in a state of hadath (ritual impurity). The matn uses the term 'أعاد' (he repeats), which the commentator explains means he must perform the prayer again as an obligation. The repetition here is for the fard itself, not a compensatory repetition for a deficiency. The commentator notes that it would be clearer to say 'batalat' (it becomes invalid). The reason the follower's prayer is invalid is that following is like building upon a foundation; if the imam's prayer was invalid, the follower's building is upon nothing. This applies whether the imam lacked a pillar or a condition. The passage then discusses a case from al-Mujtaba: if the imam himself admits he led them for a month without wudu or with impurity, the followers are not required to repeat because his admission is not accepted as it implies his own kufr (disbelief) – a fasiq's word is not accepted, let alone a kafir. The commentator objects to this reasoning, noting that praying with impurity does not necessarily cause kufr, especially since there is difference of opinion (e.g., Malik considers it sunnah in one view). Then from al-Mubtagha: only those who knew of the impurity must repeat. The imam is not required to inform the congregation, nor does he sin by not informing. The passage ends with a quote from Miraj al-Diraya regarding the imam's obligation to inform and the ruling on following someone praying a different prayer.

Key Terms
الحدث (al-hadath): Ritual impurity that invalidates wudu, such as passing wind, urine, etc.
الإعادة (al-i'adah): Repeating the prayer as a fresh obligation, not as a compensative repetition (i'adah in usuli terminology is for fixing a deficiency).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the legal reason for the follower's prayer being invalid when the imam's hadath appears?
A) The imam committed a sin by praying without wudu
B) Following is like building; if the foundation is non-existent, the building cannot stand
C) The follower should have checked the imam's state before prayer
D) The imam's prayer is valid, but the follower's intention is defective

Key Takeaway
If it becomes known that the imam was in hadath, the follower's prayer is invalid and must be repeated as a fresh obligation, unless they lack knowledge of the hadath, in which case no repetition is required.

Follower's Obligation to Repeat When Imam's Invalidity is Discovered
Ruling on nullification of follower's prayer with rational proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that the follower must repeat the prayer when the imam's prayer is found invalid, and explain the Hanafi qiyas argument 'building on nothing is impossible'.

Core Idea
If the imam's prayer is invalid, the follower's prayer built upon it is also invalid – repetition is wajib.

This lesson examines a key ruling in Hanafi fiqh: what happens when a follower discovers after the prayer that the imam was in a state of ritual impurity (hadath) or missed a pillar or condition. The Hanafi school holds that the follower's prayer is null and must be repeated, based on a powerful rational analogy. We will unpack the ruling, its proof, and its scope.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the follower's prayer when the imam's invalidity is discovered. The ruling is that the follower must repeat the prayer (i'ada) as an obligation (wajib).
The text clarifies that 'i'ada' here means performing the prayer anew, not the technical term used by usul scholars.
2
Understand the proof (dalil)
The proof is a rational analogy (qiyas): following (iqtida') is like building a structure. If the foundation (the imam's prayer) is non-existent, the building cannot stand. 'Building on nothing is impossible.'
This is a clear dalil aqli (rational proof) that the follower's prayer is invalid.
3
Note the scope of the ruling
The ruling applies whether the imam missed a pillar (rukn) or a condition (shart) that invalidates prayer. Hadath is just one example.
The passage states there is no difference between missing a rukn or a shart.
4
Consider the follower's own ijtihad
If the follower has a different belief about what invalidates prayer (e.g., a small quantity of impurity), he must follow his own ijtihad. The ruling is based on the follower's knowledge.
This is discussed in later parts of the passage, showing the principle of 'al-ibratu li ra'yi al-muqtafi'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن ظهر إن إمامه محدث أعاد أي على سبيل الفرض، فالمراد بالإعادة الإتيان بالفرض لا الإعادة في اصطلاح الأصوليين الجابرة للنقص في المؤدي، فلو قال بطلت لكان أولى. وإنما بطلت صلاة المأموم لأن الاقتداء بناء والبناء على المعدوم محال، ولا فرق في ذلك بين أن يظهر أن الإمام عدم ركناً أو شرطاً وفي المجتبى : ولو أخبرهم الإمام أنه أمهم شهراً بغير طهارة أو علمه بالنجاسة المانعة لا يلزم الإعادة لأنه صرح بكفره، وقول الفاسق غير مقبول في الديانات، فكيف قول الكافر؟ اهـ. وهو مشكل فإنه لا يكفر إذا صلى بالنجاسة المانعة عمداً للاختلاف في وجوب إزالتها فإن مالكاً يقول في قول بسنيتها، وفي المبتغى بالمعجمة ومن علم أن إمامه على غير طهارة أعاد وإلا فلا. ولا يلزم على الإمام أن يعلم الجماعة بحاله ولا يأثم بتركه . وفي معراج الدراية : ولا يلزم على الإمام المكتوبة أو بمن يصلي نافلة غير التراويح اختلف المشايخ فيه والصحيح أنه لا يجوز اهـ . قلت : يمكن أن يكون المراد بنفي الجواز عدم الاعتداد بها عن التراويح على وجه الكمال لما سنذكر أنه إذا تعمد فلم يسلم على كل شفع يكره اهـ. أقول : حيث صرح : قاضيخان بأن الصحيح أنه إذا صلى التراويح مقتدياً بمتنفل بغيرها لا يجوز بناء على أن السنة لا تتأدى بنية التطوع يكون ذلك تصحيحاً لعدم جواز اقتداء مصلي التراويح بالمفترض لأن. معنی أن السنة لا تتأدى بنية التطوع أنها لا بد لها من التعيين والإمام غير معين للتراويح، سواء كان مصلياً نفلاً أو فرضاً، فلا تصح نية التراويح من المقتدي، وقد . صرح العلامة قاسم في فتاواه ضمن رسالة فقال : فصل : إذا صلى التراويح مقتدياً بمن يصلي المكتوبة أو وتراً أو نافلة غير التراويح اختلفوا فيه منهم من بنى هذا الاختلاف على الاختلاف في النية. من قال من المشايخ إن التراويح لا تتأدى إلا بنيتها فلا تتأدى بنية الإمام وهي بخلاف نيته، ومن قال منهم إنها تتأدى بمطلق النية ينبغي أن يقول هنا إنه يصح والأصح لا يصح الاقتداء، وعلى هذا الاختلاف إذا لم يسلم من العشاء وبنى عليها التراويح، والأصح أنه لا ي. يصح وهذا أظهر لأنه مكروه اهـ. ثم راجعت الفتاوى الخانية فوجدت فيها ما نقله المؤلف فظهر أن في نسخة الشرنبلالي سقطاً وأن الصواب ما نقله المؤلف. قول المصنف : ( وإن ظهر أن إمامه (محدث) قال في النهر : بأن شهدوا أنه أحدث ثم صلى أو نفسه وكان عدلاً وإن لم يكن ندب فقط . كذا في السراج قوله : (فلو قال بطلت لكان أولى الخ) قال في النهر : فيه نظر إذ البطلان يؤذن بسبق الصحة نعم الأولى أن يقال : لا يجتزي بما أداه . واعلم أن المحدث كما عرفت ليس قيداً فلو قال : ولو ظهر أن بإمامه ما يمنع صحة الصلاة أعادها لكان أولى ليشمل ما لو أخل بركن أو شرط والعبرة لرأي المقتدي حتى لو رأى على الإمام نجاسة أقل من الدرهم واعتقد المقتدي أنه مانع والإمام خلافه أعاد ، وفي عكسه والإمام لا يعلم ذلك. لا يعيد، ولو اقتدى أحدهما بالآخر فإذا قطرة من دم وكل منهما يزعم أنها من صاحبه لفساد صلاته على كل حال . كذا في البزازية. قوله : ( وفي خزانة الأكمل لأنه سكت الخ) قال الرملي : صوابه «لا لأنه سكت الخ». فحرف النفي ساقط من خطه ولا بد منه . قال في الحاوي الزاهدي : (يو) علم الإمام بفساد صلاته المختلف فيها فلم يأمرهم بالإعادة لا يسعه ويجب العمل فيه على ما يعتقده صح» تبين له أنه صلى بغير وضوء يجب عليه الأخبار بقدر الممكن (حك ) لا يلزمه الاخبار لأنه ما معصية بل خطأ معفو عنه قال : وهذا أصح من جواب يوصج وإليه أشار أبو يوسف، وسواء كان فساد صلاته مختلفاً فيه أو متفقاً عليه فإن الإمام إذا لم يعلم فساد صلاته لا تفسد صلاة المقتدين عند الشافعي فينبغي أن لا يلزم الإمام إخبارهم بذلك أصلاً .اهـ. قوله : (الأصح أن صلاته فاسدة) قال في الشرنبلالية : فيه مخالفة لما في الهداية من التصحيح .هـ. أي لأن تعليل الهداية يقتضي الصحة . الإطلاق. وقد أشار إلى المخالفة في الفتح وحررنا المقام فيما علقناه على شرح التنوير فراجعه .
If it becomes apparent that his imam had a hadath (ritual impurity), he repeats, meaning as a duty. By 'repeat' is meant performing the prescribed prayer, not the technical 'i'ada' that compensates a deficiency in the performed prayer. So if he had said 'it is nullified' it would have been better. The prayer of the follower is nullified because following is a building, and building on nothing is impossible. There is no difference in that between the imam missing a pillar or a condition. In al-Mujtaba: If the imam informs them that he led them for a month without purity or knowing of prohibitive impurity, repetition is not required because he professed his disbelief, and the word of a sinner is not accepted in religious matters, so how about the word of a disbeliever? End. This is problematic because he does not become a disbeliever if he prays with prohibitive impurity deliberately due to disagreement on its removal obligation, for Malik says in one view it is sunna. In al-Mubtagha (with mujama): Whoever knows that his imam is not in a state of purity repeats, otherwise not. The imam is not required to inform the congregation of his state and does not sin by leaving it. In Ma'raj al-Diraya: The imam is not required... or with one praying a supererogatory other than tarawih – the mashayikh differed, the correct is it is not permissible. End. I say: It may be that the negation of permissibility means not considering it fully valid for tarawih, as we will mention that if he intentionally does not say salam after each pair it is disliked. End. I say: Where Qadikhan explicitly stated that the correct is that if one prays tarawih following a supererogatory other than it, it is not permissible, based on the position that the sunna cannot be performed by a mere intention of supererogation, this becomes a correction of the impermissibility of the tarawih follower following a muftarid. The meaning is that the sunna requires specification and the imam is not specified for tarawih, whether he is praying supererogatory or obligatory, so the intention of tarawih from the follower is not valid. Shaykh Qasim stated in his fatawa... The author's statement: 'If it becomes apparent that his imam is in a state of hadath' ... In al-Nahr: by evidence that they witnessed that he had an event then prayed, or himself if he was just, even if not something recommended only. As in al-Siraj. His statement: 'If he had said it is nullified it would have been better...' In al-Nahr: There is consideration in this, because nullification suggests prior validity. Rather it should be said: He does not suffice with what he performed. Know that 'hadath' is not a restriction, so if he said: 'If it becomes apparent that the imam has something that prevents the validity of prayer, he repeats it' that would be better to include whatever is missing a pillar or condition. The consideration is the follower's view... In al-Khazanah: It is a forgivable error. And from al-Wabari: He informs them even if it is disputed. Its analogy is with impure water or if there is dirt on his garment. End.
Source pages p. 640

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq that if a follower discovers after the prayer that his imam was in a state of hadath (ritual impurity), the follower must repeat the prayer. The commentator explains that 'i'ada' here means performing the prayer anew as an obligation, not the technical 'i'ada' used by usul scholars to fix a deficiency. The reason for nullification is that following (iqtida') is like building a structure; if the foundation (the imam's prayer) is invalid, the building collapses. The ruling applies whether the imam missed a pillar (rukn) or a condition (shart). The text then discusses whether the imam must inform the congregation if he later learns of his invalidity. There is a difference among Hanafi scholars: some say he must inform, but the preferred view (based on the opinion of Abu Yusuf) is that he is not required to inform because his mistake was a forgivable error, not a sin. The passage also addresses the case where the follower's own belief differs from the imam's regarding what invalidates—the follower must follow his own ijtihad. Abu Hanifa's position is that the imam's prayer is invalid and the follower's is built upon that, so the follower must repeat. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) have a different view on some related issues, but here the ruling is clear.

Key Terms
محدث (muhdith): One in a state of ritual impurity (hadath) that requires wudu or ghusl.
إعادة (i'ada): Performing the prayer again due to invalidity of the first one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what must a follower do if he discovers after the prayer that his imam had a hadath (ritual impurity) that was unknown to him during the prayer?
A) He does not repeat because he was unaware.
B) He must repeat the prayer because his prayer was invalid.
C) He must ask the imam to repeat for him.
D) He repeats only if the imam informs him.

Key Takeaway
The follower must repeat the prayer when the imam's prayer is found invalid, regardless of his awareness, because building on nothing is impossible.
