Imam's Duty to Inform the Congregation of His Prayer's Invalidity
Intra-Hanafi dispute on imam's obligation to inform of his prayer's invalidity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position that the imam is not required to inform the congregation if his prayer was invalid, and explain the reasoning of Abu Yusuf that it is a forgiven error.

Core Idea
The imam's error is forgiven; he need not tell the congregation, but the follower who knows must repeat.

This lesson addresses a practical and ethical question: if an imam realizes after the prayer that his own prayer was invalid (due to hadath, missing a condition, etc.), is he obliged to inform the congregation? The Hanafi school has a nuanced answer based on the nature of the error and the principles of forgiveness and trust. We will explore the main positions and the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
State the issue: informing the congregation
The issue is whether the imam must announce to the congregation that his prayer was invalid, so they can repeat.
This applies when the imam learns of the invalidity after the prayer.
2
Identify the two views
Some Hanafi scholars (e.g., from al-Mujtaba) suggest the imam must inform because the followers might rely on his silence. Others (the preferred view) say he is not required because his error is forgiven and informing could cause distress.
The text quotes al-Mujtaba holding that if the imam tells the congregation he led them without purity, they need not repeat because he has professed disbelief (a problematic statement).
3
Understand the preferred reasoning
The preferred view, attributed to Abu Yusuf, is that the imam does not have to inform and does not sin by remaining silent. The mistake is a 'khatā' ma'fu 'anhu' (forgiven error).
This is compared to a case of dirty water or impurity on the garment where the imam might not be aware.
4
Note the condition of the follower's knowledge
The ruling is different for the follower: if the follower knows of the imam's invalidity, he must repeat. The imam's silence does not affect the follower's obligation if he knows.
The imam's duty is separate from the follower's.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن ظهر إن إمامه محدث أعاد أي على سبيل الفرض، فالمراد بالإعادة الإتيان بالفرض لا الإعادة في اصطلاح الأصوليين الجابرة للنقص في المؤدي، فلو قال بطلت لكان أولى. وإنما بطلت صلاة المأموم لأن الاقتداء بناء والبناء على المعدوم محال، ولا فرق في ذلك بين أن يظهر أن الإمام عدم ركناً أو شرطاً وفي المجتبى : ولو أخبرهم الإمام أنه أمهم شهراً بغير طهارة أو علمه بالنجاسة المانعة لا يلزم الإعادة لأنه صرح بكفره، وقول الفاسق غير مقبول في الديانات، فكيف قول الكافر؟ اهـ. وهو مشكل فإنه لا يكفر إذا صلى بالنجاسة المانعة عمداً للاختلاف في وجوب إزالتها فإن مالكاً يقول في قول بسنيتها، وفي المبتغى بالمعجمة ومن علم أن إمامه على غير طهارة أعاد وإلا فلا. ولا يلزم على الإمام أن يعلم الجماعة بحاله ولا يأثم بتركه . وفي معراج الدراية : ولا يلزم على الإمام المكتوبة أو بمن يصلي نافلة غير التراويح اختلف المشايخ فيه والصحيح أنه لا يجوز اهـ . قلت : يمكن أن يكون المراد بنفي الجواز عدم الاعتداد بها عن التراويح على وجه الكمال لما سنذكر أنه إذا تعمد فلم يسلم على كل شفع يكره اهـ. أقول : حيث صرح : قاضيخان بأن الصحيح أنه إذا صلى التراويح مقتدياً بمتنفل بغيرها لا يجوز بناء على أن السنة لا تتأدى بنية التطوع يكون ذلك تصحيحاً لعدم جواز اقتداء مصلي التراويح بالمفترض لأن. معنی أن السنة لا تتأدى بنية التطوع أنها لا بد لها من التعيين والإمام غير معين للتراويح، سواء كان مصلياً نفلاً أو فرضاً، فلا تصح نية التراويح من المقتدي، وقد . صرح العلامة قاسم في فتاواه ضمن رسالة فقال : فصل : إذا صلى التراويح مقتدياً بمن يصلي المكتوبة أو وتراً أو نافلة غير التراويح اختلفوا فيه منهم من بنى هذا الاختلاف على الاختلاف في النية. من قال من المشايخ إن التراويح لا تتأدى إلا بنيتها فلا تتأدى بنية الإمام وهي بخلاف نيته، ومن قال منهم إنها تتأدى بمطلق النية ينبغي أن يقول هنا إنه يصح والأصح لا يصح الاقتداء، وعلى هذا الاختلاف إذا لم يسلم من العشاء وبنى عليها التراويح، والأصح أنه لا ي. يصح وهذا أظهر لأنه مكروه اهـ. ثم راجعت الفتاوى الخانية فوجدت فيها ما نقله المؤلف فظهر أن في نسخة الشرنبلالي سقطاً وأن الصواب ما نقله المؤلف. قول المصنف : ( وإن ظهر أن إمامه (محدث) قال في النهر : بأن شهدوا أنه أحدث ثم صلى أو نفسه وكان عدلاً وإن لم يكن ندب فقط . كذا في السراج قوله : (فلو قال بطلت لكان أولى الخ) قال في النهر : فيه نظر إذ البطلان يؤذن بسبق الصحة نعم الأولى أن يقال : لا يجتزي بما أداه . واعلم أن المحدث كما عرفت ليس قيداً فلو قال : ولو ظهر أن بإمامه Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq that if a follower discovers after the prayer that his imam was in a state of hadath (ritual impurity), the follower must repeat the prayer. The commentator explains that 'i'ada' here means performing the prayer anew as an obligation, not the technical 'i'ada' used by usul scholars to fix a deficiency. Key Terms
خطأ معفو عنه (khatā' ma'fu 'anhu): An error that is forgiven; no sin or liability attaches.
إعادة (i'ada): Repetition of prayer; here specifically the follower's obligation when he knows of imam's defect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view, what is the ruling regarding the imam informing the congregation if he discovers his prayer was invalid?
A) The imam must inform the congregation and repeats.
B) The imam is not required to inform and does not sin by remaining silent.
C) The imam must inform, but only if the defect was intentional.
D) The imam must inform only if the followers ask.

Key Takeaway
The imam is not required to inform the congregation of his prayer's invalidity; his error is forgiven. The follower must repeat only if he knows.

Illiterate Imam Leading a Literate Follower
Intra-Hanafi dispute on illiterate imam leading a literate follower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a literate person's prayer behind an illiterate imam and identify the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
When a literate follower prays behind an illiterate imam, Abu Hanifa invalidates the prayer; the Sahibayn validate it for the imam and illiterate followers.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute about congregational prayer when the imam cannot recite properly. The ruling hinges on whether the imam's omission of recitation affects the follower's prayer. Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn disagree, and their reasoning reveals fundamental principles about imamate and obligations.

Guided Path
1
State the Ruling from the Matn
Identify the initial ruling presented in the base text (al-Kanz) that the prayer is invalid when a qari follows an ummi.
The matn says: 'If an illiterate and a literate follow an illiterate... their prayers are invalid.'
2
Identify the Positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Abu Hanifa holds the prayer is invalid for all; the Sahibayn say the imam's and illiterate followers' prayers are valid, but the qari follower's prayer is invalid.
This is the core ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the Reasoning of Each Side
Abu Hanifa: the imam omitted a fard (recitation) despite ability, so his prayer is invalid, affecting the follower. Sahibayn: the imam is excused, analogous to a naked imam leading clothed followers.
The analogy with the naked imam is a key qiyas.
4
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Practical difference: whether the qari follower should repeat his prayer or not. Also affects the validity of the imam's imamate for future prayers.
Also impacts rulings on related cases like substitution in prayer.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih and Later Authority
The text mentions a correction in al-Dhakhirah suggesting the illiterate's start is invalid, but the mufta bihi in later Hanafi fatwa is often the view of the Sahibayn.
Refer to later sources like al-Hidayah and al-Dhakhirah for the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وإن اقتدى أمي وقارئ بأمي أو استخلف أمياً في الأخريين فسدت صلاتهم) أما في المسألة الأولى فهو عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا: صلاة الإمام ومن لم يقرأ تامة لأنه معذور أم قوماً معذورين وغير معذورين فصار كما إذا أم العاري عراة ولا بسين، وله أن الإمام ترك فرض القراءة مع القدرة عليها فتفسد صلاته، وهذا لأنه لو اقتدى بالقارئ تكون قراءته قراءة له يخلاف تلك المسألة وأمثالها لأن الموجود في حق الإمام لا يكون موجوداً في حق المقتدي. قيد بالاقتداء لأنه لو كان يصلي الأمي وحده والقارئ وحده فإنه جائز هو الصحيح لأنه لم يظهر منهما رغبة في الجماعة. كذا في الهداية وفي النهاية : لو افتتح الأمي ثم حضر القارئ ففيه قولان، ولو حضر الأمي بعد افتتاح القارئ فلم يقتد به وصلى منفرداً الأصح أن صلاته فاسدة، وأشار بفساد الصلاة إلى صحة شروع القارئ لاستوائهما في فرض التحريمة . وإنما اختلفا في القراءة ولا يقال لم لا يلزم القضاء على المقتدي إذا أفسد وقد صح شروعه لأنا نقول : لما شرع في صلاة الأمي أوجبها على نفسه بغير قراءة فلم يلزمه القضاء كنذر صلاة بغير قراءة لا تلزمه إلا في رواية عن أبي يوسف كذا في غاية البيان. وصحح في الذخيرة وعدم صحة شروعه وفائدته تظهر في انتقاض وضوئه بالقهقهة.
His statement: 'If an illiterate and a literate follow an illiterate, or if an illiterate appoints an illiterate as substitute in the last two rak'ats, their prayers are invalid.' For the first issue, according to Abu Hanifa it is as stated, and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: The prayer of the imam and the one who does not recite is complete, because he is excused; he led a group including both excused and unexcused, so it is like the case of a naked man leading both naked and clothed. And for Abu Hanifa, the imam abandoned the obligatory recitation despite ability, so his prayer is invalid. This is because if he were to follow a qari, his recitation would count for him, unlike that case and its like, because what is present in the imam's right is not present in the follower's right. It is restricted to the case of iqtida' because if the illiterate prays alone and the qari prays alone, it is valid—the correct view—because neither showed desire for congregation. So in al-Hidaya. And in al-Nihaya: If the illiterate begins then a qari arrives, there are two opinions. If the qari begins then an illiterate arrives and does not follow him and prays alone, the correct view is that his prayer is invalid. He indicated by 'invalidity of prayer' the validity of the qari's start, because they are equal in the obligation of the takbir (ihram). They only differed regarding recitation. It cannot be said: Why is qada (compensation) not required from the follower if he invalidated it? We say: When he began the prayer as an illiterate, he obligated a prayer on himself without recitation, so qada is not required, like a vow to pray without recitation which is not binding except in a narration from Abu Yusuf. So in Ghayat al-Bayan. And al-Dhakhirah corrected that his start is not valid; its benefit appears in the invalidation of his wudu by loud laughter.
Source pages p. 641

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling when an illiterate person (ummi, who cannot recite the Quran properly) acts as imam for a mixed congregation including a literate person (qari). According to Abu Hanifa, the prayer of all is invalid because the imam left a required obligation (recitation) despite being able to perform it properly? Actually the ummi is unable, but if a qari is present, the ummi should not lead. Abu Hanifa's reasoning: the imam's prayer is invalid because he omitted a fard, so the follower's prayer built on it is also invalid. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the imam and the ummi followers' prayers are valid because the imam is excused (he cannot read), and those followers who also cannot read are excused; the qari follower should not have followed, but his prayer? Actually the text says the prayer of the imam and 'the one who does not read' (i.e., ummi followers) is complete; the qari follower's prayer is invalid? The text says 'فسدت صلاتهم' (their prayers are invalid) in the matn, but the Sahibayn say the imam and those who did not read have valid prayers. So there is ikhtilaf. The commentator explains the difference: Abu Hanifa considers that the imam omitted a fard despite ability? The ummi is not able, so the issue is more about the qari follower's prayer. The Sahibayn analogize to a case where a naked imam leads both naked and clothed: the clothed person's prayer is valid? Actually the example of 'a'ri' (naked) leading 'urāt' (naked) and 'lābis' (clothed) – the Sahibayn say it is similar. The commentator then notes that the ruling is restricted to the case of following; if both pray separately, it is valid. There is a discussion about the ruling when a qari arrives after the ummi has started: two opinions. And when an illiterate arrives after the qari has started, the correct is that the illiterate's prayer is invalid. The benefit of the ruling that the illiterate's start is invalid appears in cases like invalidation of wudu by loud laughter. The passage clarifies that the ikhtilaf is only about recitation, not the takbir.

Key Terms
أمي (ummi): A person who cannot recite the Quran properly, either due to illiteracy or inability.
قارئ (qari): A person who can recite the Quran correctly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), what is the ruling if a literate person prays behind an illiterate imam?
A) The prayer of both is valid.
B) The prayer of both is invalid.
C) The imam's prayer is valid; the literate follower's prayer is invalid.
D) The imam's prayer is invalid; the literate follower's prayer is valid.

Key Takeaway
The prayer of a literate person behind an illiterate imam is a matter of legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school, with the preferred view holding the imam's and illiterate followers' prayers valid but the literate follower's prayer invalid.

Imam Informing Congregation of His Invalid Prayer
Discusses whether an imam must inform followers if his prayer was invalid due to impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on whether an imam must inform followers of his invalid prayer due to impurity, and identify the mufta bihi and its reasoning.

Core Idea
An imam's unintentional impurity is a forgiven error; he need not inform the congregation.

This lesson examines a nuanced Hanafi dispute: if an imam discovers after the prayer that he was ritually impure, must he inform the followers so they can repeat? The source presents conflicting positions from later Hanafi works, with the preferred view deeming it a forgiven error. We will dissect the arguments and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Determine the exact question: What should an imam do if he learns after the prayer that he had hadath or janabah, and the congregation has dispersed?
2
State the two Hanafi positions
List the view of al-Mujtaba (must inform) and al-Khazanah (forgiven error, need not inform). Note that Abu Yusuf favored the latter.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Examine the cross-madhhab element
Al-Shafi'i holds that if the imam did not know, the followers' prayer remains valid, so there is no obligation to inform. Compare with the Hanafi reasoning.
The dispute over the validity of the followers' prayer affects the obligation.
4
Analyze the tarjih
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq prefers the 'forgiven error' view, calling it 'more correct' and citing al-Hawi al-Zahidi and Abu Yusuf. Understand why: the imam's mistake was not a sin, and informing may cause unnecessary hardship.
This is the mufta bihi.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Apply the preferred view: the imam may remain silent, and the followers do not need to repeat their prayer if they were unaware of the impurity. Explore scenarios where the imam's error was not a forgiven mistake (e.g., willful negligence).
The thamarah al-khilaf is whether the followers must repeat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإعلام إذا كانوا قوماً غير معينين. وفي المجتبى ولو أم قوماً محدث أو جنب ثم علم بعد التفرق يجب الإخبار بقدر الممكن بلسانه أو كتاب أو رسول على الأصح. وفي خزانة خطأ معفو عنه وعن الوبري: يخبرهم وإن كان مختلفاً فيه ونظيره من ماء نجس أو على ثوبه نجاسة اهـ.
الأكمل : لأنه سكت
إذا رأى غيره يتوضأ .

:

Informing [the congregation]: if they are unspecified people. And in al-Mujtaba: If he led people while in a state of hadath or janabah, then he knows after they have dispersed, he must inform as much as possible, by his tongue, a letter, or a messenger, according to the soundest view. And in al-Khazanah: it is a forgiven error. And from al-Wabiri: he informs them even if there is a difference of opinion, and its like is from impure water or impurity on his garment, etc. Al-Akmal: 'because he remained silent' when he saw someone else performing ablution. Regarding: His statement: (And in al-Khazanah of al-Akmal 'because he remained silent', etc.) Al-Ramli said: Its correct form is 'not because he remained silent', etc. So the negation particle is missing from his writing and is necessary. He said in al-Hawi al-Zahidi: (If) the imam knows the invalidity of his prayer, which is disputed, and does not order them to repeat, it is not permissible for him, and he must act according to what he believes to be correct. (If) it becomes clear to him that he prayed without wudu, he must inform as much as possible. (From Hikmah?) He is not obliged to inform because it is not a sin but a forgiven error. He said: This is more correct than the answer of Yuwajaj, and Abu Yusuf indicated it. And whether the invalidity of his prayer is disputed or agreed upon, if the imam does not know the invalidity of his prayer, the prayer of the followers is not invalid according to al-Shafi'i. Therefore he should not be required to inform them at all, etc. His statement: (The correct view is that his prayer is invalid) Al-Sharnablali said in it: There is disagreement with what is authenticated in al-Hidayah. Because the reasoning of al-Hidayah requires validity. The absoluteness. And al-Fath pointed out the disagreement, and we have settled the matter in our commentary on Sharh al-Tanwir, so refer to it.
Source pages p. 641

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on an imam who discovers after the prayer that he was in a state of ritual impurity (hadath or janabah) or that his clothes were impure. The matn states 'informing' (الإعلام) as a heading. The primary issue: must the imam inform the congregation so they can repeat their prayer? The text presents multiple views. According to al-Mujtaba, if the imam knows after they have dispersed, he must inform them as best he can (by speech, letter, or messenger) — this is the soundest view. According to al-Khazanah, it is a forgiven error, so he need not inform. A similar view from al-Wabiri: he informs them despite the difference of opinion, like the case of impure water or impurity on his garment. Then the text quotes al-Akmal's comment 'because he remained silent' which seems to be corrected by al-Ramli to 'not because' (i.e., he should not remain silent). Al-Hawi al-Zahidi includes two answers: one that if he knows the invalidity, he must act according to his belief (so if he believes his prayer was invalid, he must inform); another that he is not obliged because it is a forgiven error, not a sin. The latter is considered more correct, and Abu Yusuf indicated it. Then the text mentions al-Shafi'i's view that if the imam does not know, the followers' prayer is not invalid, so he should not be required to inform. The commentator ends by noting a contradiction in al-Hidayah's authentication and promises resolution in another work. The mudhhab ikhtilaf here is between the view that informing is obligatory (possibly the majority of Hanafis) and the view that it is not because it is a forgiven error. The preferred view (as per the text) seems to be the latter, as it is called 'more correct' and attributed to Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms
إخبار (ikhbār): Informing the followers that the imam's prayer was invalid, so they can repeat their prayer.
خطأ معفو عنه (khaṭa' ma'fū 'anh): An error that is forgiven by the Law; no legal consequence or sin.
مختلف فيه (mukhtalaf fīh): A ruling that is disputed among scholars; here, the invalidity of the prayer itself is disputed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in this passage, what should an imam do if he discovers after the prayer that he was in a state of janabah?
A) He must inform every follower individually
B) He is not required to inform because it is a forgiven error
C) He must only inform if the followers ask
D) He must repeat his prayer but need not inform

Key Takeaway
The imam's unintentional impurity is a forgiven error; the relied-upon Hanafi ruling is that he need not inform the congregation.

The Ruling on an Illiterate (Ummi) Imam Leading Prayer
Ruling with proof on the invalidity of an ummi leading a qari.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an ummi leading a qari and explain the proof that every rak'ah requires recitation.

Core Idea
An ummi cannot lead a qari because recitation is required in every rak'ah, and the ummi cannot provide it even virtually.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author discusses the validity of an illiterate person (ummi) acting as imam. The key issue is whether a qari (one who can recite) can pray behind an ummi. The Hanafi school holds it invalid because the imam must be capable of reciting for the followers. Let us explore the proof and the nuanced conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main scenario
The text begins with an imam overtaken by hadath who appoints a substitute. This sets the stage for discussing the ummi imam's validity.
The ruling on istikhilaf (appointment) is also covered.
2
Extract the legal principle
The key principle: 'Every rak'ah is a prayer, and it is not devoid of recitation, either actually or virtually.'
This is the cornerstone of the proof.
3
Apply the principle to the ummi
The ummi cannot recite actually, and virtual recitation is impossible due to lack of capability. Therefore, the imamah is invalid for a qari follower.
Virtual recitation applies only to those capable but excused (e.g., forgetfulness).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Zufar held it valid because the qari can recite for himself. Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn disagreed, emphasizing the imam's role.
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.
5
Determine the practical effect
The follower (qari) must repeat his prayer if he prayed behind an ummi, as the original prayer was invalid.
Zufar's view would not require repetition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من سبقه الحدث توضأ وبنى واستخلف لو إماماً كما لو حصر عن القراءة وإن بين الجهل والعلم. وشمل ما إذا نوى الأمي إمامة القارئ أو لم ينو لأن الوجه المذكور وهو ترك الفرض مع القدرة عليه بعد ظهور الرغبة في صلاة الجماعة يوجب الفساد وإن لم ينو، ودل كلامه على أن القارىء والأخرس إذا اقتديا بالأخرس فهو كذلك بالأولى، لكن ينبغي أن لا يصح شروع القارئ اتفاقاً لعدم الاستواء في التحريمة . وفي المجتبى : لو أم من يقرأ بالفارسية وهو لا يحسن العربية القارئين جاز عنده خلافاً لهما، والأخرس إذا أم خرساناً جازت صلاتهم بالاتفاق، وفي إمامة الأخرس الأمي اختلاف المشايخ .اهـ. فالحاصل أن إمامة الإنسان لمماثله صحيحة إلا إمامة المستحاضة والضالة والخنثى المشكل لمثله غير صحيحة ولمن دونه صحيحة مطلقاً ولمن فوقه لا تصح مطلقاً. وأما في المسألة الثانية فهو عندنا خلافاً لزفر لتأدي فرض القراءة، ولنا أن كل ركعة صلاة فلا تخلو عن القراءة، إما تحقيقاً أو تقديراً ولا تقدير في حق الأمي لانعدام الأهلية فقد استخلف من لا يصلح للإمامة ففسدت صلاتهم، أما صلاة الإمام فلأنه عمل كثير وصلاة القوم مبنية عليها. وشمل كلامه ما إذا قدمه في التشهد أي قبل الفراغ منه، أما لو استخلفه بعده فهو صحيح بالإجماع لخروجه من | الصلاة بصنعه، وقيل تفسد صلاتهم عنده لا عندهما والصحيح الأول. كذا في غاية البيان. وإنما اعتبر أبو حنيفة في مسائل الأمي قدرة الغير مع أن من أصله أن القادر بقدرة غيره ليس بقادر لأنه مقيد بما إذا تعلق باختيار ذلك الغير ، أما هنا الأمي قادر على الاقتداء بالقارئ من غير اختيار القارئ فينزل قادراً على القراءة. ولهذا قالوا: لو تحرم ناوياً أن لا يؤم أحداً فائتم به رجل صح اقتداؤه. وفي المغرب: الأمي في اللغة منسوب إلى أمة العرب وهي لم تكن تكتب ولا تقرأ فاستعير لكل من لا يعرف الكتابة والقراءة. وفي فتح القدير والأمي يجب عليه كل الاجتهاد في تعلم ما تصح به الصلاة ثم في القدر الواجب وإلا فهو آثم وقدمنا نحوه في إخراج الحرف الذي يقدر على إخراجه. وسئل ظهير الدين عن القيام هل يتقدر بالقراءة ؟ فقال : لا . وكذلك ذكر في اللاحق في الشافي اهـ. أي في الكتاب المسمى بالشافي للبيهقي. وفي الخلاصة : وإمامة الألثغ لغيره ذكر الفضيلي أنها جائزة وصحح في المجتبى عدم الجواز والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم.
Whoever is overtaken by hadath, he performs wudu and builds, and he appoints a successor if he is an imam, just as he would if he were prevented from recitation. This includes whether the ummi intended to lead a qari or not, because the stated factor—abandoning an obligation despite ability after showing desire for congregational prayer—necessitates invalidation even if he did not intend. His words indicate that if a qari and a mute follow a mute, it is even more so the case, but the starting of a qari [behind a mute] should not be valid by consensus due to lack of equality in the takbir. In al-Mujtaba: If one who recites in Persian, not knowing Arabic, leads qaris, it is permissible according to him (Abu Hanifa) contrary to them (the two companions). If a mute leads mutes, their prayer is valid by consensus. In the imamah of a mute ummi, there is disagreement among the shuyukh. The gist is that imamah of a person for his like is valid except for a mustahadah, a stray animal, and a hermaphrodite—these are not valid for their like. Imamah for someone lower than oneself is valid absolutely, and for someone higher is not valid absolutely. As for the second issue, it is with us contrary to Zufar because of the abandonment of the obligation of recitation. For us, every rak'ah is a prayer, and it is not devoid of recitation, either actually or virtually, and there is no virtual recitation for the ummi due to lack of capability. So he appointed someone unfit for imamah, thus their prayer is invalid. As for the imam's prayer, it is a great action and the people's prayer is built upon it. His words include when he appoints him in the tashahhud, i.e., before completing it. If he appoints him after, it is valid by consensus because he has left the prayer by his action. It is said their prayer is invalid according to him (Abu Hanifa) not according to them (the two), and the first is correct. Abu Hanifa considered ability through another in matters of the ummi, even though his principle is that one who is able through another is not able, because it is conditional upon the choice of that other. Here the ummi is able to follow the qari without the qari's choice, so he is considered able to recite. Therefore they said: if he performs the takbir intending not to lead anyone, and a man follows him, his following is valid. In al-Mughrib: al-ummi linguistically is attributed to the Arab nation, which did not write or read, so it is used metaphorically for one who does not know writing or reading. In Fath al-Qadir: The ummi must strive to learn what makes his prayer valid, then the obligatory amount, otherwise he sins. It was asked about standing: is it determined by recitation? He said no. In al-Khulasa: Imamah of an althagh (lisping) for others: al-Fudayli said it is permissible, but al-Mujtaba declared non-permissibility.
Source pages p. 642

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario when an imam is overtaken by hadath; he may appoint a substitute (khalifah) to lead the remaining prayer. The discussion extends to the validity of an ummi (illiterate) as imam. The key point is that an ummi can lead his like (other ummis), but leading a qari (one who can recite) is generally invalid unless under specific circumstances. The Hanafi position is that if an ummi intends to lead a qari, the prayer becomes invalid because the qari loses the ability to recite properly. However, if the ummi is appointed as a substitute when the original imam is unable to continue, there are conditions. The text also distinguishes between the imamah of a mute and an ummi, and discusses the ruling of the althagh (lisping person). The commentator concludes that imamah for a superior (i.e., leading someone who is more capable in recitation) is invalid, while leading an equal or inferior is valid.

Key Terms
أمي (ummi): An illiterate person who cannot read or recite the Quran properly.
استخلاف (istikhilaf): The appointment of a successor imam when the original imam is unable to continue due to hadath or other reasons.
قارئ (qari): One who can recite the Quran correctly and fluently.
الأخرس (al-akhras): A mute person who cannot speak or recite.
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that initiates the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, it is valid because the qari can recite quietly.
B) No, it is invalid because the ummi cannot fulfill the requirement of recitation on behalf of the followers.
C) Yes, but only if the ummi apologizes.
D) No, but if the ummi recites some verses, it becomes valid.

Key Takeaway
An ummi cannot lead a qari in prayer because every rak'ah requires recitation, which the ummi cannot provide, making the prayer invalid for the followers.

The Ruling on Building Prayer after Unintentional Hadath
Explaining the definition of hadath, the ruling to build prayer with wudu, and the condition that hadath be unintended (samaawi)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for building prayer after unintentional hadath and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding external causes.

Core Idea
A prayer interrupted by unintended hadath may be continued after wudu, but only if the hadath is not caused by any action of the person.

This lesson explores a unique Hanafi concession: when a person is overtaken by hadath during prayer through no fault of their own, they can perform wudu and continue from where they left off. However, this leniency comes with strict conditions, particularly that the hadath be 'samaawi'—heavenly or beyond human control. We will examine the proof from hadith, the precise definition of unintentional hadath, and the scholarly dispute within the Hanafi school regarding borderline cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
What is the hukm when one is overtaken by unintentional hadath during prayer? Note that the passage states 'فليتوضأ وليبن' and the author explains that this is based on a hadith, overriding the qiyas that would require restarting.
The ruling is wajib (the command to build), not merely permissible.
2
Extract the condition for building
The passage explicitly states the first condition: 'أن يكون الحدث سماوياً'. Understand what samaawi means—an event beyond the person's control, not caused by their own action or its direct cause.
Examples: vomiting, nosebleed (unintentional), madhiy.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi disagreement
The text presents cases where hadath is caused by an external object (e.g., falling brick, quince, tripping). Note the positions: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say no building; Abu Yusuf permits building. Identify which view is mufta bihi.
The commentator (al-Ramli) states the correct position is عدم البناء مطلقاً (no building absolutely).
4
Understand the application of tayammum
The passage clarifies that if water is unavailable, one performs tayammum and still builds. This is derived from the chapter on tayammum and is part of the concession.
The going and coming to find water do not invalidate the prayer because they are part of the building process.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقدمه على ما يفسدها، وقدمنا أن الحدث مانعية شرعية قائمة بالأعضاء إلى غاية استعمال المزيل. قوله : (ومن سبقه حدث توضأ وبنى) والقياس فسادها لأن الحدث ينافيها والمشي والانحراف يفسدانها فأشبه الحدث العمد ولنا قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «من قاء أو رعف أو أمذى فلينصرف وليتوضأ وليبن على صلاته ما لم يتكلم» ولا نزاع في صحته مرسلاً وهو حجة عندنا وعند أكثر أهل العلم ومذهبنا ثابت عن جماعة من الصحابة وكفى بهم قدوة فوجب ترك القياس، به والبلوى فيما يسبق دون ما يتعمده فلا يلحق به. ثم لجواز البناء شروط الأول أن يكون الحدث سماوياً وهو المراد بالسبق وهو ما لا اختيار للعبد فيه ولا في سببه فلا يبني بشجة وعضة ولو المصلي
The author placed it before what invalidates prayer, stating that hadath is a legal preventer (man'iyyah shar'iyyah) residing in the limbs until the remover is used. He said: 'And whoever is overtaken by hadath should perform wudu and build upon his prayer.' Analogy would require invalidation, but we have the prophetic hadith: 'Whoever vomits, or has a nosebleed, or experiences madhiy, should leave, perform wudu, and build upon his prayer as long as he does not speak.' This hadith, though mursal, is accepted and is a proof. Thus, analogy is set aside. The first condition for building is that the hadath be heavenly (samaawi), i.e., unintentional and beyond control. Thus, one does not build upon a wound or bite, even if self-inflicted. There is disagreement regarding a brick falling from a roof, a quince from a tree, or tripping over an object placed in the mosque causing blood. The relied-upon position is that building is not permitted. The author's statement 'and he performs wudu' means when he finds water and is able to use it; if he cannot find water, he performs tayammum, as is known from the chapter on tayammum. The question was asked about one who had hadath, went to perform wudu, found no water, performed tayammum, then returned and later found water—whether his prayer becomes invalid? He said no, because the going and coming are part of the prayer's ruling, but he did not add anything to the prayer. The commentary then discusses the case of 'from himself' and the various scenarios of falling objects, detailing the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. The correct position is that building is not allowed absolutely.
Source pages p. 643

Commentary
This passage begins with the definition of hadath as a man'iyyah shar'iyyah, a legal preventer that nullifies the state of purity and prevents prayer. The author then presents the ruling: when a person is overtaken by hadath during prayer unintentionally, he should perform wudu (or tayammum if no water) and then continue his prayer from where he left off. This is a concession based on a hadith, overriding the general rule that hadath invalidates prayer. The commentator notes that analogy would require restarting the prayer, but the hadith provides a specific exception. The first condition for this building is that the hadath be 'samaawi'—that is, beyond the person's control and not caused by his own action. For example, if he intentionally wounds himself, he cannot build. The passage then delves into a dispute regarding cases where the hadath is caused by an external object like a falling brick or a quince, or tripping. The majority of Hanafi scholars hold that in such cases, the prayer is invalid and must be restarted, except according to Abu Yusuf who permits building under certain conditions. The text also covers the case where the person has to travel to find water, and the ruling on tayammum when water is absent. The overall conclusion of the commentators is that building is not permitted in any case where the hadath is caused by an external object, and the correct view is that of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad (i.e., no building). The passage is important for students to understand the concept of 'unintentional' hadath and the limitations of the building concession.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): A legal preventer (man'iyyah shar'iyyah) that nullifies the state of purity and prohibits prayer until removed.
سبق (sabaq): Being overtaken unintentionally by hadath; the event occurs without the person's choice.
سماوي (samaawi): Heavenly; an event beyond human control, not caused by the person's own action.
بناء (bina'): The act of continuing the prayer from where one left off after performing wudu.
مانعية شرعية (man'iyyah shar'iyyah): A legal preventer that nullifies the validity of an act (here, prayer) until the obstacle is removed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for building prayer after hadath in the Hanafi school?
A) The hadath must be any type of impurity.
B) The hadath must be intentional.
C) The hadath must be unintentional (samaawi).
D) The hadath can be either intentional or unintentional.

Key Takeaway
Building upon prayer after hadath is only permitted when the hadath is unintentional and beyond the person's control; if caused by an external object, the preferred Hanafi view is to restart the prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Seven Conditions for Building After Hadath in Prayer
Exposition of the seven conditions for building after hadath in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven conditions for building after hadath and apply them to determine whether a prayer can be continued or must be restarted.

Core Idea
Building is only allowed if the hadath is from the body, unavoidable, minor, not rare, and followed by no prohibited actions.

When a person experiences a minor hadath (breaking of wudu) during prayer, the Hanafi school permits continuing from where one left off after performing wudu—this is called al-bina'. However, the school imposes strict conditions to ensure the sanctity of prayer is preserved. This lesson unpacks the seven conditions mentioned in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, including key intra-Hanafi disputes on specific cases.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two categories of conditions
Conditions 1-3 relate to the nature of the hadath itself; conditions 4-7 relate to the person's actions after the hadath.
2
Analyze conditions 1-3: type of hadath
Identify that the hadath must originate from the body (not external impurity), be unavoidable (like sneezing, not intentional), necessitate only wudu (not ghusl), and not be rare (e.g., fainting and laughter are excluded).
Note the disputes: sneezing vs. clearing throat, and the woman's cotton.
3
Analyze conditions 4-7: actions after hadath
Identify that after the hadath, the person must not perform any unnecessary action (e.g., drawing water without need), must not speak or gesture with intent to communicate, must leave immediately (unless excused), and must not perform a pillar (rukn) while in hadath.
Consider exceptions for need (e.g., covering private parts for wudu).
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi differences
Note where Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ, e.g., on the woman moving her cotton, and where al-Halabi's preference differs on sneezing vs. clearing throat.
These differences have practical implications for which opinion is relied upon (mufta bihi).
5
Apply the conditions to a scenario
Take a scenario and check each condition to decide whether building is allowed. If any condition is violated, the prayer must be restarted.
Example: sneeze -> building allowed; fainting -> building not allowed.

If hadath precedes him from his sneeze or clearing his throat, and if the woman's cotton falls wet without her action, she builds; and by moving it she does not build according to him, contrary to them. Second: that the hadath necessitate wudu, so he does not build from one who sleeps and has a wet dream in prayer, nor from one whom an impure substance preventing prayer afflicts without prior hadath, whether from his body or from outside. Third: that the hadath not be rare in occurrence, so he does not build from fainting and laughter, and this and the second the author will clearly state, and the insertion of speech here as in Fath al-Qadir while speech is invalidating, not hadath, because its condition is that he not bring something contradictory after it. Fourth: that he not do an action from which he has no alternative; if he does it, he must start over, like drawing water from a well according to the chosen view, or if his bucket was torn and he patched it, likewise if he found water for wudu and went to a more distant water without excuse like forgetfulness and the like, except if the near water is in a well as we have mentioned, or if it is little, the amount of two basins, as if he found a watering hole and left it and went to another adjacent to it, then he builds. Likewise if he closed the door with both hands not intending to cover his private parts; if it was for him, it does not invalidate, or with one hand it does not invalidate absolutely. Likewise if he carried a vessel without need with both hands; if there was a need, it does not invalidate absolutely, or with one hand it does not invalidate absolutely. Likewise if he performed wudu and returned, then he remembered... For al-Halabi the issue of sneezing and clearing the throat and the difference in it, then he said: The most apparent is that he builds, meaning in the case of sneezing because it is from heaven, and if he causes hadath by clearing his throat, the most apparent is that he does not build. His statement: (And the insertion of speech here etc.) is a response to what occurred in Fath al-Qadir where he mentioned speech and laughter in this place and he said: He does not build for laughter, speech, and wet dream, for we are talking about hadath, and speech is invalidating, not hadath, but he mentioned it with laughter because it is also among the conditions of building that he not bring something contradictory after the hadath, so he mentioned it here as if he did not do as the author did, because he first mentioned that the condition of building is that it be a heavenly hadath from the body not requiring ghusl, he has no choice in it nor in its cause, and no contradictory after it from which he has no alternative. Then he took the restrictors and said: So he does not build for a wound or a bite... until he said: And not for laughter, speech, and wet dream. So in his statement there is no implication that speech and what is with it are of one valley; rather he mentioned each of them for restriction and to clarify the benefit of the previous restrictions. His statement: (as if he drew water) it is appropriate to mention this case and the one after it under the fifth condition, as is not hidden. He said in al-Siraj: Among the conditions for the permissibility of building is not to do an action that contradicts from speech, eating, drinking, and drawing water from a well. And in al-Margheenan: He may draw water from a well and build if he has no other water. And al-Karkhi said: He does not build with drawing water from a well. End. And in Sharh al-Munyah: And if the water was distant and near him a well, he does not leave the well because drawing prevents building according to the chosen view, and it was said it does not prevent if he has nothing else. End. And the appropriate is what we said, because if the author's speech is interpreted as when he is able to do otherwise, as his last expression indicates, its implication would be the permissibility of drawing water if he is not able to do otherwise, which contradicts the apparent wording of al-Siraj where he made it like eating and drinking, and contradicts what is chosen of absolute prohibition as you knew, and if not interpreted that way, it is not from our subject matter, except that he chose contrary to what is in Sharh al-Munyah, and that is what is reported from al-Margheenan. His statement: (not intending to cover the private parts) it seems it is based on the permissibility of uncovering the private parts, and it will come that it invalidates the prayer. That he forgot something and went and took it, it becomes invalid; and if he uncovered his private parts for istinja, his prayer is invalidated in the apparent narration. Likewise if the woman unveiled her forearms for wudu, and that is correct. And in al-Zahiriya from Abu Ali al-Nasafi that if he had no alternative, it does not invalidate. Likewise the woman if she needs to build, she may uncover her private parts and limbs in wudu and wash if she finds no alternative to that, end. And he who is preceded by hadath performs wudu three times three, and wipes his entire head, and rinses his mouth and nose, and performs the other sunan. And it was said he performs wudu once once, and if he increases, it becomes invalid, and the first is more correct because the obligation is fulfilled by the whole. So in al-Zahiriya. And if he washes an impurity that afflicts him, if it is from preceding hadath, he builds; if from outside, he does not build; if from both, he does not build. And if he throws away the impure garment from non-hadath and he has other garments on him, it suffices him. So in al-Zahiriya. Fifth: that he not bring something contradictory to the prayer. If he speaks the speech of people after the hadath, it becomes invalid. And in al-Zahiriya: if he seeks water by gesture or buys it by hand-to-hand exchange, it becomes invalid. Sixth: that he leave immediately. If he remains the duration of performing a pillar without excuse, it becomes invalid; if there is an excuse, then no, as if he has hadath by sleep and remains an hour then wakes up, then he builds, or stays due to crowd as in al-Khaniya. And in al-Muntaqa: if he does not intend by his staying the prayer, it does not become invalid because he did not perform a part with the hadath. We say: He is in its sanctity, so what occurs from him suitable to be part of it is turned to that unbound by intention if he is not in need of it. And in al-Zahiriya: if nosebleed overcomes him and does not stop, he stays until it stops, then performs wudu and builds. Seventh: that he not perform a pillar with the hadath. If hadath precedes him in his prostration and he raises his head intending performance, he must start over. Likewise if he recites while going, not if he says subhanallah on the more correct view because it is not part of the integral. And in al-Mujtaba: he has hadath in his bowing or in his prostration, the prayer... apparent of the school. His statement: (And likewise if the woman uncovered her forearms) al-Ramli said: This contradicts what is in al-Sirajiya, for he said: The woman, if hadath precedes her and she uncovers her forearms when washing the hands, building is permissible for her according to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, and it is the chosen view. He says: (And in al-Zahiriya from Abu Ali al-Nasafi etc.) Qadikhan said: It is the correct one, and he distinguished between it and the case if she uncovered the private parts in the prayer from the beginning. So in al-Sharnabalaliya. His statement: (if he seeks water by gesture) Sheikh Ismail said: it is stated explicitly in al-Khaniya and al-Siraj. End. And it was questioned in al-Sharnabalaliya by the issue of repelling a passerby by gesture and by what is in al-Zaylai from al-Ghayah: A person in prayer is asked for something, and he gestures with his hand or head with yes or no, his prayer does not become invalid. And likewise in al-Bahr from al-Khulasa and others. Then he said: It is transmitted in al-Bahr from Sharh al-Majma' that if he replies to salam with his hand, it becomes invalid. He said: The truth is what al-Halabi mentioned, that invalidity is not established in the school; rather some have deduced it from what is in al-Zahiriya: A person in prayer shook hands with someone with the intention of salam, so his prayer becomes invalid. He said: Based on this, it becomes invalid also if he replies with a gesture, up to what the author will mention of preferring the non-invalidity of gesture. He said in al-Sharnabalaliya: So it is not far that it be...
Source pages p. 644

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, dealing with the chapter on hadath in prayer. The author expounds the seven conditions for building (al-bina') the prayer after an event of hadath. Building means continuing the prayer after performing wudu or removing impurity, without restarting. The first condition is that the hadath must be unavoidable from the body, such as sneezing or clearing the throat, or a woman's menstrual cotton falling without her action. If she moves it herself, she does not build according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the Sahibayn. The second condition is that the hadath must necessitate wudu only, not ghusl; thus one does not build if he sleeps and has a wet dream or is struck by a severe impurity that prevents prayer. The third condition is that the hadath not be rare, like fainting or laughter, which require a fresh start. The fourth condition is that the person do no unnecessary action; if he does, he must restart. Examples include drawing water from a well when another source is available, or carrying a vessel without need. However, if the action is necessary or done with one hand, it does not invalidate. The fifth condition is that after hadath, he must not do anything that contradicts the prayer, like speaking. The sixth is that he must leave immediately unless excused, e.g., if he falls asleep or is stuck in a crowd. The seventh is that he must not perform a pillar (like a ruku' or sujood) while in a state of hadath. The text also discusses related issues: a woman may uncover her forearms for wudu if necessary; washing impurities; and the ruling on seeking water by gesture. The commentary includes differences among Hanafi scholars, such as between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on moving the cotton, and between al-Halabi and others on sneezing. The relied-upon positions are highlighted, such as the majority view that building is allowed only when the hadath is heavenly and unavoidable.

Key Terms
البناء (al-bina'): Continuing the prayer after removing the cause of hadath without restarting from the beginning.
الحدث (al-hadath): An event that breaks wudu or requires ghusl, occurring during prayer.
المناف (al-munafi): Any action or speech that contradicts the sanctity of prayer and invalidates it if done intentionally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for building after hadath according to the Hanafi school?
A) The hadath must necessitate wudu, not ghusl.
B) The hadath must be rare, like laughter.
C) No action contradictory to prayer should be performed after the hadath.
D) The person must leave immediately unless excused.

Key Takeaway
Building after hadath in prayer is only allowed under seven strict conditions: the hadath must be from the body, unavoidable, require only wudu, not rare, and followed by no unnecessary actions, no speech, immediate departure, and no pillar.

Salah — Prayer

Conditions for Building Upon Prayer After Hadath (Conditions 5–12)
Commentary listing conditions 5-12 for building after hadath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the twelve conditions for building prayer after hadath and apply them to determine whether a prayer can be continued or must be restarted.

Core Idea
Building after hadath requires immediate departure, no contradictory actions, and no performance of pillars with impurity.

In the previous lessons, we learned that if a person has a hadath during prayer, he may perform wudu and continue the prayer from where he left off, rather than restarting entirely. However, this ruling of 'bina'' is subject to strict conditions. In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the commentator lists the fifth through twelfth conditions, clarifying what invalidates building and what preserves it. Understanding these conditions is essential for knowing when your prayer remains valid after an interruption for purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall ruling
The Hanafi school permits building (bina') after a hadath during prayer, meaning one can perform wudu and continue from where they stopped, provided specific conditions are met. The act of building is permissible (mubah), not obligatory.
Other schools have varying views; some require complete restart.
2
List the conditions from the text
Extract each condition (5th to 12th) from the passage. The fifth condition prohibits actions contradictory to prayer, such as speaking. The sixth requires immediate departure without undue delay. The seventh prohibits performing a pillar while still in a state of hadath. The eighth prohibits performing a pillar while walking during return. The ninth requires that the prior hadath does not reappear after purification. The tenth pertains to followers returning to an imam. The eleventh addresses remembering a missed prayer after a celestial hadath. The twelfth prevents an imam from appointing an unqualified substitute.
These conditions are detailed in various Hanafi works referenced.
3
Distinguish between conditions and invalidators
Some conditions are prerequisites for building to be valid (e.g., immediate departure), while some actions if performed invalidate the prayer regardless of building (e.g., speaking). Knowing which actions directly invalidate versus which only prevent building is crucial.
The text lists both types; for example, speaking invalidates outright, while remaining too long prevents building but does not necessarily invalidate if one intends to wait with an excuse.
4
Apply a condition to a scenario
Take a scenario: A person has a hadath during prayer, goes to perform wudu, and on the way back recites a verse of the Quran. According to condition 8 (not performing a pillar with walking), since recitation is a pillar, this invalidates the building and he must restart.
If he had merely said a tasbih (glorification), it is not a pillar and building remains valid.
5
Note the intra-madhab differences
The text mentions minor disputes: for example, regarding a woman uncovering her forearms for wudu during prayer. The correct view in the madhhab is that it is permitted if necessary, and building is allowed. Also, the issue of gesturing for water or replying to a greeting is debated; the preferred view is that it does not invalidate unless done with full intention.
These differences illustrate the nuanced application of the conditions.

Tenth: if he was a follower, that he returns to the imam if the imam has not finished, and if there is a barrier between them that prevents the permissibility of following. So if he was alone, he has a choice between returning and completing in the place of wudu, and they differed on what is better. And if he was a follower and his imam finished, then he does not return, and if he returns they differed on the invalidity of his prayer. So if there is no barrier between them, he may follow from his place without returning. Twelfth: if he was an imam, he does not appoint as substitute one who is not fit for imama, so if he appointed a woman, he starts over.
Source pages p. 645

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, detailing the conditions for building upon one's prayer after a hadath (ritual impurity) occurs during the prayer. The author begins by discussing cases where a person forgets something and goes to retrieve it, or uncovers the awra (private parts) for istinja (cleaning after relieving oneself), stating that these invalidate the prayer. He then addresses the specific rulings for a woman who needs to uncover her forearms for wudu; the correct view according to Abu Hanifa is that it is permitted if necessary, and she may build upon her prayer. The text then outlines the method of performing wudu for one who has a hadath during prayer: washing three times, wiping the entire head, rinsing the mouth and nose, and performing the other sunan. Some say washing once is sufficient, but the first view is preferred because the obligation is fulfilled by the whole act. The passage then systematically lists the conditions for building, starting from the fifth condition: 5) Not to perform something that contradicts the prayer, such as speaking or seeking water by gesture. 6) To leave immediately; any delay equivalent to performing a pillar without excuse invalidates the prayer, but delay due to an excuse such as sleeping or crowding is permissible. 7) Not to perform a pillar with the hadath; if one intentionally performs a pillar, he must restart. 8) Not to perform a pillar while walking during return. 9) That his prior hadath does not reappear after a 'celestial hadath' (e.g., breaking wudu again after having purified). 10) For a follower (muqtadi), he must return to the imam if the imam hasn't finished; if alone, he has a choice. 11) Not to remember a missed prayer after the celestial hadath if he is a person of order. 12) An imam must not appoint an unqualified substitute; if he appoints a woman, he must restart. Throughout, the commentary references various Hanafi works like al-Zahiriyya, al-Khaniyya, and al-Mujtaba, and includes a discussion on the permissibility of gestures, concluding that invalidity by gesture is not firmly established in the madhhab. The overall emphasis is on preserving the sequence and sanctity of the prayer while allowing necessary interruptions for purification.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): A state of ritual impurity that nullifies wudu, requiring purification before prayer can continue.
بناء (bina'): To resume the prayer from where it was interrupted after performing wudu, rather than starting the entire prayer anew.
إعادة (i'ada): To restart the prayer from the beginning after invalidation.
الحدث السماوي (al-hadath al-samawi): A 'celestial hadath' that occurs after purification, such as a second breaking of wudu or the end of a time period for a mustahada.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling if a person has a hadath during prayer and remains for the duration of performing a pillar without excuse?
A) His prayer remains valid and he builds after wudu.
B) His prayer becomes invalid and he must restart.
C) He may choose to build or restart.
D) It is permissible if he intended to wait.

Key Takeaway
Building after hadath is a concession in the Hanafi school, but it is strictly conditioned on immediate departure, avoidance of contradictory actions, and maintaining the sequence of prayer.

Ruling on Appointing a Substitute Imam (Istikhlaf) During Prayer
Explaining the ruling and procedure for istikhlaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on istikhlaf, explain the procedure and conditions, and apply the correct view when water is available.

Core Idea
Istikhlaf is recommended, not obligatory; the imam may instead perform wudu and build if water is present.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the procedure and ruling for an imam who experiences hadath during prayer. It clarifies that appointing a substitute (istikhlaf) is a sunnah, not an obligation, and provides gestures to indicate remaining actions. The text also addresses an intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether istikhlaf is ever obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Istikhlaf is the act of an imam appointing a substitute when he becomes invalidated by hadath. The Hanafi ruling is that it is sunnah (recommended), not obligatory.
The text uses phrases like 'the better choice' and 'the preferred view'.
2
Understand the procedure and gestures
The imam should gesture discreetly to indicate what remains: hand on knees for bowing, on forehead for prostration, on mouth for recitation, and fingers for rak'ahs. The sunnah is to simulate a nosebleed to avoid conversation.
Gestures are only needed if the deputy does not know what is left.
3
Note the condition: water availability
If water is available in the mosque, the imam should perform wudu and build (continue) without appointing a substitute. Istikhlaf is only preferred when water is not available.
This is based on preserving the congregation.
4
Recognize the intra-Hanafi difference
Ibn al-Malik in Sharh al-Majma' considered istikhlaf obligatory, but the majority view (al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) holds it as sunnah. The relied-upon position is the majority view.
The text advises 'tadabbur' (pondering) on this disagreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (واستخلف لو إماماً) معطوف على «توضأ» أي من سبقه حدث وكان إماماً فإنه يستخلف رجلاً مكانه يأخذ بثوب رجل إلى المحراب أو يشير إليه. والسنة أن يفعله محدودب الظهر واضعاً يده في أنفه يوهم أنه قد رعف لينقطع عنه كلام الناس، ولو تكلم بطلت صلاتهم، ولو ترك ركوعاً يشير بوضع يده على ركبتيه، أو سجوداً يشير بوضعها على جبهته أو قراءة يشير بوضعها على فمه، وإن بقي عليه ركعة واحدة يشير بأصبع واحدة، وإن كان اثنين فبأصبعين. هذا إذا لم يعلم الخليفة ذلك، أما إذا علم فلا حاجة إلى ذلك. ولسجدة التلاوة بوضع أصبعه على الجبهة واللسان، وللسهو على صدره، وقيل يحول رأسه يميناً وشمالاً كذا في الظهيرية ثم الاستخلاف ليس بمتعين حتى لو كان الماء في المسجد فإنه يتوضأ ويبني ولا حاجة إلى الاستخلاف كما ذكره الشارح. وإذا لم يكن في المسجد فالأفضل الاستخلاف كما ذكره المصنف في المستصفى بناء على أن الأفضل للإمام والمقتدي البناء صيانة للجماعة وللمنفرد الاستقبال تحرزاً عن الخلاف، وصححه في السراج الوهاج. وظاهر كلام المتون أن الاستئناف أفضل في حق الكل، فما في شرح المجمع لابن الملك من أنه يجب على الإمام الاستخلاف صيانة عدم فساد الصلاة بطلب الماء بالإشارة كرد السلام وغيره بالإشارة فتأمل. قوله: (وكذا لو قرأ في ذهابه) ظاهره أنه يستقبل بالقراءة ولو كان سبق الحدث في غير حالة القيام مع أن القراءة لا تكون ركناً إلا في القيام ثم رأيت في المعراج قال : وفي المجتبى أحدث في قيامه فسبح ذاهباً أو جائياً لم تفسد ولو قرأ فسدت، وقيل إنما تفسد إذا قرأ ذاهباً وقيل على العكس والمختار ما قلنا، ولو أحدث في ركوعه أو سجوده لا تفسد بالقراءة اهـ. قوله : (صيانة للجماعة) قال في النهر : وقيده في السراج بما إذا كان لا يجد جماعة أخرى وهو الصحيح، وقيل إذا كان في الوقت سعة وينبغي وجوبه.
His statement: (and he appoints a substitute if he is an imam) is conjoined to 'he performs wudu', meaning: one who is overtaken by a hadath and is an imam, then he appoints a man in his place who takes a man's garment to the mihrab or gestures to him. And the sunna is that he does it with a bent back, placing his hand in his nose, giving the impression that he has a nosebleed, so that people's talk may stop from him. And if he speaks, their prayer becomes invalid. And if he leaves (a pillar of) bowing, he gestures by placing his hand on his knees; or for prostration, he gestures by placing it on his forehead; or for recitation, he gestures by placing it on his mouth. And if there remains one rak'ah, he gestures with one finger; if two, with two fingers. This is when the deputy does not know that. But if he knows, there is no need for that. And for the prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawa), by placing his finger on the forehead and tongue, and for forgetfulness (sahw) on his chest; and it is said he turns his head right and left. Thus in al-Zahiriyya. Then, the appointment of a substitute is not determined (i.e., not obligatory). So if there is water in the mosque, he performs wudu and builds, and there is no need for appointment of a substitute, as the commentator mentioned. And if there is not in the mosque, then the preferred view is appointment of a substitute as the author mentioned in al-Mustasfa, based on the principle that the better choice for the imam and follower is to build, for the preservation of the congregation; and for the one praying alone, to start over, to be cautious against disagreement; and it was corrected in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And the apparent wording of the texts (mutun) is that starting over (isti'naf) is better for everyone. So what is in Sharh al-Majma' by Ibn al-Malik that it is obligatory upon the imam to appoint a substitute for the preservation of... not invalidating the prayer by seeking water by gesture, like replying to salutation by gesture etc., so ponder. His statement: (and likewise if he recited in his going) its apparent meaning is that he starts over with recitation, even if the hadath occurred in other than the standing state, while recitation is only a pillar in standing. Then I saw in al-Mi'raj: he said: and in al-Mujtaba: he had a hadath in his standing, then he glorified while going or coming, it does not become invalid; but if he recited, it becomes invalid. And it is said it becomes invalid only if he recited while going; and it is said the opposite; and the chosen view is what we said. And if he had a hadath in his bowing or prostration, it does not become invalid by recitation, end quote. His statement: (for preservation of the congregation) he said in al-Nahr: and it was restricted in al-Siraj to when he cannot find another congregation, and that is the correct view; and it is said when there is ample time, and it ought to be obligatory.
Source pages p. 646

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the issue of istikhlaf (appointing a substitute imam) when the original imam experiences a hadath during prayer. The text begins by explaining that the phrase 'wa istakhlafa law imaman' is connected to the ruling on wudu: if an imam is overtaken by a hadath, he should appoint a man to replace him by taking his garment to the mihrab or gesturing. It is sunnah to do this with a bent back and hand on nose to simulate a nosebleed, to prevent people from talking. The imam uses specific gestures to indicate which pillar remains: hand on knees for bowing, forehead for prostration, mouth for recitation, and fingers for number of rak'ahs. If the deputy already knows, no gesture is needed. For sajdat al-tilawa, he gestures to forehead and tongue; for sahw (forgetfulness), to chest or turning head. The passage then clarifies that istikhlaf is not obligatory (not mu'ayyan). If water is available in the mosque, the imam can simply perform wudu and continue without a substitute. Outside the mosque, istikhlaf is preferable to preserve the congregation. The preferred view for a solitary prayer is to restart to avoid disagreement. Some scholars consider istikhlaf obligatory, but the author advises caution. The text also addresses a related issue: if a person recites while walking after a hadath, the correct view is that if he recites in his going, it invalidates the prayer; but if he is in bowing or prostration, recitation does not invalidate. Finally, it mentions that the preservation of the congregation is restricted to situations where no other congregation is available, and some consider it obligatory when time is ample.

Key Terms
استخلاف (istikhlaf): The act of an imam appointing a substitute to lead the remainder of the prayer after he becomes invalidated by hadath.
خليفة (khalifah): The substitute imam appointed to continue leading the prayer.
محارب (mihrab): The niche indicating the direction of prayer; here it refers to the front of the mosque where the imam stands.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on istikhlaf for an imam when water is available in the mosque?
A) It is obligatory to appoint a substitute.
B) It is preferred but not required.
C) The imam should perform wudu and build without appointing a substitute.
D) The prayer becomes invalid and must be restarted.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, istikhlaf is sunnah, not wajib; the imam may instead perform wudu and continue his prayer if water is available, preserving the congregation without a substitute.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
8 min
Method of Istikhlaf: Gestures and Sunan
Explanation of the sunnah gestures for istikhlaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah method for an imam to appoint a khalifa using specific gestures and identify which gesture corresponds to each missed element.

Core Idea
The imam gestures discreetly to preserve the congregation's prayer.

When an imam experiences hadath during prayer, he must appoint a substitute without speaking. This lesson unpacks the recommended (sunnah) method described in the text: a bent back, hand on nose, and precise hand gestures to indicate missed actions. Understanding these details helps maintain the validity and discipline of congregational prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main scenario
Recognize that the imam is the one who experiences hadath and must appoint a khalifa. The text coordinates 'wa istakhlaf' with 'tawadda'' (he performed wudu).
The imam's hadath triggers the need for istikhlaf.
2
Learn the sunnah posture
The imam bends his back and places his hand on his nose as if he has a nosebleed, to stop people from talking. This is a physical signal.
The goal is to avoid speaking, which would invalidate the prayer.
3
Memorize the hand gestures
For missed ruku': hand on knees. For sujud: hand on forehead. For recitation: hand on mouth. For remaining rak'ahs: one finger for one, two fingers for two. For sajda tilawa: finger on forehead and tongue. For sahw: hand on chest. Also reported: turning head right and left.
These gestures are only needed if the khalifa does not know what is missing.
4
Note the exception
If the khalifa already knows the situation, gestures are unnecessary.
This simplifies the procedure when the appointed person is already aware.

يظهر إلا أن يضيق الوقت فينبغي الوجوب لئلا تفوت الجماعة تأمل. قوله : (أو قبل أن ينوي الإمام الإمامة هذا راجع إلى المسألة الأولى وهي ما إذا نوى الخليفة الإمامة من ساعته أي لم ينو تأخير نية الإمامة إلى ولا في الخانية. قوله: (وشرط جواز صلاة الخليفة والقوم أن يصل الخليفة إلى المحراب الخ يعني أو ينوي الخليفة الإمامة حين
His statement: 'And he should appoint a successor if he is an imam' is coordinated with 'he performed wudu', meaning if a hadath preceded him and he is an imam, then he should appoint a man in his place, taking a man's garment to the mihrab or gesturing to him. And the sunnah is that he does it with a bent back, placing his hand on his nose giving the impression that he has a nosebleed, so that people stop talking. If he speaks, their prayer becomes invalid. If he leaves a bowing, he gestures by placing his hand on his knees; for prostration, by placing it on his forehead; for recitation, by placing it on his mouth. If one rak'ah remains, he gestures with one finger; if two, with two fingers. This is if the khalifa does not know; if he knows, there is no need for that. For the prostration of recitation, by placing his finger on the forehead and tongue; for forgetfulness, on his chest. It is said he turns his head right and left, as in al-Zahiriyyah. Then istikhlaf is not necessary; if water is in the mosque, he performs wudu and builds (continues), and there is no need for istikhlaf. If not in the mosque, istikhlaf is preferable, as the author mentioned in al-Mustasfa, based on the view that building is preferable for the imam and the followers to preserve the congregation, while for the individual, starting over is preferable to avoid disagreement. Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj authenticated this. The apparent meaning of the matns is that starting over is better for everyone. So what is in Sharh al-Majma' by Ibn al-Malik about the obligation of istikhlaf to save the prayer from corruption by seeking water through gestures, like responding to salam and other gestures, is subject to consideration. His statement: 'Similarly if he recited while going' apparently means he should start recitation anew even if the hadath occurred in a non-standing state, although recitation is only a pillar when standing. Then I saw in al-Mi'raj: In al-Mujtaba, if he becomes impure while standing and glorifies Allah while going or coming, it does not invalidate; if he recited, it becomes invalid. It is said it invalidates only if he recites while going; it is said the opposite; and the chosen is what we said. If he becomes impure in ruku' or sujud, it does not invalidate by recitation. His statement: 'to preserve the congregation' - in al-Nahr, it is qualified in al-Siraj as when he cannot find another congregation, and that is correct. It is said if there is ample time, it should be obligatory for the people's prayer, but there is consideration. When he appoints a successor, he does not leave imamate merely by that; hence if someone follows him immediately before wudu, it is valid according to the correct view as in al-Muhit. For this, it is said in al-Zahiriyyah and al-Khaniyyah: if the imam performs wudu in the mosque and his deputy is standing in the mihrab without performing a pillar, then the deputy steps back and the imam steps forward. If the first imam leaves the mosque, performs wudu, then returns to the mosque while his deputy has not performed a pillar, then the second is the imam. Then istikhlaf is real and legal: the first is apparent, the second is that one man from the congregation steps forward before the imam leaves the mosque; then their prayer is permissible. If two men step forward, whichever reaches the place of imamate first is more entitled. If the imam appoints one and the congregation appoints another, the one appointed by the imam is more entitled. If both intend imamate together, the prayer of the follower of the imam's khalifa is valid, while that of the follower of the congregation's khalifa is invalid. If one of them steps forward, if it is the imam's khalifa, similarly; if it is the congregation's khalifa, and they follow him, then the other intends and some follow him, the prayer of the first is valid, but not of the latter. If some of the congregation appoint one and others another, the majority is considered; if equal, their prayer is invalid. If the imam appoints a khalifa from the last rows then leaves the mosque, if the khalifa intends imamate immediately, he becomes imam, and the prayer of those before him becomes invalid, but not his own prayer nor that of the first imam and those on his right and left in his row and those behind him. If he intends to be imam when he takes the place of the first, and the first leaves before the khalifa reaches his place or before he intends imamate, their prayer is invalid. The condition for the validity of the prayer of the khalifa and the congregation is that the khalifa reaches the mihrab before the imam leaves the mosque. Muhammad did not clarify the state of the imam. Al-Tahawi mentioned that his prayer is also invalid; Abu 'Ismah mentioned that his prayer is not invalid, and that is the most correct. If he does not appoint a khalifa in the mosque and appoints from the courtyard while there are people there, the prayer of all is permissible in constrained circumstances. His statement: 'so what is in Sharh al-Majma' etc. is not hidden regarding its weakness; indeed, the speech of the matns is about restarting, and the speech of Sharh al-Majma' is about istikhlaf. So what the matns indicate about restarting being preferable for the imam means that if he appoints a successor then performs wudu, it is preferable for him to restart his prayer and not build on what he prayed; this does not contradict istikhlaf being obligatory. Yes, it contradicts what he quoted from al-Mustasfa that istikhlaf is preferable, for the apparent meaning is its non-obligation, and it is the clear unless time is constrained, then obligation is appropriate so that the congregation is not lost. Consider. His statement: 'or before the khalifa intends imamate' refers to the first case, i.e., if the khalifa intends imamate immediately, i.e., he did not delay the intention until reaching the mihrab. It is better to drop it because the apparent meaning of 'immediately' is that he intended at the time of appointment, so it is inconceivable that the imam leaves the mosque before the khalifa intends imamate. For this reason, his statement 'or before he intends' is not mentioned in al-Dhakhira nor in al-Khaniyya. His statement: 'and the condition for the validity of the prayer of the khalifa and the congregation is that the khalifa reaches the mihrab' etc., meaning or that the khalifa intends imamate at the time.
Source pages p. 646

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the ruling of istikhlaf from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It explains the sunnah method for an imam who experiences hadath (ritual impurity) during prayer to appoint a substitute. The commentary begins by linking the phrase 'واستخلف لو إماماً' to the earlier rule of wudu. The imam should gesture to a specific man, bending his back and placing his hand on his nose to simulate a nosebleed, to avoid people speaking. If he speaks, their prayer becomes invalid. The text details specific hand gestures for missed elements: hand on knees for ruku', forehead for sujud, mouth for qira'ah, etc. A single remaining rak'ah is signaled with one finger, two with two. If the khalifa already knows the situation, gestures are unnecessary. The commentary then discusses the preference between istikhlaf and isti'naf (restarting): the author of al-Mustasfa preferred istikhlaf to preserve the congregation, while the matns generally favor isti'naf. Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj authenticated the preference for istikhlaf when no other congregation is available. The text resolves an apparent contradiction by explaining that isti'naf is better for the imam after he has already appointed a khalifa and performed wudu—he should restart his prayer from the beginning rather than building on it. This does not negate the obligation of istikhlaf in the first place when time is constrained. The commentary then explores various scenarios: the imam may appoint a khalifa and later return to lead, the khalifa's imamate becomes effective only if he intends it immediately and reaches the mihrab before the imam leaves the mosque. There are intra-Hanafi disputes: al-Tahawi held the imam's prayer invalid if he leaves before the khalifa reaches the mihrab, while Abu 'Ismah held it valid, and the latter is considered the most correct (al-ashahh). The section concludes with rulings on who is entitled to lead when multiple people step forward: the imam's appointee has priority, and if the congregation splits, the majority is followed. The overarching principle is to preserve the congregation's prayer and prevent its corruption.

Key Terms
استخلاف (istikhlaf): The act of the imam appointing a substitute (khalifa) to lead the prayer when he cannot continue due to hadath.
خليفة (khalifa): The person appointed by the imam to take his place in leading the prayer.
محراب (mihrab): The niche indicating the qibla direction; here, the place where the imam stands to lead.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What gesture should the imam make if he has missed a prostration (sajdah)?
A) Place hand on knees.
B) Place hand on forehead.
C) Place hand on mouth.
D) Place hand on chest.

Key Takeaway
The imam must use specific hand gestures, not speech, to appoint a khalifa and indicate missed elements.
