Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Ruling on Istikhlaf: Sunnah, Wajib, or Preferred?
Discussion of the ruling preference and obligation of istikhlaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish when istikhlaf is sunnah mu'akkadah and when it becomes wajib, and explain the preference between istikhlaf and isti'naf based on the preservation of the congregation.

Core Idea
Istikhlaf is sunnah unless time is tight, then wajib to save the congregation.

The commentators discuss whether istikhlaf is obligatory or recommended. The text clarifies that istikhlaf is not always required; if water is available in the mosque, the imam may perform wudu and continue without appointing a substitute. However, in constrained time, it becomes wajib to preserve the congregation's prayer. This lesson untangles the competing views and their practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling
Start with the matn's apparent preference: the text indicates that istikhlaf is not necessary if water is in the mosque; the imam can perform wudu and build (bina').
The default is sunnah, not wajib.
2
Assess when istikhlaf becomes preferable
When no water is in the mosque, istikhlaf is preferable (afdal) to preserve the congregation, as stated in al-Mustasfa. Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj authenticated this.
Preserving jama'ah is the key consideration.
3
Analyze the obligation claim
Ibn al-Malik in Sharh al-Majma' argued that istikhlaf is obligatory (wajib) to prevent the prayer from becoming corrupted by gestures. The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq rebuts this by distinguishing between the time of istikhlaf and the time of isti'naf.
Sharh al-Majma' speaks about the initial appointment; the matns speak about after wudu.
4
Resolve the contradiction
The apparent conflict is resolved: the matn's preference for isti'naf applies after the imam has already appointed a khalifa and performed wudu. In that situation, it is better for the imam to restart his prayer rather than build on it. This does not contradict the obligation of istikhlaf initially.
Thus there is no real contradiction.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that istikhlaf is sunnah mu'akkadah, but it becomes wajib when time is tight and no other congregation is available. Building (bina') is preferred over full restart.
This balances preservation of congregation and avoiding undue burden.

Source Text

قوله: (واستخلف لو إماماً) معطوف على «توضأ» أي من سبقه حدث وكان إماماً فإنه يستخلف رجلاً مكانه يأخذ بثوب رجل إلى المحراب أو يشير إليه. والسنة أن يفعله محدودب الظهر واضعاً يده في أنفه يوهم أنه قد رعف لينقطع عنه كلام الناس، ولو تكلم بطلت صلاتهم، ولو ترك ركوعاً يشير بوضع يده على ركبتيه، أو سجوداً يشير بوضعها على جبهته أو قراءة يشير بوضعها على فمه، وإن بقي عليه ركعة واحدة يشير بأصبع واحدة، وإن كان اثنين فبأصبعين. هذا إذا لم يعلم الخليفة ذلك، أما إذا علم فلا حاجة إلى ذلك. ولسجدة التلاوة بوضع أصبعه على الجبهة واللسان، وللسهو على صدره، وقيل يحول رأسه يميناً وشمالاً كذا في الظهيرية ثم الاستخلاف ليس بمتعين حتى لو كان الماء في المسجد فإنه يتوضأ ويبني ولا حاجة إلى الاستخلاف كما ذكره الشارح. وإذا لم يكن في المسجد فالأفضل الاستخلاف كما ذكره المصنف في المستصفى بناء على أن الأفضل للإمام والمقتدي البناء صيانة للجماعة وللمنفرد الاستقبال تحرزاً عن الخلاف، وصححه في السراج الوهاج. وظاهر كلام المتون أن الاستئناف أفضل في حق الكل، فما في شرح المجمع لابن الملك من أنه يجب على الإمام الاستخلاف صيانة عدم فساد الصلاة بطلب الماء بالإشارة كرد السلام وغيره بالإشارة فتأمل. قوله: (وكذا لو قرأ في ذهابه) ظاهره أنه يستقبل بالقراءة ولو كان سبق الحدث في غير حالة القيام مع أن القراءة لا تكون ركناً إلا في القيام ثم رأيت في المعراج قال : وفي المجتبى أحدث في قيامه فسبح ذاهباً أو جائياً لم تفسد ولو قرأ فسدت، وقيل إنما تفسد إذا قرأ ذاهباً وقيل على العكس والمختار ما قلنا، ولو أحدث في ركوعه أو سجوده لا تفسد بالقراءة اهـ. قوله : (صيانة للجماعة) قال في النهر : وقيده في السراج بما إذا كان لا يجد جماعة أخرى وهو الصحيح، وقيل إذا كان في الوقت سعة وينبغي وجوبه لصلاة القوم ففيه نظر، وإذا استخلف لا يخرج الإمام عن الإمامة بمجرده، ولهذا لو اقتدى به إنسان من ساعته قبل الوضوء فإنه صحيح على الصحيح كما في المحيط، ولهذا قال في الظهيرية والخانية : إن الإمام لو توضأ في المسجد وخليفته قائم في المحراب ولم يؤد ركناً فإنه يتأخر الخليفة ويتقدم الإمام. ولو خرج الإمام الأول من المسجد وتوضأ ثم رجع إلى المسجد وخليفته لم يؤد ركناً فالإمام هو الثاني. ثم الاستخلاف حقيقي وحكمي؛ فالأول ظاهر والثاني أن يتقدم رجل واحد من القوم قبل أن يخرج الإمام من المسجد فإن صلاتهم جائزة، ولو تقدم رجلان فأيهما سبق إلى مكان الإمامة فهو أولى، ولو قدم الإمام رجلاً والقوم رجلاً فمن قدمه الإمام فهو أولى، وإن نويا معاً الإمامة جاز صلاة المقتدي بخليفة الإمام وفسدت على المقتدي بخليفة القوم. وإن تقدم أحدهما إن كان خليفة الإمام فكذلك، وإن كان خليفة القوم فاقتدوا به ثم نوى الآخر فاقتدى به البعض جاز صلاة الأولين دون الآخرين ولو قدم بعض القوم رجلاً والبعض رجلاً فالعبرة للأكثر، ولو استويا فسدت صلاتهم. ولو استخلف الإمام من آخر الصفوف ثم خرج من المسجد إن نوى الخليفة الإمامة من ساعته صار إماماً فتفسد صلاة من كان متقدمه دون صلاته وصلاة الإمام الأول ومن على يمينه وشماله في صفه ومن خلفه، وإن نوى أن يكون إماماً إذا قام مقام الأول وخرج الأول قبل أن يصل الخليفة إلى مكانه أو قبل أن ينوي الإمامة فسدت صلاتهم وشرط جواز صلاة الخليفة والقوم أن يصل الخليفة إلى المحراب قبل أن يخرج الإمام عن المسجد، ولم يبين محمد حال الإمام. وذكر الطحاوي أن صلاته فاسدة أيضاً، وذكر أبو عصمة أن صلاته لا تفسد وهو الأصح. ولو لم يستخلف في المسجد واستخلف من الرحبة وفيها قوم جازت صلاة الكل عند الضيق قوله : (فما في شرح المجمع (الخ لا يخفى ما فيه على النبية فإن كلام المتون في الاستئناف وكلام شرح المجمع في الاستخلاف فما أفاده كلام المتون من أن الأفضل في حق الإمام الاستئناف معناه إذا استخلف ثم توضأ فالأفضل في حقه أن يستأنف صلاته ولا يبني على ما صلى فلا ينافي كون الاستخلاف واجباً . نعم ينافيه ما نقله عن المستصفى من أن الاستخلاف أفضل فإن المتبادر منه عدم وجوبه وهو الذي يظهر إلا أن يضيق الوقت فينبغي الوجوب لئلا تفوت الجماعة تأمل. قوله : (أو قبل أن ينوي الإمام الإمامة هذا راجع إلى المسألة الأولى وهي ما إذا نوى الخليفة الإمامة من ساعته أي لم ينو تأخير نية الإمامة إلى أن يصل إلى المحراب، والأولى إسقاطه لأن المتبادر من قوله من ساعته أنه نوى حين الاستخلاف فلا يتصور خروج الإمام من المسجد قبل أن ينوي الخليفة الإمامة، ولذا لم يذكر قوله أو قبل أن ينوي الخ) لا في الذخيرة ولا في الخانية. قوله: (وشرط جواز صلاة الخليفة والقوم أن يصل الخليفة إلى المحراب الخ يعني أو ينوي الخليفة الإمامة حين
His statement: 'And he should appoint a successor if he is an imam' is coordinated with 'he performed wudu', meaning if a hadath preceded him and he is an imam, then he should appoint a man in his place, taking a man's garment to the mihrab or gesturing to him. And the sunnah is that he does it with a bent back, placing his hand on his nose giving the impression that he has a nosebleed, so that people stop talking. If he speaks, their prayer becomes invalid. If he leaves a bowing, he gestures by placing his hand on his knees; for prostration, by placing it on his forehead; for recitation, by placing it on his mouth. If one rak'ah remains, he gestures with one finger; if two, with two fingers. This is if the khalifa does not know; if he knows, there is no need for that. For the prostration of recitation, by placing his finger on the forehead and tongue; for forgetfulness, on his chest. It is said he turns his head right and left, as in al-Zahiriyyah. Then istikhlaf is not necessary; if water is in the mosque, he performs wudu and builds (continues), and there is no need for istikhlaf. If not in the mosque, istikhlaf is preferable, as the author mentioned in al-Mustasfa, based on the view that building is preferable for the imam and the followers to preserve the congregation, while for the individual, starting over is preferable to avoid disagreement. Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj authenticated this. The apparent meaning of the matns is that starting over is better for everyone. So what is in Sharh al-Majma' by Ibn al-Malik about the obligation of istikhlaf to save the prayer from corruption by seeking water through gestures, like responding to salam and other gestures, is subject to consideration. His statement: 'Similarly if he recited while going' apparently means he should start recitation anew even if the hadath occurred in a non-standing state, although recitation is only a pillar when standing. Then I saw in al-Mi'raj: In al-Mujtaba, if he becomes impure while standing and glorifies Allah while going or coming, it does not invalidate; if he recited, it becomes invalid. It is said it invalidates only if he recites while going; it is said the opposite; and the chosen is what we said. If he becomes impure in ruku' or sujud, it does not invalidate by recitation. His statement: 'to preserve the congregation' - in al-Nahr, it is qualified in al-Siraj as when he cannot find another congregation, and that is correct. It is said if there is ample time, it should be obligatory for the people's prayer, but there is consideration. When he appoints a successor, he does not leave imamate merely by that; hence if someone follows him immediately before wudu, it is valid according to the correct view as in al-Muhit. For this, it is said in al-Zahiriyyah and al-Khaniyyah: if the imam performs wudu in the mosque and his deputy is standing in the mihrab without performing a pillar, then the deputy steps back and the imam steps forward. If the first imam leaves the mosque, performs wudu, then returns to the mosque while his deputy has not performed a pillar, then the second is the imam. Then istikhlaf is real and legal: the first is apparent, the second is that one man from the congregation steps forward before the imam leaves the mosque; then their prayer is permissible. If two men step forward, whichever reaches the place of imamate first is more entitled. If the imam appoints one and the congregation appoints another, the one appointed by the imam is more entitled. If both intend imamate together, the prayer of the follower of the imam's khalifa is valid, while that of the follower of the congregation's khalifa is invalid. If one of them steps forward, if it is the imam's khalifa, similarly; if it is the congregation's khalifa, and they follow him, then the other intends and some follow him, the prayer of the first is valid, but not of the latter. If some of the congregation appoint one and others another, the majority is considered; if equal, their prayer is invalid. If the imam appoints a khalifa from the last rows then leaves the mosque, if the khalifa intends imamate immediately, he becomes imam, and the prayer of those before him becomes invalid, but not his own prayer nor that of the first imam and those on his right and left in his row and those behind him. If he intends to be imam when he takes the place of the first, and the first leaves before the khalifa reaches his place or before he intends imamate, their prayer is invalid. The condition for the validity of the prayer of the khalifa and the congregation is that the khalifa reaches the mihrab before the imam leaves the mosque. Muhammad did not clarify the state of the imam. Al-Tahawi mentioned that his prayer is also invalid; Abu 'Ismah mentioned that his prayer is not invalid, and that is the most correct. If he does not appoint a khalifa in the mosque and appoints from the courtyard while there are people there, the prayer of all is permissible in constrained circumstances. His statement: 'so what is in Sharh al-Majma' etc. is not hidden regarding its weakness; indeed, the speech of the matns is about restarting, and the speech of Sharh al-Majma' is about istikhlaf. So what the matns indicate about restarting being preferable for the imam means that if he appoints a successor then performs wudu, it is preferable for him to restart his prayer and not build on what he prayed; this does not contradict istikhlaf being obligatory. Yes, it contradicts what he quoted from al-Mustasfa that istikhlaf is preferable, for the apparent meaning is its non-obligation, and it is the clear unless time is constrained, then obligation is appropriate so that the congregation is not lost. Consider. His statement: 'or before the khalifa intends imamate' refers to the first case, i.e., if the khalifa intends imamate immediately, i.e., he did not delay the intention until reaching the mihrab. It is better to drop it because the apparent meaning of 'immediately' is that he intended at the time of appointment, so it is inconceivable that the imam leaves the mosque before the khalifa intends imamate. For this reason, his statement 'or before he intends' is not mentioned in al-Dhakhira nor in al-Khaniyya. His statement: 'and the condition for the validity of the prayer of the khalifa and the congregation is that the khalifa reaches the mihrab' etc., meaning or that the khalifa intends imamate at the time.
Source pages p. 646

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the ruling of istikhlaf from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It explains the sunnah method for an imam who experiences hadath (ritual impurity) during prayer to appoint a substitute. The commentary begins by linking the phrase 'واستخلف لو إماماً' to the earlier rule of wudu. The imam should gesture to a specific man, bending his back and placing his hand on his nose to simulate a nosebleed, to avoid people speaking. If he speaks, their prayer becomes invalid. The text details specific hand gestures for missed elements: hand on knees for ruku', forehead for sujud, mouth for qira'ah, etc. A single remaining rak'ah is signaled with one finger, two with two. If the khalifa already knows the situation, gestures are unnecessary. The commentary then discusses the preference between istikhlaf and isti'naf (restarting): the author of al-Mustasfa preferred istikhlaf to preserve the congregation, while the matns generally favor isti'naf. Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj authenticated the preference for istikhlaf when no other congregation is available. The text resolves an apparent contradiction by explaining that isti'naf is better for the imam after he has already appointed a khalifa and performed wudu—he should restart his prayer from the beginning rather than building on it. This does not negate the obligation of istikhlaf in the first place when time is constrained. The commentary then explores various scenarios: the imam may appoint a khalifa and later return to lead, the khalifa's imamate becomes effective only if he intends it immediately and reaches the mihrab before the imam leaves the mosque. There are intra-Hanafi disputes: al-Tahawi held the imam's prayer invalid if he leaves before the khalifa reaches the mihrab, while Abu 'Ismah held it valid, and the latter is considered the most correct (al-ashahh). The section concludes with rulings on who is entitled to lead when multiple people step forward: the imam's appointee has priority, and if the congregation splits, the majority is followed. The overarching principle is to preserve the congregation's prayer and prevent its corruption.

Key Terms
بناء (bina'): Continuing the prayer from where it was interrupted after wudu, without starting over.
استئناف (isti'naf): Restarting the prayer from the beginning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does istikhlaf become wajib according to the relied-upon Hanafi position?
A) Always, because the imam must preserve the congregation.
B) Only if water is available in the mosque.
C) When the congregation would otherwise lose the prayer due to constrained time and lack of other congregation.
D) Never, because restarting is always better.

Key Takeaway
Istikhlaf is sunnah mu'akkadah, but wajib when time is tight to preserve the congregation.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Conditions for the Khalifa's Imamate and Intra-Hanafi Disputes
Conditions for validity of the khalifa's imamate and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for the validity of the khalifa's prayer, explain the dispute between al-Tahawi and Abu 'Ismah, and apply the correct position.

Core Idea
The khalifa's prayer is valid only if he reaches the mihrab before the imam leaves.

The commentary details the precise conditions for the khalifa to become imam and for the congregation's prayer to remain valid. It also records an important intra-Hanafi disagreement: does the original imam's prayer become invalid if he leaves before the khalifa reaches the mihrab? This lesson clarifies these conditions and the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic condition
The text states that the validity of the khalifa's prayer and the congregation's prayer depends on the khalifa reaching the mihrab before the imam leaves the mosque.
Reaching the mihrab is the key moment.
2
Note the intention requirement
The khalifa must intend imamate; it can be immediate or delayed until he reaches the mihrab. If he delays intention and the imam leaves before he intends, the prayer becomes invalid.
Intention is a separate condition from physical arrival.
3
Understand the dispute
Imam Muhammad did not specify the ruling on the original imam's prayer. Al-Tahawi said it becomes invalid; Abu 'Ismah said it remains valid. The commentator declares Abu 'Ismah's view as the most correct (al-ashahh).
The dispute is about the imam's own prayer, not the congregation's.
4
Apply the condition in scenarios
If the imam leaves before the khalifa intends, all prayers (imam, khalifa, congregation) are invalid. If the khalifa intends immediately but the imam leaves before the khalifa reaches, the imam's prayer is valid per Abu 'Ismah.
This shows the practical outcome of the dispute.

رأيت في المعراج قال : وفي المجتبى أحدث في قيامه فسبح ذاهباً أو جائياً لم تفسد ولو قرأ فسدت، وقيل إنما تفسد إذا قرأ ذاهباً وقيل على العكس والمختار ما قلنا، ولو أحدث في ركوعه أو سجوده لا تفسد بالقراءة بمجرده، ولهذا لو اقتدى به إنسان من ساعته قبل الوضوء فإنه صحيح على الصحيح كما في المحيط، ولهذا قال في الظهيرية والخانية : إن الإمام لو توضأ في المسجد وخليفته قائم في المحراب ولم يؤد ركناً فإنه يتأخر الخليفة ويتقدم الإمام. ولو خرج الإمام الأول من المسجد وتوضأ ثم رجع إلى المسجد وخليفته لم يؤد ركناً فالإمام هو الثاني. ثم الاستخلاف حقيقي وحكمي؛ فالأول ظاهر والثاني أن يتقدم رجل واحد من القوم قبل أن يخرج الإمام من المسجد فإن صلاتهم جائزة، ولو تقدم رجلان فأيهما سبق إلى مكان الإمامة فهو أولى، ولو قدم الإمام رجلاً والقوم رجلاً فمن قدمه الإمام فهو أولى، وإن نويا معاً الإمامة جاز صلاة المقتدي بخليفة الإمام وفسدت على المقتدي بخليفة القوم. وإن تقدم أحدهما إن كان خليفة الإمام فكذلك، وإن كان خليفة القوم فاقتدوا به ثم نوى الآخر فاقتدى به البعض جاز صلاة الأولين دون الآخرين ولو قدم بعض القوم رجلاً والبعض رجلاً فالعبرة للأكثر، ولو استويا فسدت صلاتهم. ولو استخلف الإمام من آخر الصفوف ثم خرج من المسجد إن نوى الخليفة الإمامة من ساعته صار إماماً فتفسد صلاة من كان متقدمه دون صلاته وصلاة الإمام الأول ومن على يمينه وشماله في صفه ومن خلفه، وإن نوى أن يكون إماماً إذا قام مقام الأول وخرج الأول قبل أن يصل الخليفة إلى مكانه أو قبل أن ينوي الإمامة فسدت صلاتهم وشرط جواز صلاة الخليفة والقوم أن يصل الخليفة إلى المحراب قبل أن يخرج الإمام عن المسجد، ولم يبين محمد حال الإمام. وذكر الطحاوي أن صلاته فاسدة أيضاً، وذكر أبو عصمة أن صلاته لا تفسد وهو الأصح. ولو لم يستخلف في المسجد واستخلف من الرحبة وفيها قوم جازت صلاة الكل عند الضيق قوله : (فما في شرح المجمع (الخ لا يخفى ما فيه على النبية فإن كلام المتون في الاستئناف وكلام شرح المجمع في الاستخلاف فما أفاده كلام المتون من أن الأفضل في حق الإمام الاستئناف معناه إذا استخلف ثم توضأ فالأفضل في حقه أن يستأنف صلاته ولا يبني على ما صلى فلا ينافي كون الاستخلاف واجباً . نعم ينافيه ما نقله عن المستصفى من أن الاستخلاف أفضل فإن المتبادر منه عدم وجوبه وهو الذي يظهر إلا أن يضيق الوقت فينبغي الوجوب لئلا تفوت الجماعة تأمل. قوله : (أو قبل أن ينوي الإمام الإمامة هذا راجع إلى المسألة الأولى وهي ما إذا نوى الخليفة الإمامة من ساعته أي لم ينو تأخير نية الإمامة إلى أن يصل إلى المحراب، والأولى إسقاطه لأن المتبادر من قوله من ساعته أنه نوى حين الاستخلاف فلا يتصور خروج الإمام من المسجد قبل أن ينوي الخليفة الإمامة، ولذا لم يذكر قوله أو قبل أن ينوي الخ) لا في الذخيرة ولا في الخانية. قوله: (وشرط جواز صلاة الخليفة والقوم أن يصل الخليفة إلى المحراب الخ يعني أو ينوي الخليفة الإمامة حين
His statement: 'And he should appoint a successor if he is an imam' is coordinated with 'he performed wudu', meaning if a hadath preceded him and he is an imam, then he should appoint a man in his place, taking a man's garment to the mihrab or gesturing to him. And the sunnah is that he does it with a bent back, placing his hand on his nose giving the impression that he has a nosebleed, so that people stop talking. If he speaks, their prayer becomes invalid. If he leaves a bowing, he gestures by placing his hand on his knees; for prostration, by placing it on his forehead; for recitation, by placing it on his mouth. If one rak'ah remains, he gestures with one finger; if two, with two fingers. This is if the khalifa does not know; if he knows, there is no need for that. For the prostration of recitation, by placing his finger on the forehead and tongue; for forgetfulness, on his chest. It is said he turns his head right and left, as in al-Zahiriyyah. Then istikhlaf is not necessary; if water is in the mosque, he performs wudu and builds (continues), and there is no need for istikhlaf. If not in the mosque, istikhlaf is preferable, as the author mentioned in al-Mustasfa, based on the view that building is preferable for the imam and the followers to preserve the congregation, while for the individual, starting over is preferable to avoid disagreement. Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj authenticated this. The apparent meaning of the matns is that starting over is better for everyone. So what is in Sharh al-Majma' by Ibn al-Malik about the obligation of istikhlaf to save the prayer from corruption by seeking water through gestures, like responding to salam and other gestures, is subject to consideration. His statement: 'Similarly if he recited while going' apparently means he should start recitation anew even if the hadath occurred in a non-standing state, although recitation is only a pillar when standing. Then I saw in al-Mi'raj: In al-Mujtaba, if he becomes impure while standing and glorifies Allah while going or coming, it does not invalidate; if he recited, it becomes invalid. It is said it invalidates only if he recites while going; it is said the opposite; and the chosen is what we said. If he becomes impure in ruku' or sujud, it does not invalidate by recitation. His statement: 'to preserve the congregation' - in al-Nahr, it is qualified in al-Siraj as when he cannot find another congregation, and that is correct. It is said if there is ample time, it should be obligatory for the people's prayer, but there is consideration. When he appoints a successor, he does not leave imamate merely by that; hence if someone follows him immediately before wudu, it is valid according to the correct view as in al-Muhit. For this, it is said in al-Zahiriyyah and al-Khaniyyah: if the imam performs wudu in the mosque and his deputy is standing in the mihrab without performing a pillar, then the deputy steps back and the imam steps forward. If the first imam leaves the mosque, performs wudu, then returns to the mosque while his deputy has not performed a pillar, then the second is the imam. Then istikhlaf is real and legal: the first is apparent, the second is that one man from the congregation steps forward before the imam leaves the mosque; then their prayer is permissible. If two men step forward, whichever reaches the place of imamate first is more entitled. If the imam appoints one and the congregation appoints another, the one appointed by the imam is more entitled. If both intend imamate together, the prayer of the follower of the imam's khalifa is valid, while that of the follower of the congregation's khalifa is invalid. If one of them steps forward, if it is the imam's khalifa, similarly; if it is the congregation's khalifa, and they follow him, then the other intends and some follow him, the prayer of the first is valid, but not of the latter. If some of the congregation appoint one and others another, the majority is considered; if equal, their prayer is invalid. If the imam appoints a khalifa from the last rows then leaves the mosque, if the khalifa intends imamate immediately, he becomes imam, and the prayer of those before him becomes invalid, but not his own prayer nor that of the first imam and those on his right and left in his row and those behind him. If he intends to be imam when he takes the place of the first, and the first leaves before the khalifa reaches his place or before he intends imamate, their prayer is invalid. The condition for the validity of the prayer of the khalifa and the congregation is that the khalifa reaches the mihrab before the imam leaves the mosque. Muhammad did not clarify the state of the imam. Al-Tahawi mentioned that his prayer is also invalid; Abu 'Ismah mentioned that his prayer is not invalid, and that is the most correct. If he does not appoint a khalifa in the mosque and appoints from the courtyard while there are people there, the prayer of all is permissible in constrained circumstances. His statement: 'so what is in Sharh al-Majma' etc. is not hidden regarding its weakness; indeed, the speech of the matns is about restarting, and the speech of Sharh al-Majma' is about istikhlaf. So what the matns indicate about restarting being preferable for the imam means that if he appoints a successor then performs wudu, it is preferable for him to restart his prayer and not build on what he prayed; this does not contradict istikhlaf being obligatory. Yes, it contradicts what he quoted from al-Mustasfa that istikhlaf is preferable, for the apparent meaning is its non-obligation, and it is the clear unless time is constrained, then obligation is appropriate so that the congregation is not lost. Consider. His statement: 'or before the khalifa intends imamate' refers to the first case, i.e., if the khalifa intends imamate immediately, i.e., he did not delay the intention until reaching the mihrab. It is better to drop it because the apparent meaning of 'immediately' is that he intended at the time of appointment, so it is inconceivable that the imam leaves the mosque before the khalifa intends imamate. For this reason, his statement 'or before he intends' is not mentioned in al-Dhakhira nor in al-Khaniyya. His statement: 'and the condition for the validity of the prayer of the khalifa and the congregation is that the khalifa reaches the mihrab' etc., meaning or that the khalifa intends imamate at the time.
Source pages p. 646

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the ruling of istikhlaf from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It explains the sunnah method for an imam who experiences hadath (ritual impurity) during prayer to appoint a substitute. The commentary begins by linking the phrase 'واستخلف لو إماماً' to the earlier rule of wudu. The imam should gesture to a specific man, bending his back and placing his hand on his nose to simulate a nosebleed, to avoid people speaking. If he speaks, their prayer becomes invalid. The text details specific hand gestures for missed elements: hand on knees for ruku', forehead for sujud, mouth for qira'ah, etc. A single remaining rak'ah is signaled with one finger, two with two. If the khalifa already knows the situation, gestures are unnecessary. The commentary then discusses the preference between istikhlaf and isti'naf (restarting): the author of al-Mustasfa preferred istikhlaf to preserve the congregation, while the matns generally favor isti'naf. Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj authenticated the preference for istikhlaf when no other congregation is available. The text resolves an apparent contradiction by explaining that isti'naf is better for the imam after he has already appointed a khalifa and performed wudu—he should restart his prayer from the beginning rather than building on it. This does not negate the obligation of istikhlaf in the first place when time is constrained. The commentary then explores various scenarios: the imam may appoint a khalifa and later return to lead, the khalifa's imamate becomes effective only if he intends it immediately and reaches the mihrab before the imam leaves the mosque. There are intra-Hanafi disputes: al-Tahawi held the imam's prayer invalid if he leaves before the khalifa reaches the mihrab, while Abu 'Ismah held it valid, and the latter is considered the most correct (al-ashahh). The section concludes with rulings on who is entitled to lead when multiple people step forward: the imam's appointee has priority, and if the congregation splits, the majority is followed. The overarching principle is to preserve the congregation's prayer and prevent its corruption.

Key Terms
الطحاوي (al-Tahawi): A prominent Hanafi scholar (d. 321 AH) known for his work on ikhtilaf.
أبو عصمة (Abu 'Ismah): A Hanafi scholar whose view is considered the most correct (al-ashahh) in this issue.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling on the original imam's prayer if the khalifa reaches the mihrab after the imam has left the mosque?
A) The imam's prayer is valid.
B) The imam's prayer is invalid.
C) The imam's prayer is valid only if he intended to return.
D) The imam's prayer is suspended until the khalifa's prayer is completed.

Key Takeaway
The khalifa's prayer requires reaching the mihrab before the imam leaves; the imam's own prayer remains valid per the relied-upon view.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
8 min
Basic Principle and Types of Istikhlaf
Fundamental rule and types of istikhlaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between real and legal istikhlaf and state the basic principle that the imam does not leave imamate by mere appointment.

Core Idea
The imam remains imam until the substitute actually leads a rak'ah or intends imamate.

This lesson covers the foundational principle of istikhlaf: the imam does not automatically lose his role when he appoints a substitute. We will explore the difference between real and legal istikhlaf, and how the congregation's prayer is affected when a member steps forward without explicit appointment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic principle
Read the opening statement: 'When he appoints a substitute, the imam does not leave the imamate by his mere act.' This is the foundational rule. Note that the imam's imamate persists until the substitute actually leads a rak'ah or intends imamate.
This principle is from al-Muhit.
2
Distinguish real vs legal istikhlaf
Real istikhlaf is when the imam explicitly designates a substitute. Legal istikhlaf occurs when a member of the congregation steps forward before the imam leaves the mosque. Understand that both are valid but have different conditions.
Legal istikhlaf is also called 'hukmi'.
3
Apply the rule to multiple candidates
If two step forward, the one reaching the imam's place first has priority. If the imam appoints one and the people appoint another, the imam's choice prevails. If both intend imamate, followers of the imam's substitute pray validly, followers of the people's substitute pray invalidly.
This shows the superiority of the imam's appointment.

كتاب الصلاة - باب الحدث في الصلاة

لصلاة القوم ففيه نظر، وإذا استخلف لا يخرج الإمام عن الإمامة بمجرده، ولهذا لو اقتدى به إنسان من ساعته قبل الوضوء فإنه صحيح على الصحيح كما في المحيط، ولهذا قال في الظهيرية والخانية : إن الإمام لو توضأ في المسجد وخليفته قائم في المحراب ولم يؤد ركناً فإنه يتأخر الخليفة ويتقدم الإمام. ولو خرج الإمام الأول من المسجد وتوضأ ثم رجع إلى المسجد وخليفته لم يؤد ركناً فالإمام هو الثاني. ثم الاستخلاف حقيقي وحكمي؛ فالأول ظاهر والثاني أن يتقدم رجل واحد من القوم قبل أن يخرج الإمام من المسجد فإن صلاتهم جائزة، ولو تقدم رجلان فأيهما سبق إلى مكان الإمامة فهو أولى، ولو قدم الإمام رجلاً والقوم رجلاً فمن قدمه الإمام فهو أولى، وإن نويا معاً الإمامة جاز صلاة المقتدي بخليفة الإمام وفسدت على المقتدي بخليفة القوم. وإن تقدم أحدهما إن كان خليفة الإمام فكذلك، وإن كان خليفة القوم فاقتدوا به ثم نوى الآخر فاقتدى به البعض جاز صلاة الأولين دون الآخرين ولو قدم بعض القوم رجلاً والبعض رجلاً فالعبرة للأكثر، ولو استويا فسدت صلاتهم. ولو استخلف الإمام من آخر الصفوف ثم خرج من المسجد إن نوى الخليفة الإمامة من ساعته صار إماماً فتفسد صلاة من كان متقدمه دون صلاته وصلاة الإمام الأول ومن على يمينه وشماله في صفه ومن خلفه، وإن نوى أن يكون إماماً إذا قام مقام الأول وخرج الأول قبل أن يصل الخليفة إلى مكانه أو قبل أن ينوي الإمامة فسدت صلاتهم وشرط جواز صلاة الخليفة والقوم أن يصل الخليفة إلى المحراب قبل أن يخرج الإمام عن المسجد، ولم يبين محمد حال الإمام.
وذكر الطحاوي أن صلاته فاسدة أيضاً، وذكر أبو عصمة أن صلاته لا تفسد وهو الأصح. ولو لم يستخلف في المسجد واستخلف من الرحبة وفيها قوم جازت صلاة الكل
عند الضيق قوله : (فما في شرح المجمع (الخ لا يخفى ما فيه على النبية فإن كلام المتون في الاستئناف وكلام شرح المجمع في الاستخلاف فما أفاده كلام المتون من أن الأفضل في حق الإمام الاستئناف معناه إذا استخلف ثم توضأ فالأفضل في حقه أن يستأنف صلاته ولا يبني على ما صلى فلا ينافي كون الاستخلاف واجباً . نعم ينافيه ما نقله عن المستصفى من أن الاستخلاف أفضل فإن المتبادر منه عدم وجوبه وهو الذي يظهر إلا أن يضيق الوقت فينبغي الوجوب لئلا تفوت الجماعة تأمل. قوله : (أو قبل أن ينوي الإمام الإمامة هذا راجع إلى المسألة الأولى وهي ما إذا نوى الخليفة الإمامة من ساعته أي لم ينو تأخير نية الإمامة إلى أن يصل إلى المحراب، والأولى إسقاطه لأن المتبادر من قوله من ساعته أنه نوى حين الاستخلاف فلا يتصور خروج الإمام من المسجد قبل أن ينوي الخليفة الإمامة، ولذا لم يذكر قوله أو قبل أن ينوي الإمامة لا في الذخيرة ولا في الخانية. قوله: (وشرط جواز صلاة الخليفة والقوم أن يصل الخليفة إلى المحراب الخ يعني أو ينوي الخليفة الإمامة حين
إذا كانت الرحبة متصلة بالمسجد كذا في الظهيرية. وإذا استخلف الإمام رجلاً فإنه يتعين للإمامة إن قام مقام الأول حتى لو تأخر بعد التقدم فسدت صلاته، وإذا قام الخليفة مقامه صار الأول مقتدياً به خرج من المسجد أو لا. حتى لو تذكر فائتة أو تكلم لم تفسد صلاة القوم. ومقتضى ما قدمناه أنه لا يصير مقتدياً بالخليفة ما دام في المسجد، وللخليفة الاستخلاف إذا أحدث. فلو استخلف الخليفة من غير حدث إن قدمه قبل أن يقوم في مكان الإمامة والإمام الأول في المسجد جاز، ولو تذكر الخليفة أنه على غير وضوء فقدم آخر ولم يقم في موضع الإمامة جاز إذا كان الأول في المسجد، ولو أحدث الخليفة بعد ما قام في موضع الإمامة فانصرف فقبل أن يخرج دخل الأول متوضئاً فقدمه جاز، ولو لم يقم الخليفة في موضع الإمامة حتى أحدث فدخل الأول فقدمه لم يجز والمسألة متأوّلة : وتأويلها مع الإمام رجل آخر سواه ولو كبر الخليفة ينوي الاستقبال جازت صلاة من استقبل وفسدت صلاة من لم يستقبل وكذا صلاة الإمام الأول تفسد إن بني على صلاة نفسه. وفي الخلاصة : فإن نوى الثاني بعدما تقدم إلى المحراب أن لا يكون خليفة للأول ويصلي صلاة نفسه لم يفسد ذلك صلاة من اقتدى به وفي المجتبى : والإمام المحدث على إمامته ما لم يخرج من المسجد أو يقوم خليفته مقامه أو يستخلف القوم غيره أو يتقدم بنفسه. وفي الظهيرية: رجلان وجد في السفر ماء قليلاً فقال أحدهما هو نجس، وقال الآخر هو طاهر، فتوضأ أحدهما وتيمم ثم أمهما من توضأ بماء مطلق ثم سبقه الحدث يصلي كل واحد من المقتديين وحده من غير أن يقتدي بالآخر، فلو رجع الإمام

يصير
الآخر
الاستخلاف كما يدل عليه قوله ولو استخلف الإمام من آخر الصفوف الخ». وظاهر كلامه أن إماماً وإن لم ينو وسيأتي الاتفاق على أنه لا يكون إماماً ما لم ينو الإمامة. قوله : يصير (قبل أن يخرج الإمام عن المسجد أي أو يجاوز الصفوف في الصحراء. قوله : (ومقتضى ما قدمناه أن مقتدياً الخ) الذي قدمه هو قوله وإذا استخلف لا يخرج الإمام عن الإمامة بمجرده الخ» فإنه يقتضي أنه ما دام في المسجد ولم يؤد الخليفة ركناً يبقى على إمامته لكن جمع بينهما في النهر بأن ما تقدم محمول على ما إذا لم يقم الخليفة مقامه ناوياً الإمامة اهـ . لكن ينافيه عبارة الظهيرية والخانية السابقة هناك فإن مقتضاها أنه لا يخرج عن الإمامة ما لم يؤد الخليفة ركناً وإن كان قائماً مقامه، ناوياً الإمامة إلا أن تحمل تلك العبارة على ما إذا لم ينو الخليفة الإمامة وإن كان قام مقامه، وما هنا على ما إذا قام مقامه ونوى الإمامة لما في الدراية اتفقت الروايات على أن الخليفة لا يكون إماماً لم ينو الإمامة. قوله : قوله : (لم يجز) أي لخلو مقام الإمام. قوله : (يصلي كل واحد من المقتديين وحده) لأنه يعتقد أن صاحبه محدث به أفتى أئمة بلخ كذا في النهر عن تيمم القنية قال: فإطلاق فساد صلاة القوم يستثنى منه هذا وقياسه أنه لو أم صبياً وامرأة ثم سبقه الحدث فذهب قبل الاستخلاف
(Book of Prayer - Chapter of Hadath in Prayer) ... For the prayer of the people, there is consideration. When he appoints a substitute, the imam does not leave the imamate by his mere act; therefore, if someone follows him immediately before wudu, it is valid according to the correct view as in al-Muhit. Hence it is said in al-Zahiriyya and al-Khaniyya: If the imam performs wudu in the mosque while his substitute stands at the mihrab and has not performed a rak'ah, then the substitute steps back and the imam steps forward. If the first imam leaves the mosque, performs wudu, returns, and his substitute has not performed a rak'ah, then the second is the imam. Then istikhlaf is real and legal; the first is apparent, the second is that one man from the people steps forward before the imam leaves the mosque, then their prayer is permissible. If two men step forward, whichever reaches the imam's place first is more deserving. If the imam appoints a man and the people appoint a man, the one appointed by the imam is more deserving. If both intend imamah together, the prayer of the follower of the imam's substitute is valid, and the prayer of the follower of the people's substitute is invalid. If one of them steps forward, if it is the imam's substitute, similar; if it is the people's substitute and they follow him, then another intends and some follow him, the prayer of the first group is valid, not the others. If some people appoint one man and others another man, the majority is considered; if equal, their prayer is invalid. If the imam appoints a substitute from the last row and then leaves the mosque, if the substitute intends imamah immediately, he becomes imam, so the prayer of those ahead of him is invalid, not his own prayer, nor the prayer of the first imam, nor those on his right and left in his row, nor those behind him. If he intends to be imam when he stands in place of the first, and the first leaves before the substitute reaches his place or before he intends imamah, their prayer is invalid. The condition for validity of the prayer of the substitute and the people is that the substitute reaches the mihrab before the imam leaves the mosque. Muhammad did not clarify the status of the imam. Al-Tahawi said his prayer is also invalid. Abu 'Isma said his prayer is not invalid, and this is the more correct. If he does not appoint a substitute in the mosque but appoints from the courtyard, and there are people in it, the prayer of all is valid when there is constraint. His words: "what is in Sharh al-Majma'..." are not hidden from the intelligent. The text of the Matn speaks about restarting, while Sharh al-Majma' speaks about istikhlaf. What the Matn indicates, that it is preferable for the imam to restart, means when he has appointed a substitute and then performed wudu, it is better for him to restart his prayer and not build on what he prayed, so it does not contradict istikhlaf being obligatory. Indeed, it contradicts what he narrated from al-Mustasfa that istikhlaf is better, because the apparent meaning is it is not obligatory, and that is what appears, unless time is tight, then it should be obligatory so that congregation is not missed. Reflect. His words: "or before the imam intends imamah" refers to the first issue, i.e., when the substitute intends imamah immediately, meaning he did not delay the intention of imamah until reaching the mihrab. It is better to drop it, because the apparent meaning of "immediately" is that he intended at the time of appointment, so it is inconceivable that the imam leaves the mosque before the substitute intends imamah. Hence he did not mention "or before he intends imamah" in al-Dhakhira nor in al-Khaniyya. His words: "the condition for validity of the prayer of the substitute and the people is that the substitute reaches the mihrab..." meaning or the substitute intends imamah when the courtyard is connected to the mosque, as in al-Zahiriyya. When the imam appoints a man, he becomes designated for imamah if he takes the place of the first, such that if he delays after stepping forward, his prayer is invalid. When the substitute takes his place, the first becomes a follower of him, whether he left the mosque or not. Even if he remembers a missed prayer or speaks, the prayer of the people is not invalid. The implication of what we presented is that he does not become a follower of the substitute as long as he is in the mosque. The substitute may appoint a substitute if he has hadath. If the substitute appoints another without hadath, and he presents him before standing in the place of imamah while the first imam is in the mosque, it is permissible. If the substitute remembers he is not in wudu and presents another without standing in the imam's place, it is permissible if the first is in the mosque. If the substitute has hadath after standing in the imam's place and leaves, and before he exits, the first enters with wudu and presents him, it is permissible. If the substitute does not stand in the imam's place until he has hadath, then the first enters and presents him, it is not permissible, and the issue is subject to interpretation: its interpretation is with another imam besides him. If the substitute says the takbir intending to face (the qibla) and to lead, the prayer of those who face is valid, and the prayer of those who do not face is invalid, and likewise the prayer of the first imam is invalid if he builds on his own prayer. In al-Khulasa: If the second, after stepping to the mihrab, intends not to be a substitute for the first but to pray his own prayer, that does not invalidate the prayer of those who follow him. In al-Mujtaba: The imam who has hadath remains in his imamah as long as he does not leave the mosque, or his substitute stands in his place, or the people appoint someone else, or he himself steps forward. In al-Zahiriyya: Two men on a journey find a little water. One says it is najis, the other says it is tahir. One performs wudu and the other tayammum. Then the one who performed wudu with absolute water leads them, then he is overtaken by hadath. Each of the followers prays alone without following the other. If the imam returns... when he stands in his place, the other becomes... istikhlaf as indicated by his words "even if the imam appoints from the last row..." The apparent meaning of his words is that even if he (the substitute) did not intend (imamah), but it will come that there is agreement he is not imam unless he intends imamah. His words: "becomes" before the imam leaves the mosque, i.e., or passes the rows in the desert. His words: "the implication of what we presented is that he does not become a follower..." what he presented is his statement: "When he appoints a substitute, the imam does not leave the imamate by his mere act", which implies that as long as he is in the mosque and the substitute has not performed a rak'ah, he remains in his imamate. But in al-Nahr, a reconciliation was made: what preceded is interpreted as the case where the substitute has not stood in his place intending imamah. However, the wording of al-Zahiriyya and al-Khaniyya earlier contradicts this, because they imply he does not leave the imamate unless the substitute performs a rak'ah, even if he is standing in his place intending imamah, unless that wording is interpreted as when the substitute did not intend imamah though he stood in his place, while what is here is when he stood in his place and intended imamah, because in al-Diraya, the narrations agree that the substitute is not imam unless he intends imamah. His words: "it is not permissible" i.e., because the imam's place is empty. His words: "each of the followers prays alone" because he believes his companion has hadath. The imams of Balkh gave fatwa accordingly, as in al-Nahr from Tayammum al-Qunya. He said: The general statement of invalidity of the people's prayer is excepted by this, and by analogy, if he leads a boy and a woman, then he is overtaken by hadath and leaves before appointing a substitute...
Source pages p. 647

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq is an expansion on the rules of istikhlāf (appointing a substitute imam) when the original imam loses his wudu (hadath) during prayer. The author, Ibn Nujaym, is commenting on the matn of Kanz al-Daqā’iq, clarifying conditions and resolving apparent contradictions between earlier Hanafi sources.

The passage begins by establishing the basic principle: when an imam appoints a substitute (khalīfa), he does not automatically leave the imamate. If someone starts following him immediately before he goes to make wudu, the following is valid. However, if the imam leaves the mosque, performs wudu, and returns before the substitute has performed a rak‘ah, the imam resumes his role. The substitute steps back. This shows that the substitute only becomes the actual imam if the original imam leaves completely or the substitute actually leads a rak‘ah.

The author then distinguishes between ‘real’ istikhlāf (the imam explicitly appoints someone) and ‘legal’ istikhlāf (a member of the congregation steps forward to lead without explicit appointment). In the latter case, if one person steps forward before the imam leaves the mosque, the congregation’s prayer is valid. If two step forward, the one who reaches the imam’s place first has priority. If the imam appoints one and the congregation appoints another, the imam’s choice prevails.

A key scenario: if the imam appoints a substitute from the last row and then leaves the mosque, the substitute becomes imam only if he intends imamate immediately. If he delays his intention until he reaches the mihrab, and the imam leaves before that, the prayer of the congregation is invalid. In such a case, Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybānī) does not clarify the status of the original imam’s prayer. Al-Ṭaḥāwī says it is also invalid, while Abū ‘Iṣma says it is not invalid, and Ibn Nujaym declares the latter as the correct view.

Further conditions: the substitute must reach the mihrab (or at least intend imamate) before the imam exits the mosque. If the imam appoints someone from the courtyard (raḥba) that is connected to the mosque, the prayer of all is valid when there is constriction (ḍīq). The passage also discusses whether istikhlāf is obligatory or merely preferable. The matn suggests that restarting the prayer (isti’nāf) is preferable, but the author reconciles this by saying that istikhlāf is obligatory when time is tight, to preserve the congregation.

The commentary then addresses a discrepancy: earlier it was stated that the imam remains imam as long as he is in the mosque even if the substitute has stood in his place, but later it is said that once the substitute stands and intends imamate, the original imam becomes a follower. The author resolves this by interpreting the earlier statement as referring to a case where the substitute has not yet intended imamate. He cites al-Dirāya that all narrations agree the substitute is not imam unless he intends imamate.

A special case from al-Ẓāhiriyya: two travelers disagree about the purity of water. One performs wudu, the other tayammum. The one with wudu leads, then breaks wudu. In this situation, each follower prays individually because they cannot agree on the validity of the other’s purity. This is an exception to the general rule that congregation is invalid. The author notes that the imams of Balkh gave fatwa on this.

Key Terms
الاستخلاف (al-istikhlāf): The act of the imam appointing a substitute (khalīfa) to lead the prayer when he cannot continue due to hadath or other reason
الخليفة (al-khalīfa): The person appointed by the imam to take over leading the prayer
الحدث (al-ḥadath): Ritual impurity that breaks wudu, requiring the imam to leave the prayer to renew it
حقيقي (ḥaqīqī): Real istikhlāf: explicit appointment by the imam
حكمي (ḥukmī): Legal istikhlāf: when a congregant steps forward without explicit appointment, but the action is legally treated as istikhlāf

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, when does the substitute (khalīfa) actually become the imam during prayer?
A) As soon as the original imam appoints him.
B) Only after he reaches the mihrab and intends imamah.
C) Only after the original imam leaves the mosque.
D) Only after performing one rak'ah.

Key Takeaway
The imam remains imam until the substitute physically takes over; appointment alone does not transfer imamate.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Condition for Substitute to Become Imam and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Condition for substitution and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for the substitute to become imam and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute about the original imam's prayer status when he leaves before the substitute intends imamate.

Core Idea
The substitute becomes imam only when he reaches the mihrab and intends imamate before the original imam leaves.

This lesson focuses on the precise moment the substitute assumes leadership. The passage introduces a critical condition: the substitute must reach the mihrab (or at least intend imamate) before the original imam exits the mosque. A dispute arises among Hanafi authorities about whether the original imam's own prayer is valid if he leaves before this condition is met. Imam Muhammad is silent, al-Tahawi says it is invalid, but Abu 'Isma argues it remains valid, and Ibn Nujaym declares this the more correct view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for substitution
Read: 'The condition for validity of the prayer of the substitute and the people is that the substitute reaches the mihrab before the imam leaves the mosque.' Note that the substitute must physically arrive or intend imamate. This is a condition for the congregation's prayer to be valid.
The passage also mentions an alternative: intending imamate when the courtyard is connected.
2
Analyze the status of the original imam
Imam Muhammad did not clarify. Al-Tahawi claimed the original imam's prayer becomes invalid. Abu 'Isma said it is not invalid, and this is deemed al-asahh (most correct). Understand the rationale: the imam remains imam until the substitute actually takes over.
This is an intra-Hanafi khilaf.
3
Apply the settled view
According to the preferred view (Abu 'Isma), the original imam's prayer remains valid. He can either complete it as a follower or continue his own prayer if he returns.
The thamarah: if invalid, he must repeat prayer; if valid, he may continue.

كتاب الصلاة - باب الحدث في الصلاة

لصلاة القوم ففيه نظر، وإذا استخلف لا يخرج الإمام عن الإمامة بمجرده، ولهذا لو اقتدى به إنسان من ساعته قبل الوضوء فإنه صحيح على الصحيح كما في المحيط، ولهذا قال في الظهيرية والخانية : إن الإمام لو توضأ في المسجد وخليفته قائم في المحراب ولم يؤد ركناً فإنه يتأخر الخليفة ويتقدم الإمام. ولو خرج الإمام الأول من المسجد وتوضأ ثم رجع إلى المسجد وخليفته لم يؤد ركناً فالإمام هو الثاني. ثم الاستخلاف حقيقي وحكمي؛ فالأول ظاهر والثاني أن يتقدم رجل واحد من القوم قبل أن يخرج الإمام من المسجد فإن صلاتهم جائزة، ولو تقدم رجلان فأيهما سبق إلى مكان الإمامة فهو أولى، ولو قدم الإمام رجلاً والقوم رجلاً فمن قدمه الإمام فهو أولى، وإن نويا معاً الإمامة جاز صلاة المقتدي بخليفة الإمام وفسدت على المقتدي بخليفة القوم. وإن تقدم أحدهما إن كان خليفة الإمام فكذلك، وإن كان خليفة القوم فاقتدوا به ثم نوى الآخر فاقتدى به البعض جاز صلاة الأولين دون الآخرين ولو قدم بعض القوم رجلاً والبعض رجلاً فالعبرة للأكثر، ولو استويا فسدت صلاتهم. ولو استخلف الإمام من آخر الصفوف ثم خرج من المسجد إن نوى الخليفة الإمامة من ساعته صار إماماً فتفسد صلاة من كان متقدمه دون صلاته وصلاة الإمام الأول ومن على يمينه وشماله في صفه ومن خلفه، وإن نوى أن يكون إماماً إذا قام مقام الأول وخرج الأول قبل أن يصل الخليفة إلى مكانه أو قبل أن ينوي الإمامة فسدت صلاتهم وشرط جواز صلاة الخليفة والقوم أن يصل الخليفة إلى المحراب قبل أن يخرج الإمام عن المسجد، ولم يبين محمد حال الإمام.
وذكر الطحاوي أن صلاته فاسدة أيضاً، وذكر أبو عصمة أن صلاته لا تفسد وهو الأصح. ولو لم يستخلف في المسجد واستخلف من الرحبة وفيها قوم جازت صلاة الكل
عند الضيق قوله : (فما في شرح المجمع (الخ لا يخفى ما فيه على النبية فإن كلام المتون في الاستئناف وكلام شرح المجمع في الاستخلاف فما أفاده كلام المتون من أن الأفضل في حق الإمام الاستئناف معناه إذا استخلف ثم توضأ فالأفضل في حقه أن يستأنف صلاته ولا يبني على ما صلى فلا ينافي كون الاستخلاف واجباً . نعم ينافيه ما نقله عن المستصفى من أن الاستخلاف أفضل فإن المتبادر منه عدم وجوبه وهو الذي يظهر إلا أن يضيق الوقت فينبغي الوجوب لئلا تفوت الجماعة تأمل. قوله : (أو قبل أن ينوي الإمام الإمامة هذا راجع إلى المسألة الأولى وهي ما إذا نوى الخليفة الإمامة من ساعته أي لم ينو تأخير نية الإمامة إلى أن يصل إلى المحراب، والأولى إسقاطه لأن المتبادر من قوله من ساعته أنه نوى حين الاستخلاف فلا يتصور خروج الإمام من المسجد قبل أن ينوي الخليفة الإمامة، ولذا لم يذكر قوله أو قبل أن ينوي الإمامة لا في الذخيرة ولا في الخانية. قوله: (وشرط جواز صلاة الخليفة والقوم أن يصل الخليفة إلى المحراب الخ يعني أو ينوي الخليفة الإمامة حين
إذا كانت الرحبة متصلة بالمسجد كذا في الظهيرية. وإذا استخلف الإمام رجلاً فإنه يتعين للإمامة إن قام مقام الأول حتى لو تأخر بعد التقدم فسدت صلاته، وإذا قام الخليفة مقامه صار الأول مقتدياً به خرج من المسجد أو لا. حتى لو تذكر فائتة أو تكلم لم تفسد صلاة القوم. ومقتضى ما قدمناه أنه لا يصير مقتدياً بالخليفة ما دام في المسجد، وللخليفة الاستخلاف إذا أحدث. فلو استخلف الخليفة من غير حدث إن قدمه قبل أن يقوم في مكان الإمامة والإمام الأول في المسجد جاز، ولو تذكر الخليفة أنه على غير وضوء فقدم آخر ولم يقم في موضع الإمامة جاز إذا كان الأول في المسجد، ولو أحدث الخليفة بعد ما قام في موضع الإمامة فانصرف فقبل أن يخرج دخل الأول متوضئاً فقدمه جاز، ولو لم يقم الخليفة في موضع الإمامة حتى أحدث فدخل الأول فقدمه لم يجز والمسألة متأوّلة : وتأويلها مع الإمام رجل آخر سواه ولو كبر الخليفة ينوي الاستقبال جازت صلاة من استقبل وفسدت صلاة من لم يستقبل وكذا صلاة الإمام الأول تفسد إن بني على صلاة نفسه. وفي الخلاصة : فإن نوى الثاني بعدما تقدم إلى المحراب أن لا يكون خليفة للأول ويصلي صلاة نفسه لم يفسد ذلك صلاة من اقتدى به وفي المجتبى : والإمام المحدث على إمامته ما لم يخرج من المسجد أو يقوم خليفته مقامه أو يستخلف القوم غيره أو يتقدم بنفسه. وفي الظهيرية: رجلان وجد في السفر ماء قليلاً فقال أحدهما هو نجس، وقال الآخر هو طاهر، فتوضأ أحدهما وتيمم ثم أمهما من توضأ بماء مطلق ثم سبقه الحدث يصلي كل واحد من المقتديين وحده من غير أن يقتدي بالآخر، فلو رجع الإمام

الآخر
الاستخلاف كما يدل عليه قوله ولو استخلف الإمام من آخر الصفوف الخ». وظاهر كلامه أن إماماً وإن لم ينو وسيأتي الاتفاق على أنه لا يكون إماماً ما لم ينو الإمامة. قوله : يصير (قبل أن يخرج الإمام عن المسجد أي أو يجاوز الصفوف في الصحراء. قوله : (ومقتضى ما قدمناه أن مقتدياً الخ) الذي قدمه هو قوله وإذا استخلف لا يخرج الإمام عن الإمامة بمجرده الخ» فإنه يقتضي أنه ما دام في المسجد ولم يؤد الخليفة ركناً يبقى على إمامته لكن جمع بينهما في النهر بأن ما تقدم محمول على ما إذا لم يقم الخليفة مقامه ناوياً الإمامة اهـ . لكن ينافيه عبارة الظهيرية والخانية السابقة هناك فإن مقتضاها أنه لا يخرج عن الإمامة ما لم يؤد الخليفة ركناً وإن كان قائماً مقامه، ناوياً الإمامة إلا أن تحمل تلك العبارة على ما إذا لم ينو الخليفة الإمامة وإن كان قام مقامه، وما هنا على ما إذا قام مقامه ونوى الإمامة لما في الدراية اتفقت الروايات على أن الخليفة لا يكون إماماً لم ينو الإمامة. قوله : قوله : (لم يجز) أي لخلو مقام الإمام. قوله : (يصلي كل واحد من المقتديين وحده) لأنه يعتقد أن صاحبه محدث به أفتى أئمة بلخ كذا في النهر عن تيمم القنية قال: فإطلاق فساد صلاة القوم يستثنى منه هذا وقياسه أنه لو أم صبياً وامرأة ثم سبقه الحدث فذهب قبل الاستخلاف
(Book of Prayer - Chapter of Hadath in Prayer) ... For the prayer of the people, there is consideration. When he appoints a substitute, the imam does not leave the imamate by his mere act; therefore, if someone follows him immediately before wudu, it is valid according to the correct view as in al-Muhit. Hence it is said in al-Zahiriyya and al-Khaniyya: If the imam performs wudu in the mosque while his substitute stands at the mihrab and has not performed a rak'ah, then the substitute steps back and the imam steps forward. If the first imam leaves the mosque, performs wudu, returns, and his substitute has not performed a rak'ah, then the second is the imam. Then istikhlaf is real and legal; the first is apparent, the second is that one man from the people steps forward before the imam leaves the mosque, then their prayer is permissible. If two men step forward, whichever reaches the imam's place first is more deserving. If the imam appoints a man and the people appoint a man, the one appointed by the imam is more deserving. If both intend imamah together, the prayer of the follower of the imam's substitute is valid, and the prayer of the follower of the people's substitute is invalid. If one of them steps forward, if it is the imam's substitute, similar; if it is the people's substitute and they follow him, then another intends and some follow him, the prayer of the first group is valid, not the others. If some people appoint one man and others another man, the majority is considered; if equal, their prayer is invalid. If the imam appoints a substitute from the last row and then leaves the mosque, if the substitute intends imamah immediately, he becomes imam, so the prayer of those ahead of him is invalid, not his own prayer, nor the prayer of the first imam, nor those on his right and left in his row, nor those behind him. If he intends to be imam when he stands in place of the first, and the first leaves before the substitute reaches his place or before he intends imamah, their prayer is invalid. The condition for validity of the prayer of the substitute and the people is that the substitute reaches the mihrab before the imam leaves the mosque. Muhammad did not clarify the status of the imam. Al-Tahawi said his prayer is also invalid. Abu 'Isma said his prayer is not invalid, and this is the more correct. If he does not appoint a substitute in the mosque but appoints from the courtyard, and there are people in it, the prayer of all is valid when there is constraint. His words: "what is in Sharh al-Majma'..." are not hidden from the intelligent. The text of the Matn speaks about restarting, while Sharh al-Majma' speaks about istikhlaf. What the Matn indicates, that it is preferable for the imam to restart, means when he has appointed a substitute and then performed wudu, it is better for him to restart his prayer and not build on what he prayed, so it does not contradict istikhlaf being obligatory. Indeed, it contradicts what he narrated from al-Mustasfa that istikhlaf is better, because the apparent meaning is it is not obligatory, and that is what appears, unless time is tight, then it should be obligatory so that congregation is not missed. Reflect. His words: "or before the imam intends imamah" refers to the first issue, i.e., when the substitute intends imamah immediately, meaning he did not delay the intention of imamah until reaching the mihrab. It is better to drop it, because the apparent meaning of "immediately" is that he intended at the time of appointment, so it is inconceivable that the imam leaves the mosque before the substitute intends imamah. Hence he did not mention "or before he intends imamah" in al-Dhakhira nor in al-Khaniyya. His words: "the condition for validity of the prayer of the substitute and the people is that the substitute reaches the mihrab..." meaning or the substitute intends imamah when the courtyard is connected to the mosque, as in al-Zahiriyya. When the imam appoints a man, he becomes designated for imamah if he takes the place of the first, such that if he delays after stepping forward, his prayer is invalid. When the substitute takes his place, the first becomes a follower of him, whether he left the mosque or not. Even if he remembers a missed prayer or speaks, the prayer of the people is not invalid. The implication of what we presented is that he does not become a follower of the substitute as long as he is in the mosque. The substitute may appoint a substitute if he has hadath. If the substitute appoints another without hadath, and he presents him before standing in the place of imamah while the first imam is in the mosque, it is permissible. If the substitute remembers he is not in wudu and presents another without standing in the imam's place, it is permissible if the first is in the mosque. If the substitute has hadath after standing in the imam's place and leaves, and before he exits, the first enters with wudu and presents him, it is permissible. If the substitute does not stand in the imam's place until he has hadath, then the first enters and presents him, it is not permissible, and the issue is subject to interpretation: its interpretation is with another imam besides him. If the substitute says the takbir intending to face (the qibla) and to lead, the prayer of those who face is valid, and the prayer of those who do not face is invalid, and likewise the prayer of the first imam is invalid if he builds on his own prayer. In al-Khulasa: If the second, after stepping to the mihrab, intends not to be a substitute for the first but to pray his own prayer, that does not invalidate the prayer of those who follow him. In al-Mujtaba: The imam who has hadath remains in his imamah as long as he does not leave the mosque, or his substitute stands in his place, or the people appoint someone else, or he himself steps forward. In al-Zahiriyya: Two men on a journey find a little water. One says it is najis, the other says it is tahir. One performs wudu and the other tayammum. Then the one who performed wudu with absolute water leads them, then he is overtaken by hadath. Each of the followers prays alone without following the other. If the imam returns... when he stands in his place, the other becomes... istikhlaf as indicated by his words "even if the imam appoints from the last row..." The apparent meaning of his words is that even if he (the substitute) did not intend (imamah), but it will come that there is agreement he is not imam unless he intends imamah. His words: "becomes" before the imam leaves the mosque, i.e., or passes the rows in the desert. His words: "the implication of what we presented is that he does not become a follower..." what he presented is his statement: "When he appoints a substitute, the imam does not leave the imamate by his mere act", which implies that as long as he is in the mosque and the substitute has not performed a rak'ah, he remains in his imamate. But in al-Nahr, a reconciliation was made: what preceded is interpreted as the case where the substitute has not stood in his place intending imamah. However, the wording of al-Zahiriyya and al-Khaniyya earlier contradicts this, because they imply he does not leave the imamate unless the substitute performs a rak'ah, even if he is standing in his place intending imamah, unless that wording is interpreted as when the substitute did not intend imamah though he stood in his place, while what is here is when he stood in his place and intended imamah, because in al-Diraya, the narrations agree that the substitute is not imam unless he intends imamah. His words: "it is not permissible" i.e., because the imam's place is empty. His words: "each of the followers prays alone" because he believes his companion has hadath. The imams of Balkh gave fatwa accordingly, as in al-Nahr from Tayammum al-Qunya. He said: The general statement of invalidity of the people's prayer is excepted by this, and by analogy, if he leads a boy and a woman, then he is overtaken by hadath and leaves before appointing a substitute...
Source pages p. 647

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq is an expansion on the rules of istikhlāf (appointing a substitute imam) when the original imam loses his wudu (hadath) during prayer. The author, Ibn Nujaym, is commenting on the matn of Kanz al-Daqā’iq, clarifying conditions and resolving apparent contradictions between earlier Hanafi sources.

The passage begins by establishing the basic principle: when an imam appoints a substitute (khalīfa), he does not automatically leave the imamate. If someone starts following him immediately before he goes to make wudu, the following is valid. However, if the imam leaves the mosque, performs wudu, and returns before the substitute has performed a rak‘ah, the imam resumes his role. The substitute steps back. This shows that the substitute only becomes the actual imam if the original imam leaves completely or the substitute actually leads a rak‘ah.

The author then distinguishes between ‘real’ istikhlāf (the imam explicitly appoints someone) and ‘legal’ istikhlāf (a member of the congregation steps forward to lead without explicit appointment). In the latter case, if one person steps forward before the imam leaves the mosque, the congregation’s prayer is valid. If two step forward, the one who reaches the imam’s place first has priority. If the imam appoints one and the congregation appoints another, the imam’s choice prevails.

A key scenario: if the imam appoints a substitute from the last row and then leaves the mosque, the substitute becomes imam only if he intends imamate immediately. If he delays his intention until he reaches the mihrab, and the imam leaves before that, the prayer of the congregation is invalid. In such a case, Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybānī) does not clarify the status of the original imam’s prayer. Al-Ṭaḥāwī says it is also invalid, while Abū ‘Iṣma says it is not invalid, and Ibn Nujaym declares the latter as the correct view.

Further conditions: the substitute must reach the mihrab (or at least intend imamate) before the imam exits the mosque. If the imam appoints someone from the courtyard (raḥba) that is connected to the mosque, the prayer of all is valid when there is constriction (ḍīq). The passage also discusses whether istikhlāf is obligatory or merely preferable. The matn suggests that restarting the prayer (isti’nāf) is preferable, but the author reconciles this by saying that istikhlāf is obligatory when time is tight, to preserve the congregation.

The commentary then addresses a discrepancy: earlier it was stated that the imam remains imam as long as he is in the mosque even if the substitute has stood in his place, but later it is said that once the substitute stands and intends imamate, the original imam becomes a follower. The author resolves this by interpreting the earlier statement as referring to a case where the substitute has not yet intended imamate. He cites al-Dirāya that all narrations agree the substitute is not imam unless he intends imamate.

A special case from al-Ẓāhiriyya: two travelers disagree about the purity of water. One performs wudu, the other tayammum. The one with wudu leads, then breaks wudu. In this situation, each follower prays individually because they cannot agree on the validity of the other’s purity. This is an exception to the general rule that congregation is invalid. The author notes that the imams of Balkh gave fatwa on this.

Key Terms
المحراب (al-mihrāb): The niche or place where the imam stands to lead prayer
الأصح (al-aṣaḥḥ): The more correct view
الطحاوي (al-Ṭaḥāwī): Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi (d. 321/933), a major Hanafi scholar
أبو عصمة (Abū 'Iṣma): A Hanafi scholar (likely al-Samarqandi)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which Hanafi scholar's view is declared the more correct (al-asahh) regarding the original imam's prayer when he leaves before the substitute intends imamate?
A) Imam Muhammad
B) Al-Tahawi
C) Abu 'Isma
D) Ibn Nujaym

Key Takeaway
The substitute becomes imam only when he reaches the mihrab and intends imamate before the imam leaves; the original imam's prayer remains valid per the preferred view.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Obligation vs Recommendation of Istikhlaf and the Courtyard Case
Obligation vs recommendation and ruling on courtyard appointment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine when istikhlaf becomes obligatory versus recommended, and apply the rule for appointing a substitute from the courtyard.

Core Idea
Istikhlaf is recommended but becomes obligatory when time is tight to preserve congregation.

This lesson reconciles two apparently conflicting statements: the matn says restarting (isti'naf) is preferable, but the Sharh al-Majma' suggests istikhlaf is better. The author clarifies that istikhlaf is generally recommended, but becomes obligatory if the time for prayer is short, to avoid losing the congregation. Additionally, if the imam appoints a substitute from the courtyard (connected to the mosque), the prayer is valid when there is constriction.

Guided Path
1
Understand the tension between texts
The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq indicates that for the imam, restarting the prayer (isti'naf) after hadath is preferable. Sharh al-Majma' says istikhlaf is better. Ibn Nujaym resolves: istikhlaf is obligatory when time is tight; otherwise recommended.
The key is time constraint (diyq).
2
Apply the obligation condition
If the prayer time is about to expire, the imam must appoint a substitute to preserve the congregation's prayer. If time is ample, he may restart.
This is from the principle that preserving congregation is prioritized.
3
Rule for appointment from courtyard
If the imam is outside and appoints a substitute from the courtyard (rahba) that is connected to the mosque, and there are people in the courtyard, their prayer is valid when there is constriction (e.g., mosque is full).
Condition: the courtyard must be contiguous with the mosque.

كتاب الصلاة - باب الحدث في الصلاة

لصلاة القوم ففيه نظر، وإذا استخلف لا يخرج الإمام عن الإمامة بمجرده، ولهذا لو اقتدى به إنسان من ساعته قبل الوضوء فإنه صحيح على الصحيح كما في المحيط، ولهذا قال في الظهيرية والخانية : إن الإمام لو توضأ في المسجد وخليفته قائم في المحراب ولم يؤد ركناً فإنه يتأخر الخليفة ويتقدم الإمام. ولو خرج الإمام الأول من المسجد وتوضأ ثم رجع إلى المسجد وخليفته لم يؤد ركناً فالإمام هو الثاني. ثم الاستخلاف حقيقي وحكمي؛ فالأول ظاهر والثاني أن يتقدم رجل واحد من القوم قبل أن يخرج الإمام من المسجد فإن صلاتهم جائزة، ولو تقدم رجلان فأيهما سبق إلى مكان الإمامة فهو أولى، ولو قدم الإمام رجلاً والقوم رجلاً فمن قدمه الإمام فهو أولى، وإن نويا معاً الإمامة جاز صلاة المقتدي بخليفة الإمام وفسدت على المقتدي بخليفة القوم. وإن تقدم أحدهما إن كان خليفة الإمام فكذلك، وإن كان خليفة القوم فاقتدوا به ثم نوى الآخر فاقتدى به البعض جاز صلاة الأولين دون الآخرين ولو قدم بعض القوم رجلاً والبعض رجلاً فالعبرة للأكثر، ولو استويا فسدت صلاتهم. ولو استخلف الإمام من آخر الصفوف ثم خرج من المسجد إن نوى الخليفة الإمامة من ساعته صار إماماً فتفسد صلاة من كان متقدمه دون صلاته وصلاة الإمام الأول ومن على يمينه وشماله في صفه ومن خلفه، وإن نوى أن يكون إماماً إذا قام مقام الأول وخرج الأول قبل أن يصل الخليفة إلى مكانه أو قبل أن ينوي الإمامة فسدت صلاتهم وشرط جواز صلاة الخليفة والقوم أن يصل الخليفة إلى المحراب قبل أن يخرج الإمام عن المسجد، ولم يبين محمد حال الإمام.
وذكر الطحاوي أن صلاته فاسدة أيضاً، وذكر أبو عصمة أن صلاته لا تفسد وهو الأصح. ولو لم يستخلف في المسجد واستخلف من الرحبة وفيها قوم جازت صلاة الكل
عند الضيق قوله : (فما في شرح المجمع (الخ لا يخفى ما فيه على النبية فإن كلام المتون في الاستئناف وكلام شرح المجمع في الاستخلاف فما أفاده كلام المتون من أن الأفضل في حق الإمام الاستئناف معناه إذا استخلف ثم توضأ فالأفضل في حقه أن يستأنف صلاته ولا يبني على ما صلى فلا ينافي كون الاستخلاف واجباً . نعم ينافيه ما نقله عن المستصفى من أن الاستخلاف أفضل فإن المتبادر منه عدم وجوبه وهو الذي يظهر إلا أن يضيق الوقت فينبغي الوجوب لئلا تفوت الجماعة تأمل. قوله : (أو قبل أن ينوي الإمام الإمامة هذا راجع إلى المسألة الأولى وهي ما إذا نوى الخليفة الإمامة من ساعته أي لم ينو تأخير نية الإمامة إلى أن يصل إلى المحراب، والأولى إسقاطه لأن المتبادر من قوله من ساعته أنه نوى حين الاستخلاف فلا يتصور خروج الإمام من المسجد قبل أن ينوي الخليفة الإمامة، ولذا لم يذكر قوله أو قبل أن ينوي الإمامة لا في الذخيرة ولا في الخانية. قوله: (وشرط جواز صلاة الخليفة والقوم أن يصل الخليفة إلى المحراب الخ يعني أو ينوي الخليفة الإمامة حين
إذا كانت الرحبة متصلة بالمسجد كذا في الظهيرية. وإذا استخلف الإمام رجلاً فإنه يتعين للإمامة إن قام مقام الأول حتى لو تأخر بعد التقدم فسدت صلاته، وإذا قام الخليفة مقامه صار الأول مقتدياً به خرج من المسجد أو لا. حتى لو تذكر فائتة أو تكلم لم تفسد صلاة القوم. ومقتضى ما قدمناه أنه لا يصير مقتدياً بالخليفة ما دام في المسجد، وللخليفة الاستخلاف إذا أحدث. فلو استخلف الخليفة من غير حدث إن قدمه قبل أن يقوم في مكان الإمامة والإمام الأول في المسجد جاز، ولو تذكر الخليفة أنه على غير وضوء فقدم آخر ولم يقم في موضع الإمامة جاز إذا كان الأول في المسجد، ولو أحدث الخليفة بعد ما قام في موضع الإمامة فانصرف فقبل أن يخرج دخل الأول متوضئاً فقدمه جاز، ولو لم يقم الخليفة في موضع الإمامة حتى أحدث فدخل الأول فقدمه لم يجز والمسألة متأوّلة : وتأويلها مع الإمام رجل آخر سواه ولو كبر الخليفة ينوي الاستقبال جازت صلاة من استقبل وفسدت صلاة من لم يستقبل وكذا صلاة الإمام الأول تفسد إن بني على صلاة نفسه. وفي الخلاصة : فإن نوى الثاني بعدما تقدم إلى المحراب أن لا يكون خليفة للأول ويصلي صلاة نفسه لم يفسد ذلك صلاة من اقتدى به وفي المجتبى : والإمام المحدث على إمامته ما لم يخرج من المسجد أو يقوم خليفته مقامه أو يستخلف القوم غيره أو يتقدم بنفسه. وفي الظهيرية: رجلان وجد في السفر ماء قليلاً فقال أحدهما هو نجس، وقال الآخر هو طاهر، فتوضأ أحدهما وتيمم ثم أمهما من توضأ بماء مطلق ثم سبقه الحدث يصلي كل واحد من المقتديين وحده من غير أن يقتدي بالآخر، فلو رجع الإمام
