الآخر
الاستخلاف كما يدل عليه قوله ولو استخلف الإمام من آخر الصفوف الخ». وظاهر كلامه أن إماماً وإن لم ينو وسيأتي الاتفاق على أنه لا يكون إماماً ما لم ينو الإمامة. قوله : يصير (قبل أن يخرج الإمام عن المسجد أي أو يجاوز الصفوف في الصحراء. قوله : (ومقتضى ما قدمناه أن مقتدياً الخ) الذي قدمه هو قوله وإذا استخلف لا يخرج الإمام عن الإمامة بمجرده الخ» فإنه يقتضي أنه ما دام في المسجد ولم يؤد الخليفة ركناً يبقى على إمامته لكن جمع بينهما في النهر بأن ما تقدم محمول على ما إذا لم يقم الخليفة مقامه ناوياً الإمامة اهـ . لكن ينافيه عبارة الظهيرية والخانية السابقة هناك فإن مقتضاها أنه لا يخرج عن الإمامة ما لم يؤد الخليفة ركناً وإن كان قائماً مقامه، ناوياً الإمامة إلا أن تحمل تلك العبارة على ما إذا لم ينو الخليفة الإمامة وإن كان قام مقامه، وما هنا على ما إذا قام مقامه ونوى الإمامة لما في الدراية اتفقت الروايات على أن الخليفة لا يكون إماماً لم ينو الإمامة. قوله : قوله : (لم يجز) أي لخلو مقام الإمام. قوله : (يصلي كل واحد من المقتديين وحده) لأنه يعتقد أن صاحبه محدث به أفتى أئمة بلخ كذا في النهر عن تيمم القنية قال: فإطلاق فساد صلاة القوم يستثنى منه هذا وقياسه أنه لو أم صبياً وامرأة ثم سبقه الحدث فذهب قبل الاستخلاف
(Book of Prayer - Chapter of Hadath in Prayer) ... For the prayer of the people, there is consideration. When he appoints a substitute, the imam does not leave the imamate by his mere act; therefore, if someone follows him immediately before wudu, it is valid according to the correct view as in al-Muhit. Hence it is said in al-Zahiriyya and al-Khaniyya: If the imam performs wudu in the mosque while his substitute stands at the mihrab and has not performed a rak'ah, then the substitute steps back and the imam steps forward. If the first imam leaves the mosque, performs wudu, returns, and his substitute has not performed a rak'ah, then the second is the imam. Then istikhlaf is real and legal; the first is apparent, the second is that one man from the people steps forward before the imam leaves the mosque, then their prayer is permissible. If two men step forward, whichever reaches the imam's place first is more deserving. If the imam appoints a man and the people appoint a man, the one appointed by the imam is more deserving. If both intend imamah together, the prayer of the follower of the imam's substitute is valid, and the prayer of the follower of the people's substitute is invalid. If one of them steps forward, if it is the imam's substitute, similar; if it is the people's substitute and they follow him, then another intends and some follow him, the prayer of the first group is valid, not the others. If some people appoint one man and others another man, the majority is considered; if equal, their prayer is invalid. If the imam appoints a substitute from the last row and then leaves the mosque, if the substitute intends imamah immediately, he becomes imam, so the prayer of those ahead of him is invalid, not his own prayer, nor the prayer of the first imam, nor those on his right and left in his row, nor those behind him. If he intends to be imam when he stands in place of the first, and the first leaves before the substitute reaches his place or before he intends imamah, their prayer is invalid. The condition for validity of the prayer of the substitute and the people is that the substitute reaches the mihrab before the imam leaves the mosque. Muhammad did not clarify the status of the imam. Al-Tahawi said his prayer is also invalid. Abu 'Isma said his prayer is not invalid, and this is the more correct. If he does not appoint a substitute in the mosque but appoints from the courtyard, and there are people in it, the prayer of all is valid when there is constraint. His words: "what is in Sharh al-Majma'..." are not hidden from the intelligent. The text of the Matn speaks about restarting, while Sharh al-Majma' speaks about istikhlaf. What the Matn indicates, that it is preferable for the imam to restart, means when he has appointed a substitute and then performed wudu, it is better for him to restart his prayer and not build on what he prayed, so it does not contradict istikhlaf being obligatory. Indeed, it contradicts what he narrated from al-Mustasfa that istikhlaf is better, because the apparent meaning is it is not obligatory, and that is what appears, unless time is tight, then it should be obligatory so that congregation is not missed. Reflect. His words: "or before the imam intends imamah" refers to the first issue, i.e., when the substitute intends imamah immediately, meaning he did not delay the intention of imamah until reaching the mihrab. It is better to drop it, because the apparent meaning of "immediately" is that he intended at the time of appointment, so it is inconceivable that the imam leaves the mosque before the substitute intends imamah. Hence he did not mention "or before he intends imamah" in al-Dhakhira nor in al-Khaniyya. His words: "the condition for validity of the prayer of the substitute and the people is that the substitute reaches the mihrab..." meaning or the substitute intends imamah when the courtyard is connected to the mosque, as in al-Zahiriyya. When the imam appoints a man, he becomes designated for imamah if he takes the place of the first, such that if he delays after stepping forward, his prayer is invalid. When the substitute takes his place, the first becomes a follower of him, whether he left the mosque or not. Even if he remembers a missed prayer or speaks, the prayer of the people is not invalid. The implication of what we presented is that he does not become a follower of the substitute as long as he is in the mosque. The substitute may appoint a substitute if he has hadath. If the substitute appoints another without hadath, and he presents him before standing in the place of imamah while the first imam is in the mosque, it is permissible. If the substitute remembers he is not in wudu and presents another without standing in the imam's place, it is permissible if the first is in the mosque. If the substitute has hadath after standing in the imam's place and leaves, and before he exits, the first enters with wudu and presents him, it is permissible. If the substitute does not stand in the imam's place until he has hadath, then the first enters and presents him, it is not permissible, and the issue is subject to interpretation: its interpretation is with another imam besides him. If the substitute says the takbir intending to face (the qibla) and to lead, the prayer of those who face is valid, and the prayer of those who do not face is invalid, and likewise the prayer of the first imam is invalid if he builds on his own prayer. In al-Khulasa: If the second, after stepping to the mihrab, intends not to be a substitute for the first but to pray his own prayer, that does not invalidate the prayer of those who follow him. In al-Mujtaba: The imam who has hadath remains in his imamah as long as he does not leave the mosque, or his substitute stands in his place, or the people appoint someone else, or he himself steps forward. In al-Zahiriyya: Two men on a journey find a little water. One says it is najis, the other says it is tahir. One performs wudu and the other tayammum. Then the one who performed wudu with absolute water leads them, then he is overtaken by hadath. Each of the followers prays alone without following the other. If the imam returns... when he stands in his place, the other becomes... istikhlaf as indicated by his words "even if the imam appoints from the last row..." The apparent meaning of his words is that even if he (the substitute) did not intend (imamah), but it will come that there is agreement he is not imam unless he intends imamah. His words: "becomes" before the imam leaves the mosque, i.e., or passes the rows in the desert. His words: "the implication of what we presented is that he does not become a follower..." what he presented is his statement: "When he appoints a substitute, the imam does not leave the imamate by his mere act", which implies that as long as he is in the mosque and the substitute has not performed a rak'ah, he remains in his imamate. But in al-Nahr, a reconciliation was made: what preceded is interpreted as the case where the substitute has not stood in his place intending imamah. However, the wording of al-Zahiriyya and al-Khaniyya earlier contradicts this, because they imply he does not leave the imamate unless the substitute performs a rak'ah, even if he is standing in his place intending imamah, unless that wording is interpreted as when the substitute did not intend imamah though he stood in his place, while what is here is when he stood in his place and intended imamah, because in al-Diraya, the narrations agree that the substitute is not imam unless he intends imamah. His words: "it is not permissible" i.e., because the imam's place is empty. His words: "each of the followers prays alone" because he believes his companion has hadath. The imams of Balkh gave fatwa accordingly, as in al-Nahr from Tayammum al-Qunya. He said: The general statement of invalidity of the people's prayer is excepted by this, and by analogy, if he leads a boy and a woman, then he is overtaken by hadath and leaves before appointing a substitute...

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq is an expansion on the rules of istikhlāf (appointing a substitute imam) when the original imam loses his wudu (hadath) during prayer. The author, Ibn Nujaym, is commenting on the matn of Kanz al-Daqā’iq, clarifying conditions and resolving apparent contradictions between earlier Hanafi sources.

The passage begins by establishing the basic principle: when an imam appoints a substitute (khalīfa), he does not automatically leave the imamate. If someone starts following him immediately before he goes to make wudu, the following is valid. However, if the imam leaves the mosque, performs wudu, and returns before the substitute has performed a rak‘ah, the imam resumes his role. The substitute steps back. This shows that the substitute only becomes the actual imam if the original imam leaves completely or the substitute actually leads a rak‘ah.

The author then distinguishes between ‘real’ istikhlāf (the imam explicitly appoints someone) and ‘legal’ istikhlāf (a member of the congregation steps forward to lead without explicit appointment). In the latter case, if one person steps forward before the imam leaves the mosque, the congregation’s prayer is valid. If two step forward, the one who reaches the imam’s place first has priority. If the imam appoints one and the congregation appoints another, the imam’s choice prevails.

A key scenario: if the imam appoints a substitute from the last row and then leaves the mosque, the substitute becomes imam only if he intends imamate immediately. If he delays his intention until he reaches the mihrab, and the imam leaves before that, the prayer of the congregation is invalid. In such a case, Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybānī) does not clarify the status of the original imam’s prayer. Al-Ṭaḥāwī says it is also invalid, while Abū ‘Iṣma says it is not invalid, and Ibn Nujaym declares the latter as the correct view.

Further conditions: the substitute must reach the mihrab (or at least intend imamate) before the imam exits the mosque. If the imam appoints someone from the courtyard (raḥba) that is connected to the mosque, the prayer of all is valid when there is constriction (ḍīq). The passage also discusses whether istikhlāf is obligatory or merely preferable. The matn suggests that restarting the prayer (isti’nāf) is preferable, but the author reconciles this by saying that istikhlāf is obligatory when time is tight, to preserve the congregation.

The commentary then addresses a discrepancy: earlier it was stated that the imam remains imam as long as he is in the mosque even if the substitute has stood in his place, but later it is said that once the substitute stands and intends imamate, the original imam becomes a follower. The author resolves this by interpreting the earlier statement as referring to a case where the substitute has not yet intended imamate. He cites al-Dirāya that all narrations agree the substitute is not imam unless he intends imamate.

A special case from al-Ẓāhiriyya: two travelers disagree about the purity of water. One performs wudu, the other tayammum. The one with wudu leads, then breaks wudu. In this situation, each follower prays individually because they cannot agree on the validity of the other’s purity. This is an exception to the general rule that congregation is invalid. The author notes that the imams of Balkh gave fatwa on this.

Key Terms
الضيق (al-ḍīq): Time constraint; when the prayer time is about to expire
الاستئناف (al-isti’nāf): Restarting the prayer from the beginning after hadath
الرحبة (al-raḥba): Courtyard or open area attached to the mosque

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Nujaym, when does istikhlaf become obligatory (wajib)?
A) Always, as soon as the imam has hadath.
B) When the mosque is crowded.
C) When the prayer time is tight (diyq).
D) Never, it is always mandub.

Key Takeaway
Istikhlaf is recommended but obligatory when time is tight; appointment from a connected courtyard is valid.

The Deputy (Khalifah) When the Imam Becomes Impure
Rulings on deputy (khalifah) when imam becomes impure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a deputy assumes imamate and apply them to various scenarios when the imam becomes impure.

Core Idea
The deputy only becomes imam when he intentionally takes the imam's place; until then the original imam retains authority.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq consolidates several Hanafi sources on the rulings of appointing a deputy when the imam becomes impure during prayer. It clarifies that the deputy must actively assume leadership and that the original imam remains in authority until certain conditions are met. We will work through the key scenarios to understand the practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the appointment of a deputy by an imam who becomes impure. The ruling is that it is permissible and the deputy's prayer as imam is valid if he takes the place of the imam with intention.
The passage cites multiple authoritative sources (al-Zahiriyyah, al-Khulasa, al-Mujtaba).
2
Determine when the original imam ceases to be imam
The imam with hadath remains imam until one of four things occur: he exits the mosque, his deputy takes his place (with intention), the congregation appoints another, or he himself steps forward again. Until then, he is still considered the imam.
If the deputy has not yet taken the place, the original imam is still the imam even if he has hadath.
3
Analyze the scenarios of deputization
The text covers several scenarios: the deputy appointing another deputy, the deputy realizing he has no wudu, the deputy becoming impure after taking the place, etc. In each case, the key is whether the deputy has taken the place of imamate and whether the original imam is still present.
Scenarios where the deputy does not take the place may render the change invalid.
4
Note the effect on the congregation
If the deputy intends to pray alone (not as khalifah), the followers' prayers remain valid as long as they followed him with the intention of congregational prayer. However, if he builds on his own prayer, the original imam's prayer becomes invalid if he follows.
The intention of the deputy affects the validity of the followers' prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا كانت الرحبة متصلة بالمسجد كذا في الظهيرية. وإذا استخلف الإمام رجلاً فإنه يتعين للإمامة إن قام مقام الأول حتى لو تأخر بعد التقدم فسدت صلاته، وإذا قام الخليفة مقامه صار الأول مقتدياً به خرج من المسجد أو لا. حتى لو تذكر فائتة أو تكلم لم تفسد صلاة القوم. ومقتضى ما قدمناه أنه لا يصير مقتدياً بالخليفة ما دام في المسجد، وللخليفة الاستخلاف إذا أحدث. فلو استخلف الخليفة من غير حدث إن قدمه قبل أن يقوم في مكان الإمامة والإمام الأول في المسجد جاز، ولو تذكر الخليفة أنه على غير وضوء فقدم آخر ولم يقم في موضع الإمامة جاز إذا كان الأول في المسجد، ولو أحدث الخليفة بعد ما قام في موضع الإمامة فانصرف فقبل أن يخرج دخل الأول متوضئاً فقدمه جاز، ولو لم يقم الخليفة في موضع الإمامة حتى أحدث فدخل الأول فقدمه لم يجز والمسألة متأوّلة : وتأويلها مع الإمام رجل آخر سواه ولو كبر الخليفة ينوي الاستقبال جازت صلاة من استقبل وفسدت صلاة من لم يستقبل وكذا صلاة الإمام الأول تفسد إن بني على صلاة نفسه. وفي الخلاصة : فإن نوى الثاني بعدما تقدم إلى المحراب أن لا يكون خليفة للأول ويصلي صلاة نفسه لم يفسد ذلك صلاة من اقتدى به وفي المجتبى : والإمام المحدث على إمامته ما لم يخرج من المسجد أو يقوم خليفته مقامه أو يستخلف القوم غيره أو يتقدم بنفسه.
If the courtyard is connected to the mosque, as in al-Zahiriyyah. And when the imam appoints a man as deputy, he becomes designated for imamate if he takes the place of the first, so that if he delays after advancing, his prayer becomes invalid. And when the deputy takes his place, the first becomes a follower of him, whether he left the mosque or not. Even if he remembers a missed prayer or speaks, it does not invalidate the prayer of the congregation. The implication of what we have presented is that he does not become a follower of the deputy as long as he is in the mosque. And the deputy may appoint a deputy if he becomes impure. If the deputy appoints a deputy without [himself] becoming impure, if he [the new deputy] advances before standing in the place of imamate while the original imam is in the mosque, it is permissible. If the deputy remembers that he is not upon wudu, and he presents another and does not stand in the place of imamate, it is permissible if the first is in the mosque. If the deputy becomes impure after standing in the place of imamate and then leaves, and before he exits, the first [original imam] enters, having performed wudu, and he presents him, it is permissible. If the deputy does not stand in the place of imamate until he becomes impure, and then the first enters and presents him, it is not permissible, and the issue is subject to interpretation. Its interpretation is that there is with the imam another man besides him. And if the deputy says the takbir intending [only] the facing [Qibla], the prayer of those who face [with him] is valid, and the prayer of those who do not face is invalid. Similarly, the prayer of the first imam becomes invalid if he builds upon his own prayer. And in al-Khulasa: If the second, after advancing to the mihrab, intends not to be a deputy for the first and to pray his own prayer, that does not invalidate the prayer of those who follow him. And in al-Mujtaba: The imam who has hadath remains upon his imamate as long as he has not left the mosque, or his deputy has not taken his place, or the congregation has not appointed someone else, or he himself has not advanced [again].
Source pages p. 648

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the rules regarding the deputy (خليفة) when the imam becomes impure during prayer. It is a ruling that consolidates several sources: al-Zahiriyyah, al-Khulasa, and al-Mujtaba. The key principle is that the deputy only becomes the actual imam when he intentionally takes the imam's place. If he does so, the original imam becomes a follower, even if he hasn't left the mosque. However, as long as the original imam remains in the mosque and the deputy has not performed a rak'ah, the original imam retains his position. The text details various scenarios: if the deputy himself becomes impure, he can appoint another deputy; if the deputy intends to pray alone, the followers' prayers are not invalidated. The relied-upon position is that the imam with hadath remains imam until he exits the mosque, his deputy takes over, the congregation appoints another, or he himself steps forward again.

Key Terms
الخليفة (al-khalīfah): The person appointed by the imam to lead the prayer when the imam becomes impure.
الاستخلاف (al-istikhilāf): The act of appointing a deputy to lead the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following does NOT end the original imam's imamate?
A) The deputy taking his place with intention
B) The imam exiting the mosque
C) The imam appointing a deputy by pointing
D) The congregation appointing another imam

Key Takeaway
The original imam with hadath remains in authority until his deputy physically takes the place with intention, exits the mosque, or the congregation appoints another.

Two Travelers with Conflicting Water Purity
Presents a case where two people disagree on water purity and the imam becomes impure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why each follower must pray alone when their beliefs about the imam's purity conflict, and identify the condition of valid congregation.

Core Idea
When followers' beliefs about the imam's purity conflict, valid congregation is impossible; each must pray alone.

This passage from al-Zahiriyyah presents a challenging scenario: two travelers disagree on the purity of a small amount of water, leading to conflicting views on the validity of each other's purification. The ruling reveals a key principle: the validity of congregational prayer depends on the followers' belief in the imam's purity. Let's see how the Hanafi school resolves this dilemma.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the conflict
Two travelers find a small amount of water. One believes it is pure, the other believes it is impure. They perform wudu and tayammum respectively, then one leads the prayer but becomes impure.
The conflict is about the water's purity, not about the imam's intention.
2
Determine the ruling for each follower
The passage states that each follower prays alone (without following the other) because their beliefs about the imam's purification differ. The prayer is valid (sahih) due to necessity.
The ruling applies when the imam remains in the mosque after becoming impure.
3
Understand the reason: conflicting beliefs
The mutawaddi' believes his wudu is valid (water is pure), but the mutayammim believes the water is impure, so the wudu is invalid. Thus, each believes the other's purification is invalid, making it impossible to follow the imam.
This is a case of 'al-iktilaf fi al-i'tiqad' (conflict in belief).
4
Analyze the exception when imam leaves
If the imam leaves the mosque after becoming impure, his imamate ends entirely. The followers' prayer becomes invalid (fasid) because there is no imam. This is cited from al-Muhit.
The passage implies that as long as the imam remains, the followers can complete their prayer alone.
5
Summarize the principle
Valid congregation requires that followers believe the imam is in a state of purity. When beliefs conflict, congregation is broken, but each follower's individual prayer remains valid under necessity.
This principle is specific to cases where the imam's impurity is uncertain to one follower.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الظهيرية: رجلان وجد في السفر ماء قليلاً فقال أحدهما هو نجس، وقال الآخر هو طاهر، فتوضأ أحدهما وتيمم ثم أمهما من توضأ بماء مطلق ثم سبقه الحدث يصلي كل واحد من المقتديين وحده من غير أن يقتدي بالآخر، فلو رجع الإمام بعدما توضأ يقتدي بمن يظنه طاهراً .اهـ. ظاهره أنه لا فرق بين أي يخرج الإمام من المسجد أو لم يخرج. وإذا خرج الإمام من المسجد خرج عن الإمامة ولم يبق لهما إمام، وقد صرحوا ببطلان صلاة المقتدي في هذه الحالة، ولذا قال في المحيط : رجل أم رجلاً فأحدثا معاً وخرجا من المسجد فصلاة الإمام تامة وصلاة المقتدي فاسدة لأنه لم يبق له إمام في المسجد اهـ. فبقاؤهما فيها من غير إمام مشكل إلا أن يقال ذلك للضرورة إذ لا يمكن اقتداء أحدهما بالآخر لأن المتيمم إن تقدم ففي اعتقاد المتوضىء أن تيممه باطل لطهارة الماء عنده، وإن تقدم المتوضىء ففي اعتقاد المتيمم أنه توضأ بماء نجس والله سبحانه أعلم.
And in al-Zahiriyyah: Two men found a little water while traveling, and one said it is impure, and the other said it is pure. One of them performed wudu and the other performed tayammum, then he who performed wudu with unrestricted water led them in prayer. Then he became impure. Each of the followers prays alone without following the other. If the imam returns after performing wudu, he follows whom he thinks is pure. (End quote) Its apparent meaning is that there is no difference between whether the imam leaves the mosque or not. And when the imam leaves the mosque, he leaves imamate, and there remains no imam for them. And they have explicitly stated the invalidity of the follower's prayer in this situation. For this reason, it is said in al-Muhit: A man led another man; both became impure together and left the mosque. The prayer of the imam is complete, and the prayer of the follower is invalid because there remained no imam for him in the mosque. So their remaining without an imam is problematic, unless it is said that it is for necessity, since it is not possible for one to follow the other because if the one who performed tayammum advances, in the belief of the one who performed wudu, his tayammum is invalid due to the water being pure according to him; and if the one who performed wudu advances, in the belief of the one who performed tayammum, he performed wudu with impure water. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 648

Commentary
This passage from al-Zahiriyyah, reported in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, presents a specific scenario: two travelers find a small amount of water. One believes it is impure, the other pure. They perform wudu and tayammum respectively, then one leads the prayer but becomes impure. The ruling is that each follower prays individually because they have conflicting beliefs about the purity of the water and thus about the validity of the imam's purification. The commentator notes that the imam's exit from the mosque ends imamate entirely, and if both become impure and exit, the follower's prayer is invalid because there is no imam. However, in this case, they remain, but cannot follow each other due to their conflicting beliefs. The practical consequence is that each prays alone.

Key Terms
متيمم (mutayammim): One who performs tayammum instead of wudu due to unavailability or impurity of water.
متوضئ (mutawaddi'): One who performs wudu with water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why must each follower pray alone in the case of the two travelers?
A) Because the imam left the mosque
B) Because they disagree on the purity of the water, so each believes the other's purification is invalid
C) Because they are in a journey
D) Because they have no water

Key Takeaway
When followers have conflicting beliefs about the imam's purity, they cannot validly follow him; each must complete their prayer individually.

The Permissibility of Appointing a Deputy When the Imam Cannot Recite Due to Anxiety (Ḥaṣar)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on appointing deputy for inability to recite due to anxiety, plus note on janāzah prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on appointing a deputy when the imam is unable to recite due to anxiety, and apply the qiyas used by Abu Hanifa to similar scenarios.

Core Idea
Anxiety (ḥaṣar) permits a deputy; forgetting (nisyān) does not — consensus blocks the latter.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rāʼiq addresses a nuanced scenario: an imam leading prayer suddenly finds himself unable to recite due to anxiety or fear (ḥaṣar). Can he appoint a deputy to complete the prayer in his place? The text presents the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imām Abū Ḥanīfa and the Ṣāḥibayn (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad al-Shaybānī), along with a related discussion about janāzah prayer. Understanding this ikhtilāf sharpens your ability to distinguish between valid and invalid excuses for delegating leadership in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario and the ruling sought
The passage asks: When an imam cannot recite due to anxiety (ḥaṣar), may he appoint a deputy to lead the remaining prayer? Note that forgetting (nisyān) is excluded by consensus.
Ḥaṣar is defined as constriction of the chest, not forgetfulness.
2
Locate Abū Ḥanīfa's proof: qiyās to the case of ḥadath
Abū Ḥanīfa analogizes this situation to when an imam breaks his wuḍūʼ – in both cases, the imam becomes unfit to continue, so he may appoint a deputy.
The ʻillah (effective cause) is unfitness for imāmate due to an impediment.
3
Examine the Ṣāḥibayn's objection: rarity prevents qiyās
The two companions argue that this scenario is rare (nādir), and rare cases are not extended by qiyās. They require the imam to complete his own prayer alone.
This objection is based on the principle that qiyās applies to frequent occurrences.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilāf (practical consequence)
Under Abū Ḥanīfa, the deputy's prayer is valid and the congregation is valid. Under the Ṣāḥibayn, the imam cannot delegate and must pray individually, leading to a different ruling for the followers.
The text then shifts to a secondary issue about two travelers (tayammum vs. wuḍūʼ) and appointing a deputy for janāzah prayer.
5
Extract the ruling for janāzah prayer
The passage concludes that the most correct view (al-aṣaḥḥ) per al-Nahr is the permissibility of appointing a deputy in the funeral prayer, though earlier scholars differed.
This expands the scope of the ruling beyond the original ḥaṣar case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المجتبى : وفي جواز الاستخلاف في صلاة الجنازة اختلاف المشايخ . قوله : (كما لو حصر عن القراءة أي جاز لمن سبقه الحدث الاستخلاف إذا كان إماماً كما جاز للإمام الاستخلاف إذا عجز عن القراءة وحصر» بوزن «تعب» فعالاً ومصدراً العي وضيق الصدر، ويقال حصر يحصر حصراً من باب علم، ويجوز أن يكون حصر فعل ما لم يسم فاعله من حصره إذا حبسه من باب نصر ومعناه منع وحبس عن القراءة بسبب خجل أو خوف قال في غاية البيان وبالوجهين حصل لي السماع. وقد وردت اللغتان بهما في كتب اللغة كالصحاح وغيره، وأما انكار المطرزي ضم الحاء فهو في مكسور العين لأنه لازم لا يجيء له مفعول ما لم يسم فاعله لا في مفتوح العين لأنه متعد يجوز بناء الفعل منه للمفعول وصورة المسألة إذا لم يقدر الإمام على القراءة لأجل خجل يعتريه، أما إذا نسي القراءة أصلاً لا يجوز الاستخلاف بالإجماع لأن صار أمياً، واستخلاف الأمي لا يجوز هذا كله عند أبي حنيفة وقالا : لا يجوز لأنه يندر وجوده، وله أن وأتم كل صلاة نفسه أن يصح بجامع أن كل واحد في المسألتين غير صالح للإمامة، ويظهر لي أن ما في القنية ضعيف بل صلاتهما فاسدة لخلو مكان الإمام، ولذا أطلقه الكثير وسيأتي في آخر الباب ما يرشد إلى ذلك ولم أر من نبه على هذا .اهـ. قال الشيخ اسمعيل أقول : القياس المذكور غير صحيح لأن كلاً من الصبي والمرأة صلاته لا شبهة في صحتها من حيث نفس الأمر، وأما المتوضىء والمتيمم فلا يخلو أمرهما من أحد شيئين، إما نجاسة الماء فالتيمم صحيح والوضوء باطل، أو بالعكس فالمقتدي بالنظر إلى نفس الأمر واحد واعتقاد كل منهما ذلك، وإذا كان واحداً فحكمه الانفراد كما سيأتي مع أن قوله في صورة الصبي والمرأة فذهب قبل الاستخلاف لا حاجة إليه لأن فرض المسألة أن ليس غيرهما فيهما لا يتأتى الاستخلاف، وما ظهر له من الضعف ضعيف لعدم ملاحظة المدرك فليتدبر اهـ. وكان معنى قوله فحكمه الانفراد أي الاستقلال بالاستخلاف كما يأتي آخر الباب متناً. قلت: وبهذا التقرير تنحل عرا الإشكال الذي ذكره المؤلف قوله : يقتدي بمن ظنه طاهراً) أي يقتدي الإمام بمن ظنه منهما أنه متطهر لأنه إذا ظنه متطهراً تكون صلاته صحيحة في زعمه فيقتدي به لتعينه للاستخلاف كما مر . قوله : ( وفي جواز الاستخلاف الخ قال في النهر : والأصح جوازه كما في
And in al-Mujtaba: Regarding the permissibility of appointing a deputy in the funeral prayer, there is disagreement among the scholars. His saying: (Just as if he is unable to recite) i.e., it is permissible for one whom hadath preceded to appoint a deputy if he is an imam, just as it is permissible for an imam to appoint a deputy if he is unable to recite and is hindered (ḥaṣar). [Ḥaṣar is like ta‘iba in form, meaning inability and constriction of chest.] The issue is when the imam cannot recite due to anxiety that overcomes him. As for if he forgets the recitation entirely, it is not permissible to appoint a deputy by consensus because he becomes an ummi (illiterate), and appointing an ummi as deputy is not permissible. All this is according to Abu Hanifa. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: It is not permissible because it rarely occurs. And he has to complete each prayer himself. It is valid by the common element that each one in the two issues is not fit for imamate. And it appears to me that what is in al-Qunyah is weak; rather, both prayers are invalid due to the emptiness of the imam's place. Therefore, many have expressed this, and it will come at the end of the chapter indicating that, and I have not seen anyone pointing this out. The sheikh Ismail said: The mentioned analogy is not correct because the prayer of each of the boy and woman is unquestionably valid in reality, whereas the one who performed wudu and the one who performed tayammum, their matter is not free from one of two things: either the water is impure, so tayammum is valid and wudu is invalid, or the opposite. So the follower, from the perspective of reality, is one, and each of them has that belief, and when it is one, its ruling is individuation (al-infiraad) as will come, although his statement in the case of the boy and woman 'and he went before appointment of a deputy' is unnecessary because the premise of the issue is that there is none other than them, so appointment of a deputy is not possible. And what appeared to him as weak is itself weak due to lack of consideration of the source, so let one reflect. And the meaning of his statement 'so its ruling is individuation' is independence in appointing a deputy as will come in the text at the end of the chapter. I say: With this clarification, the knots of the problem that the author mentioned are untied. His saying: 'He follows whom he thinks is pure' means that the imam follows whomever of them he thinks is purified because if he thinks he is purified, his prayer is correct in his opinion, so he follows him for the purpose of appointing a deputy as mentioned. His saying: (And regarding the permissibility of appointment of a deputy) he said in al-Nahr: The most correct is its permissibility as in
Source pages p. 649

Commentary
This passage discusses the permissibility of appointing a deputy when the imam is unable to recite due to anxiety (ḥaṣar). Abu Hanifa permits it, analogizing it to the case where the imam becomes impure. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree because the scenario is rare. The commentator then deals with a criticism from al-Qunyah regarding the two travelers case, asserting that each follower must pray alone. Sheikh Ismail refutes an analogy to a child and a woman. The excerpt ends with a note about the permissibility of appointing a deputy in janazah prayer, citing al-Nahr that the correct view is permissibility.

Key Terms
الحصر (al-ḥaṣar): Inability to recite due to anxiety, fear, or constriction of the chest.
الأمي (al-ummī): One who does not know any Qur'anic recitation; if the imam forgets, he becomes like an ummi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They argue that the imam's prayer becomes invalid anyway.
B) They argue that the scenario is too rare to apply qiyas.
C) They argue that the deputy must be an imam himself.
D) They argue that the imam should have memorized the prayer.

Key Takeaway
An imam unable to recite due to anxiety (ḥaṣar) may appoint a deputy according to Abu Hanifa, but the Ṣāḥibayn object due to rarity; forgetting entirely is a different case by consensus.

Invalidity of Follower's Prayer When Imam Leaves the Mosque After Hadath
Ruling on follower's prayer validity when imam exits mosque after hadath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when both imam and follower have hadath and leave the mosque, and explain why the follower's prayer is invalid.

Core Idea
A follower's prayer becomes invalid when the imam leaves the mosque because the imam ceases to be an imam.

In congregational prayer, the imam's presence is essential for the validity of the follower's prayer. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses a scenario where both the imam and follower experience hadath (ritual impurity) and leave the mosque. It clarifies that the imam's prayer remains complete, but the follower's prayer becomes invalid because the imam has exited the state of imamate. Understanding this ruling helps prevent unknowingly performing an invalid prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Identify the specific situation: both imam and follower have hadath and both leave the mosque.
Hadath here refers to minor ritual impurity that invalidates wudu.
2
Identify the ruling for the imam
Find the ruling for the imam: his prayer is complete and valid, despite leaving the mosque.
3
Identify the ruling for the follower
Find the ruling for the follower: his prayer is invalid (fasid), not merely incomplete.
The text from al-Muhit explicitly states this.
4
Explain the legal cause
Analyze why the follower's prayer is invalid: the imam left the mosque, thereby ceasing to be an imam for the follower. The congregation is broken.
The imam's physical exit from the mosque ends his role as imam.
5
Consider the problematic stay
Note the additional nuance: if both stay in the mosque without an imam, it is problematic, but perhaps permissible by necessity since they cannot follow each other due to conflicting beliefs about purity.
This shows the depth of Hanafi reasoning in edge cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بعدما توضأ يقتدي بمن يظنه طاهراً .اهـ. ظاهره أنه لا فرق بين أي يخرج الإمام من المسجد أو لم يخرج. وإذا خرج الإمام من المسجد خرج عن الإمامة ولم يبق لهما إمام، وقد صرحوا ببطلان صلاة المقتدي في هذه الحالة، ولذا قال في المحيط : رجل أم رجلاً فأحدثا معاً وخرجا من المسجد فصلاة الإمام تامة وصلاة المقتدي فاسدة لأنه لم يبق له إمام في المسجد اهـ. فبقاؤهما فيها من غير إمام مشكل إلا أن يقال ذلك للضرورة إذ لا يمكن اقتداء أحدهما بالآخر لأن المتيمم إن تقدم ففي اعتقاد المتوضىء أن تيممه باطل لطهارة الماء عنده، وإن تقدم المتوضىء ففي اعتقاد المتيمم أنه توضأ بماء نجس والله سبحانه أعلم. وفي المجتبى : وفي جواز الاستخلاف في صلاة الجنازة اختلاف المشايخ .
After he performed wudu, he follows someone he thinks is pure. Apparently there is no difference whether the imam leaves the mosque or not. When the imam leaves the mosque, he leaves the imamate and there is no longer any imam for them (the followers). They explicitly stated the invalidity of the follower's prayer in this situation. Hence it is said in al-Muhit: A man led a man in prayer; both had hadath and left the mosque; the imam's prayer is complete, but the follower's prayer is invalid because there is no imam for him in the mosque. So their staying in the mosque without an imam is problematic, unless it is said that it is for necessity, since neither can follow the other, because if the one who performed tayammum comes forward, the one with wudu believes his tayammum is invalid (due to his belief that water is pure), and if the one with wudu comes forward, the one who performed tayammum believes he performed wudu with impure water. And Allah knows best. In al-Mujtaba: There is a difference of opinion among the mashayikh regarding the permissibility of appointing a substitute in the funeral prayer.
Source pages p. 649

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a ruling about following an imam when there is a situation of both having hadath. The author explains that if both the imam and the follower experience hadath and leave the mosque, the imam's prayer is valid but the follower's is invalid because the imam is no longer acting as an imam inside the mosque. The text then addresses a scenario where one has performed wudu with pure water and the other with impure water (or tayammum), and they cannot lead each other due to conflicting beliefs. The passage ends by noting a difference of opinion among scholars about appointing a substitute in the funeral prayer.

Key Terms
الحدث (al-hadath): Ritual impurity that invalidates wudu.
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution with earth when water is unavailable or harmful.
الاستخلاف (al-istikhlaaf): Appointment of a substitute imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Valid if he continues alone.
B) Invalid because there is no imam in the mosque.
C) Should be repeated after purification.
D) Valid if he follows another person.

Key Takeaway
A follower's prayer becomes invalid if the imam leaves the mosque after hadath, because the imam ceases to be an imam, breaking the congregation.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Istikhlaaf Due to Hassar
Intra-Hanafi dispute on istikhlaaf due to shyness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on istikhlaaf due to hassar, and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
When the imam cannot recite from shyness, Abu Hanifa permits a substitute; the Sahibayn forbid it.

This passage examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether an imam who cannot recite because of shyness (hassar) may appoint a substitute. The key distinction is between forgetfulness (nisyan) and shyness (hassar). Abu Hanifa allows istikhlaaf by analogy with hadath, while the two disciples consider it too rare. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to apply Hanafi tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish hassar from nisyan
Identify the key difference: hassar is inability due to shyness, while nisyan is forgetfulness. The text states that forgetfulness makes the imam an ummi, and istikhlaaf is invalid by consensus.
This distinction is crucial for the entire dispute.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and dalil
Abu Hanifa permits istikhlaaf. His proof is qiyas: just as istikhlaaf is allowed for hadath (an inability to continue prayer), it is also allowed for inability to recite due to shyness — both are genuine impediments.
The basis is the common illa of inability.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and dalil
The Sahibayn do not permit it because such shyness is extremely rare (yandiru wujuduhu). Rarity makes it akin to exceptional cases that are not legislated.
They argue that rarity prevents analogy.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The text counters rarity does not negate the need; the inability to recite is even more binding (alzam) than hadath. Need remains whenever it occurs.
The response shows that the illa is present regardless of frequency.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and thamarah al-khilaf
The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq supports Abu Hanifa; the relied-upon position is permissibility. The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa the substitute's prayer is valid and followers continue; under the Sahibayn the prayer becomes invalid.
Tarjih weighs the strength of the illa over rarity.

His statement: (As if he was prevented from recitation) i.e., it is permissible for one who has been overtaken by hadath to appoint a substitute if he is the imam, just as it is permissible for the imam to appoint a substitute if he is unable to recite and is prevented. The word 'hassar' has the weight of 'ta'ab' (tired) as a verb and noun, meaning inability and constriction of the chest. It is said 'hasira yahsaru hasaran' from the category of 'alima', and it is also possible that 'husira' is the passive of 'hasarah' (to confine) from the category of 'nasara', meaning he was prevented and restrained from recitation due to shyness or fear. It is said in Ghayat al-Bayan that I heard both versions. Both languages are mentioned in lexicons like al-Sihah etc. As for al-Mutarrizi's denial of the dammah on the ha, in the case of a kasrah on the 'ain it is intransitive and does not have a passive form, but in the case of a fatha on the 'ain it is transitive and may be used in the passive. The scenario of the issue is when the imam cannot recite due to shyness that befalls him. But if he forgot the recitation entirely, appointing a substitute is not permissible by consensus because he has become like an ummi (illiterate), and appointing an ummi is not permissible. All this according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is not permissible because its occurrence is rare. And he (Abu Hanifa) that he completes his prayer himself... (the text continues with detailed arguments, comparisons, and responses).
Source pages p. 649

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the permissibility of appointing a substitute imam (istikhlaaf) when the imam is unable to recite the Quran in prayer due to shyness (hassar an al-qiraa). The text first defines the term 'hassar' linguistically, then presents the condition: if the imam forgets the recitation entirely, istikhlaaf is not allowed by consensus because he becomes like an illiterate (ummi). The core dispute is between Abu Hanifa, who permits istikhlaaf in this case by analogy with hadath, and the two disciples (Sahibayn), who disallow it arguing that the situation is rare. The passage then discusses various related cases: a woman/child imam, the haqin (one with urinary retention), and the rulings on the substitute's prayer and the followers' prayer. The author leans towards the permissibility of istikhlaaf, citing sources like al-Muhit and al-Nahr, and concludes that the relied-upon position is the unrestricted permissibility.

Key Terms
الحصر (al-hassar): Inability to recite due to shyness or fear, not forgetfulness.
الأمي (al-ummi): One who cannot read or recite Quran at all.
الاستخلاف (al-istikhlaaf): Appointment of a substitute imam during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Not permissible only if the imam forgot the recitation.

Key Takeaway
When shyness prevents recitation, the imam may appoint a substitute (mufta bihi); forgetfulness is different and istikhlaaf is invalid by consensus.

Ruling on Istikhalf When Imam Cannot Recite
Intra-Hanafi dispute on istikhalf when imam cannot recite.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on istikhalf when the imam becomes unable to recite, and apply the intra-madhhab differentiation to determine the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
If the imam has recited the obligatory amount, istikhalf is impermissible; if not, it is permissible, but the haqin case has disagreement.

This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the imam's appointment of a substitute (istikhalf) when he becomes unable to recite the Quran during prayer. While there is consensus on some aspects, Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn part ways on the ruling for the haqin and the validity of the prayer when the imam becomes illiterate. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for a mufti or imam to know how to proceed in such emergencies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the triggering condition
Determine when istikhalf becomes an issue: the imam has not yet recited the obligatory amount of Quran (fatiha?). If he has recited it, istikhalf is invalid by consensus.
The consensus is that once the obligation is fulfilled, there is no need to substitute.
2
Analyse Abu Hanifa's position on the haqin
For the haqin (one in urgent need of urination), Abu Hanifa prohibits istikhalf because the cause is not rare; the prayer can be completed with difficulty.
Abu Hanifa distinguishes between hasr (inability to recite) and the haqin's situation.
3
Analyse the Sahibayn's position on the haqin
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad permit istikhalf for the haqin, as they consider the need to preserve the congregation's prayer.
The Sahibayn apply istihsan here.
4
Contrast the ruling when imam becomes illiterate during prayer
According to Abu Hanifa, if a reciting imam loses ability to recite, his prayer becomes invalid and must be restarted; the congregation's prayer is also invalid. The Sahibayn allow continuation without recitation by istihsan, analogous to an ummi.
There are two narrations from the Sahibayn – one permitting, one invalidating.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, the imam and congregation repeat the prayer; under the Sahibayn (one narration), they may continue without recitation, and the prayer is valid.
The author leans toward the more permissive view for istikhalf generally.

Source Text

كتاب الصلاة - باب الحدث في الصلاة
هذا الاستخلاف في الحدث بعلة العجز وهو هنا ألزم والعجز عن القراءة غير نادر. وأشار بالمنع عن القراءة إلى أنه لم يقرأ مقدار الفرض فيفيد أنه لو قرأه لا يجوز الاستخلاف إجماعاً لعدم الحاجة إليه، وذكره في المحيط بصيغة «قيل». وظاهره أن المذهب الإطلاق وهو الذي ينبغي اعتماده لما صرحوا في فتح المصلي على إمامه بأنها لا تفسد على الصحيح، سواء قرأ الإمام ما تجوز به الصلاة أو لا، فكذلك هنا يجوز الاستخلاف مطلقاً. وقيد بالمنع عنها لأنه لو أصاب الإمام وجع في البطن فاستخلف رجلاً لم يجز، فلو قعد وأتم صلاته جاز، ولو صار الإمام حاقناً بحيث لا يمكنه المضي فذكر في غير رواية الأصولي أن على قول أبي حنيفة ليس له أن يستخلف، وعلى قول أبي يوسف له ذلك. أبو حنيفة فرق بين مسألة الحصر في القراءة. كذا في الظهيرية والحاقن الذي له بول كثير كذا في المغرب وفي غاية البيان. ثم عندهما إذا لم يستخلف كيف يصنف؟ قال بعض الشارحين : يتم صلاته بلا قراءة إلحاقاً له بالأمي، وهذا سهو لأن مذهبهما أنه يستقبل وبه صرح فحر الإسلام في شرح الجامع الصغير لأنه قال في عامة الكتب : إن الحصر لما كان نادراً أشبه الجنابة وبها لا تتم الصلاة فكذا بالحصر اهـ والعجب من الشارح أنه جعل الحصر عن القراءة كالجنابة ونقل عنهما أنه يتمها بغير قراءة وكذا المحقق في فتح القدير. وفي البدائع : وعندهما لا يجوز وتفسد صلاتهم وهو شاهد لما في غاية البيان والظاهر أن عنهما روايتين .
وبين السراج قوله : (لا يجوز الاستخلاف بالإجماع (الخ) أقول : لم يذكر حكم صلاة القوم ولا حكم صلاته. أما الأول فظاهر وهو أن صلاتهم تفسد لأن إمامهم صار أمياً وهو ليس أهلاً لها، وأما صلاة الإمام فقد رأيت في الفصل السابع من الذخيرة أن القارىء إذا صلى بعض صلاته فنسي القراءة وصار أمياً فسدت صلاته عند أبي حنيفة ويستقبلها، وعلى قولهما لا تفسد ويبني عليها استحساناً وهو قول زفر اهـ.
قوله : (فكذلك هنا الخ قال في النهر أقول : يمكن الفرق بأن عدم الفساد في الفتح لإطلاق الحديث الآتي، والفساد هنا للعمل الكثير بلا حاجة .اهـ. وفيه أن الحاجة للإتيان بالواجب أو المسنون باقية، ولذا أيد في الشرنبلالية كلام المؤلف بما ذكره في الفتاوى الصغرى أنه كتب في شرحه على الجامع الصغير أنه على قياس ما ذكر في الجامع الصغير أن نفس الفتح لا يفسد فلا يفسد أيضاً هنا، لأن الفتح ليس بعمل كثير فلو أفسد إنما يفسد لا لأنه عمل كثير لكن لأنه غير محتاج إليه وهنا هو محتاج إليه فلا يفسد .اهـ. والاحتياج لما قلنا قوله (والحاقن الخ) قال في النهر : وبالباء الموحدة من يدافع الغائط، وبالزاي من يدافعهما قال بعضهم: والحاذق من يدافع ومن أثبته في البول ففيهما أو في الغائط أولى قوله : (إذا لم يستخلف) أي من حصر عن القراءة قوله : (قال بعض الشارحين)
Book of Prayer - Section on Event during Prayer. This is the appointing of a substitute in the event due to the cause of incapacity, and it is here more binding, and incapacity to recite is not rare. And he indicated by the prohibition of recitation that he did not recite the obligatory amount, thus if he recited it, appointing a substitute is not permissible by consensus due to lack of need. And it is mentioned in al-Muhit with the phrase 'qila'. And its apparent meaning is that the school is unrestricted, and that is what should be relied upon because they explicitly stated in Fath al-Musalli ala Imamihi that opening does not invalidate according to the correct view, whether the imam recited what suffices for the prayer or not. So similarly here, appointing a substitute is absolutely permissible. And he restricted it with the prohibition because if the imam has a stomach ache and appoints a substitute, it is not permissible. If he sits and completes his prayer, it is permissible. And if the imam becomes haqin (in need of urination) such that he cannot continue, it is mentioned in a non-Usuli narration that according to Abu Hanifa he should not appoint a substitute, and according to Abu Yusuf he may. Abu Hanifa distinguished between the issue of inability to recite. Similarly in al-Zahiriya, and the haqin who has much urine, similarly in al-Mughrib and Ghayat al-Bayan. Then according to the two, if he does not appoint a substitute, what should he do? Some commentators said: he completes his prayer without recitation, likening him to an illiterate. This is an oversight because their madhhab is that he should start again, as explicitly stated by Fakhr al-Islam in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir because he said in many books: Since inability to recite is rare, it resembles janabah, and prayer is not valid with janabah, so likewise with inability. And it is strange that the commentator made inability to recite like janabah and reported that according to the two he completes it without recitation, and similarly the muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir. In al-Bada'i': according to the two it is not permissible and their prayer is invalid, and that supports what is in Ghayat al-Bayan, and it appears that from them there are two narrations. And between al-Siraj his statement: (Appointing a substitute is not permissible by consensus) I say: He did not mention the ruling of the people's prayer nor the ruling of his prayer. As for the first, it is clear: their prayer is invalid because their imam has become illiterate and is not fit for it. As for the prayer of the imam, I saw in the seventh chapter of al-Dhakhira that if a reciter prays part of his prayer then forgets the recitation and becomes illiterate, his prayer is invalid according to Abu Hanifa and he must start again. According to the two, it does not invalidate and he builds upon it by istihsan, and this is the statement of Zufar. His statement: (So similarly here) he said in al-Nahr: I say: The difference is possible: the non-invalidation in opening is due to the absolute nature of the hadith that follows, and the invalidation here is due to much action without need. But the need to perform the obligatory or recommended act remains, so the commentary in al-Shurnublaliyya supports the author's statement with what is mentioned in al-Fatawa al-Sughra that he wrote in his commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir that analogously to what is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir, the opening itself does not invalidate, so it does not invalidate here either, because opening is not a major action. If it invalidates, it only invalidates not because it is a major action but because it is unnecessary, and here it is necessary, so it does not invalidate. And the need is as we said. His statement (the haqin) he said in al-Nahr: With the single ba refers to one who represses stool, and with the zay refers to one who represses both. Some said: the haziq is one who represses, and whoever affirms it for urine then for both or for stool is more appropriate. His statement: (if he does not appoint a substitute) i.e., one who is unable to recite. His statement: (Some commentators said)

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq discusses the ruling of appointing a substitute (istikhalf) during prayer when the imam becomes unable to recite due to an event (hadath) or other excuses. The author begins by stating that the issue of istikhalf in the event is due to the cause of incapacity, and specifically, the incapacity to recite is not rare. He then explains that if the imam has not recited the obligatory amount of Quran, then appointing a substitute is permissible by consensus because there is a need. However, if he has already recited the obligatory amount, then there is no need and istikhalf is not permissible. The author notes that some sources (like al-Muhit) mention this as 'qila' (it is said), but the apparent position of the school is unrestricted permission, relying on the analogy with the case of 'Fath al-Musalli ala Imamihi' (opening the prayer for the imam), which does not invalidate the prayer whether or not the imam has recited. The author then adds a qualification: if the imam has a stomach ache and appoints a substitute, it is not permissible because the prayer itself is valid (since the imam can sit). However, if he sits and completes the prayer, it is permissible. Then he contrasts this with the case of being 'haqin' (in dire need of urination). According to a non-Usuli narration, Abu Hanifa prohibits istikhalf for the haqin, while Abu Yusuf permits it. Abu Hanifa distinguishes this from the case of inability to recite. The author cites al-Zahiriya and other works. He then discusses what the two imams (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say if the imam does not appoint a substitute: some commentators say he completes his prayer without recitation, likening him to an illiterate person, but the author rejects this as an oversight because the actual position of the two imams is that he must start the prayer anew, as stated by Fakhr al-Islam in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir. The author explains that the reasoning is that inability to recite is rare, like janabah (major impurity), and prayer is not valid with janabah, so similarly here. In al-Bada'i', it is reported that according to the two imams, istikhalf is not permissible and the prayer of the congregation is invalid. This supports the view in Ghayat al-Bayan, and it appears there are two narrations from the two imams on this point. The author then quotes al-Siraj's statement that 'appointing a substitute is not permissible by consensus', and he comments that the ruling for the congregation's prayer is clear: it is invalid because the imam has become illiterate. For the imam himself, he cites from al-Dhakhira that according to Abu Hanifa, if a reciter prays part of his prayer then forgets the recitation and becomes illiterate, his prayer is invalid and he must start again, while according to the two imams (and Zufar), it does not invalidate and he builds upon it by istihsan. Then the author addresses a potential objection that the analogy with 'Fath al-Musalli' might not hold because the invalidation there is due to the absence of need, while here there is need. He argues that the need to perform the obligatory or recommended act (like recitation) is present, so the analogy holds. The text ends with explanations of the terms 'haqin' and the ruling if the imam does not appoint a substitute.

Key Terms
الاستخلاف (al-istikhalf): appointing a substitute to lead the prayer in place of the original imam due to an excuse
الحصر (al-hasr): inability to recite the Quran during prayer due to a physical condition (like constipation or inability to articulate)
الحاقن (al-haqin): one who is in urgent need of urination and cannot continue prayer properly

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the prayer of the congregation when the imam becomes illiterate (unable to recite) during prayer, according to Abu Hanifa?
A) The congregation's prayer remains valid.
B) The congregation's prayer is invalid.
C) The congregation's prayer is valid only if the imam appoints a substitute.
D) The congregation's prayer is valid only if they finish without recitation.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of istikhalf depends on whether the imam has fulfilled the recitation obligation, and the intra-Hanafi dispute on the haqin and hasr cases shows the nuanced application of qiyas and istihsan.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Leaving the Mosque Due to Suspected Hadath: Invalidation of Prayer
Ruling with proof using qiyas and istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on prayer when the imam leaves the mosque due to false suspicion of hadath, and distinguish between genuine and false suspicion in terms of invalidation.

Core Idea
Prayer is invalid if the imam leaves based on false suspicion; only a genuine excuse allows continuation.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a key ruling: the imam's prayer is invalid if he leaves the mosque due to a false suspicion of hadath. The commentator differentiates between a valid excuse (genuine suspicion) and a false one, and also addresses a misunderstanding about turning away from the qibla. As we walk through the text, we will uncover the reasoning via qiyas and istihsan, and identify the conditions for the prayer to remain valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The imam leaves the mosque due to suspicion of hadath. The text states the ruling: he must restart (istighbal), meaning his prayer is invalid.
The default ruling for leaving the mosque with any suspicion is that the prayer is invalid, but exceptions are discussed.
2
Analyze the proof: Qiyas and Istihsan
The commentator uses qiyas (analogy) to turning away from the qibla, which would normally invalidate the prayer. But istihsan (juristic preference) saves the prayer when the imam leaves with intention of rectification and does not actually leave the mosque. If he does leave, the excuse must be genuine.
The analogy would make the prayer invalid, but istihsan introduces an exception based on the imam's intention.
3
Distinguish between zann and tawahhum
The ruling is conditioned on 'zann' (preponderant suspicion), not mere 'tawahhum' (imagination). Only zann gives a valid excuse; tawahhum does not justify leaving.
This distinction affects other cases like suspecting wudu expiry or impurity on clothes.
4
Address the intra-Hanafi dispute
Some from al-Tanjis claimed that turning the chest away from the qibla does not invalidate the prayer. The commentator rejects this, stating that intentionally turning away is rebellious and invalidates the prayer.
The dispute is resolved by noting that the imam who leaves with a false suspicion is not excused, unlike one who turns with an excuse.
5
Extend to istikhalf (appointing a substitute)
Istikhalf is treated like leaving the mosque: if done without genuine excuse, it invalidates the prayer. The imam must have intended rectification and the suspicion must be genuine.
If the substitute performed a rukn, the imam cannot resume imamah; otherwise, there is disagreement among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.

قوله : (وإن خرج من المسجد بظن الحدث أو جن أو احتلم أو أغمي عليه استقبل أما فسادها بالخروج من المسجد لتوهم الحدث ولم يكن موجوداً فلوجود المنافي من غير عذر، والقياس فسادها بالانحراف عن القبلة مطلقاً لما ذكرنا لكن استحسنوا بقاءها عند عدم الخروج لأنه انصرف على قصد الإصلاح لأنه لو تحقق ما توهمه بني على صلاته فألحق قصد الإصلاح بحقيقته ما لم يختلف المكان ،بالخروج، وقد فهم بعضهم من هذا كما ذكره في التنجيس أن المصلي إذا حول صدره عن القبلة لا تفسد صلاته وأن القول بفسادها أليق بقولهما وليس بشيء لأن أبا حنيفة إنما قال بعدم فساد صلاته عند عدم الخروج لأجل أنه معذور بتوهم الحدث، وأما من حول صدره عن القبلة فهو ماء، أو كان في الظهر فظن أنه لم يصل الفجر، أو رأى حمرة في ثوبه فظن أنها نجاسة، فانصرف حيث تفسد صلاته وإن لم يخرج من المسجد لأن الانصراف على سبييل الرفض، ولهذا لو تحقق ما توهمه يستقبل، وهذا هو الأصل Book of Prayer - Section on Event during Prayer. He left the mosque with suspicion of hadath, or became insane, or had a wet dream, or fainted: he must restart, even if he preceded. His statement: (And if he left the mosque with suspicion of hadath, or became insane, or had a wet dream, or fainted: he must restart) As for its invalidation by leaving the mosque due to imagining hadath while it was not present, it is due to the presence of a contradictory action without excuse. The analogy would invalidate it by turning away from the qibla absolutely, as we mentioned, but they deemed it remaining by istihsan when not leaving, because he turned with the intention of rectification. If what he imagined were true, he would build on his prayer, so the intention of rectification is attached to its reality as long as the place does not change by leaving. Some understood from this, as mentioned in al-Tanjis, that if the worshipper turns his chest away from the qibla, his prayer does not invalidate, and that the statement of its invalidation is more consistent with their view, but that is nothing because Abu Hanifa only said that his prayer does not invalidate when not leaving because he is excused by imagining the event. As for one who turns his chest away from the qibla, he is rebellious and disobedient, not deserving leniency. So the statement of invalidation is more consistent with the view of all, as is not hidden. He restricted it with suspicion of hadath because if he suspected that he began without wudu, or was wiping over his leather socks and suspected that the wiping period had expired, or was performing tayammum and saw a mirage and thought it was water, or was in zuhr and thought he had not prayed fajr, or saw redness on his garment and thought it was impurity, and he turns away, then his prayer is invalid even if he does not leave the mosque, because the turning away is in the manner of abandonment. For this, if what he imagined were true, he would restart. This is the principle, and istikhalf is like leaving the mosque because it is a major action that invalidates it. He only expressed it with suspicion (zann) instead of imagination (tawahhum) because it is the preponderant side and imagination is the weak side. The preponderant side is as stated by Imam al-Sighnaqi, author of al-Nihaya, and similarly in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. His statement: (And it is strange from the commentator) That is because there is contradiction in his speech. He said in al-Nahr: Since its completion without recitation indicates its validity, and it being like janabah necessitates invalidity. His statement: (And it appears that from them there are two narrations) And on this, the commentator's statement 'like janabah' is taken to mean that the comparison is only to the rarity, and his statement that he completes it is based on the other narration, so his speech is valid. His statement: (And istikhalf is like leaving the mosque) He said in al- Inaya: And if he had appointed a substitute and then it became clear that he had not had an event, his prayer is invalid even if he did not leave the mosque, due to the presence of major action without excuse, unlike if what he imagined were true, then the action does not invalidate because of the excuse. So istikhalf is like leaving the mosque: for its validity it requires the intention of rectification and the presence of an excuse. His statement: (So it appears that if there is no evidence for the suspicion) there is discussion, because its implication would apply to imagination a fortiori, while it is explicitly stated in al-Muhit contrary to that. Its wording: An imam imagined and appointed a substitute, then it became clear that it was water and not blood. Shaykh Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl said: If the substitute performed a rukn of the prayer, it is not permissible for the imam to take the imamate again, but he follows the substitute. If he had not performed a rukn but stood in the mihrab, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf he may take the imamate. According to Muhammad, it is not permissible. And similarly in al-Dhakhira. And in al-Zahiriyya, Muhammad said: His prayer is invalid. The conclusion is that what he researched is not supported by this transmitted material from which the case of doubt is understood a fortiori, with the expression of al-Hidaya and others of suspicion secondarily as imagination. And what is in al-Tanjis is not explicit in the claimed meaning due to the possibility of an apparent intention: that he had a nosebleed.
Source pages p. 651

Commentary
This portion of the commentary addresses the ruling when the imam leaves the mosque due to suspicion of hadath (ritual impurity), or becomes insane, has a wet dream, or faints. The base text states that in these cases, he must restart his prayer (istighbal), meaning his current prayer is invalidated. The commentator explains that the invalidation is due to leaving the mosque without a genuine hadath, which is an action contrary to the prayer without an excuse. By analogy (qiyas), turning away from the qibla should also invalidate the prayer, but the scholars applied istihsan (juristic preference) to allow the prayer to remain valid if the imam does not actually leave the mosque, because he turned with the intention of rectification (qasd al-islah). If his suspicion were real (e.g., he actually had hadath), he would build on the prayer. So the intention of rectification is attached to the reality as long as the place does not change. The commentator then addresses a misunderstanding derived from al-Tanjis: some thought that if a worshipper turns his chest away from the qibla, his prayer does not invalidate. The commentator rejects this, stating that Abu Hanifa's ruling of non-invalidation was only for the case where he does not leave the mosque and is excused by the suspicion of hadath. But one who intentionally turns away from the qibla is rebellious and deserves no leniency; thus the prayer is invalid. The commentator then clarifies that the ruling is restricted to suspicion (zann) of hadath, not mere imagination (tawahhum). He gives examples: if he suspects that he began without wudu, or that his wiping period expired, etc., and he turns away, his prayer is invalid even if he does not leave the mosque, because the turning away is in the manner of abandonment. If the suspicion were true, he would have to restart. He then states that istikhalf (appointing a substitute) is like leaving the mosque in that it is a major action that invalidates the prayer unless there is an excuse. The commentator discusses the difference between zann and tawahhum, and attributes the preponderant side to Imam al-Sighnaqi. He then summarizes a discussion from al- Inaya: if an imam appointed a substitute and then it turned out he did not have hadath, his prayer is invalid because of work without excuse, unless he had genuine suspicion. The text ends with a narration from al-Muhit and a ruling from Shaykh Abu Bakr regarding the imam's regaining the imamah after appointing a substitute, with differences between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. The conclusion is that the researched point is not supported by the transmitted material.

Key Terms
الظن (al-zann): preponderant belief or suspicion, as opposed to mere imagination (tawahhum); in this context, it is the basis for ruling on the intention to rectify
التوهم (al-tawahhum): mere imagination or weak suspicion without evidence
الاستخلاف (al-istikhalf): appointing a substitute imam; compared to leaving the mosque in terms of being a major action

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if an imam leaves the mosque due to a false suspicion of hadath, what is the ruling on his prayer?
A) It is valid and he can continue.
B) It is invalid and he must restart.
C) It is valid if he had the intention of rectification.
D) It is invalid only if he did not recite the obligatory amount.

Key Takeaway
Leaving the mosque due to false suspicion of hadath invalidates the prayer; only a genuine excuse allows continuation.

Exiting Mosque with False Suspicion of Hadath
Explains nullification of prayer by exiting mosque with false suspicion of hadath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a person exits the mosque due to a false suspicion of hadath and explain the role of istihsan in preserving the prayer.

Core Idea
False suspicion of hadath nullifies prayer if he exits the mosque; istihsan preserves it only if he does not exit.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a nuanced ruling: what happens when a praying person suspects he has broken his wudu, exits the mosque to check, but finds he was mistaken? The Hanafi school distinguishes between exiting the mosque (which nullifies) and simply turning away (which may be excused). The key is the presence or absence of a valid excuse and the intention behind the action. We will unpack the qiyas, the istihsan, and the limits of leniency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is exiting the mosque due to a false suspicion of hadath. The ruling is that the prayer becomes null (batil) and must be restarted.
The text explicitly says 'استقبل' (he restarts).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is based on qiyas and istihsan. By strict qiyas, any deviation from the qiblah would nullify, but the Hanafi school applies istihsan to preserve the prayer when the person does not exit the mosque.
Istihsan is a juristic preference that departs from qiyas for a more equitable result.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The istihsan argument: if the suspicion were true, the person would be allowed to build upon his prayer after renewing wudu. So the intention of correction is attached to its reality, as long as the place does not change (i.e., he does not exit the mosque).
The phrase 'ألحق قصد الإصلاح بحقيقته' – the intention of correction is treated like the reality.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is a potential misunderstanding: some think that any turning from the qiblah nullifies, but the text clarifies that exiting due to a false suspicion is treated leniently only if he does not exit. Deliberate turning is not excused.
The text refutes those who extend the leniency to intentional turning away.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi position: the prayer is invalid if he exits the mosque with a false suspicion. If he turns but does not exit, the prayer is preserved due to istihsan. This is the relied-upon view.
The text also mentions that other suspicions (like doubting wudu validity) also nullify if they lead to turning away, even without exiting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خرج من المسجد بظن الحدث أو جن أو احتلم أو أغمي عليه استقبل وإن سبقه. قوله : (وإن خرج من المسجد بظن الحدث أو جن أو احتلم أو أغمي عليه استقبل أما فسادها بالخروج من المسجد لتوهم الحدث ولم يكن موجوداً فلوجود المنافي من غير عذر، والقياس فسادها بالانحراف عن القبلة مطلقاً لما ذكرنا لكن استحسنوا بقاءها عند عدم الخروج لأنه انصرف على قصد الإصلاح لأنه لو تحقق ما توهمه بني على صلاته فألحق قصد الإصلاح بحقيقته ما لم يختلف المكان، بالخروج، وقد فهم بعضهم من هذا كما ذكره في التنجيس أن المصلي إذا حول صدره عن القبلة لا تفسد صلاته وأن القول بفسادها أليق بقولهما وليس بشيء لأن أبا حنيفة إنما قال بعدم فساد صلاته عند عدم الخروج لأجل أنه معذور بتوهم الحدث، وأما من حول صدره عن القبلة فهو متمرد عاص لا يستحق التخفيف، فالقول بالفساد أليق بقول الكل كما لا يخفى. قيد بظن الحدث لأنه لو ظن أنه افتتح على غير وضوء أو كان ماسحاً على الخفين فظن أن مدة مسحه قد انقضت أو كان متيمماً فرأى سراباً فظنه ماء، أو كان في الظهر فظن أنه لم يصل الفجر، أو رأى حمرة في ثوبه فظن أنها نجاسة، فانصرف حيث تفسد صلاته وإن لم يخرج من المسجد لأن الانصراف على سبيل الرفض، ولهذا لو تحقق ما توهمه يستقبل، وهذا هو الأصل والاستخلاف كالخروج من المسجد لأنه عمل كثير فيبطلها.
He who exits the mosque due to a suspicion of hadath, or becomes insane, or has a wet dream, or faints, restarts (the prayer) even if he was preceded (by an event). His statement: (And if he exits the mosque due to a suspicion of hadath, or becomes insane, or has a wet dream, or faints, he restarts. As for its nullification by exiting the mosque due to the suspicion of hadath when it was not present, it is due to the existence of a contradictory element without an excuse. The analogy is its nullification by turning away from the qiblah absolutely, for what we mentioned, but they applied istihsan to preserve it when he did not exit because he turned with the intention of correction. For if what he suspected were true, he would build upon his prayer, so the intention of correction is attached to its reality as long as the place does not differ by exiting. And some understood from this, as mentioned in al-Tanjis, that if a worshipper turns his chest away from the qiblah, his prayer does not become invalid, and that the statement of its invalidity is more appropriate to their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's) statement, but it is nothing. Because Abu Hanifa only said there is no invalidation in the case of non-exit due to his being excused by the suspicion of hadath. As for one who turns his chest from the qiblah, he is rebellious, disobedient, and does not deserve leniency. So the statement of invalidity is more appropriate to the statement of all, as is not hidden. It is restricted to the suspicion of hadath because if he suspected that he began without wudu, or was wiping on khuffs and suspected his wiping period had expired, or was performing tayammum and saw a mirage and thought it was water, or was in Zuhr and suspected he had not performed Fajr, or saw redness on his garment and suspected it was impurity, and he turned away, then his prayer becomes invalid even if he did not exit the mosque, because the turning away is in the manner of abandonment. Hence if what he suspected were true, he would restart, and this is the principle. And istikhlaf is like exiting the mosque because it is a lot of action and thus invalidates it.
Source pages p. 651

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter on hadath in prayer. It states that if a person exits the mosque due to a suspicion that he has broken his wudu, or if he becomes insane, has a wet dream, or faints during prayer, he must restart his prayer from the beginning. The commentary explains the ruling: the prayer is nullified by exiting the mosque because the suspicion was false, so there was no valid excuse. By analogy (qiyas), any major deviation from the qiblah would nullify prayer, but the Hanafi school applies istihsan (juristic preference) to preserve the prayer when the person does not exit the mosque, because he turned with the intention of rectifying his state. If his suspicion were true, he would be allowed to build upon his prayer after renewing wudu, so the intention of correction is treated like the reality as long as the place does not change. The text distinguishes between one who exits the mosque due to suspicion (excused, hence leniency) and one who deliberately turns away from the qiblah (unexcused, hence prayer invalid). The ruling is restricted to suspicion of hadath; other suspicions (like doubting the validity of wudu or the completion of a previous prayer) also invalidate prayer if they lead to turning away, even without exiting the mosque, because that turning is considered abandonment. Istikhlaf (appointing a substitute imam) is treated like exiting the mosque because it involves many actions.

Key Terms
ظن الحدث (zann al-hadath): Suspicion of having broken ritual purity (hadath) based on a likely indication.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that allows departing from strict analogy (qiyas) for a more equitable ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is permissible and does not affect the prayer.
C) It is recommended and the prayer continues.
D) It is only allowed if the imam is insane.

Key Takeaway
Exiting the mosque with a false suspicion of hadath nullifies the prayer; the Hanafi school preserves the prayer only when the person does not exit and the suspicion is genuine.
