Specific Nullifiers of Prayer and Their Timing
Lists events that nullify prayer and explains their rationale and timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five specific nullifiers of prayer mentioned in the Hanafi school and apply the timing condition (before final sitting) to determine whether a prayer is nullified.

Core Idea
Madness, fainting, wet dream, loud laughter, and looking with discharge nullify prayer only if they occur before the final sitting.

You already know that speech and intentional hadath break the prayer. But what about events beyond your control, like fainting or a wet dream, or actions like loud laughter? This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that such events do nullify the prayer, but with a critical timing condition. Understanding this distinction ensures you know exactly when a prayer is invalid and must be repeated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage lists five events that nullify prayer: madness (junun), fainting (ighma'), wet dream (ihtilam), loud laughter (qahqaha), and looking at a woman with discharge (nazar ma'a al-inzal). The ruling is that each invalidates the prayer (batil) under certain conditions.
These are specific; general bodily discharges (e.g., from illness) are not automatically nullifiers.
2
Locate the dalil
For loud laughter, the author cites the Prophet's hadith: 'Let him build upon his prayer as long as he does not speak.' Since laughter is akin to speech, it triggers the same nullification.
The hadith is used as dalil by analogy (qiyas) – qahqaha is like kalam.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith treats speech as a cutoff. The author argues that loud laughter (qahqaha) falls under 'not speaking' because it is an act that produces words/sounds contrary to the prayer's solemnity. Hence, it nullifies just as speech does.
A light smile (tabassum) does not nullify because it does not produce sound.
4
Note the timing condition
All these nullifiers only take effect if they occur before the final sitting (qu'ud qadr al-tashahhud). After that sitting, even intentional hadath does not nullify the prayer, so these events are even less impactful.
The final sitting is considered a strong integral (rukn) that makes the prayer less vulnerable to nullification.
5
Understand the rationale
The first three events (madness, fainting, wet dream) are rare, so they are not analogized to vomiting/nosebleed (which do not nullify). They are treated as disruptive events that break continuity. The author also notes that these events involve confusion (idtirab) or pause (mukth), and in either case the person is performing an action (sana') that invalidates the prayer.
The principle: any extraneous action (sana') that takes the person out of the state of prayer is nullifying.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما فسادها بما ذكر من الجنون والإغماء والاحتلام فلأنه يندر وجود هذه العوارض فلم تكن في معنى ما ورد به النص من القيء والرعاف وكذلك إذا قهقه لأنه بمنزلة الكلام وهو قاطع لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام وليبن على صلاته ما لم يتكلم. وكذا لو نظر إلى امرأة فأنزل. ومحل الفساد بهذه الأشياء قبل القعود قدر التشهد أما بعده فلا لما سنذكره أن من تعمد الحدث بعده لا يفسدها فهذا أولى ولا يخلوا لموصوف بها عن اضطراب أو مكث، وكيفما كان فالصنع منه موجود على القول باشتراطه للخروج، أما في الاضطراب فظاهر، في المكث فلأنه يصير به مؤدياً جزءاً من الصلاة مع الحدث والأداء صنع منه.
As for its nullification by what was mentioned of madness, fainting, and wet dream, it is because these accidents are rare, so they are not in the meaning of what the text came with of vomiting and nosebleed. And likewise if he laughs loudly (qahqaha), for it is like speech, and it is a cutoff due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'And let him build upon his prayer as long as he does not speak.' And likewise if he looks at a woman and discharges. And the place of nullification by these things is before sitting for the measure of tashahhud; after it there is no nullification, as we will mention that one who intentionally causes hadath after it does not invalidate it, so this is more appropriate. And it is not devoid for the one described by these of confusion or pause, and however it is, the action is present from him according to the opinion requiring it for exit. As for confusion, it is apparent; as for pause, because he thereby performs a part of the prayer with hadath, and performance is an action from him.
Source pages p. 652

Commentary
This passage is a ruling that lists specific nullifiers of prayer and their underlying reasons. The text states that madness (junun), fainting (ighma'), and wet dream (ihtilam) nullify prayer because these events are rare and thus not included in the category of what the texts address (like vomiting or nosebleed, which do not nullify). Loud laughter (qahqaha) nullifies because it is comparable to speech, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Let him build upon his prayer as long as he does not speak.' Looking at a woman with discharge also nullifies. Importantly, these nullifiers only affect the prayer if they occur before sitting for the duration of tashahhud (the final sitting). If they occur after that, the prayer is not nullified because even intentional hadath after the final sitting does not invalidate the prayer. The explanation adds that these events necessarily involve either confusion (idtirab) or a pause (mukth), and in either case, the person is performing an action (sana') that invalidates the prayer based on the principle that exiting the prayer requires a deliberate action.

Key Terms
قهقهة (qahqaha): Loud, audible laughter that nullifies prayer; it is considered akin to speech.
قعود قدر التشهد (qu'ud qadr al-tashahhud): The sitting posture for the duration required to recite the tashahhud (the testimony of faith) in the final rak'ah.
جنون (junun): Loss of sanity or consciousness due to mental disturbance; one of the nullifiers of prayer.
إغماء (ighma'): Fainting; a state of unconsciousness that nullifies prayer.
احتلام (ihtilam): Wet dream; nocturnal emission that nullifies prayer if it occurs during prayer (before final sitting).
نظر مع الإنزال (nazar ma'a al-inzal): Looking at a woman with seminal discharge; a specific nullifier.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The prayer is valid but he must perform sajda sahw.
C) The prayer is not nullified.
D) The prayer is invalid and must be restarted.

Key Takeaway
The prayer is nullified by madness, fainting, wet dream, loud laughter, and looking with discharge only if they occur before the final sitting of tashahhud.

Boundaries of the Prayer Place (Musalla) and Ruling on Movement
Defines the boundaries of the musalla for movement nullification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the boundaries of the musalla for a man and a woman, and apply the ruling on forward movement with and without a sutra.

Core Idea
Exit your musalla, lose your prayer – but the musalla's size depends on your situation and whether you have a sutra.

The Hanafi school carefully defines the space within which a worshipper may move during prayer without invalidating it. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on earlier rulings, clarifying the boundaries for different scenarios: a congregational prayer in a mosque, a woman praying at home, and a lone worshipper in the desert. It also records a disagreement between the majority and Qadi al-Nasafi regarding the woman's musalla.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
The text first equates a house, funeral prayer place, and graveyard with a mosque: all are considered a single unit (buq'ah wahidah) for movement rules.
This means moving within these spaces is allowed as long as you stay within the designated prayer area.
2
Note the woman's exception
Unlike a man, a woman's prayer becomes invalid if she steps out of her musalla. Her house is not like a mosque for a man – she has a smaller, fixed area.
Al-Nasafi disagrees, holding that a woman's house is like a mosque for a man, so her prayer does not invalidate by exiting her immediate spot.
3
Apply the desert scenario
For a person praying in the open desert, the extent of the rows (if in congregation) defines the musalla for lateral and backward movement. For forward movement, if there is no sutra, only the place of prostration counts.
If alone, the musalla is the prostration spot in all four directions unless a sutra is placed, in which case the area within the sutra becomes the musalla.
4
Resolve the internal conflict
The author rejects al-Hidayah's view that without a sutra, the imam's rows extend behind him. Instead, he upholds al-Bada'i's position: the imam's forward limit is his prostration spot.
This shows the importance of later tarjih within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدار ومصلى الجنازة والجبانة كالمسجد إذ له حكم البقعة الواحدة - كذا قالوا - إلا في المرأة فإنها إن خرجت عن مصلاها فسدت صلاتها : وليس البيت لها كالمسجد للرجل. وقال القاضي الإمام أبو علي النسفي : لا تفسد صلاتها والبيت لها كالمسجد للرجل. كذا في فتاوى قاضيخان وإن كان يصلي في الصحراء فمقدار الصفوف له حكم المسجدان مشى يمنة أو يسرة أو خلفاً، وإن مشى أمامه وليس بين يديه سترة فالصحيح هو التقدير بموضع السجود، وإن كان وحده فمسجده موضع سجود، من الجوانب الأربع إلا إذا مشى أمامه وبين يديه سترة فيعطي لداخلها حكم المسجد. كذا في البدائع. وفي فتح القدير والأوجه إذا لم يكن سترة أن يعتبر موضع سجوده لأن الإمام منفرد في حق نفسه والمنفرد حكمه ذلك .اهـ. وهذا البحث هو ما صححه في البدائع، فعلم أن ما في الهداية من أن الإمام إذا لم يكن بين يديه سترة فمقدار الصفوف خلفه ضعيف، وأما فسادها بما ذكر من الجنون والإغماء والاحتلام فلأنه يندر وجود هذه العوارض فلم تكن في معنى ما ورد به النص من القيء والرعاف وكذلك إذا قهقه لأنه بمنزلة الكلام وهو قاطع لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام وليبن على صلاته ما لم يتكلم. وكذا لو نظر إلى امرأة فأنزل. ومحل الفساد بهذه الأشياء قبل القعود قدر التشهد أما بعده فلا لما سنذكره أن من تعمد الحدث بعده لا يفسدها فهذا أولى ولا يخلوا لموصوف بها عن اضطراب أو مكث، وكيفما كان فالصنع منه موجود على القول باشتراطه للخروج، أما في الاضطراب فظاهر، في المكث فلأنه يصير به مؤدياً جزءاً من الصلاة مع الحدث والأداء صنع منه.
And the house, the funeral prayer place, and the graveyard are like the mosque, for it has the ruling of one site - thus they said - except for the woman, for if she exits her prayer place, her prayer becomes invalid: and the house is not like the mosque for the man. And Qadi Imam Abu Ali al-Nasafi said: her prayer does not become invalid, and the house is like the mosque for the man. Likewise in Fatawa Qadikhan. And if he prays in the desert, the extent of the rows has the ruling of the mosque if he walks right, left, or behind. And if he walks forward and there is no sutra (screen) in front of him, the correct view is the estimation by the place of prostration. And if he is alone, his mosque is the place of prostration from the four directions, except if he walks forward and there is a sutra in front of him, then its interior is given the ruling of the mosque. Likewise in al-Bada'i'. And in Fath al-Qadir: and the preferred view when there is no sutra is that the place of his prostration is considered, because the imam is alone in respect to himself, and the ruling for the one alone is that. ... And this research is what was corrected in al-Bada'i', so it is known that what is in al-Hidayah that if the imam has no sutra in front of him, the extent of the rows behind him is weak.
Source pages p. 652

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings regarding the definition of 'masjid' (place of prayer) for the purpose of nullification by moving. It begins by stating that a house, a funeral prayer place, and a graveyard are treated like a mosque, meaning they are considered one unit of space. However, for a woman, if she walks out of her prayer place (musalla), her prayer becomes invalid, and her house is not like the mosque for a man (i.e., she cannot move around freely). Imam Abu Ali al-Nasafi disagrees, holding that her prayer is not invalidated and her house is like the mosque for a man. For someone praying in the desert, the extent of the rows (if praying in congregation) constitutes the 'mosque' for lateral movements. If walking forward and there is no sutra (a barrier like a wall), the valid view is to estimate by the place of prostration (i.e., the spot where his head touches). If alone, his 'mosque' is the place of prostration in all four directions, except if he walks forward with a sutra, then the area enclosed by the sutra is considered the mosque. The text notes that the Hidayah's ruling that the imam's rows extend behind him even without a sutra is considered weak in the Bada'i'. The passage also repeats the earlier nullifiers (madness, etc.) but that part is likely an OCR duplication; we treat it as part of the same textual unit.

Key Terms
المصلى (al-musalla): The specific place designated for prayer, whether in a mosque, house, or open space.
سترة (sutra): A barrier (like a wall or pillar) placed in front of the worshipper to mark the prayer area.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The area of the rows behind him.
B) The place of his prostration from all four directions.
C) The place where his head touches (sajdah spot).
D) The entire desert.

Key Takeaway
The musalla is a defined space; forward movement without a sutra is strictly limited, while lateral and backward movement are more permissible, and the woman's musalla is particularly restricted.

Ruling on Suspecting Hadath and Imam's Substitution in Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on restarting prayer when fearing hadath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on restarting prayer when fearing hadath and explain why Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf differ.

Core Idea
A mere suspicion of hadath does not invalidate prayer, but fear plus actual hadath triggers a dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on restarting.

This passage examines two interrelated scenarios: (1) a person who suspects hadath without clear evidence, and (2) a person who fears hadath and leaves the prayer before it occurs. The Hanafi school's founders, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, differ on whether the prayer must be restarted in the second case. Additionally, the passage discusses the effect of an imam substituting due to doubt and the rulings for a woman leaving her prayer place.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
The passage presents two distinct cases: (a) a person who suspects hadath without evidence (e.g., doubting exhalation of wind), and (b) a person who fears hadath will occur and leaves the prayer before it happens. Recognize that each carries different rulings.
The first case is based on qiyas, the second involves an intra-Hanafi dispute.
2
Analyze the default ruling for baseless suspicion
When the suspicion has no supporting evidence, the passage states that restarting (isti'naf) is required 'absolutely' based on analogy. This is the general Hanafi principle: unsubstantiated doubt is ignored.
The author notes he has not seen a clear transmission for this, indicating caution.
3
Examine the fear-and-hadath scenario
A person fears hadath will overtake him, leaves the prayer, and then hadath actually occurs. According to Abu Hanifa, the prayer is invalid and must be restarted. Abu Yusuf holds the prayer remains valid.
This is a khilaf within the Hanafi school itself (intra-Hanafi).
4
Consider the imam's substitution due to doubt
If the imam doubts his purity and appoints a substitute, the entire congregation's prayer is invalidated. This ruling is from al-Tanjis and underscores that uncertainty about purity during prayer nullifies the act.
The imam's doubt is treated as a cause of invalidating the prayer for all followers.
5
Apply the ruling on place to women
The passage states that leaving the prayer place (musalla) invalidates a woman's prayer, unless the later view of Abu Ali al-Nasafi is accepted. This illustrates how analogous reasoning (qiyas) extends rulings from men to women with differences.
The default view treats a woman's house as unlike a mosque for a man; Al-Nasafi treats them as analogous.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرجوح. وصور مسألة الظن - الشمني - بأن خرج شيء من أنفه فظن أنه رعف، فظاهره أنه لو لم يكن للظن دليل بأن شك في خروج ريح ونحوه فإنه يستقبل مطلقاً بالانحراف عملاً بما هو القياس لكني لم أره منقولاً، وإنما في التنجيس: لو شك الإمام في الصلاة فاستخلف فسدت صلاتهم، ولو خاف سبق الحدث فانصرف ثم سبقه الحدث فالاستئناف لازم عند أبي حنيفة خلافاً لأبي يوسف كذا في المجمع والدار ومصلى الجنازة والجبانة كالمسجد إذ له حكم البقعة الواحدة - كذا قالوا - إلا في المرأة فإنها إن خرجت عن مصلاها فسدت صلاتها : وليس البيت لها كالمسجد للرجل. وقال القاضي الإمام أبو علي النسفي : لا تفسد صلاتها والبيت لها كالمسجد للرجل. كذا في فتاوى قاضيخان
The preponderated (view). And the forms of the issue of suspicion - al-Shamni - that something came out of his nose and he thought it was a nosebleed, then it is apparent that if there is no evidence for the suspicion, such as doubting the exit of wind and the like, then he absolutely restarts with deviation (facing qibla?), acting upon analogy, but I have not seen it transmitted. And in al-Tanjis: If the imam has doubt in the prayer and appoints a successor, their prayer is invalidated. And if one fears the precedence of hadath and leaves, then hadath overtakes him, then restarting is necessary according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to Abu Yusuf. Similarly, in the congregational mosque, the house, the funeral prayer place, and the cemetery are like the mosque, for they have the ruling of a single place - thus they said - except for a woman, for if she leaves her prayer place, her prayer is invalidated: and the house for her is not like the mosque for a man. And Judge Imam Abu Ali al-Nasafi said: Her prayer is not invalidated, and the house for her is like the mosque for a man. Thus in Fatawa Qadikhan.
Source pages p. 652

Commentary
This passage discusses the handling of doubt (shakk) regarding ritual impurity (hadath) during prayer. It begins by citing al-Shamni's scenario where something exits the nose and the person suspects it is blood, noting that if the doubt has no supporting evidence (e.g., similar to doubting the release of wind), the prayer must be restarted completely, based on qiyas (analogy), although the author has not seen this transmitted from earlier authorities. The text then references al-Tanjis (likely a work) regarding the imam: if he doubts his purity and appoints a successor, the entire congregation's prayer is invalidated. A distinct case is also mentioned: if a person fears hadath may occur and leaves the prayer, then hadath actually happens, Abu Hanifa rules that restarting (isti'naf) is necessary, while Abu Yusuf holds otherwise. The passage then shifts to the ruling of the prayer place: a mosque, a house (private prayer area), a funeral prayer area, and a cemetery all share the same ruling of being a single place (i.e., moving within them does not invalidate prayer), except for a woman—if she steps out of her designated prayer spot (musalla) within her house, her prayer is invalid, because the house is not like the mosque for her. However, Imam Abu Ali al-Nasafi diverges, stating that the house for a woman is analogous to the mosque for a man, so leaving it does not invalidate. This difference is recorded in Fatawa Qadikhan.

Key Terms
الظن (al-zann): A doubt or suspicion about the occurrence of hadath, without certain knowledge.
التنجيس (al-tanjis): A work or chapter title referenced; possibly a Hanafi fiqh book or a section on impurities.
الاستئناف (al-isti'naf): Restarting the prayer from the beginning because the current one is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is valid and no action is needed.
B) The prayer is invalid and must be restarted.
C) The prayer is valid but wudu must be repeated.
D) The prayer is suspended until the doubt is resolved.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, leaving prayer due to fear of hadath triggers a dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf when hadath subsequently occurs, with Abu Hanifa requiring restart and Abu Yusuf deeming the prayer valid.

The Prayer Place in the Desert and the Imam's Forward Limit
Clarifies the boundaries of the prayer place and the effect of the imam moving forward.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the permissible forward movement of the imam in desert prayer and apply the correct limit (place of prostration) as opposed to the rows behind.

Core Idea
The imam's forward limit in the desert is his place of prostration, not the rows behind, when he lacks a sutrah.

The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a nuance in Hanafi fiqh: where exactly can the imam move forward without invalidating the prayer? The answer depends on whether he has a sutrah (screen). This lesson unpacks the correct ruling and corrects a weaker position from al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify the act under discussion: the imam's forward movement during prayer in the open desert. The ruling: if he moves forward beyond the defined limit, the prayer becomes invalid.
The prayer is otherwise valid if he moves sideways or backward within the rows.
2
Distinguish the key variables
Determine whether the imam has a sutrah (screen) in front of him. This distinguishes two scenarios: with a sutrah, the permissible forward area is the interior of the sutrah; without a sutrah, it is only the place of prostration.
Also note whether the imam is alone or leading a congregation—the ruling for a single person is analogous.
3
Locate the evidence (t‘alīl)
The reasoning is based on qiyas (analogy): the imam, regarding his own forward space, is treated like a person praying alone, whose mosque is his place of prostration from all sides. This is the ratio legis (t‘alīl) for the ruling.
The proof is not a direct text but a derived analogy within the madhhab.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi correction
Al-Hidayah stated that the imam's forward limit without a sutrah is the extent of the rows behind him. This passage corrects that: the correct view (as in al-Bada‘i‘ and Fath al-Qadir) is the place of prostration. The earlier view is declared weak.
This correction is an example of tarjih (preference) among Hanafi positions.
5
Apply the ruling
Apply the mufta bihi (operative) ruling: the imam may not move forward beyond his place of prostration if he has no sutrah; if he has a sutrah, he may move within the interior of the sutrah.
The practical consequence: in large gatherings, the imam's forward movement is severely restricted unless a sutrah is placed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كان يصلي في الصحراء فمقدار الصفوف له حكم المسجدان مشى يمنة أو يسرة أو خلفاً، وإن مشى أمامه وليس بين يديه سترة فالصحيح هو التقدير بموضع السجود، وإن كان وحده فمسجده موضع سجود، من الجوانب الأربع إلا إذا مشى أمامه وبين يديه سترة فيعطي لداخلها حكم المسجد. كذا في البدائع. وفي فتح القدير والأوجه إذا لم يكن سترة أن يعتبر موضع سجوده لأن الإمام منفرد في حق نفسه والمنفرد حكمه ذلك .اهـ. وهذا البحث هو ما صححه في البدائع، فعلم أن ما في الهداية من أن الإمام إذا لم يكن بين يديه سترة فمقدار الصفوف خلفه ضعيف
And if he prays in the desert, then the extent of the rows has the ruling of the mosque; if he walks right, left, or backward, (it is fine). And if he walks forward and there is no screen in front of him, then the correct (view) is the estimation by the place of prostration. And if he is alone, his mosque is his place of prostration, from all four sides, except if he walks forward and there is a screen in front of him, then the interior (of the screen) is given the ruling of the mosque. Thus in al-Bada'i'. And in Fath al-Qadir, the preferred view is that if there is no screen, his place of prostration is considered, because the imam is alone with respect to himself, and the ruling for one alone is that. End. And this research is what was corrected in al-Bada'i'. Thus it is known that what is in al-Hidayah – that the imam, if there is no screen in front of him, (the limit is) the extent of the rows behind him – is weak.
Source pages p. 652

Commentary
This passage defines the prayer space (musalla) for one praying in an open desert. It begins by stating that the rows behind the imam have the ruling of the mosque—meaning moving right, left, or backward within the row area does not invalidate prayer. However, if the imam moves forward without a sutrah (screen), the correct view is that the limit is his place of prostration (mawdi' al-sujud). For a person praying alone, his entire surrounding area up to the place of prostration in all directions is his mosque, unless he moves forward beyond a sutrah, in which case the area inside the sutrah is the mosque. These rulings are from al-Bada'i' and Fath al-Qadir. The author then corrects a position in al-Hidayah that for the imam without a screen, the limit is the extent of the rows behind him; this is declared weak, and the correct view is the place of prostration.

Key Terms
الصفوف (al-sufuf): The rows of worshippers behind the imam; their extent defines the prayer place in the desert.
السترة (al-sutrah): A screen or barrier placed in front of the praying person; it defines the allowed forward limit.
موضع السجود (mawdi' al-sujud): The spot where the forehead rests during prostration; used as a measure for the prayer place.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The extent of the rows behind him.
B) The place of his prostration.
C) The entire area of the congregation.
D) Any distance as long as he faces the qibla.

Key Takeaway
The imam's forward limit in desert prayer is his place of prostration unless he has a sutrah; the view that it is the rows behind is weak.

Invalidators of Prayer: Specific Events and Proof
Lists specific invalidators of prayer and provides proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the specific events that invalidate prayer (insanity, fainting, wet dream, loud laughter, looking and emitting) and explain the hadith proof for loud laughter as a disconnector.

Core Idea
Loud laughter invalidates prayer because it is analogous to speech; the hadith 'build upon your prayer as long as you do not speak' establishes speech as a disconnector.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq lists additional invalidators of prayer beyond ordinary hadath. It explains the reasoning behind each, particularly loud laughter, which is treated like speech due to the prophetic command. Understanding these invalidators is essential for preserving the validity of salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the listed invalidators
Read the source and list the specific events that invalidate prayer: insanity (junun), fainting (ighma'), wet dream (ihtilam), loud laughter (qahqahah), and looking at a woman with emission.
These are in addition to normal hadath (breaking wudu).
2
Understand the rationale for insanity, fainting, wet dream
These are rare events and are not analogous to the explicit text about vomiting and nosebleed. They are not covered by qiyas but are separate invalidators due to their disruptive nature.
The text says 'they are not in the meaning of what the text came with'.
3
Analyze the ruling for loud laughter
Loud laughter is likened to speech because both involve vocalization. The hadith 'Let him build upon his prayer as long as he does not speak' indicates that speech cuts off prayer; thus, loud laughter does the same.
Smile (tabassum) does not invalidate.
4
Trace the dalil for loud laughter
The proof is a hadith (Sunnah ahad). The operative phrase is 'as long as he does not speak.' In Hanafi usul, this command indicates that speech (and its equivalent) invalidates prayer.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut but accepted as evidence.
5
Note the inclusion of looking and emitting
Looking at a woman and ejaculating is also an invalidator. It is treated as an extreme form of hadath that disrupts the state of prayer.
This is analogized to other invalidators.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما فسادها بما ذكر من الجنون والإغماء والاحتلام فلأنه يندر وجود هذه العوارض فلم تكن في معنى ما ورد به النص من القيء والرعاف وكذلك إذا قهقه لأنه بمنزلة الكلام وهو قاطع لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام وليبن على صلاته ما لم يتكلم. وكذا لو نظر إلى امرأة فأنزل. ومحل الفساد بهذه الأشياء قبل القعود قدر التشهد أما بعده فلا لما سنذكره أن من تعمد الحدث بعده لا يفسدها فهذا أولى ولا يخلوا لموصوف بها عن اضطراب أو مكث، وكيفما كان فالصنع منه موجود على القول باشتراطه للخروج، أما في الاضطراب فظاهر، في المكث فلأنه يصير به مؤدياً جزءاً من الصلاة مع الحدث والأداء صنع منه.
And as for its invalidation by what was mentioned of insanity, fainting, and wet dream, it is because these occurrences are rare, so they are not in the meaning of what the text came with of vomiting and nosebleed. Similarly, if he laughs loudly, because it is in the position of speech, and it is a disconnection due to his statement, peace be upon him, "And let him build upon his prayer as long as he does not speak." And likewise if he looks at a woman and emits. And the place of invalidation by these things is before the sitting of the amount of tashahhud. As for after it, then no, because we will mention that whoever deliberately performs hadath after it does not invalidate it, so this is more appropriate. And he who is described by these is not free from disturbance or staying. However it may be, the action from him exists on the opinion that it is a condition for exiting (the prayer). As for disturbance, it is apparent; as for staying, it is because he thereby performs a part of the prayer with hadath, and performing is an action from him.
Source pages p. 652

Commentary
This passage explains the invalidators (mufsidat) of prayer beyond ordinary hadath. It states that insanity (junun), fainting (ighma'), and wet dream (ihtilam) invalidate the prayer because, though rare, they are not analogous to the events explicitly mentioned in the primary texts (like vomiting and nosebleed). Loud laughter (qahqaha) also invalidates because it resembles speech, which cuts off prayer per the hadith. Similarly, looking at a woman and ejaculating invalidates. The key timing rule: these invalidators only cause invalidation if they occur before the final sitting (qa'dah) of the amount of tashahhud. After that, even deliberate hadath does not invalidate (as will be discussed later), so these are even less likely to invalidate. The passage also addresses that when such an event occurs, the person inevitably experiences either disturbance (idtirab) or staying (mukth) – in either case, the person is committing an action (san') with hadath, which invalidates if it is a condition for exiting the prayer.

Key Terms
القعود قدر التشهد (al-qu'ud qadr al-tashahhud): The sitting in the final rak'ah for the duration needed to recite the tashahhud.
القهقهة (al-qahqahah): Loud laughter that is audible to oneself; it invalidates prayer because it resembles speech.
الاضطراب (al-idtirab): Agitation or involuntary movement; here it refers to the natural disturbance when an invalidating event occurs.
المكث (al-mukth): Staying in place; here it means remaining in prayer while experiencing hadath, which is considered an action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT listed as an invalidator of prayer in this passage?
A) Loud laughter
B) Fainting
C) Vomiting
D) Looking at a woman and emitting

Key Takeaway
Loud laughter invalidates prayer because it is like speech; insanity, fainting, wet dream, and looking with emission are also invalidators, all subject to the timing rule of before the final sitting.

Timing and Action: When Invalidators Apply
Explains the timing rule and the concept of action when invalidators occur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that invalidators affect prayer only before the final sitting (qa'dah) and explain why remaining in prayer after hadath constitutes an action.

Core Idea
After sitting for the tashahhud, the prayer is complete and not invalidated by subsequent events.

This segment clarifies a critical timing nuance: events that normally invalidate prayer (like insanity, fainting, or loud laughter) only do so before the worshipper has sat for the tashahhud. After that, the prayer is sound. It also explains that when such events occur, the worshiper inevitably performs an action (disturbance or staying), which counts as a deliberate act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the timing rule
Read the line: 'the place of invalidation by these things is before the sitting of the amount of tashahhud. As for after it, then no.' This is the key rule.
The final sitting is a wajib act that signals the end of the prayer's vulnerable state.
2
Understand the analogy to deliberate hadath
The text says that even deliberate hadath (breaking wudu) after the qa'dah does not invalidate, so these events are even less likely to invalidate after that point.
This is an analogy (a min qabi al-mawl?) showing that after qa'dah, the prayer is secure.
3
Analyze the concept of 'action' (san')
When an invalidating event occurs, the person inevitably experiences disturbance (idtirab) or stays in place (mukth). Both are considered actions by the worshiper because they involve voluntary or involuntary movement while in prayer.
The action is a condition for exiting the prayer; performing any action with hadath invalidates.
4
Determine the consequence
If the event occurs before qa'dah: prayer is invalid. If after: prayer is valid. The worshiper's action (disturbance or staying) is part of the invalidation process before qa'dah.
This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school.

Source Text

Hadath After Tashahhud: Validity and Required Actions
States ruling and provides hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for hadath after tashahhud, identify the wajib actions (wudu and salam), and explain the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
Hadath after tashahhud: prayer valid, wudu and salam become wajib.

This lesson addresses a common situation in salah: what happens if a person loses wudu after the final sitting but before saying salam? The Hanafi school provides a specific ruling that balances the validity of the prayer with the obligation of purity for the salam. The key evidence is a hadith from Ibn Umar reported by Tirmidhi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is experiencing hadath (ritual impurity) after completing the tashahhud but before saying salam. The ruling is that the prayer is valid (sahih).
This is the primary ruling from the passage.
2
Identify the wajib actions
The person must perform wudu and then say salam. Both become wajib because salam requires purity, and wudu is needed to achieve that purity.
If neglected, it is makruh tahrimi, and if the salam is missed entirely, the prayer must be repeated.
3
Locate the dalil
The evidence is a hadith from Tirmidhi: 'When a man experiences hadath while he has sat at the end of his prayer before saying salam, then his prayer is valid.'
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit statement 'his prayer is valid' (jāzat ṣalātuh) directly proves the ruling. The condition 'sat at the end' indicates the final sitting (tashahhud).
The hadith does not require immediate salam; it allows building upon the prayer after wudu.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may require the repetition of the entire prayer if hadath occurs before salam, because they consider taslim a rukn that must be performed in a state of purity.
The Hanafi position relies on the explicit hadith and the principle that building upon a valid prayer is permitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حدث بعد التشهد توضأ وسلم وإن تعمده أو تكلم تمت صلاته. قوله : (وإن سبقه حدث بعد التشهد توضأ وسلم لأن التسليم واجب ولا بد له من الوضوء ليأتي به فالوضوء والسلام واجبان فلو لم يفعل كره تحريماً. والشروط التي قدمناها لصحة البناء لا بد منها للسلام حتى لو لم يتوضأ فوراً أو أتى بمناف بعده فاته السلام ووجب عليه إعادتها لإقامة الواجب لأنه حكم كل صلاة أديت مع كراهة التحريم، وإن كان إماماً استخلف من يسلم بالقوم . قوله : (وإن تعمده أو تكلم تمت صلاته أي تعمد الحدث لحديث الترمذي عن ابن عمر قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا أحدث ـ يعني الرجل ـ وقد جلس في آخر صلاته قبل أن يسلم فقد جازت صلاته و معنى قوله «تمت صلاته تمت فرائض بها ولهذا تفسد بفعل المنافي وإلا فمعلوم أنها لم تتم بسائر ما يسب إنيها من الواجبات لعدم خروجه
Hadath after tashahhud: he performs wudu and says salam, and if he deliberately does it or speaks, his prayer is complete. His statement: (And if hadath overtakes him after tashahhud, he performs wudu and says salam, because taslim is obligatory and he must have wudu to perform it, so wudu and salam are both obligatory. If he does not do so, it is prohibitively disliked. The conditions we previously stated for building (upon prayer) are necessary for salam, so if he does not perform wudu immediately or does something contradictory after it, the salam is missed and it becomes obligatory to repeat the prayer to fulfill the obligation, because this is the ruling of every prayer performed with prohibitive dislike. And if he is an imam, he appoints a successor to say salam to the people. His statement: (And if he deliberately does it or speaks, his prayer is complete), meaning he deliberately performs hadath, due to the hadith of Tirmidhi from Ibn Umar who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: When a man experiences hadath while he has sat at the end of his prayer before saying salam, then his prayer is valid. And the meaning of his statement "his prayer is complete" is that its obligatory acts are complete by it; therefore it is invalidated by contradictory actions; otherwise it is known that it is not complete with all the other obligatory aspects due to his not having exited.
Source pages p. 653

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling for a person who experiences hadath (breaking wudu) after completing the tashahhud in the final sitting. The core ruling is: he should make wudu and then say the salam, and his prayer is valid. The commentary explains that taslim (saying salam) is wajib, and since he must be in a state of purity to utter it, both wudu and salam become wajib. If he neglects them, it is makruh tahrimi. The conditions for building upon the previous prayer (such as not doing something contradictory) are also necessary for the salam. If he delays wudu or does an invalidating act, he loses the opportunity for salam and must repeat the prayer. For an imam, he should appoint a successor to lead the salam. The passage then addresses the scenario where the person deliberately commits hadath or speaks after tashahhud: the prayer is still complete, based on the hadith from Tirmidhi where the Prophet said that if a man experiences hadath after sitting at the end of prayer before salam, his prayer is valid. The commentary clarifies that 'complete' means the obligatory acts (fara'id) are fulfilled, but not necessarily the wajibat; hence contradictory actions can still invalidate.

Key Terms
التسليم (al-taslim): The final salutation (salam) to exit prayer; it is wajib in the Hanafi school.
الحدث (al-hadath): Ritual impurity that breaks wudu (e.g., passing wind, urine, etc.).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person experiences hadath after completing the tashahhud but before saying salam, what must he do?
A) Repeat the entire prayer.
B) Make wudu and then say salam.
C) Say salam immediately without wudu.
D) Make wudu and repeat the prayer from the beginning.

Key Takeaway
After tashahhud, hadath does not invalidate prayer; wudu and salam become wajib.

Sleep During Prayer and Its Effect on Wudu
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of sleep during prayer on wudu, with critical refinement by al-Ramli.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi ruling on sleep during prayer and distinguish between cases requiring building versus restarting the prayer.

Core Idea
Sleep while lying down breaks wudu; intent determines whether you build or restart.

A person praying may fall asleep, raising questions about the validity of wudu and the prayer itself. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq) presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: does sleep nullify wudu? The author critically refines earlier views, distinguishing between unintentional dozing and deliberate sleep while lying down. Understanding this ruling is essential for anyone leading or performing long prayers, especially in congregation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The passage discusses a person who falls asleep during prayer. It distinguishes between dozing (nu'as) and lying down (idtija') while sleeping. Identify the two scenarios mentioned.
2
State the disputed question
The core issue is whether sleep (specifically while lying down) nullifies wudu. Note that there are multiple views within the Hanafi school.
3
Identify the two positions
One view (from al-Zahiriya) says sleep does not break wudu; the other (relied upon by al-Ramli) says it does. Also note the distinction for deliberate sleep.
4
Examine the evidence and reasoning
The opposing view relies on the principle that only exiting of wudu (hadath) breaks it. The correct view argues that sleep leads to loss of control, thus it is a naqid. The intent (deliberate vs unintentional) is also considered.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If sleep breaks wudu, the person must perform wudu and can build upon the prayer if unintentional; if deliberate, they must restart. If it does not break, no action is needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العناية : وإنما قال أو نام فاحتلم لأن النوم بانفراده ليس بمفسد وكذا الاحتلام المنفرد عن النوم وهو البلوغ بالسن فجمع بينهما بياناً للمراد اهـ. وفي الظهيرية المصلى إذا نعس في صلاته فاضطجع، قيل تنتقض طهارته فيتوضأ ويبني وقيل لا تفسد صلاته ولا تنتقض عهارته اهـ. قوله : (لأن النوم بانفراده ليس بمفسد قال الرملي : ذكر في التتارخانية أقوالاً واختلاف تصحيح في المسألة، وكذلك ذكر في الجوهرة في نوم المضطجع والمريض في الصلاة اختلافاً، والصحيح أنه ينقض وبه نأخذ ونقل في التتارخانية عن المحيط في النوم مضطجعاً الحال لا يخلو إن غلبت عيناه فنام ثم اضطجع في حالة نومه فهو بمنزلة ما لو سبقه الحدث يتوضأ ويبني، ولو تعمد النوم في الصلاة مضطجعاً فإنه يتوضأ ويستقبل الصلاة هكذا حكي عن مشايخنا اهـ. فراجع المنقول ولا تغتر بما أطلقه هنا .اهـ.
Al-Inayah: And he only said "or slept and had a wet dream" because sleep alone is not an invalidator, and likewise wet dream alone (without sleep) is puberty by age. So he combined them to clarify the intended meaning. End. And in al-Zahiriya: The one praying: if he dozes in his prayer and lies down, it is said his purity is broken, so he performs wudu and builds (upon his prayer). And it is said his prayer is not invalidated and his purity is not broken. End. His statement: (Because sleep alone is not an invalidator). Al-Ramli said: It is mentioned in al-Tatar Khaniyya that there are statements and differences in correction on the issue. Also mentioned in al-Jawhara regarding the sleep of one lying down and the sick in prayer, there is difference. And the correct (view) is that it breaks (wudu) and we take that. And it is narrated in al-Tatar Khaniyya from al-Muhit: Regarding sleep while lying down: it is not free from (the possibility that) if his eyes overcame him and he slept then lay down in his sleep, it is like the case of hadath overtaking him: he performs wudu and builds. And if he deliberately sleeps while lying down in prayer, then he performs wudu and restarts the prayer. Thus it is narrated from our scholars. End. So review the transmitted narrations and do not be deceived by what he has absolutely stated here. End.
Source pages p. 653

Commentary
This passage delves into the effect of sleep during prayer. It begins with a comment from al-Inayah on why the author of the matn mentioned 'or slept and had a wet dream' together: because sleep alone does not invalidate prayer, and wet dream alone (without sleep) is simply puberty by age, so combining them clarifies the intended meaning. Then a ruling from al-Zahiriya is quoted: if a person dozes (na'asa) in prayer and lies down, there are two views: one says his wudu is broken so he must perform wudu and build upon his prayer; the other says neither his prayer nor purity is invalidated. The commentary by al-Ramli then addresses the statement that 'sleep alone is not an invalidator.' He notes that in al-Tatar Khaniyya there are multiple opinions and corrections, and similarly in al-Jawhara there is disagreement about the sleep of one lying down and the sick. The correct view, according to al-Ramli, is that sleep does break wudu, and this is what we adopt. He further cites from al-Muhit that if a person falls asleep and then lies down while asleep, it is like hadath overtaking him – he makes wudu and builds. But if he deliberately sleeps lying down, he must perform wudu and restart the prayer. The lesson concludes with a warning to review the transmitted sources and not rely solely on the apparent absolute statement.

Key Terms
النعاس (al-nu'as): Drowsiness or dozing; a light sleep where the person may remain somewhat aware. According to the mufta bihi, it does not break wudu unless it turns into deep sleep.
الاضطجاع (al-idtija'): Lying down; if done in prayer while sleeping, it is a key factor in determining wudu nullification. Deliberate sleep while lying down requires restarting prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the correct view according to al-Ramli regarding sleep while lying down in prayer?
A) It does not break wudu.
B) It breaks wudu and requires wudu and building.
C) It invalidates the prayer completely.
D) It is permissible and no action needed.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi is that sleep during prayer breaks wudu, but the prayer can be saved by building if unintentional; deliberate sleep while lying down requires restart.

8 min
Hadath after Tashahhud: Basic Ruling and Proof
Explanation of ruling on hadath after tashahhud with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for hadath after tashahhud and explain why wudu is required before salam.

Core Idea
Hadath after tashahhud does not invalidate prayer; wudu and wajib salam must follow.

When a person has an event (hadath) after the tashahhud but before the salam, the prayer is still valid because the obligatory parts (fara'id) are complete. However, salam is wajib and requires a state of purity, so one must perform wudu. This lesson explores the evidence and practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the scenario: hadath occurs after tashahhud. The ruling: wudu and salam are required. The prayer is valid but makruh tahriman if wudu is omitted.
Makruh tahriman means the prayer is valid but should be repeated to avoid sin.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith cited: from Ibn Umar, the Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'If a man has an event while sitting at the end of his prayer before salam, his prayer is valid.'
The hadith is from Tirmidhi and others.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'جازت صلاته' indicates permissibility and validity. In Hanafi usul, this shows that the fara'id are complete, but the prayer is not fully complete until salam is given with purity.
Salam is considered a wajib, not a rukn.
4
Apply the conditions for building (bina')
If one does not perform wudu immediately or performs a contradictory act, he misses the salam. Then the prayer becomes like one performed with karahah tahrimiyyah, requiring repetition.
The imam must appoint a substitute to give salam.
5
Note the karahah and required action
If wudu and salam are omitted, the prayer is valid but makruh tahriman. The person must repeat the prayer to perform the wajib correctly. This is the same ruling for any prayer performed with such karahah.
Repeating is to remove the sin of neglecting a wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حدث بعد التشهد توضأ وسلم وإن تعمده أو تكلم تمت صلاته وبطلت أن رأى متيمم ماء العناية : وإنما قال أو نام فاحتلم لأن النوم بانفراده ليس بمفسد وكذا الاحتلام المنفرد عن النوم وهو البلوغ بالسن فجمع بينهما بياناً للمراد اهـ. فعلى هذا الاحتلام هو البلوغ أعم من الإنزال أو السن فالمراد في المختصر هو الأوّل. وفي الظهيرية المصلى إذا نعس في صلاته فاضطجع، قيل تنتقض طهارته فيتوضأ ويبني وقيل لا تفسد صلاته ولا تنتقض عهارته اهـ. ولعل المصنف إنما عبر بالاستقبال في هذه المسائل كغيره دون الفساد لما أن الفساد فيها ليس مقصوداً فيثاب على ما فعله منها بخلاف ما إذا أفسدها قصداً فإنه لا ثواب له فيما أداه بل يأثم لأن قطعها لغير ضرورة حرام. قوله : (وإن سبقه حدث بعد التشهد توضأ وسلم لأن التسليم واجب ولا بد له من الوضوء ليأتي به فالوضوء والسلام واجبان فلو لم يفعل كره تحريماً. والشروط التي قدمناها لصحة البناء لا بد منها للسلام حتى لو لم يتوضأ فوراً أو أتى بمناف بعده فاته السلام ووجب عليه إعادتها لإقامة الواجب لأنه حكم كل صلاة أديت مع كراهة التحريم، وإن كان إماماً استخلف من يسلم بالقوم . قوله : (وإن تعمده أو تكلم تمت صلاته أي تعمد الحدث لحديث الترمذي عن ابن عمر قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا أحدث ـ يعني الرجل ـ وقد جلس في آخر صلاته قبل أن يسلم فقد جازت صلاته»(١) و معنى قوله «تمت صلاته تمت فرائض بها ولهذا تفسد بفعل المنافي وإلا فمعلوم أنها لم تتم بسائر ما يسب إنيها من الواجبات لعدم خروجه البداية التي هي متن الهداية. قوله : (لأن النوم بانفراده ليس بمفسد قال الرملي : ذكر في التتارخانية أقوالاً واختلاف تصحيح في المسألة، وكذلك ذكر في الجوهرة في نوم المضطجع والمريض في الصلاة اختلافاً، والصحيح أنه ينقض وبه نأخذ ونقل في التتارخانية عن المحيط في النوم مضطجعاً الحال لا يخلو إن غلبت عيناه فنام ثم اضطجع في حالة نومه فهو بمنزلة ما لو سبقه الحدث يتوضأ ويبني، ولو تعمد النوم في الصلاة مضطجعاً فإنه يتوضأ ويستقبل الصلاة هكذا حكي عن مشايخنا اهـ. فراجع المنقول ولا تغتر بما أطلقه هنا .اهـ. قوله : (فعلى هذا الاحتلام هو البلوغ) قال في النهر : فيه نظر لقول أهل اللغة الاحتلام اسم لما يراه النائم ثم غلب على ما يراه من خاص. وأيضاً لو كان نفس البلوغ لكان قول القدوري وغيره بلوغ الصبي بالاحتلام والإحبال والإنزال وإلا فحتى يتم له ثماني عشرة سنة غير واقع في محله وكأن الداعي إلى هذا التكلف ذكر النوم معه ولا يكون تصريحاً بما علم التزاماً زيادة في الإيضاح ولا سيما والكتاب ألفه لولده .اهـ. قال الشيخ اسمعيل : نعم ما ذكره في العناية أشار إلى نحوه في المغرب بقوله : والحالم المحتلم في الأصل ثم عم فقيل لمن بلغ مبلغ (١) رواه الترمذي في كتاب الصلاة باب ۱۸۳. أبو داود في كتاب الصلاة باب ۱۸۷، ۲۳۰. ابن ماجه في كتاب الإقامة باب ۱۳۸ . الدارمي في كتاب الوضوء باب ١١٤ أحمد في مسنده (٦/ ٢٧٢). بلفظ السلام وهو واجب بالاتفاق حتى إن هذه الصلاة تكون مؤداة على وجه مكروه فتعاد على وجه غير مكروه كما هو الحكم في كل صلاة أديت مع الكراهة. كذا في شرح منية المصلي، وفيه أنه لا خلاف بين أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه في أن من سبقه الحدث بعده يتوضأ ويسلم، وإنما الخلاف فيما إذا لم يتوضأ حتى أتى بمناف فعند أبي حنيفة بطلت صلاته لعدم الخروج بصنعه، وعندهما لا تبطل لأنه ليس بفرض عندهما اهـ. وفيه نظر، بل لا يكاد يصح لأنه إذا أتى بمناف بعد سبق الحدث فقد خرج منها بصنعه، ولهذا قال الشارح الزيلعي : وكذا إذا سبقه الحدث بعد التشهد ثم أحدث متعمداً قبل أن يتوضأ تمت صلاته ولم يحك خلافاً، وإنما ثمرة الخلاف تظهر فيما إذا خرج منها لا بصنعه كالمسائل الأثني عشرية كما سنقرره إن شاء الله تعالى. وشمل تعمد الحدث القهقهة عمداً فصلاته تامة وبطل وضوءه لوجودها في أثناء الصلاة فصار كنية الإقامة في هذه الحالة وكذا لو قهقه في سجود السهو . وإن قهقه الإمام أو أحدث متعمداً ثم قهقه القوم فعليه الوضوء دونهم لخروجهم منها بحدث الإمام بخلاف قهقهتهم بعد سلامه لأنهم لا يخرجون منها بسلامه فبطلت طهارتهم، وإن قهقهوا معاً أو القوم فعليهم الوضوء والحاصل أن القوم يخرجون من الصلاة بحدث الإمام عمداً اتفاقاً، ولهذا لا يسلمون ولا يخرجون منها بسلامه عندهما خلافاً لمحمد، وأما بكلامه فعن أبي حنيفة روايتان في رواية كالسلام فيسلمون وتنتقض طهارتهم بالقهقهة، وفي رواية كالحدث العمد فلا سلام ولا نقض بها كذا في المحيط . قوله : ( وبطلت أن رأى متيمم ماء) أي بطلت صلاته بالقدرة على استعمال الماء، ولا عبرة بالرؤية المجردة عن القدرة بدليل ما قدمه في بابه. وإنما بطلت لأن عدم الماء شرط في الابتداء فكان شرط البقاء كسائر الشروط وكالمكفر بالصوم إذا أيسر ليس له البناء لأنه برؤية الماء ظهر حكم الحدث السابق فكأنه شرع على غير وضوء بخلاف ما إذا سبقه الحدث لأنه شرع بوضوء تام أطلقه فشمل ما إذا رأى المتيمم قبل سبق الحدث أو بعده، وفي الثاني خلاف والصحيح هو البطلان كما في المحيط، وجزم به الشارح. واختار في النهاية أنه دون فساد. وفي فتح القدير : والذي يظهر أن الأسباب المتعاقبة كالبول ثم الرعاف ثم القيء إذا أوجبت أحداثاً متعاقبة يجزئه عنها وضوء واحد، فالأوجه ما في شرح الكنز وهو الموافق لما قدمناه من قول محمد فيمن حلف لا يتوضأ من الرعاف فبال ثم رعف ثم توضأ أنه يحنث . يوجب كما قدمنا النظر فيه في باب الغسل فالأوجه ما في النهاية وهو الحق في وإن قلنا لا يبني الرجال حالم وهو المراد به في الحديث خذ من كل حالم (١) . قوله : (وفيه نظر الخ) قال في النهر : (١) رواه أبو داود في كتاب الزكاة باب ٥ أحمد في مسنده (٣٤١/٤).
If an event occurs after the tashahhud, he performs wudu and says the salam. And if he deliberately does it or speaks, his prayer is complete. And if a mutayammim sees water, his prayer becomes invalid. Al-Inayah: He only said 'or he sleeps and has a wet dream' because sleep alone is not a nullifier, likewise wet dream alone is not, and it is puberty by age, so he combined them as clarification of intent. So according to this, ihtilam is puberty, general regardless of emission or age, so the intended meaning in al-Mukhtasar is the first. In al-Zahiriyyah: The one praying, if he dozes in his prayer and then lies down, it is said his purity is broken so he performs wudu and builds upon his prayer, and it is said his prayer is not invalidated nor is his purity broken. Perhaps the author used the term 'istiqbal' (resumption) in these issues like others instead of 'fasad' because invalidity is not intended in them, so he is rewarded for what he did, contrary to if he deliberately invalidates it, then he has no reward for what he performed, rather he sins because cutting it without necessity is haram. His statement: 'And if an event overtakes him after tashahhud, he performs wudu and says salam because the salam is obligatory and he must have wudu to perform it, so wudu and salam are obligatory. If he does not do so, it is makruh tahriman. The conditions we presented for the validity of building are necessary for the salam, so that if he does not perform wudu immediately or does something contradictory afterwards, he misses the salam and it is necessary for him to repeat the prayer to perform the wajib, because that is the ruling of every prayer performed with karahah tahrimiyyah. And if he is an imam, he appoints someone to give salam to the people.' His statement: 'And if he deliberately does it or speaks, his prayer is complete' meaning he deliberately causes the event, due to the hadith of Tirmidhi from Ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah said: 'If a man has an event while he is sitting at the end of his prayer before he says salam, his prayer is valid.' The meaning of 'his prayer is complete' is that its obligatory parts are complete, and therefore it is invalidated by a contradictory act; otherwise it is known that it did not complete all the wajibat because he did not exit. This is the beginning which is the text of al-Hidayah. His statement: 'Because sleep alone is not a nullifier' – al-Ramli said: in al-Tatarkhaniyyah there are statements and differences of correction on this issue, and likewise in al-Jawharah there is difference on the sleep of one lying down and the sick in prayer, but the correct view is that it breaks purity and we take it. It is narrated in al-Tatarkhaniyyah from al-Muhit regarding sleep lying down: the situation is that if his eyes overcome him and he sleeps then lies down in his sleep, it is like an event overtaking him, he performs wudu and builds. If he deliberately sleeps lying down in his prayer, then he performs wudu and starts the prayer over; thus it is related from our shuyukh. So refer to what is transmitted and do not be deceived by his general statement here. His statement: 'According to this, ihtilam is puberty' – al-Nahr said: there is consideration in this because the linguists say ihtilam is a name for what the sleeper sees, then it became dominant for what he sees of a specific kind. Also, if it were itself puberty, then the statement of al-Quduri and others that a child reaches puberty by ihtilam, impregnation, and emission, otherwise until he completes eighteen years, would not be accurate. The motivation for this exaggerated effort seems to be the mention of sleep with it, and it is not an explicit statement of what is known implicitly, as an increase in clarification, especially since the book was written for his son. Shaykh Ismail said: Indeed, what was mentioned in al-Inayah indicated something similar in al-Mughrib: 'al-Halim and al-Muhtalim originally, then it became general, so it was said for one who has reached the age of puberty.' (Footnote: Narrated by Tirmidhi in Kitab al-Salah, bab 183; Abu Dawud in Kitab al-Salah, bab 187, 230; Ibn Majah in Kitab al-Iqamah, bab 138; al-Darimi in Kitab al-Wudu, bab 114; Ahmad in his Musnad 6/272). With the word salam, and it is obligatory by consensus, so much so that this prayer is performed in a makruh manner, so it is repeated in a non-makruh manner, as is the ruling for every prayer performed with karahah. Thus in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. And in it, there is no disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two companions regarding one who is overtaken by an event after it, that he performs wudu and says salam. The disagreement is only when he does not perform wudu until he does something contradictory – according to Abu Hanifa, his prayer becomes invalid because he did not exit by his own action, while according to them it does not become invalid because it is not a fard according to them. But this is questionable; indeed it is hardly sound because by doing something contradictory after being overtaken by the event, he exits by his own action. Therefore, al-Zaylai said: Likewise, if he is overtaken by an event after tashahhud and then deliberately causes an event before performing wudu, his prayer is complete and no disagreement is reported. The fruit of the difference appears only when he exits not by his own action, like the twelve issues, as we will discuss if Allah wills. His deliberate causing of the event includes deliberate laughter, so his prayer is complete but his wudu is invalid because it occurred during the prayer, so it becomes like the intention of staying in that case. Likewise, if he laughs during sujud al-sahw. If the imam laughs or deliberately causes an event and then the people laugh, then the imam must perform wudu but not the people because they exit by the imam's event, contrary to their laughter after his salam because they do not exit by his salam, so their purity is invalidated. If they laugh together, or the people laugh, then they must perform wudu. The conclusion is that the people exit the prayer by the imam's deliberate event by agreement, hence they do not say salam, and they do not exit by his salam according to the two companions, contrary to Muhammad. As for his speech, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: in one narration it is like salam, so they say salam and their purity is broken by laughter; in another narration it is like deliberate event, so no salam and no break by it. Thus in al-Muhit. His statement: 'And if a mutayammim sees water, his prayer becomes invalid' – meaning his prayer becomes invalid due to ability to use water. Mere sight without ability is not considered, as evidenced by what was presented in its chapter. It becomes invalid because the absence of water is a condition at the beginning, so it remains a condition for staying, like other conditions, and like the one who makes expiation by fasting and becomes wealthy, he cannot build because by seeing water the ruling of the previous event appears, so it is as if he began without wudu, contrary to the one overtaken by an event because he began with complete wudu, which he released. This includes if the mutayammim sees water before being overtaken by an event or after. In the second case there is disagreement, and the correct view is invalidity as in al-Muhit, and the commentator affirmed it. He chose in al-Nihayah that it is less than invalidity. In Fath al-Qadir: it appears that successive causes like urination then nosebleed then vomiting, if they necessitate successive events, a single wudu suffices for them. So the most appropriate is what is in Sharh al-Kanz, which is in agreement with what we presented from Muhammad regarding one who swore not to perform wudu from nosebleed, then urinated, then had a nosebleed, then performed wudu – that he is oath-breaking. This necessitates, as we presented, consideration in the chapter of ghusl, so the most appropriate is what is in al-Nihayah, and it is the truth, and if we say he does not build, the men are dreaming (?) and that is meant in the hadith 'take from every dreamer' (Footnote: Narrated by Abu Dawud in Kitab al-Zakah, bab 5; Ahmad in his Musnad 4/341). His statement: 'And there is consideration, etc.' – al-Nahr said:
Source pages p. 653

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, expanding on rulings related to events (hadath) during prayer. The author, Imam al-Kasani (or the commentator of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq), explains several key scenarios. First, if a person has an event (e.g., breaking wudu) after the tashahhud but before salam, he must perform wudu and then say salam. This is because salam is wajib and requires wudu. If he fails to do so, the prayer is valid but makruh tahriman (prohibitively disliked); he should repeat it to be free of karahah. If he is an imam, he should appoint someone to lead the salam. Second, if he deliberately causes the event or speaks after the event, his prayer is still valid (complete in terms of fara'id) due to the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'If a man has an event while sitting at the end of his prayer before salam, his prayer is valid.' However, deliberate laughter (qahqaha) during prayer invalidates wudu but not the prayer itself in this context, as it occurs after the event. The text also delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute: if one does not perform wudu after the event and instead does something contradictory (like speaking), Abu Hanifa says his prayer becomes invalid because he exited by his own action, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it does not become invalid because salam is not fard according to them. The commentator sides with the view that it is valid, following al-Zaylai. Third, regarding a mutayammim (one performing tayammum), if he sees water (or gains ability to use it) during prayer, his prayer becomes invalid because the absence of water is a continuing condition. This applies whether he sees water before or after an event, though there is a difference of opinion. The text also discusses related issues like sleep, wet dream (ihtilam), and the distinction between deliberate and involuntary acts. Throughout, the Hanafi position is upheld, with references to authoritative sources like al-Hidayah, al-Muhit, and al-Nahr.

Key Terms
الحدث (al-hadath): State of ritual impurity that invalidates wudu, here refers to minor hadath (breaking wudu).
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The testimony recited in the last sitting of prayer.
الكراهة التحريمية (al-karahah al-tahrimiyyah): Prohibitively disliked – a ruling near haram; prayer valid but must be repeated to avoid sin.
البناء (al-bina'): Continuing prayer after interruption without restarting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person has an event (hadath) after the tashahhud but before salam, what must he do?
A) He must start the prayer over from the beginning.
B) He must perform wudu and then say salam; his prayer is valid.
C) His prayer becomes invalid immediately and he must repeat it.
D) He can ignore the event and continue with salam without wudu.

Key Takeaway
Hadath after tashahhud does not invalidate the prayer; wudu and salam must follow, and omission makes it makruh tahriman.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Deliberate Hadath and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on deliberate hadath and speaking after tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding prayer validity when one deliberately causes hadath or speaks after tashahhud without wudu, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Deliberate hadath after tashahhud: prayer complete in fara'id; dispute on effect of speaking without wudu.

When a person deliberately causes an event (hadath) after tashahhud, or speaks after the hadath without performing wudu, there is a well-known disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). This lesson unpacks the proofs and practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the Hanafi positions
Scenario: hadath occurs after tashahhud, person does not perform wudu and instead speaks or does a contradictory act. Abu Hanifa: prayer becomes invalid. Sahibayn: prayer remains valid.
2
Identify the basis of the ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa views that exiting prayer requires one's own action (salam) and if one speaks, he exits without proper completion, thus invalid. Sahibayn see salam as not fard (only wajib), so speaking does not invalidate a prayer whose fara'id are complete.
The difference hinges on the status of salam as fard vs wajib.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
The hadith (Tirmidhi) says the prayer is valid after hadath. Both sides use it. The commentary notes that the phrase 'تمت صلاته' means fara'id complete, but that does not automatically prevent invalidity by a later contradictory act.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: According to Abu Hanifa, if one speaks after hadath without wudu, he must repeat the entire prayer. According to Sahibayn, the prayer is valid and no repetition needed. The commentator (al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) favors the Sahibayn.
The fruit of difference appears when exiting without action (e.g., sleep) as per al-Zaylai.
5
Determine the tarjih
The mufta bihi position is that of the Sahibayn: the prayer remains valid. This is supported by al-Zaylai and the majority of later Hanafi scholars.
The commentator notes that if one deliberately causes hadath before wudu, the prayer is complete without dispute (al-Zaylai).

ولهذا تفسد بفعل المنافي وإلا فمعلوم أنها لم تتم بسائر ما يسب إنيها من الواجبات لعدم خروجه البداية التي هي متن الهداية. قوله : (لأن النوم بانفراده ليس بمفسد قال الرملي : ذكر في التتارخانية أقوالاً واختلاف تصحيح في المسألة، وكذلك ذكر في الجوهرة في نوم المضطجع والمريض في الصلاة اختلافاً، والصحيح أنه ينقض وبه نأخذ ونقل في التتارخانية عن المحيط في النوم مضطجعاً الحال لا يخلو إن غلبت عيناه فنام ثم قبل أن يتوضأ تمت صلاته ولم يحك خلافاً، وإنما ثمرة الخلاف تظهر فيما إذا خرج منها لا بصنعه كالمسائل الأثني عشرية كما سنقرره إن شاء الله تعالى. وشمل تعمد الحدث القهقهة عمداً فصلاته تامة وبطل وضوءه لوجودها في أثناء الصلاة فصار كنية الإقامة في هذه الحالة وكذا لو قهقه في سجود السهو . وإن قهقه الإمام أو أحدث متعمداً ثم قهقه القوم فعليه الوضوء دونهم لخروجهم منها بحدث الإمام بخلاف قهقهتهم بعد سلامه لأنهم لا يخرجون منها بسلامه فبطلت طهارتهم، وإن قهقهوا معاً أو القوم فعليهم الوضوء والحاصل أن القوم يخرجون من الصلاة بحدث الإمام عمداً اتفاقاً، ولهذا لا يسلمون ولا يخرجون منها بسلامه عندهما خلافاً لمحمد، وأما بكلامه فعن أبي حنيفة روايتان في رواية كالسلام فيسلمون وتنتقض طهارتهم بالقهقهة، وفي رواية كالحدث العمد فلا سلام ولا نقض بها كذا في المحيط . قوله : ( وبطلت أن رأى متيمم ماء) أي بطلت صلاته بالقدرة على استعمال الماء، ولا عبرة بالرؤية المجردة عن القدرة بدليل ما قدمه في بابه. وإنما بطلت لأن عدم الماء شرط في الابتداء فكان شرط البقاء كسائر الشروط وكالمكفر بالصوم إذا أيسر ليس له البناء لأنه برؤية الماء ظهر حكم الحدث السابق فكأنه شرع على غير وضوء بخلاف ما إذا سبقه الحدث لأنه شرع بوضوء تام أطلقه فشمل ما إذا رأى المتيمم قبل سبق الحدث أو بعده، وفي الثاني خلاف والصحيح هو البطلان كما في المحيط، وجزم به الشارح. واختار في النهاية أنه دون فساد. وفي فتح القدير : والذي يظهر أن الأسباب المتعاقبة كالبول ثم الرعاف ثم القيء إذا أوجبت أحداثاً متعاقبة يجزئه عنها وضوء واحد، فالأوجه ما في شرح الكنز وهو الموافق لما قدمناه من قول محمد فيمن حلف لا يتوضأ من الرعاف فبال ثم رعف ثم توضأ أنه يحنث . يوجب كما قدمنا النظر فيه في باب الغسل فالأوجه ما في النهاية وهو الحق في وإن قلنا لا يبني الرجال حالم وهو المراد به في الحديث خذ من كل حالم (١) . قوله : (وفيه نظر الخ) قال في النهر : (١) رواه أبو داود في كتاب الزكاة باب ٥ أحمد في مسنده (٣٤١/٤).
If an event occurs after the tashahhud, he performs wudu and says the salam. And if he deliberately does it or speaks, his prayer is complete. And if a mutayammim sees water, his prayer becomes invalid. Al-Inayah: He only said 'or he sleeps and has a wet dream' because sleep alone is not a nullifier, likewise wet dream alone is not, and it is puberty by age, so he combined them as clarification of intent. So according to this, ihtilam is puberty, general regardless of emission or age, so the intended meaning in al-Mukhtasar is the first. In al-Zahiriyyah: The one praying, if he dozes in his prayer and then lies down, it is said his purity is broken so he performs wudu and builds upon his prayer, and it is said his prayer is not invalidated nor is his purity broken. Perhaps the author used the term 'istiqbal' (resumption) in these issues like others instead of 'fasad' because invalidity is not intended in them, so he is rewarded for what he did, contrary to if he deliberately invalidates it, then he has no reward for what he performed, rather he sins because cutting it without necessity is haram. His statement: 'And if an event overtakes him after tashahhud, he performs wudu and says salam because the salam is obligatory and he must have wudu to perform it, so wudu and salam are obligatory. If he does not do so, it is makruh tahriman. The conditions we presented for the validity of building are necessary for the salam, so that if he does not perform wudu immediately or does something contradictory afterwards, he misses the salam and it is necessary for him to repeat the prayer to perform the wajib, because that is the ruling of every prayer performed with karahah tahrimiyyah. And if he is an imam, he appoints someone to give salam to the people.' His statement: 'And if he deliberately does it or speaks, his prayer is complete' meaning he deliberately causes the event, due to the hadith of Tirmidhi from Ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah said: 'If a man has an event while he is sitting at the end of his prayer before he says salam, his prayer is valid.' The meaning of 'his prayer is complete' is that its obligatory parts are complete, and therefore it is invalidated by a contradictory act; otherwise it is known that it did not complete all the wajibat because he did not exit. This is the beginning which is the text of al-Hidayah. His statement: 'Because sleep alone is not a nullifier' – al-Ramli said: in al-Tatarkhaniyyah there are statements and differences of correction on this issue, and likewise in al-Jawharah there is difference on the sleep of one lying down and the sick in prayer, but the correct view is that it breaks purity and we take it. It is narrated in al-Tatarkhaniyyah from al-Muhit regarding sleep lying down: the situation is that if his eyes overcome him and he sleeps then lies down in his sleep, it is like an event overtaking him, he performs wudu and builds. If he deliberately sleeps lying down in his prayer, then he performs wudu and starts the prayer over; thus it is related from our shuyukh. So refer to what is transmitted and do not be deceived by his general statement here. His statement: 'According to this, ihtilam is puberty' – al-Nahr said: there is consideration in this because the linguists say ihtilam is a name for what the sleeper sees, then it became dominant for what he sees of a specific kind. Also, if it were itself puberty, then the statement of al-Quduri and others that a child reaches puberty by ihtilam, impregnation, and emission, otherwise until he completes eighteen years, would not be accurate. The motivation for this exaggerated effort seems to be the mention of sleep with it, and it is not an explicit statement of what is known implicitly, as an increase in clarification, especially since the book was written for his son. Shaykh Ismail said: Indeed, what was mentioned in al-Inayah indicated something similar in al-Mughrib: 'al-Halim and al-Muhtalim originally, then it became general, so it was said for one who has reached the age of puberty.' (Footnote: Narrated by Tirmidhi in Kitab al-Salah, bab 183; Abu Dawud in Kitab al-Salah, bab 187, 230; Ibn Majah in Kitab al-Iqamah, bab 138; al-Darimi in Kitab al-Wudu, bab 114; Ahmad in his Musnad 6/272). With the word salam, and it is obligatory by consensus, so much so that this prayer is performed in a makruh manner, so it is repeated in a non-makruh manner, as is the ruling for every prayer performed with karahah. Thus in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. And in it, there is no disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two companions regarding one who is overtaken by an event after it, that he performs wudu and says salam. The disagreement is only when he does not perform wudu until he does something contradictory – according to Abu Hanifa, his prayer becomes invalid because he did not exit by his own action, while according to them it does not become invalid because it is not a fard according to them. But this is questionable; indeed it is hardly sound because by doing something contradictory after being overtaken by the event, he exits by his own action. Therefore, al-Zaylai said: Likewise, if he is overtaken by an event after tashahhud and then deliberately causes an event before performing wudu, his prayer is complete and no disagreement is reported. The fruit of the difference appears only when he exits not by his own action, like the twelve issues, as we will discuss if Allah wills. His deliberate causing of the event includes deliberate laughter, so his prayer is complete but his wudu is invalid because it occurred during the prayer, so it becomes like the intention of staying in that case. Likewise, if he laughs during sujud al-sahw. If the imam laughs or deliberately causes an event and then the people laugh, then the imam must perform wudu but not the people because they exit by the imam's event, contrary to their laughter after his salam because they do not exit by his salam, so their purity is invalidated. If they laugh together, or the people laugh, then they must perform wudu. The conclusion is that the people exit the prayer by the imam's deliberate event by agreement, hence they do not say salam, and they do not exit by his salam according to the two companions, contrary to Muhammad. As for his speech, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: in one narration it is like salam, so they say salam and their purity is broken by laughter; in another narration it is like deliberate event, so no salam and no break by it. Thus in al-Muhit. His statement: 'And if a mutayammim sees water, his prayer becomes invalid' – meaning his prayer becomes invalid due to ability to use water. Mere sight without ability is not considered, as evidenced by what was presented in its chapter. It becomes invalid because the absence of water is a condition at the beginning, so it remains a condition for staying, like other conditions, and like the one who makes expiation by fasting and becomes wealthy, he cannot build because by seeing water the ruling of the previous event appears, so it is as if he began without wudu, contrary to the one overtaken by an event because he began with complete wudu, which he released. This includes if the mutayammim sees water before being overtaken by an event or after. In the second case there is disagreement, and the correct view is invalidity as in al-Muhit, and the commentator affirmed it. He chose in al-Nihayah that it is less than invalidity. In Fath al-Qadir: it appears that successive causes like urination then nosebleed then vomiting, if they necessitate successive events, a single wudu suffices for them. So the most appropriate is what is in Sharh al-Kanz, which is in agreement with what we presented from Muhammad regarding one who swore not to perform wudu from nosebleed, then urinated, then had a nosebleed, then performed wudu – that he is oath-breaking. This necessitates, as we presented, consideration in the chapter of ghusl, so the most appropriate is what is in al-Nihayah, and it is the truth, and if we say he does not build, the men are dreaming (?) and that is meant in the hadith 'take from every dreamer' (Footnote: Narrated by Abu Dawud in Kitab al-Zakah, bab 5; Ahmad in his Musnad 4/341). His statement: 'And there is consideration, etc.' – al-Nahr said:
