Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, expanding on rulings related to events (hadath) during prayer. The author, Imam al-Kasani (or the commentator of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq), explains several key scenarios. First, if a person has an event (e.g., breaking wudu) after the tashahhud but before salam, he must perform wudu and then say salam. This is because salam is wajib and requires wudu. If he fails to do so, the prayer is valid but makruh tahriman (prohibitively disliked); he should repeat it to be free of karahah. If he is an imam, he should appoint someone to lead the salam. Second, if he deliberately causes the event or speaks after the event, his prayer is still valid (complete in terms of fara'id) due to the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'If a man has an event while sitting at the end of his prayer before salam, his prayer is valid.' However, deliberate laughter (qahqaha) during prayer invalidates wudu but not the prayer itself in this context, as it occurs after the event. The text also delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute: if one does not perform wudu after the event and instead does something contradictory (like speaking), Abu Hanifa says his prayer becomes invalid because he exited by his own action, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it does not become invalid because salam is not fard according to them. The commentator sides with the view that it is valid, following al-Zaylai. Third, regarding a mutayammim (one performing tayammum), if he sees water (or gains ability to use it) during prayer, his prayer becomes invalid because the absence of water is a continuing condition. This applies whether he sees water before or after an event, though there is a difference of opinion. The text also discusses related issues like sleep, wet dream (ihtilam), and the distinction between deliberate and involuntary acts. Throughout, the Hanafi position is upheld, with references to authoritative sources like al-Hidayah, al-Muhit, and al-Nahr.

Key Terms
التسليم (al-tasleem): The salam that concludes the prayer.
المبطلات (al-mubtilat): Acts that invalidate the prayer if done deliberately.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon position) in the Hanafi school, if a person has hadath after tashahhud and then speaks without performing wudu, what is the status of his prayer?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid and no repetition is needed.
C) The prayer is valid but must be repeated to avoid karahah.
D) The prayer is suspended until he performs wudu and says salam.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that prayer after hadath and subsequent speaking remains valid; the dispute with Abu Hanifa is acknowledged but the practice follows the Sahibayn.

Salah — Prayer

Laughter (Qahqaha) during Prayer after Tashahhud
Ruling on laughter (qahqaha) during prayer after tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for deliberate laughter (qahqaha) during prayer after tashahhud and identify its effect on wudu and the prayer.

Core Idea
Deliberate laughter after tashahhud: prayer valid, wudu invalidated.

The passage discusses the effect of deliberate laughter (qahqaha) during prayer, specifically after tashahhud. Laughter invalidates wudu but does not invalidate the prayer itself according to the rule for after tashahhud. This lesson clarifies the distinction and its application for the imam and congregation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Deliberate laughter (qahqaha) during prayer after tashahhud: prayer is complete (valid), but wudu is broken.
Laughter is considered a contradictory act, but because fara'id are complete, the prayer remains valid.
2
Apply the hadith and principle
The same hadith (Tirmidhi) applies: the prayer is valid. Laughter is included under deliberate hadath? The text says 'deliberate hadath includes laughter'.
3
Distinguish between imam and congregation
If the imam laughs or has a deliberate event, the congregation exits the prayer by his event (by agreement). If the congregation laughs after imam's event, they must perform wudu but do not need to repeat prayer? The text is specific.
The imam's deliberate event causes the congregation to exit the prayer.
4
Analyze the effect on wudu and prayer
For the person who laughs: wudu is invalidated because laughter breaks wudu when it occurs during prayer. But since the prayer's fara'id are complete, the prayer is not invalidated. He must perform wudu for any future prayer.
5
Note the case of sujud al-sahw
Laughter during sujud al-sahw also invalidates wudu but does not affect the prayer's validity after tashahhud.

المحيط، وجزم به الشارح. واختار في النهاية أنه دون فساد. وفي فتح القدير : والذي يظهر أن الأسباب المتعاقبة كالبول ثم الرعاف ثم القيء إذا أوجبت أحداثاً متعاقبة يجزئه عنها وضوء واحد، فالأوجه ما في شرح الكنز وهو الموافق لما قدمناه من قول محمد فيمن حلف لا يتوضأ من الرعاف فبال ثم رعف ثم توضأ أنه يحنث . يوجب كما قدمنا النظر فيه في باب الغسل فالأوجه ما في النهاية وهو الحق في وإن قلنا لا يبني الرجال حالم وهو المراد به في الحديث خذ من كل حالم (١) . قوله : (وفيه نظر الخ) قال في النهر : (١) رواه أبو داود في كتاب الزكاة باب ٥ أحمد في مسنده (٣٤١/٤).
If an event occurs after the tashahhud, he performs wudu and says the salam. And if he deliberately does it or speaks, his prayer is complete. And if a mutayammim sees water, his prayer becomes invalid. Al-Inayah: He only said 'or he sleeps and has a wet dream' because sleep alone is not a nullifier, likewise wet dream alone is not, and it is puberty by age, so he combined them as clarification of intent. So according to this, ihtilam is puberty, general regardless of emission or age, so the intended meaning in al-Mukhtasar is the first. In al-Zahiriyyah: The one praying, if he dozes in his prayer and then lies down, it is said his purity is broken so he performs wudu and builds upon his prayer, and it is said his prayer is not invalidated nor is his purity broken. Perhaps the author used the term 'istiqbal' (resumption) in these issues like others instead of 'fasad' because invalidity is not intended in them, so he is rewarded for what he did, contrary to if he deliberately invalidates it, then he has no reward for what he performed, rather he sins because cutting it without necessity is haram. His statement: 'And if an event overtakes him after tashahhud, he performs wudu and says salam because the salam is obligatory and he must have wudu to perform it, so wudu and salam are obligatory. If he does not do so, it is makruh tahriman. The conditions we presented for the validity of building are necessary for the salam, so that if he does not perform wudu immediately or does something contradictory afterwards, he misses the salam and it is necessary for him to repeat the prayer to perform the wajib, because that is the ruling of every prayer performed with karahah tahrimiyyah. And if he is an imam, he appoints someone to give salam to the people.' His statement: 'And if he deliberately does it or speaks, his prayer is complete' meaning he deliberately causes the event, due to the hadith of Tirmidhi from Ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah said: 'If a man has an event while he is sitting at the end of his prayer before he says salam, his prayer is valid.' The meaning of 'his prayer is complete' is that its obligatory parts are complete, and therefore it is invalidated by a contradictory act; otherwise it is known that it did not complete all the wajibat because he did not exit. This is the beginning which is the text of al-Hidayah. His statement: 'Because sleep alone is not a nullifier' – al-Ramli said: in al-Tatarkhaniyyah there are statements and differences of correction on this issue, and likewise in al-Jawharah there is difference on the sleep of one lying down and the sick in prayer, but the correct view is that it breaks purity and we take it. It is narrated in al-Tatarkhaniyyah from al-Muhit regarding sleep lying down: the situation is that if his eyes overcome him and he sleeps then lies down in his sleep, it is like an event overtaking him, he performs wudu and builds. If he deliberately sleeps lying down in his prayer, then he performs wudu and starts the prayer over; thus it is related from our shuyukh. So refer to what is transmitted and do not be deceived by his general statement here. His statement: 'According to this, ihtilam is puberty' – al-Nahr said: there is consideration in this because the linguists say ihtilam is a name for what the sleeper sees, then it became dominant for what he sees of a specific kind. Also, if it were itself puberty, then the statement of al-Quduri and others that a child reaches puberty by ihtilam, impregnation, and emission, otherwise until he completes eighteen years, would not be accurate. The motivation for this exaggerated effort seems to be the mention of sleep with it, and it is not an explicit statement of what is known implicitly, as an increase in clarification, especially since the book was written for his son. Shaykh Ismail said: Indeed, what was mentioned in al-Inayah indicated something similar in al-Mughrib: 'al-Halim and al-Muhtalim originally, then it became general, so it was said for one who has reached the age of puberty.' (Footnote: Narrated by Tirmidhi in Kitab al-Salah, bab 183; Abu Dawud in Kitab al-Salah, bab 187, 230; Ibn Majah in Kitab al-Iqamah, bab 138; al-Darimi in Kitab al-Wudu, bab 114; Ahmad in his Musnad 6/272). With the word salam, and it is obligatory by consensus, so much so that this prayer is performed in a makruh manner, so it is repeated in a non-makruh manner, as is the ruling for every prayer performed with karahah. Thus in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. And in it, there is no disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two companions regarding one who is overtaken by an event after it, that he performs wudu and says salam. The disagreement is only when he does not perform wudu until he does something contradictory – according to Abu Hanifa, his prayer becomes invalid because he did not exit by his own action, while according to them it does not become invalid because it is not a fard according to them. But this is questionable; indeed it is hardly sound because by doing something contradictory after being overtaken by the event, he exits by his own action. Therefore, al-Zaylai said: Likewise, if he is overtaken by an event after tashahhud and then deliberately causes an event before performing wudu, his prayer is complete and no disagreement is reported. The fruit of the difference appears only when he exits not by his own action, like the twelve issues, as we will discuss if Allah wills. His deliberate causing of the event includes deliberate laughter, so his prayer is complete but his wudu is invalid because it occurred during the prayer, so it becomes like the intention of staying in that case. Likewise, if he laughs during sujud al-sahw. If the imam laughs or deliberately causes an event and then the people laugh, then the imam must perform wudu but not the people because they exit by the imam's event, contrary to their laughter after his salam because they do not exit by his salam, so their purity is invalidated. If they laugh together, or the people laugh, then they must perform wudu. The conclusion is that the people exit the prayer by the imam's deliberate event by agreement, hence they do not say salam, and they do not exit by his salam according to the two companions, contrary to Muhammad. As for his speech, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: in one narration it is like salam, so they say salam and their purity is broken by laughter; in another narration it is like deliberate event, so no salam and no break by it. Thus in al-Muhit. His statement: 'And if a mutayammim sees water, his prayer becomes invalid' – meaning his prayer becomes invalid due to ability to use water. Mere sight without ability is not considered, as evidenced by what was presented in its chapter. It becomes invalid because the absence of water is a condition at the beginning, so it remains a condition for staying, like other conditions, and like the one who makes expiation by fasting and becomes wealthy, he cannot build because by seeing water the ruling of the previous event appears, so it is as if he began without wudu, contrary to the one overtaken by an event because he began with complete wudu, which he released. This includes if the mutayammim sees water before being overtaken by an event or after. In the second case there is disagreement, and the correct view is invalidity as in al-Muhit, and the commentator affirmed it. He chose in al-Nihayah that it is less than invalidity. In Fath al-Qadir: it appears that successive causes like urination then nosebleed then vomiting, if they necessitate successive events, a single wudu suffices for them. So the most appropriate is what is in Sharh al-Kanz, which is in agreement with what we presented from Muhammad regarding one who swore not to perform wudu from nosebleed, then urinated, then had a nosebleed, then performed wudu – that he is oath-breaking. This necessitates, as we presented, consideration in the chapter of ghusl, so the most appropriate is what is in al-Nihayah, and it is the truth, and if we say he does not build, the men are dreaming (?) and that is meant in the hadith 'take from every dreamer' (Footnote: Narrated by Abu Dawud in Kitab al-Zakah, bab 5; Ahmad in his Musnad 4/341). His statement: 'And there is consideration, etc.' – al-Nahr said:
Source pages p. 653

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, expanding on rulings related to events (hadath) during prayer. The author, Imam al-Kasani (or the commentator of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq), explains several key scenarios. First, if a person has an event (e.g., breaking wudu) after the tashahhud but before salam, he must perform wudu and then say salam. This is because salam is wajib and requires wudu. If he fails to do so, the prayer is valid but makruh tahriman (prohibitively disliked); he should repeat it to be free of karahah. If he is an imam, he should appoint someone to lead the salam. Second, if he deliberately causes the event or speaks after the event, his prayer is still valid (complete in terms of fara'id) due to the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'If a man has an event while sitting at the end of his prayer before salam, his prayer is valid.' However, deliberate laughter (qahqaha) during prayer invalidates wudu but not the prayer itself in this context, as it occurs after the event. The text also delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute: if one does not perform wudu after the event and instead does something contradictory (like speaking), Abu Hanifa says his prayer becomes invalid because he exited by his own action, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it does not become invalid because salam is not fard according to them. The commentator sides with the view that it is valid, following al-Zaylai. Third, regarding a mutayammim (one performing tayammum), if he sees water (or gains ability to use it) during prayer, his prayer becomes invalid because the absence of water is a continuing condition. This applies whether he sees water before or after an event, though there is a difference of opinion. The text also discusses related issues like sleep, wet dream (ihtilam), and the distinction between deliberate and involuntary acts. Throughout, the Hanafi position is upheld, with references to authoritative sources like al-Hidayah, al-Muhit, and al-Nahr.

Key Terms
القهقهة (al-qahqaha): Deliberate, audible laughter during prayer.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration for forgetfulness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person laughs deliberately during the final sitting (tashahhud) of prayer, what happens according to the Hanafi school?
A) His prayer becomes invalid and he must repeat it.
B) His prayer remains valid, but his wudu is invalidated.
C) His prayer and wudu both remain valid because it is minor laughter.
D) His prayer is suspended until he performs ghusl.

Key Takeaway
Deliberate laughter after tashahhud invalidates wudu but not the prayer; the congregation exits by the imam's deliberate event.

Salah — Prayer

Mutayammim Seeing Water: Invalidity of Prayer
Ruling on mutayammim seeing water during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a mutayammim's prayer becomes invalid upon seeing (or gaining ability to use) water, and explain why the condition of water absence is a condition of validity throughout the prayer.

Core Idea
Seeing water during prayer invalidates tayammum and thus the prayer.

The passage addresses a key rule for one performing tayammum: if he sees water (or becomes able to use it) during the prayer, his prayer becomes invalid. This is because the absence of water is a condition not only at the start but for the entire duration of prayer. This lesson examines the evidence and the distinction from the hadath case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
A person who made tayammum (due to water absence) sees water or gains the ability to use it while still in prayer. Ruling: his prayer becomes invalid (batalat).
2
Understand the reason
Absence of water is a shart (condition) for the permissibility of tayammum. This condition must continue throughout the prayer. If water becomes available, the condition is broken, and the tayammum becomes void, hence the prayer is invalid.
Unlike hadath after tashahhud, where the condition was purity, here the condition is the ongoing inability to use water.
3
Distinguish from the hadath case
In hadath after tashahhud, the prayer was valid because the fara'id were complete. Here, the prayer is invalid because a condition (lack of water) was violated, and the prayer was built on a non-valid substitute.
4
Consider the disagreement
There is a difference of opinion if the mutayammim sees water after an event (hadath) occurs. The correct view is that it becomes invalid, as if he started without wudu.
5
Apply the general principle
The rule is that conditions required at the beginning of prayer (like water absence for tayammum, or covering awrah) must remain throughout. If they cease, the prayer is invalidated.
Analogous to one making expiation by fasting and becoming wealthy – he cannot build.

بصنعه، وعندهما لا تبطل لأنه ليس بفرض عندهما اهـ. وفيه نظر، بل لا يكاد يصح لأنه إذا أتى بمناف بعد سبق الحدث فقد خرج منها بصنعه، ولهذا قال الشارح الزيلعي : وكذا إذا سبقه الحدث بعد التشهد ثم أحدث متعمداً قبل أن يتوضأ تمت صلاته ولم يحك خلافاً، وإنما ثمرة الخلاف تظهر فيما إذا خرج منها لا بصنعه كالمسائل الأثني عشرية كما سنقرره إن شاء الله تعالى. وشمل تعمد الحدث القهقهة عمداً فصلاته تامة وبطل وضوءه لوجودها في أثناء الصلاة فصار كنية الإقامة في هذه الحالة وكذا لو قهقه في سجود السهو . وإن قهقه الإمام أو أحدث متعمداً ثم قهقه القوم فعليه الوضوء دونهم لخروجهم منها بحدث الإمام بخلاف قهقهتهم بعد سلامه لأنهم لا يخرجون منها بسلامه فبطلت طهارتهم، وإن قهقهوا معاً أو القوم فعليهم الوضوء والحاصل أن القوم يخرجون من الصلاة بحدث الإمام عمداً اتفاقاً، ولهذا لا يسلمون ولا يخرجون منها بسلامه عندهما خلافاً لمحمد، وأما بكلامه فعن أبي حنيفة روايتان في رواية كالسلام فيسلمون وتنتقض طهارتهم بالقهقهة، وفي رواية كالحدث العمد فلا سلام ولا نقض بها كذا في المحيط . قوله : ( وبطلت أن رأى متيمم ماء) أي بطلت صلاته بالقدرة على استعمال الماء، ولا عبرة بالرؤية المجردة عن القدرة بدليل ما قدمه في بابه. وإنما بطلت لأن عدم الماء شرط في الابتداء فكان شرط البقاء كسائر الشروط وكالمكفر بالصوم إذا أيسر ليس له البناء لأنه برؤية الماء ظهر حكم الحدث السابق فكأنه شرع على غير وضوء بخلاف ما إذا سبقه الحدث لأنه شرع بوضوء تام أطلقه فشمل ما إذا رأى المتيمم قبل سبق الحدث أو بعده، وفي الثاني خلاف والصحيح هو البطلان كما في المحيط، وجزم به الشارح. واختار في النهاية أنه دون فساد. وفي فتح القدير : والذي يظهر أن الأسباب المتعاقبة كالبول ثم الرعاف ثم القيء إذا أوجبت أحداثاً متعاقبة يجزئه عنها وضوء واحد، فالأوجه ما في شرح الكنز وهو الموافق لما قدمناه من قول محمد فيمن حلف لا يتوضأ من الرعاف فبال ثم رعف ثم توضأ أنه يحنث . يوجب كما قدمنا النظر فيه في باب الغسل فالأوجه ما في النهاية وهو الحق في وإن قلنا لا يبني الرجال حالم وهو المراد به في الحديث خذ من كل حالم (١) . قوله : (وفيه نظر الخ) قال في النهر : (١) رواه أبو داود في كتاب الزكاة باب ٥ أحمد في مسنده (٣٤١/٤).
If an event occurs after the tashahhud, he performs wudu and says the salam. And if he deliberately does it or speaks, his prayer is complete. And if a mutayammim sees water, his prayer becomes invalid. Al-Inayah: He only said 'or he sleeps and has a wet dream' because sleep alone is not a nullifier, likewise wet dream alone is not, and it is puberty by age, so he combined them as clarification of intent. So according to this, ihtilam is puberty, general regardless of emission or age, so the intended meaning in al-Mukhtasar is the first. In al-Zahiriyyah: The one praying, if he dozes in his prayer and then lies down, it is said his purity is broken so he performs wudu and builds upon his prayer, and it is said his prayer is not invalidated nor is his purity broken. Perhaps the author used the term 'istiqbal' (resumption) in these issues like others instead of 'fasad' because invalidity is not intended in them, so he is rewarded for what he did, contrary to if he deliberately invalidates it, then he has no reward for what he performed, rather he sins because cutting it without necessity is haram. His statement: 'And if an event overtakes him after tashahhud, he performs wudu and says salam because the salam is obligatory and he must have wudu to perform it, so wudu and salam are obligatory. If he does not do so, it is makruh tahriman. The conditions we presented for the validity of building are necessary for the salam, so that if he does not perform wudu immediately or does something contradictory afterwards, he misses the salam and it is necessary for him to repeat the prayer to perform the wajib, because that is the ruling of every prayer performed with karahah tahrimiyyah. And if he is an imam, he appoints someone to give salam to the people.' His statement: 'And if he deliberately does it or speaks, his prayer is complete' meaning he deliberately causes the event, due to the hadith of Tirmidhi from Ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah said: 'If a man has an event while he is sitting at the end of his prayer before he says salam, his prayer is valid.' The meaning of 'his prayer is complete' is that its obligatory parts are complete, and therefore it is invalidated by a contradictory act; otherwise it is known that it did not complete all the wajibat because he did not exit. This is the beginning which is the text of al-Hidayah. His statement: 'Because sleep alone is not a nullifier' – al-Ramli said: in al-Tatarkhaniyyah there are statements and differences of correction on this issue, and likewise in al-Jawharah there is difference on the sleep of one lying down and the sick in prayer, but the correct view is that it breaks purity and we take it. It is narrated in al-Tatarkhaniyyah from al-Muhit regarding sleep lying down: the situation is that if his eyes overcome him and he sleeps then lies down in his sleep, it is like an event overtaking him, he performs wudu and builds. If he deliberately sleeps lying down in his prayer, then he performs wudu and starts the prayer over; thus it is related from our shuyukh. So refer to what is transmitted and do not be deceived by his general statement here. His statement: 'According to this, ihtilam is puberty' – al-Nahr said: there is consideration in this because the linguists say ihtilam is a name for what the sleeper sees, then it became dominant for what he sees of a specific kind. Also, if it were itself puberty, then the statement of al-Quduri and others that a child reaches puberty by ihtilam, impregnation, and emission, otherwise until he completes eighteen years, would not be accurate. The motivation for this exaggerated effort seems to be the mention of sleep with it, and it is not an explicit statement of what is known implicitly, as an increase in clarification, especially since the book was written for his son. Shaykh Ismail said: Indeed, what was mentioned in al-Inayah indicated something similar in al-Mughrib: 'al-Halim and al-Muhtalim originally, then it became general, so it was said for one who has reached the age of puberty.' (Footnote: Narrated by Tirmidhi in Kitab al-Salah, bab 183; Abu Dawud in Kitab al-Salah, bab 187, 230; Ibn Majah in Kitab al-Iqamah, bab 138; al-Darimi in Kitab al-Wudu, bab 114; Ahmad in his Musnad 6/272). With the word salam, and it is obligatory by consensus, so much so that this prayer is performed in a makruh manner, so it is repeated in a non-makruh manner, as is the ruling for every prayer performed with karahah. Thus in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. And in it, there is no disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two companions regarding one who is overtaken by an event after it, that he performs wudu and says salam. The disagreement is only when he does not perform wudu until he does something contradictory – according to Abu Hanifa, his prayer becomes invalid because he did not exit by his own action, while according to them it does not become invalid because it is not a fard according to them. But this is questionable; indeed it is hardly sound because by doing something contradictory after being overtaken by the event, he exits by his own action. Therefore, al-Zaylai said: Likewise, if he is overtaken by an event after tashahhud and then deliberately causes an event before performing wudu, his prayer is complete and no disagreement is reported. The fruit of the difference appears only when he exits not by his own action, like the twelve issues, as we will discuss if Allah wills. His deliberate causing of the event includes deliberate laughter, so his prayer is complete but his wudu is invalid because it occurred during the prayer, so it becomes like the intention of staying in that case. Likewise, if he laughs during sujud al-sahw. If the imam laughs or deliberately causes an event and then the people laugh, then the imam must perform wudu but not the people because they exit by the imam's event, contrary to their laughter after his salam because they do not exit by his salam, so their purity is invalidated. If they laugh together, or the people laugh, then they must perform wudu. The conclusion is that the people exit the prayer by the imam's deliberate event by agreement, hence they do not say salam, and they do not exit by his salam according to the two companions, contrary to Muhammad. As for his speech, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: in one narration it is like salam, so they say salam and their purity is broken by laughter; in another narration it is like deliberate event, so no salam and no break by it. Thus in al-Muhit. His statement: 'And if a mutayammim sees water, his prayer becomes invalid' – meaning his prayer becomes invalid due to ability to use water. Mere sight without ability is not considered, as evidenced by what was presented in its chapter. It becomes invalid because the absence of water is a condition at the beginning, so it remains a condition for staying, like other conditions, and like the one who makes expiation by fasting and becomes wealthy, he cannot build because by seeing water the ruling of the previous event appears, so it is as if he began without wudu, contrary to the one overtaken by an event because he began with complete wudu, which he released. This includes if the mutayammim sees water before being overtaken by an event or after. In the second case there is disagreement, and the correct view is invalidity as in al-Muhit, and the commentator affirmed it. He chose in al-Nihayah that it is less than invalidity. In Fath al-Qadir: it appears that successive causes like urination then nosebleed then vomiting, if they necessitate successive events, a single wudu suffices for them. So the most appropriate is what is in Sharh al-Kanz, which is in agreement with what we presented from Muhammad regarding one who swore not to perform wudu from nosebleed, then urinated, then had a nosebleed, then performed wudu – that he is oath-breaking. This necessitates, as we presented, consideration in the chapter of ghusl, so the most appropriate is what is in al-Nihayah, and it is the truth, and if we say he does not build, the men are dreaming (?) and that is meant in the hadith 'take from every dreamer' (Footnote: Narrated by Abu Dawud in Kitab al-Zakah, bab 5; Ahmad in his Musnad 4/341). His statement: 'And there is consideration, etc.' – al-Nahr said:
Source pages p. 653

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, expanding on rulings related to events (hadath) during prayer. The author, Imam al-Kasani (or the commentator of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq), explains several key scenarios. First, if a person has an event (e.g., breaking wudu) after the tashahhud but before salam, he must perform wudu and then say salam. This is because salam is wajib and requires wudu. If he fails to do so, the prayer is valid but makruh tahriman (prohibitively disliked); he should repeat it to be free of karahah. If he is an imam, he should appoint someone to lead the salam. Second, if he deliberately causes the event or speaks after the event, his prayer is still valid (complete in terms of fara'id) due to the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'If a man has an event while sitting at the end of his prayer before salam, his prayer is valid.' However, deliberate laughter (qahqaha) during prayer invalidates wudu but not the prayer itself in this context, as it occurs after the event. The text also delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute: if one does not perform wudu after the event and instead does something contradictory (like speaking), Abu Hanifa says his prayer becomes invalid because he exited by his own action, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it does not become invalid because salam is not fard according to them. The commentator sides with the view that it is valid, following al-Zaylai. Third, regarding a mutayammim (one performing tayammum), if he sees water (or gains ability to use it) during prayer, his prayer becomes invalid because the absence of water is a continuing condition. This applies whether he sees water before or after an event, though there is a difference of opinion. The text also discusses related issues like sleep, wet dream (ihtilam), and the distinction between deliberate and involuntary acts. Throughout, the Hanafi position is upheld, with references to authoritative sources like al-Hidayah, al-Muhit, and al-Nahr.

Key Terms
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution with pure earth as substitute for wudu when water unavailable.
القدرة على استعمال الماء (al-qudrah 'ala isti'mal al-ma'): Ability to use water (physical and legal ability).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A mutayammim sees a river during his prayer but it is on the other side of a high wall. What is the ruling?
A) His prayer becomes invalid because he saw water.
B) His prayer remains valid because he cannot actually use the water.
C) His prayer is suspended until he finds a way to the water.
D) He must repeat his tayammum but can continue the prayer.

Key Takeaway
The mutayammim's prayer is built on the condition of water unavailability; if that condition breaks, the entire prayer is invalidated.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Hadath After Tashahhud and Qahqaha in Prayer: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute and qahqaha rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the validity of prayer when a munafi occurs after hadath post-tashahhud, and apply the rulings on qahqaha to imam and followers.

Core Idea
Exiting prayer requires the salam — a munafi before wudu does not count, according to Abu Hanifa.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into a subtle intra-Hanafi disagreement. After tashahhud, if a person is overtaken by hadath, all agree he needs wudu and salam. But what if he performs an invalidating act (munafi) before wudu? Abu Hanifa invalidates the prayer; the Sahibayn uphold it. The passage then expands on qahqaha (loud laughter) and its effect on imam and followers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
The text states that salam after hadath is obligatory by consensus, though the prayer is performed with dislike (makruh) and should be repeated without karaha. Recognize that the prayer itself is valid but deficient.
This is the agreed starting point.
2
Locate the point of disagreement
The dispute arises when a person overtaken by hadath after tashahhud does not perform wudu but instead performs a munafi (invalidating act) like speaking or laughing. Abu Hanifa says the prayer becomes invalid; the Sahibayn say it remains valid.
The disagreement is about the status of salam after hadath.
3
Analyze the reasoning
Abu Hanifa argues that the person exits by his own action (the munafi) rather than the prescribed exit (salam), so the prayer is invalid. The Sahibayn hold that salam is not fard after hadath, so the prayer is still valid despite the munafi.
The commentator (Ibn Nujaym) leans towards Abu Hanifa, calling the Sahibayn's view 'hardly correct'.
4
Examine the application to qahqaha
The text rules that intentional qahqaha during prayer invalidates wudu but not the prayer itself. Consider scenarios: imam laughs, followers laugh; their wudu and prayer status differ depending on timing.
The followers exit by the imam's hadath, but not by his salam according to the Sahibayn.
5
Note the 'twelve issues'
The commentator mentions that the fruit (thamarah) of the dispute appears in cases where the person exits not by his own action, which are enumerated elsewhere as the twelve issues. This contextualizes the scope of the ikhtilaf.
These are specific scenarios where the Salam is not the exit mechanism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بلفظ السلام وهو واجب بالاتفاق حتى إن هذه الصلاة تكون مؤداة على وجه مكروه فتعاد على وجه غير مكروه كما هو الحكم في كل صلاة أديت مع الكراهة. كذا في شرح منية المصلي، وفيه أنه لا خلاف بين أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه في أن من سبقه الحدث بعده يتوضأ ويسلم، وإنما الخلاف فيما إذا لم يتوضأ حتى أتى بمناف فعند أبي حنيفة بطلت صلاته لعدم الخروج بصنعه، وعندهما لا تبطل لأنه ليس بفرض عندهما اهـ. وفيه نظر، بل لا يكاد يصح لأنه إذا أتى بمناف بعد سبق الحدث فقد خرج منها بصنعه، ولهذا قال الشارح الزيلعي : وكذا إذا سبقه الحدث بعد التشهد ثم أحدث متعمداً قبل أن يتوضأ تمت صلاته ولم يحك خلافاً، وإنما ثمرة الخلاف تظهر فيما إذا خرج منها لا بصنعه كالمسائل الأثني عشرية كما سنقرره إن شاء الله تعالى. وشمل تعمد الحدث القهقهة عمداً فصلاته تامة وبطل وضوءه لوجودها في أثناء الصلاة فصار كنية الإقامة في هذه الحالة وكذا لو قهقه في سجود السهو . وإن قهقه الإمام أو أحدث متعمداً ثم قهقه القوم فعليه الوضوء دونهم لخروجهم منها بحدث الإمام بخلاف قهقهتهم بعد سلامه لأنهم لا يخرجون منها بسلامه فبطلت طهارتهم، وإن قهقهوا معاً أو القوم فعليهم الوضوء والحاصل أن القوم يخرجون من الصلاة بحدث الإمام عمداً اتفاقاً، ولهذا لا يسلمون ولا يخرجون منها بسلامه عندهما خلافاً لمحمد، وأما بكلامه فعن أبي حنيفة روايتان في رواية كالسلام فيسلمون وتنتقض طهارتهم بالقهقهة، وفي رواية كالحدث العمد فلا سلام ولا نقض بها كذا في المحيط .
With the wording of salam, and it is obligatory by consensus, to the extent that this prayer is performed in a disliked manner, so it is repeated in a non-disliked manner, as is the ruling in every prayer performed with dislike. Thus in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. And it contains that there is no disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two companions regarding one who is overtaken by hadath after it: he performs wudu and says salam. The disagreement is only when he does not perform wudu until he does something invalidating: according to Abu Hanifa, his prayer is invalid because he did not exit by his own action; according to them, it is not invalid because the salam is not obligatory in their view. [End] And there is consideration, rather it is hardly valid, because if he does something invalidating after being overtaken by hadath, he has exited from it by his own action. Hence the commentator al-Zayla'i said: Similarly, if he is overtaken by hadath after tashahhud, then intentionally creates hadath before performing wudu, his prayer is complete, and he did not cite disagreement. The fruit of the disagreement only appears in cases where he exits from it not by his own action, like the twelve issues, as we will explain if Allah wills. And it includes intentional hadath: intentional qahqaha, so his prayer is complete and his wudu is invalid because it occurs during the prayer, so it becomes like the intention of iqama in this case. Similarly, if he laughs during sajdah al-sahw. And if the imam laughs or intentionally creates hadath, and then the followers laugh, the imam must perform wudu but not the followers, because they exit from the prayer by the imam's hadath, unlike their laughter after his salam, because they do not exit by his salam, so their purity is invalid. If they laugh together, or the followers only, they must perform wudu. The conclusion is that the followers exit from the prayer by the imam's intentional hadath by agreement, therefore they do not say salam and do not exit by his salam according to them, contrary to Muhammad. As for his speech, from Abu Hanifa there are two narrations: in one narration, it is like the salam, so they say salam and their purity is vitiated by qahqaha; in another narration, it is like intentional hadath, so they do not say salam and it is not vitiated. Thus in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 654

Commentary
This passage from the commentary deals with two related issues: being overtaken by hadath (ritual impurity) after the tashahhud, and the effect of qahqaha (loud laughter) during prayer. The author first states that saying the salam after hadath is obligatory by consensus, though the prayer is considered makruh and should be repeated without karaha. He then clarifies the intra-Hanafi dispute: if one is overtaken by hadath after tashahhud, all agree he must renew wudu and say salam. The dispute arises if he performs an invalidating act (munafi) before wudu. Abu Hanifa says the prayer is invalid because he did not exit by his own intentional action (the salam), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it remains valid, as salam is not fard for them after hadath. The passage then discusses that the true fruit of the disagreement appears in cases where one exits without his own action (like the twelve known issues). Next, it addresses qahqaha: if one laughs intentionally during prayer, the prayer itself is valid but wudu is invalidated. Detailed rules follow: if the imam laughs or deliberately creates hadath, the imam's wudu breaks but the followers' wudu does not, unless they laugh after his salam. There are also different narrations from Abu Hanifa regarding the followers' exit by the imam's speech.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity that nullifies wudu, whether minor (like urine) or major (janabah). Here it specifically refers to minor hadath occurring after tashahhud.
قهقهة (qahqaha): Loud laughter that is audible to others; it invalidates wudu but not the prayer itself.
مناف (munafi): An act that is inconsistent with the prayer, such as speaking, eating, or laughing; nullifies the prayer if done intentionally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the effect of intentional qahqaha (loud laughter) during prayer on the prayer and wudu?
A) Prayer invalid, wudu invalid
B) Prayer valid, wudu invalid
C) Prayer invalid, wudu valid
D) Both valid

Key Takeaway
Exiting prayer by an invalidating act before wudu after hadath does not constitute a valid exit per Abu Hanifa, making the prayer invalid; the Sahibayn differ, but the mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
